شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
وَهُذَا بِخِلَافِ خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ فِي الْبَيْعِ لِاَنَّ الْخِيَارَ دَاخِلٌ عَلَى الْحُكْمِ دُوْنَ السَّبَبِ وَلِهَذَا لَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يَبِيعُ فَبَاعَ بِشَرْطِ الْخِيَارِ يَحْنَثُ ترجمہ : ۔ اور یہ بیچ میں خیار شرط کے خلاف ہے، اس لئے کہ خیار شرط داخل ہے حکم پر نہ کہ سبب پر ، اور اسی وجہ سے اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ نہیں بیچے گا پھر اس نے خیار کی شرط کے ساتھ بیچا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح:- مصنف نے امام شافعی کے ایک استدلال کا جواب دے رہے ہیں امام شافعی سے فرماتے ہیں کہ تعلیق بالشرط مانع حکم ہے، مانع سبب نہیں ہے، جیسے دیکھئے اس مثال میں ، اگر کسی نے خیار شرط کے ساتھ بیچ کی تو بیع منعقد ہو جاتی ہے مگر ملک کا نفاذ نہیں ہوتا ہے، تو خیار شرط بیع کے حکم (ملک ) پر داخل ہوتی ہے اور سبب ( بیع ) پر داخل نہیں ہوتی ہے، معلوم ہوا کہ شرط مانع حکم ہے نہ کے مانع سبب، امام شافعی اللہ نے طلاق وعتاق کو بیچ پر قیاس کیا۔ مصنف اللہ اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ بالکل صحیح کہا آپ نے ، خیار شرط حکم ( ملک ) سے مانع ہے نہ کہ سبب سے یعنی بیج سے مگر آپ کا ایک کو دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے، قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔ کیونکہ بیع از قبیل اثبات ہے، اس میں مشتری کے لئے مبیع ثابت ہوتی ہے اور بائع کے لئے ملک شمن ثابت ہوتا ہے اور جو چیز از قبیل اثبات ہوتی ہے ، اس میں تعلیق درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ تعلیق سے قمار (جوے) کے معنی پیدا ہوتے ہیں اس لئے کہ شرط پر معلق ہے تو پتہ نہیں شرط ہوگی یا نہیں اگر شرط ہوگی تو بیع ہوگی ، ورنہ نہ ہوگی تو یہ جوا اور قمار ہے ، اور قمار حرام ہے ، اسی لئے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے بیع و شرط سے منع کیا ہے ، پس قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ بیع میں خیار شرط جائز نہ ہو مگر خیار شرط خلاف قیاس لوگوں کو غبن اور دھوکہ سے بچانے کے لئے حدیث سے ثابت ہے، پس ضرورةً اس کا ثبوت ہوا، لہذا یہ بقد رضرورت ہی رہے گا، اور یہاں شرط کو حکم پر داخل ماننے سے ضرورت پوری ہو جاتی ہے،اور سبب پر داخل ماننا امر زائد ہے، کیوں کہ سبب پر داخل ماننے سے دو چیزوں کی نفی ہوگی ، سبب کی بھی نفی ہوگی اور اس کے ضمن میں حکم کی بھی حالانکہ صرف حکم کی نفی سے کام چل جاتا ہے، لہذا اس کو حکم پر داخل مانا گیا، تا کہ شرط کا اثر کم ے کم ظاہر ہو اور ضرورت بھی پوری ہو جائے، اور چونکہ خیار شرط حکم پر داخل ہوتا ہے نہ کہ بیع پر ، لہذا اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ میں بیع نہیں کروں گا اور خیار شرط کے ساتھ اس نے بیع کی تو حانث ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ خیار کے ساتھ بیع منعقد ہو جاتی ہے۔ رہا طلاق و عتاق کا مسئلہ تو وہ از قبیل اسقاط ہے، اس میں ملک نکاح کو اور ملک یمین کو ساقط کرنا ہوتا ہے لہذا اس میں تعلیق سے قمار کے معنی پیدا نہیں ہوتے ، لہذا یہاں تعلیق مانع سبب ہوگی نہ کہ مانع حکم ۔ تو دونوں الگ الگ ہیں ایک کو دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔

الفيضُ الحجازي
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
وَإِذَا ثَبَتَ أَنَّ التَّعْلِيْقَ تَصَرُّفْ فِى السَّبَبِ بِاعْدَامِهِ إِلَى زَمَانِ وَجُوْدِ الشَّرْطِ لَا فِي أَحْكَامِهِ صَحَ تَعْلِيقُ الطَّلَاقِ وَالْعَتَاقِ بِالْمِلْكِ وَبَطَلَ التَّكْفِيرُ بِالْمَالِ قَبْلَ الْحِنْثِ وَفَرْقُهُ بَيْنَ الْمَالِي وَالْبَدَنِي سَاقِطْ لِاَنَ حَقَّ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى فِي الْمَالِي فِعْلُ الْآدَاءِ وَالْمَالُ الَةٌ وَإِنَّمَا يَقْصَدْ عَيْنَ الْمَالِ فِي حُقوقِ الْعِبَادِ ترجمہ: اور جب یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ تعلیق تصرف ہے سبب کے اندر ،سبب کے شرط کے پائے جانے کے زمانہ تک معدوم کرنے کے ذریعے ، نہ کہ سبب کے احکام میں تو طلاق اور عتاق کو ملک پر معلق کرنا صحیح ہو گیا اور حانث ہونے سے پہلے مال کے ذریعے کفارہ دینا باطل ہو گیا، اور امام شافعی لینے کا فرق کرنا مالی اور بدنی کے درمیان ساقط (باطل ) ہے، اس لیے کہ مالی میں اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق فعل ادا ہے ، اور مال ایک آلہ ہے ، اور عین مال مقصود ہوتا ہے حقوق العباد میں۔
شریح : ۔ اس میں تیسرے اور چوتھے مقدمہ کی تردید ہے، جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ جب گذشتہ تقریر سے یہ بات ثابت ہوگئی کہ تعلیق بالشرط مانع سبب ہے یعنی شرط کے پائے جانے کے زمانے تک سبب کو معدوم کر دیتا ہے نہ کہ حکم کو، یعنی مانع سبب ہے نہ کہ مانع حکم ، تو اس سے تیسرا اور چوتھا مقدمہ خود ہی باطل ہو گیا ، اور طلاق وعتناق کو ملک پر معلق کرنا صحیح ہو گیا، اور حانث ہونے سے پہلے مالی کفارہ باطل ہو گیا، لہذا ان نكحتك فانت طالق - ان مللتك فانت حر صحیح ہے، کیونکہ تعلیق نے انت طالق اور انت حر کو سبب بننے سے روک دیا، شرط کے پائے جانے تک، لہذا جب سبب منعقد نہیں ہوا تو فی الحال محل کی ضرورت نہیں ، لہذا یہ کلام لغو نہیں ہوگا، بلکہ جب شرط پائی جائیگی یعنی وہ عورت سے نکاح کرے گا یا غلام کا مالک ہو گا تو اس وقت (انت طالق اور انت حر ) سبب بنے گا اور اس وقت محل موجود ہو گا تو گویا اس نے اسی وقت (انت طالق اور انت حر ) کہا ہے پس عورت پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔
اسی طرح حانث ہونے سے پہلے کفارہ مالی دینا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وجوب کفارہ کا سبب یمین نہیں ہے بلکہ حانث ہونا ہے اور یہ سب پایا نہیں گیا کیونکہ تعلیق بالشرط مانع سبب ہے یعنی تعلیق بالشرط میں شرط کے پائے جانے سے پہلے سبب منعقد ہوتا ہی نہیں ہے، تو حانث ہونے سے پہلے مالی کفارہ ادا کرنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے، امام شافعی عطاللہ نے یمین کو سب قرار دیا ہے یہ صحیح نہیں ہے، کیونکہ یمین کا انعقاد تو پر یعنی قسم پوری کرنے کے لئے ہوتا ہے، اس کو کفارہ کا سبب نہیں بنا سکتے ، کفارہ کا سبب تو حانث ہونا ہے۔
And this is contrary to khiyar al-shart in sale because the option enters upon the ruling not upon the cause, and for this reason if someone swore that he will not sell, and then he sold with a condition of option, he breaks his oath. Translation: And this is contrary to khiyar al-shart in sale, because khiyar al-shart enters upon the ruling not upon the cause, and for this reason if someone swore that he will not sell, then he sold with a condition of option, he becomes a breaker of oath. Explanation: The author is responding to an argument of Imam al-Shafi'i. Imam al-Shafi'i says that ta'liq bi al-shart is a preventer of the ruling, not a preventer of the cause. As seen in this example: if someone sold with khiyar al-shart, the sale is concluded but ownership is not executed. So khiyar al-shart enters upon the ruling (ownership) of the sale, not upon the cause (the sale itself). It becomes known that the condition is a preventer of the ruling, not a preventer of the cause. Imam al-Shafi'i analogized talaq and itq to sale. The author is responding that what you said is correct: khiyar al-shart prevents the ruling, not the cause, i.e., the sale. But your analogy of one to the other is not correct; it is an analogy with a difference (qiyas ma'a al-fariq). Because sale is of the category of establishment (ithbat); in it the sold object is established for the buyer and ownership of the price is established for the seller. And a thing that is of the category of establishment, ta'liq is not valid in it because ta'liq creates the meaning of gambling (qimar), since it is suspended on a condition, and it is not known whether the condition will occur or not. If the condition occurs, the sale occurs, otherwise not. This is gambling and qimar, and qimar is haram. For this reason, the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibited sale and condition. So the requirement of qiyas was that khiyar al-shart should not be permissible in sale, but khiyar al-shart is against qiyas, established by hadith to protect people from deception and fraud. So out of necessity it is established. Therefore it remains only to the extent of necessity. And here considering the condition as entering upon the ruling fulfills the necessity, while considering it entering upon the cause is an extra matter, because considering it entering upon the cause would negate two things: it would negate the cause, and within it also the ruling, whereas only negating the ruling suffices. Therefore it was considered as entering upon the ruling so that the effect of the condition appears minimally and the necessity is fulfilled. And since khiyar al-shart enters upon the ruling not upon the sale, if someone swore that he will not sell and he sold with khiyar al-shart, he breaks his oath, because the sale is concluded with the option. As for the issue of talaq and itq, they are of the category of annulment (isqat); in them, ownership of marriage and ownership of the slave are annulled. Therefore ta'liq in them does not create the meaning of gambling. Hence, here ta'liq is a preventer of the cause, not a preventer of the ruling. So both are separate; analogizing one to the other is qiyas ma'a al-fariq. And when it is established that ta'liq is a disposition in the cause by making it nonexistent until the time of the condition's occurrence, not in its rulings, then ta'liq of talaq and itq upon ownership becomes valid, and paying expiation (kaffara) with wealth before breaking the oath becomes invalid. And his (Imam al-Shafi'i's) differentiation between mali (financial) and badani (physical) is invalid because in financial matters, the right of Allah is the act of performance, and wealth is a tool, and the specific wealth is intended in the rights of the servants. Translation: And when it is established that ta'liq is a disposition in the cause by making it nonexistent until the time of the condition's occurrence, not in its rulings, then ta'liq of talaq and itq upon ownership becomes correct, and paying expiation with wealth before breaking the oath becomes invalid. And Imam al-Shafi'i's making a distinction between financial and physical is invalid, because in financial matters Allah's right is the act of performance, and wealth is a tool, and the specific wealth is intended in the rights of the servants. Explanation: In this, the third and fourth premises are refuted. The summary is that when from the previous discussion it is established that ta'liq bi al-shart is a preventer of the cause, i.e., it makes the cause nonexistent until the condition occurs, not the ruling, i.e., it is a preventer of the cause not a preventer of the ruling, then the third and fourth premises become invalid themselves. And ta'liq of talaq and itq upon ownership becomes valid, and paying financial expiation before breaking the oath becomes invalid. Therefore, 'If I marry you, you are divorced' and 'If I own you, you are free' are valid, because ta'liq prevented 'you are divorced' and 'you are free' from becoming a cause until the condition occurs. So when the cause is not concluded, there is no need for the locus at that moment; thus this speech is not pointless. Rather, when the condition occurs, i.e., he marries that woman or becomes owner of the slave, then ('you are divorced' and 'you are free') become a cause, and the locus exists at that time, so it is as if he said ('you are divorced' and 'you are free') at that time. So divorce occurs upon the woman and the slave becomes free. Similarly, paying financial expiation before breaking the oath is not valid, because the cause for the obligation of expiation is not the oath itself but the breaking of the oath, and this has not occurred yet, because ta'liq bi al-shart is a preventer of the cause, i.e., in ta'liq bi al-shart, the cause is not concluded before the condition occurs. So paying financial expiation before breaking the oath is not valid. Imam al-Shafi'i considered the oath as the cause; this is not correct, because the oath is concluded for fulfilling the oath; it cannot be made the cause of expiation. The cause of expiation is the breaking of the oath.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi refutation of Imam al-Shafi'i's position on ta'liq (suspension by condition) in talaq and itq compared to khiyar al-shart in sale. The Hanafi author begins by stating that khiyar al-shart in sale enters upon the ruling (hukm), not the cause (sabab). This is why, if someone swears not to sell and then sells with an option, he breaks his oath—because the sale is concluded. Imam al-Shafi'i analogized talaq and itq to sale, arguing that ta'liq should also be a preventer of the ruling. The Hanafi response is that this analogy is invalid (qiyas ma'a al-fariq) because sale is a transaction of establishment (ithbat)—it creates ownership—and ta'liq in such a transaction would imply gambling (qimar), which is prohibited. However, khiyar al-shart is an exception, proven by hadith to protect people from harm, and it is limited to necessity. Therefore, in sale, ta'liq is restricted to entering upon the ruling only. In contrast, talaq and itq are acts of annulment (isqat)—they remove ownership. Ta'liq in these does not imply gambling because the effect is simply delayed; when the condition occurs, it is as if the statement was made at that moment. Thus, here ta'liq prevents the cause (the spoken words from taking effect immediately) until the condition is met. The passage then establishes the principle that ta'liq is a disposition in the cause, making it nonexistent until the condition occurs, not a disposition in the ruling. This validates suspended talaq and itq (e.g., 'If I marry you, you are divorced'). It also invalidates paying expiation (kaffara) before breaking the oath, because the cause for expiation is the breaking of the oath, not the oath itself. Imam al-Shafi'i's distinction between financial and physical acts is also rejected: in financial acts, Allah's right is the act of performance, not the specific wealth, whereas in rights of servants, the specific wealth is intended. The Hanafi position is based on the foundational texts and rational analysis, distinguishing between types of legal acts.

Key Terms
التعليق بالشرط (al-ta'liq bi al-shart): A disposition in the cause by making it nonexistent until the time of the condition's occurrence.
قياس مع الفارق (qiyas ma'a al-fariq): An analogy that is invalid because the two cases are fundamentally different in their legal nature.
إثبات (ithbat): Legal acts that establish ownership or rights (e.g., sale).
إسقاط (isqat): Legal acts that annul rights or ownership (e.g., talaq, itq).

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in this passage, why is paying kaffara before breaking an oath invalid in a conditional oath?
A) Because the oath itself is not a cause for kaffara; the cause is the breaking of the oath, and ta'liq prevents the cause from existing until the condition occurs.
B) Because kaffara must be paid in cash only, not in kind.
C) Because the Prophet forbade paying kaffara early.
D) Because the oath is considered a mere promise, not a legal cause.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes acts of establishment (ithbat) from annulment (isqat); ta'liq is man'i sabab in isqat and man'i hukm in ithbat by necessity, and analogizing between them is qiyas ma'a al-fariq.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Refutation of Conjunction Necessitating Conjunction in Ruling
Refutes a Maliki qiyas on conjunction using dependency analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Maliki claim that conjunction (qiran) in wording necessitates conjunction in ruling, and apply the Hanafi principle that legal sharing arises only from dependency or need.

Core Idea
Conjunction does not create legal sharing; only dependency or need can.

This lesson examines a key usul dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Malik regarding the effect of conjunction (qiran) on legal rulings. The Maliki position holds that when two sentences are joined by 'and', they must share the same ruling—a claim the Hanafi tradition refutes as invalid. By analyzing grammatical dependency and contextual cues, you will learn why the Hanafi school rejects automatic sharing and instead grounds rulings on independent proofs like the hadith 'The pen is lifted from three'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested claim
Recognize that the Maliki argument asserts that conjunction in wording (e.g., 'Establish prayer and give zakat') forces the two clauses to share the same legal ruling. Understand that they apply this to derive that zakat is not obligatory on the insane because prayer is not.
The contested claim is that qiran fi al-nazm necessitates qiran fi al-hukm.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school denies automatic sharing. Sharing only occurs when one clause is dependent on the other (e.g., an incomplete sentence needing a predicate, or a conditional context). The primary proof for the ruling on the insane is the hadith 'The pen is lifted from three'—not conjunction.
The hadith establishes lack of taklif, not conjunction.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
Imam Malik analogizes conjunction of complete sentences to conjunction of incomplete sentences. In the incomplete case (e.g., 'Zaynab is divorced and Hind'), the second clause borrows the predicate from the first. Maliki extends this to complete sentences, arguing they share in ruling if not in wording.
The qiyas treats all conjunctions as creating dependency.
4
Apply the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes dependency: incomplete sentences need completion, so sharing is forced. Complete sentences are independent, so no sharing unless context shows need (e.g., 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free'—the second clause is deficient in suspension). The hadith overrides any conjunction-based argument.
The Hanafi response shows that the Maliki qiyas is invalid (fasid) because it ignores the reason (illah) for sharing.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Both schools agree zakat is not obligatory on the insane, but for different reasons. Maliki says due to conjunction, Hanafi says due to lack of taklif (ḥadīth). The practical difference appears in cases where the hadith does not apply—then Hanafi might still require zakat even if the clause is conjoined, while Maliki would not.
The dispute is methodological, not always practical.

وَمِنْهَا مَا قَالَ بَعْضُهُمْ أَنَّ الْقِرَانَ فِي النَّظْمِ يُوجِبُ الْقِرَانَ فِي الْحُكْمِ مِثْلُ قَوْلِ بَعْضِهِمْ فِى قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَاقِيْمُوا الصَّلوةَ وَأتُوا الزَّكُوةُ إِنَّ القِرَانَ يُؤْجِبْ أَنْ لا تَجِبَ الزَّكْوةُ عَلَى الصَّبِى قَالُوا لِاَنَّ الْعَطْفَ يَقْتَضِي الْمُشَارَكَةَ وَأَعْتَبَرُوا بِالْجُمْلَةِ النَّاقِصَةِ إِذَا عُطِفَتْ عَلَى الْكَامِلَةِ وَهَذَا فَاسِدٌ لِاَنَّ الشَّرْكَةَ إِنَّمَا وَجَبَتْ فِي الْجُمْلَةِ النَّاقْصَةِ لِاِفْتِقَارِهَا إِلى مَايَتِمُ بِهِ فَإِذَا تَمَّ بِنَفْسِهِ لَمْ تَجِبٍ الشَّرُكَةُ إِلَّا فِيْمَا يَفْتَقِرُ اِلَيْهِ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا فِي قَوْلِ الرَّجُلِ لِاِمْرَأَتِهِ إِنْ دَخَلْتِ الدَّارَ فَأَنْتِ طَالِقٌ وَعَبْدِى حَرّانَ الْعِتْقَ يَتَعَلَّقُ بالشَّرْطِ لِأَنَّهُ فِي حَقَّ التَّعْلِيقِ قَاصِرْ
ترجمہ :۔ اور ان وجوہ فاسدہ میں سے ایک وجہ وہ ہے جو بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ لفظ میں قران ملاپ ) واجب کرتا ہے حکم میں قرآن کو جیسے ان میں سے بعض حضرات کا قول ہے اللہ تعالی کے ارشاد و اقیموا الصلوة وأتوا الزكوة میں کہ قران واجب کرتا ہے اس بات کو کہ واجب نہیں ہے بچہ پر زکوۃ ، انہوں نے کہا اس لئے کہ عطف تقاضا کرتا ہے مشارکت کا اور ان حضرات نے قیاس کیا ہے جملہ کا قصہ پر جب کہ اس کا عطف کیا جائے جملہ کاملہ پر اور یہ قیاس فاسد ہے اس لئے کہ شرکت واجب ہوتی ہے جملہ کا قصہ میں اس کے محتاج ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کلام کی طرف جس کے ذریعہ وہ تام ہو جائے ، پس جب کلام تام ہو بذات خود تو شرکت واجب نہ ہوگی مگر اس چیز میں جس کی جانب احتیاج ہو، اور اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا ہے مرد کے قول میں اپنی بیوی سے ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق وعبدی حر کہ عشق متعلق ہو گا شرط کے ساتھ اس لئے کہ یہ تعلیق کے حق میں قاصر ہے۔ تشریح : وجوہ فاسدہ میں سے آخری وجہ فاسد بیان کر رہے ہیں اس کے قائل امام مالک یہ ہیں ، وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قران فی النظم قران فی الحکم کو واجب کرتا ہے یعنی دو کلام جب حرف عطف کے ذریعہ جمع ہو جائیں تو یہ دلیل ہوگی اس بات کی کہ یہ دونوں کلام حکم میں بھی شریک ہیں ، اسی لئے وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مجنون پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ اللہ تعالی کا ارشاد ہے واقیموا الصلوة وأتوا الزكوة اقامت صلوۃ اور ایتاء زکوۃ دو جملوں کو حرف عطف کے ذریعہ جمع کیا گیا ہے تو یہ عطف تقاضا کرتا ہے کہ دونوں جملوں میں حکم میں بھی شرکت ہے ، دونوں میں حکم میں بھی برابری ہے اور حکم میں شرکت اور برابری کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایک واجب ہوگا، تو دوسرا بھی واجب ہوگا اگر ایک واجب نہیں ہے تو دوسرا بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور یہاں نماز مجنون پر واجب نہیں ہے تو زکوۃ بھی واجب نہ ہوگی ، کیونکہ دو جملوں کا بذریعہ عطف جمع ہونا حکم میں شرکت کا تقاضا کرتا ہے ہمارے نزدیک بھی مجنون پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے لیکن اس دلیل سے نہیں جو امام مالک بیان کر رہے ہیں بلکہ ہمارا مستدل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں فرما یا رفع القلم عن ثلاثۃ تین آدمیوں سے قلم اٹھادیا گیا ہے، نائم صبی اور مجنون سے قلم اٹھا دینے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ مکلف نہیں ہیں لہذا جب مکلف نہیں ہیں تو زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ امام مالک عالیہ اس وجہ فاسد میں استدلال کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ اگر جملہ نا قصہ کا عطف جملہ کاملہ پر کیا جائے تو اس وقت دونوں جملے خبر میں شریک ہوتے ہیں جیسی زینب طالق و هند نا قصہ کا عطف کاملہ پر ہے اور دونوں خبر میں شریک ہیں ، یعنی زینب اور ھند دونوں پر طلاق واقع ہوگی تو ایسے ہی اگر جملہ کاملہ کا کاملہ پر عطف کیا جائے تو دونوں اگر چہ خبر میں شریک نہ ہونگے کیونکہ دونوں کامل جملے ہیں، البتہ حکم میں شریک ہو جائیں گے، جیسے زینب طالق و ھند طالق ۔ بہر حال امام مالک جملہ کاملہ کے کاملہ پر عطف کو جملہ کا قصہ کے کاملہ پر عطف کرنے پر قیاس کرتے ہیں۔۔ مگر ہم اس کو استدلال فاسد کہتے ہیں، کیونکہ نا قصہ کے کاملہ پر عطف کی صورت میں جو دونوں خبر میں شریک ہیں وہ اس وجہ سے نہیں کہ دونوں حرف عطف سے جمع ہوئے ہیں، بلکہ اس وجہ سے کہ ناقصہ میں خبر کی ضرورت ہے اس لئے وہ کا ملہ کا محتاج ہے، اس لئے خبر میں نا قصہ کو کاملہ کے ساتھ شریک کر دیا۔ اور کاملہ دوسرے کاملہ کا محتاج نہیں ہے ،لہذا شرکت بھی نہ ہو سکے گی۔ ہاں اگر کا ملہ بھی کبھی کسی چیز میں دوسرے کا ملہ کا محتاج ہو جائے تو احتیاج کی حد تک شرکت ثابت ہو جائے گی جیسے کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق و عبدی حر یہاں دو جملے اگر چہ کامل ہیں مگر دوسرا جملہ تعلیق میں پہلے کا محتاج ہے تو تعلیق میں دوسرے کو پہلے کے ساتھ شریک کر دینگے اور یوں کہیں گے کہ طلاق اور آزادی دونوں شرط پر معلق ہونگے ، کیونکہ دلالت حال کا تقاضا ہے کہ متکلم کا مقصد طلاق اور آزادی دونوں کو شرط پر معلق کرنا ہے ۔ ہاں اگر شوہر یوں کہے ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق وزينب طالق تو یہاں دونوں جملے مستقل ہیں، دوسرا تعلیق میں بھی پہلے کا محتاج نہیں ہے، لہذا پہلا جملہ تو شرط پر معلق رہے گا مگر دوسرا معلق نہ ہوگا بلکہ منجر ہوگا یعنی زینب پر فور اطلاق پڑ جائے گی کیونکہ اگر وہ دوسرے جملے کو بھی تعلیق میں پہلے کے ساتھ شریک کرنا چاہتا تو زینب کے بعد خبر نہ لاتا صرف یوں کہتا ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق وزينب ، وجوهِ فاسدہ کا بیان مکمل ہو گیا۔
And among these (invalid arguments) is what some scholars said: that conjunction in wording necessitates conjunction in ruling, like the saying of some of them regarding the statement of Allah Almighty: 'Establish prayer and give zakat' – that the conjunction necessitates that zakat is not obligatory on a child. They said because the conjunctive particle requires sharing, and they analogized with the incomplete sentence when it is conjoined to the complete sentence. And this is invalid because sharing is only obligatory in the incomplete sentence due to its need for what completes it; so when it is complete by itself, sharing is not obligatory except in what it needs. And for this reason we said regarding a man's statement to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free' – the emancipation is attached to the condition because it is deficient in the context of suspension. 
Translation: Among these invalid arguments is one that some scholars stated: that conjunction in wording necessitates conjunction in ruling. For example, some of them said regarding Allah's command 'Establish prayer and give zakat' that the conjunction necessitates that zakat is not obligatory on a child. They said because the conjunctive requires sharing, and they analogized with the incomplete sentence when conjoined to a complete sentence. But this analogy is invalid because sharing only becomes obligatory in the incomplete sentence due to its need for the speech that completes it; so when the speech is complete by itself, sharing is not obligatory except in that which it needs. And for this reason we said regarding a man's statement to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free' that the emancipation is attached to the condition because it is deficient in the context of suspension. Explanation: We are now explaining the last invalid argument from the invalid arguments; its proponent is Imam Malik. He says that conjunction in wording necessitates conjunction in ruling, meaning when two statements are joined by a conjunctive letter, this is evidence that these two statements share in ruling. For this reason he says that zakat is not obligatory on the insane because Allah says 'Establish prayer and give zakat' – the establishment of prayer and giving of zakat are two sentences joined by a conjunctive letter, so this conjunctive requires the two sentences to share in ruling; there is equality in ruling. The meaning of sharing and equality in ruling is that if one is obligatory, the other is also obligatory; if one is not obligatory, the other is also not obligatory. Since prayer is not obligatory on the insane, zakat will also not be obligatory. According to us, zakat is also not obligatory on the insane, but not due to this evidence mentioned by Imam Malik; rather our evidence is the hadith in which he said: 'The pen is lifted from three' – the pen is lifted from the sleeping, the child, and the insane. This means they are not legally responsible; since they are not responsible, zakat will not be obligatory. Imam Malik, in using this invalid argument, says that if an incomplete sentence is conjoined to a complete sentence, then both sentences share in the predicate, like 'Zaynab is divorced and Hind' – an incomplete sentence conjoined to a complete one, and both share in the predicate, i.e., divorce occurs on both Zaynab and Hind. Similarly, if a complete sentence is conjoined to a complete sentence, even though they do not share in the predicate because both are complete sentences, they will nevertheless share in ruling, like 'Zaynab is divorced and Hind is divorced'. In any case, Imam Malik analogizes the conjunction of a complete sentence to a complete sentence to the conjunction of an incomplete sentence to a complete sentence. But we call this analogy invalid, because in the case of an incomplete sentence conjoined to a complete one, the sharing in the predicate is not due to their being joined by a conjunctive letter, but because the incomplete sentence needs a predicate; so it is dependent on the complete one, therefore the incomplete is made to share with the complete in the predicate. But a complete sentence is not dependent on another complete sentence, so sharing cannot occur. Yes, if a complete sentence is sometimes dependent on another complete sentence in some matter, then sharing will be established to the extent of the need. For example, if someone says to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free' – here the two sentences are complete, but the second sentence is dependent on the first in the context of suspension, so we will make the second share with the first in suspension, and say that both divorce and emancipation are suspended on the condition, because the context indicates that the speaker intends both divorce and emancipation to be suspended on the condition. Yes, if the husband says: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and Zaynab is divorced' – here both sentences are independent, the second is not dependent on the first even in suspension; so the first sentence remains suspended on the condition, but the second is not suspended; rather it becomes immediate, meaning divorce occurs on Zaynab immediately, because if he had wanted the second sentence also to share with the first in suspension, he would not have brought the predicate after Zaynab, but would have said only: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and Zaynab'. The explanation of the invalid arguments is complete.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage presents a usul dispute between the Hanafi school and some scholars (identified as Imam Malik) regarding the principle that conjunction (qiran) in wording necessitates conjunction in ruling. The Maliki position argues that when two sentences are joined by the conjunctive wa, they must share the same legal ruling. They apply this to the verse 'Establish prayer and give zakat', claiming that since prayer is not obligatory on a child or an insane person (non-mukallaf), zakat also should not be obligatory on them. The Hanafi response, as articulated by the commentator, is twofold. First, they reject the general principle: conjunction in wording does not automatically create sharing in ruling. Sharing only occurs when one clause is dependent on the other, as in the case of an incomplete sentence (jummah nakisa) needing a complete sentence to complete its meaning. When sentences are complete by themselves, no inherent sharing exists. Second, they provide a specific Hanafi proof for the ruling that zakat is not obligatory on the insane: the hadith 'The pen is lifted from three' (sleeping, child, insane), which establishes that these individuals are not mukallaf. The Hanafi analysis distinguishes between dependent and independent clauses. The example of a conditional statement illustrates: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free' – the second clause ('my slave is free') is considered qasir (deficient) in the context of ta'liq (suspension) because the context indicates the speaker intends both results to be conditional. Thus, sharing in the condition is established due to need. In contrast, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and Zaynab is divorced' – the second clause is independent, so Zaynab's divorce is immediate, not conditional. This dispute is a key example of Hanafi usul al-fiqh methodology, emphasizing that grammatical and contextual analysis, not mere conjunction, determines legal sharing.

Key Terms
الْقِرَانَ (al-qiran): Conjunction in wording, i.e., joining two sentences with a conjunctive particle (like wa).
الْجُمْلَةِ النَّاقِصَةِ (al-jumlah al-naqisah): An incomplete sentence that requires another sentence to complete its meaning (e.g., lacking a predicate).
الْجُمْلَةِ الْكَامِلَةِ (al-jumlah al-kamilah): A complete sentence that is grammatically independent and does not need another for completion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi refutation in this passage, why does the second clause in 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free' share in the condition?
A) Because both clauses are complete sentences
B) Because the conjunctive 'and' automatically creates sharing
C) Because the second clause is dependent on the first in the context of suspension (qasir fi al-ta'liq)
D) Because the husband explicitly says so

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, conjunction in wording does not mechanically create legal sharing; sharing arises only when one clause is dependent on the other or when context demands it, and rulings are ultimately based on direct textual proofs.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Refutation of Imam Malik's Qiyas on Sentence Conjunction
Refutation of Imam Malik's qiyas on sentence conjunction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of 'need' to determine whether two conjoined sentences share a ruling and critique the competing qiyas of Imam Malik.

Core Idea
Conjunction does not force sharing; need does.

In this passage, a Hanafi scholar dismantles Imam Malik's argument that two complete sentences joined by 'and' automatically share the same ruling. The debate arises from a question about zakat on the insane: Malik uses conjunction reasoning, while the Hanafis rely on the hadith 'the pen is lifted.' Understanding this dispute requires analyzing the role of need (iḥtiyāj) in conjunction, not the conjunction itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Both schools agree zakat is not obligatory on the insane, but they differ on the proof. Identify the two proofs: Malik's qiyas based on conjunction vs. the Hanafi hadith.
2
Analyze Malik's qiyas
Malik analogizes conjunction of complete sentences to conjunction of incomplete and complete. In the latter, the incomplete shares the predicate (news) with the complete. He claims the same sharing of ruling occurs for two complete sentences.
3
Identify the Hanafi critique
The Hanafi response: sharing in the incomplete case is due to the incomplete's need for a predicate, not due to the conjunction itself. Two complete sentences have no such need, so they do not share rulings automatically.
4
Examine the exception
If one complete sentence depends on another (e.g., a conditional), then need arises and sharing occurs to that extent. Analyze the example: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free' vs. 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and Zaynab is divorced.'
5
Apply the principle
The Hanafi principle: sharing requires a basis of need (iḥtiyāj). Mere conjunction ('aṭf) is insufficient. This is a key usul al-fiqh distinction with practical fiqh consequences.

نہیں ہے تو دوسرا بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور یہاں نماز مجنون پر واجب نہیں ہے تو زکوۃ بھی واجب نہ ہوگی ، کیونکہ دو جملوں کا بذریعہ عطف جمع ہونا حکم میں شرکت کا تقاضا کرتا ہے ہمارے نزدیک بھی مجنون پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہے لیکن اس دلیل سے نہیں جو امام مالک بیان کر رہے ہیں بلکہ ہمارا مستدل وہ حدیث ہے جس میں فرما یا رفع القلم عن ثلاثۃ تین آدمیوں سے قلم اٹھادیا گیا ہے، نائم صبی اور مجنون سے قلم اٹھا دینے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ مکلف نہیں ہیں لہذا جب مکلف نہیں ہیں تو زکوۃ واجب نہ ہوگی ۔ امام مالک عالیہ اس وجہ فاسد میں استدلال کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ اگر جملہ نا قصہ کا عطف جملہ کاملہ پر کیا جائے تو اس وقت دونوں جملے خبر میں شریک ہوتے ہیں جیسی زینب طالق و هند نا قصہ کا عطف کاملہ پر ہے اور دونوں خبر میں شریک ہیں ، یعنی زینب اور ھند دونوں پر طلاق واقع ہوگی تو ایسے ہی اگر جملہ کاملہ کا کاملہ پر عطف کیا جائے تو دونوں اگر چہ خبر میں شریک نہ ہونگے کیونکہ دونوں کامل جملے ہیں، البتہ حکم میں شریک ہو جائیں گے، جیسے زینب طالق و ھند طالق ۔ بہر حال امام مالک جملہ کاملہ کے کاملہ پر عطف کو جملہ کا قصہ کے کاملہ پر عطف کرنے پر قیاس کرتے ہیں۔۔ مگر ہم اس کو استدلال فاسد کہتے ہیں، کیونکہ نا قصہ کے کاملہ پر عطف کی صورت میں جو دونوں خبر میں شریک ہیں وہ اس وجہ سے نہیں کہ دونوں حرف عطف سے جمع ہوئے ہیں، بلکہ اس وجہ سے کہ ناقصہ میں خبر کی ضرورت ہے اس لئے وہ کا ملہ کا محتاج ہے، اس لئے خبر میں نا قصہ کو کاملہ کے ساتھ شریک کر دیا۔ اور کاملہ دوسرے کاملہ کا محتاج نہیں ہے ،لہذا شرکت بھی نہ ہو سکے گی۔ ہاں اگر کا ملہ بھی کبھی کسی چیز میں دوسرے کا ملہ کا محتاج ہو جائے تو احتیاج کی حد تک شرکت ثابت ہو جائے گی جیسے کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق و عبدی حر یہاں دو جملے اگر چہ کامل ہیں مگر دوسرا جملہ تعلیق میں پہلے کا محتاج ہے تو تعلیق میں دوسرے کو پہلے کے ساتھ شریک کر دینگے اور یوں کہیں گے کہ طلاق اور آزادی دونوں شرط پر معلق ہونگے ، کیونکہ دلالت حال کا تقاضا ہے کہ متکلم کا مقصد طلاق اور آزادی دونوں کو شرط پر معلق کرنا ہے ۔ ہاں اگر شوہر یوں کہے ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق وزينب طالق تو یہاں دونوں جملے مستقل ہیں، دوسرا تعلیق میں بھی پہلے کا محتاج نہیں ہے، لہذا پہلا جملہ تو شرط پر معلق رہے گا مگر دوسرا معلق نہ ہوگا بلکہ منجر ہوگا یعنی زینب پر فور اطلاق پڑ جائے گی کیونکہ اگر وہ دوسرے جملے کو بھی تعلیق میں پہلے کے ساتھ شریک کرنا چاہتا تو زینب کے بعد خبر نہ لاتا صرف یوں کہتا ان دخلت الدار فانت طالق وزينب ، وجوهِ فاسدہ کا بیان مکمل ہو گیا۔
If not, then the second would not be obligatory. And here, since prayer is not obligatory upon the insane, zakat would also not be obligatory, because joining two sentences by conjunction requires sharing in the ruling. According to us, zakat is also not obligatory upon the insane, but not by this proof that Imam Malik is presenting. Rather, our proof is the hadith in which it is said: 'The pen is lifted from three' – the pen is lifted from the sleeping, the child, and the insane, meaning they are not legally responsible. Therefore, when they are not responsible, zakat would not be obligatory. Imam Malik, may Allah elevate him, argues with this invalid reasoning, saying: If an incomplete sentence is conjoined with a complete sentence, then both sentences share in the predicate, like 'Zaynab is divorced and Hind' – the incomplete is conjoined with the complete, both share in the predicate, i.e., divorce occurs for both Zaynab and Hind. Similarly, if a complete sentence is conjoined with another complete sentence, although they do not share in the predicate because both are complete sentences, they will still share in the ruling, like 'Zaynab is divorced and Hind is divorced'. In any case, Imam Malik analogizes the conjunction of complete with complete upon the conjunction of incomplete with complete. But we call this reasoning invalid, because the sharing of both in the predicate in the case of incomplete with complete is not due to both being joined by the conjunction, but because the incomplete is in need of a predicate, so it needs the complete. Therefore, the incomplete is made to share in the predicate with the complete. And a complete is not in need of another complete, so sharing cannot occur. Yes, if a complete sometimes becomes in need of another complete in some matter, then sharing will be established to the extent of need. For example, if someone said to his wife: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free.' Here, although both sentences are complete, the second sentence is in need of the first in conditioning. So we will make the second share with the first in conditioning, and say that both divorce and freeing are conditional upon the condition, because the context indicates that the speaker intends to make both conditional. Yes, if the husband says: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and Zaynab is divorced,' then both sentences are independent; the second is not in need of the first even in conditioning. So the first sentence will remain conditional, but the second will not be conditional; rather, it will be immediate, meaning Zaynab will be divorced instantly, because if he wanted to make the second share with the first in conditioning, he would not have brought the predicate after Zaynab; he would have just said: 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and Zaynab.' The explanation of invalid aspects is complete.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi refutation of Imam Malik's reasoning regarding conjunction of sentences. The context is a broader discussion about whether zakat is obligatory upon the insane. Imam Malik argued that since prayer is not obligatory on the insane, by analogy, zakat should also not be obligatory, based on the principle that two sentences joined by 'and' share the same ruling. The Hanafis agree that zakat is not obligatory on the insane but reject Malik's proof. Their proof is the hadith 'the pen is lifted from three' (the sleeping, the child, and the insane), indicating they are not legally responsible. The core of the dispute is about the effect of conjunction (عطف) on two sentences. Malik argues that joining a complete sentence to another complete sentence makes them share the ruling, analogous to joining an incomplete sentence to a complete one, where they share the predicate. The Hanafi response: sharing in the incomplete case is due to the incomplete's need for the complete, not due to the conjunction itself. Two complete sentences are independent and do not share the ruling unless one is dependent on the other in some aspect. For example, if a husband says, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and my slave is free,' the second clause is conditional because it needs the first to be meaningful; thus both depend on the condition. But if he says, 'If you enter the house, you are divorced and Zaynab is divorced,' the second is unconditional because it is complete in itself and not dependent on the first. Thus, the Hanafi position is that mere conjunction does not force sharing of ruling; need is the determining factor.

Key Terms
عطف (‘aṭf): Conjunction; joining two sentences or words with a conjunction (e.g., و).
جملة ناقصة (jumla nāqiṣa): Incomplete sentence that needs a predicate (e.g., مبتدأ without خبر).
جملة كاملة (jumla kāmila): Complete sentence that does not lack essential parts.
محتاج (muḥtāj): In need of something else to complete its meaning or legal effect.
تعلیق (ta‘līq): Conditioning; making a ruling dependent on a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, why do two complete sentences joined by 'and' not automatically share the same ruling?
A) Because they are joined by a conjunction.
B) Because a complete sentence is not in need of another complete sentence.
C) Because the ruling is always explicitly mentioned for each.
D) Because the speaker intends them to be separate.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, conjunction alone does not create a shared ruling; the underlying factor is need (iḥtiyāj), which determines whether two conjoined sentences are legally linked.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Third Type of Time-Bound Obligation: Hajj and the Internal Hanafi Dispute
Defines the third type of time-bound obligation with problematic expansibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the third type of time-bound obligation in Hanafi usul and explain the internal Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of Hajj, including the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Hajj's time is both a container and a standard, making it a problematic time-bound obligation.

In this lesson, we explore the third category of time-bound obligations in Hanafi usul: those bound to a time whose expansibility is problematic (mushkil). The prime example is Hajj, a lifelong obligation that must be performed once. Its time (months of Hajj) is ambiguous—it resembles both a container (zarf) within which the act can be done at any point, and a standard (miyar) that determines the act's occurrence. This ambiguity leads to an internal Hanafi dispute about whether one must perform Hajj in the first available year or may delay.

Guided Path
1
Understand the three types of time-bound obligations
Recall the Hanafi classification: (1) clearly expansive time (e.g., fasting Ramadan), (2) time with unclear expansibility (e.g., salat within its window), and (3) problematic expansibility (the subject of this lesson).
2
Analyze why Hajj's time is 'mushkil'
The text explains that Hajj months (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, ten days of Dhul Hijjah) are partly a container (most days are not spent in rituals) and partly a standard (only one Hajj can be performed in the entire period). This dual nature makes the time problematic.
The Arabic term 'mushkil' here refers to conceptual uncertainty, not just textual ambiguity.
3
State the two Hanafi positions
Imam Muhammad holds that delay is permissible as long as Hajj is performed before death. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that it must be performed in the first year's Hajj months as a precaution against missing it due to unknown lifespan.
Both are within the Hanafi school; this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The dispute affects only whether delaying is sinful, not the validity of Hajj itself. According to Abu Yusuf, delaying without excuse is a sin but the Hajj is valid; according to Muhammad, there is no sin if the obligation is ultimately fulfilled.
This principle is crucial in fatwa: validity and sinfulness are independent.
5
Understand the implication for intention
The text notes that if someone sets out for the Haram without explicit intention, the default assumption is they intend the obligatory Hajj (Hajjat al-Islam), not nafl, because the obligation is outstanding.
This is based on the principle that the default of the obligated is to fulfill the obligation.

Source Text

وَمِنْ حُكْمِه اَنَّ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ يَسَعُهُ التَّاخِيرُ لَكِنْ بِشَرْطِ أَنْ لَا يَفُوتَهُ فِي عُمُرِهِ وَعِنْدَ أَبِيْ يُوْسُفَ اللهِ، يَتَعَيَّنُ عَلَيْهِ الْآدَاءُ فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَجَّ مِنَ الْعَامِ الْأَوَّلِ اِحْتِيَاطًا اِحْتِرَارًا عَنِ الْفَوَاتِ وَظَهَرَ ذَلِكَ فِى حَقَّ الْمَائِم لَا غَيْرَ حَتَّى يَبْقَى النَّقْل مَشْرُوعًا وَجَوَارُهُ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ بِدَلَالَةِ تَعَيُّن مِنَ الْمُؤدِى إِذِ الظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ لَا يَقْصُدُ النَّفْلَ وَعَلَيْهِ حُجَةُ الإِسْلَام ترجمہ : ۔ اور تیسری قسم وہ امر ہے جو موقت ہے ایسے وقت کے ساتھ جس کا توسع مشکل ہے ، اور وہ حج ہے، اس لئے کہ حج عمر کا فریضہ ہے اور اس کا وقت حج کے مہینے ہیں ، اور اس کی حیات ایسی مدت عمر میں کہ اس کا بعض حصہ دوسرے حج کے لئے فاضل ہو مشتبہ ہے، اور اس قسم کا حکم امام محمد اللہ کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ اس میں تاخیر کی گنجائش ہے اس شرط کے ساتھ کہ حج اس سے فوت نہ ہو اس کی عمر میں ، اور امام ابو یوسف اللہ کے نزدیک متعین ہے اس پر ادائیگی پہلے سال کے اشہر حج میں فوت ہونے سے احتراز کرتے ہوئے احتیاطاً ، پس ظاہر ہوگا یہ اختلاف گناہ کے حق میں نہ کہ اس کے علاوہ میں ، یہاں تک کہ نفل مشروع باقی رہے گا اور باقی رہے گا حج کا جواز اطلاق نیت کے وقت ادا کرنے والے کی جانب سے تعین کی دلالت سے، اس لئے کہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ وہ نہیں قصد کرے گا نفل کا ، حالانکہ اس کے ذمہ فرض حج ہے۔ تشریح:- مقید بالوقت کی تیسری قسم یہ ہے کہ وہ وقت جس کے ساتھ مامور بہ کو مقید کیا گیا ہے وہ وقت مشتبہ ہو، یعنی وقت معیار کے بھی مشابہ ہو اور ظرف کے بھی سارے دن حج میں صرف نہیں ہوتے بلکہ کچھ دنوں میں حج ہوتا ہے باقی وقت بچا رہتا ہے، تو اس لحاظ سے حج کا وقت ظرف ہوا لیکن اگر اس اعتبار سے دیکھا جائے کہ حج کے مہینوں میں صرف ایک ہی حج ادا ہو سکتا ہے، ایک سے زائد حج ادا نہیں ہو سکتے ، اس لحاظ سے حج کا وقت معیار کے مشابہ ہوا ،لہذا جب حج کا وقت ظرف کے بھی مشابہ ہے اور معیار کے بھی مشابہ ہے تو حج کا وقت مشتبہ مشکل ہوگا یقینی طور پر نہ طرف کہہ سکتے ہیں اور نہ معیار۔
And the third type is that which is time-bound with a time whose expansibility is problematic, and that is Hajj, for it is the obligation of a lifetime and its time is the months of Hajj, and a person's life is such a period that some part of it may be surplus for another Hajj is doubtful. Its ruling: according to Muhammad, he may delay it but on condition that it not pass him by in his lifetime; according to Abu Yusuf, it is determined upon him to perform in the months of Hajj of the first year as a precaution to avoid missing it. And this difference appears only in the case of sin, not otherwise, so that nafl remains legitimate and its permissibility upon absolute intention is indicated by the determination from the performer, for the apparent is that he does not intend nafl, while the Hajjat al-Islam is obligatory upon him. Translation: The third type is that command which is time-bound with a time whose expansibility is difficult, and that is Hajj, because Hajj is a lifelong obligation and its time is the months of Hajj, and his life is such a period that some portion of it may be surplus for another Hajj is doubtful. The ruling for this type according to Imam Muhammad is that he may delay it on condition that Hajj does not escape him in his lifetime; and according to Imam Abu Yusuf, it is determined upon him to perform in the months of Hajj of the first year, as a precaution to avoid missing it. So this difference appears only regarding sin, not otherwise, such that nafl remains prescribed, and the permissibility of Hajj upon absolute intention is indicated by the determination from the performer, because it is apparent that he does not intend nafl, while Hajjat al-Islam is due upon him. Explanation: The third type of time-bound obligation is that the time with which the commanded action is restricted is uncertain, i.e., it resembles both a standard (miyar) and a container (zarf), like Hajj, because the time of Hajj is partly a standard and partly a container. The problematic nature of Hajj's time is twofold: (1) The time of Hajj is Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the ten days of Dhul Hijjah, yet not all these days are spent on Hajj; rather, Hajj occurs in a few days and the rest of the time remains, so from this perspective the time of Hajj is a container. But if one looks at the fact that in the months of Hajj only one Hajj can be performed, not more than one, then from this perspective the time of Hajj resembles a standard. Therefore, since the time of Hajj resembles both a container and a standard, the time of Hajj is uncertain and problematic: it cannot definitely be called one or the other.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage introduces and explains the third category of time-bound obligations (al-muqayyad bi-waqt) in usul al-fiqh—that which is bound to a time whose expansibility is problematic (mushkil). The author identifies Hajj as the prime example. It is defined as a lifetime obligation (fard al-umr) because it must be performed at least once in a person's life, but its time—the months of Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah—is such that only one Hajj can be performed per year, yet within that period there is extra time that could theoretically be used for another Hajj if it were possible. This creates a problem: is the time a container (zarf) within which the act can be done anytime, or a standard (miyar) that determines the act's occurrence? The text then presents a Hanafi internal ikhtilaf: Imam Muhammad holds that delay is permissible as long as one does not miss Hajj entirely in one's lifetime, while Imam Abu Yusuf holds that it must be performed in the first available year to avoid the risk of missing it. This difference is only in terms of sinfulness (whether one commits a sin by delaying) but does not affect the validity of the Hajj itself; thus, if one delays without a valid reason according to Abu Yusuf, he sins, but his Hajj remains valid. The passage further notes that if someone embarks on a journey to the Haram without explicit intention, it is presumed he intends Hajj (not nafl) because he is obligated to perform Hajj. The explanation (tashrih) clarifies why Hajj's time is considered uncertain: it has aspects of both a container (since most of the months are not spent in Hajj rituals) and a standard (since only one Hajj can be performed in that entire period).

Key Terms
موقت (muwaqqat): An obligation that is bound to a specific time.
مشکل (mushkil): Problematic or uncertain; here it describes a time that is ambiguous between being a standard and a container.
فرض العمر (fard al-umr): A lifelong obligation that must be performed once in a lifetime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the time is clearly a standard and should not be delayed.
B) As a precaution to avoid missing the obligation due to unknown lifespan.
C) Because the time is expansive enough to allow multiple Hajjs in one year.
D) Because delaying would nullify the obligation.

Key Takeaway
The third type of time-bound obligation is exemplified by Hajj, whose time is problematic (mushkil), and the internal Hanafi dispute concerns only sinfulness, not validity.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Third Type of Muwaqqat: Hajj and the Dispute on Immediacy
Defining the third type of muwaqqat with the Hajj example and the internal Hanafi dispute on immediacy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the third type of muwaqqat as defined by Hanafi usul, and explain the internal Hanafi dispute regarding the immediacy of Hajj.

Core Idea
Hajj's time is problematic (mushkil): it is both a container and a measure, leading to disagreement on whether performance is immediate or can be delayed.

We have already learned the first two types of muwaqqat: that with a fixed time (muttafaq) and that with no specific time (musawwa). Now we encounter the third and most subtle type: muwaqqat bi-waqt mushkil. This passage defines it with the example of Hajj and then unpacks an internal Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf. Understanding this category is essential for correctly applying the rulings of obligations that span a lifetime, like Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Recall the three types of muwaqqat
In Hanafi usul, time-bound obligations are divided into three categories: (1) muwaqqat bi-waqt muttafaq (fixed time), (2) muwaqqat bi-waqt ghayr mahdud (no specific time), and (3) muwaqqat bi-waqt mushkil (problematic time). Place this passage in the context of the third category.
Hajj is the paradigmatic example of the third type.
2
Define 'muwaqqat bi-waqt mushkil'
Identify the key features: the time is problematic because it is uncertain whether it is a measure (miyar) of the action or a container (zarf) for it. For Hajj, the months of Hajj are the time frame, but one's lifespan is also a period that may allow for another Hajj. This ambiguity makes it mushkil.
The term mushkil here is a technical usul term for ambiguous texts, applied to time.
3
State the two positions on immediacy
Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) holds that delay (tarakhi) is permissible as long as Hajj is performed before death. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that performance is due immediately (fawr) in the first year out of precaution (ihtiyat) to avoid missing it altogether.
Both are valid Hanafi positions; neither is considered a deviation.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The disagreement affects only the ruling on sin: according to Abu Yusuf, delaying beyond the first year incurs sin; according to Muhammad, sin only occurs if one dies without performing Hajj. The validity of the act (if performed later) and the permissibility of performing nafl Hajj are unaffected.
This thamarah shows that the ikhtilaf is limited to the moral dimension, not the legal validity.
5
Apply the rule: intention determines fard vs nafl
The passage adds that if someone performs Hajj with an absolute intention (without specifying fard or nafl), it counts as fard because the default is that he intends the fard. However, if he explicitly intends nafl, it is valid as nafl, even if fard is still owed, because the time is a container that can accommodate both.
This is a unique Hanafi position based on the ambiguous nature of the time.

وَالتَّوْعَ الثَّالِثُ الْمُوَقَّتُ بِوَقْتٍ مُشْكِلٍ تَوَسُّعُهُ وَهُوَ الْحَجُّ فَإِنَّهُ فَرْضُ الْعُمْرِ وَوَقْتُهُ أَشْهُرُ الْحَجِّ وَحَيَاتُهُ مُدَّةً يَفْضُلُ بَعْضُهَا لِحَجَّةٍ أُخْرَى مُشْكِلٌ وَمِنْ حُكْمِهِ أَنَّ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ يَسَعُهُ التَّأْخِيرُ لَكِنْ بِشَرْطِ أَنْ لَا يَفُوتَهُ فِي عُمُرِهِ وَعِنْدَ أَبِي يُوسُفَ يَتَعَيَّنُ عَلَيْهِ الْأَدَاءُ فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَجِّ مِنَ الْعَامِ الْأَوَّلِ احْتِيَاطًا احْتِرَازًا عَنِ الْفَوَاتِ وَظَهَرَ ذَلِكَ فِي حَقِّ [الْمَأْثَم؟] لَا غَيْرَ حَتَّى يَبْقَى النَّفْلُ مَشْرُوعًا وَجَوَازُهُ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ بِدَلَالَةِ تَعَيُّنٍ مِنَ الْمُؤَدِّي إِذِ الظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ لَا يَقْصُدُ النَّفْلَ وَعَلَيْهِ حُجَّةُ الْإِسْلَام
And the third type is that which is time-bound with a time whose expansion is problematic, and it is Hajj, for it is the obligation of a lifetime, and its time is the months of Hajj, and his lifetime is a period, a part of which remains for another Hajj, problematic. And from its ruling is that according to Muhammad he is allowed to delay it but with the condition that it is not missed in his lifetime, and according to Abu Yusuf, it becomes determined upon him to perform it in the months of Hajj of the first year, out of precaution, to avoid missing it. And this appears only in the matter of [sin?], not otherwise, so that the supererogatory remains prescribed, and its permissibility upon absolute (intention) is by indication of determination from the performer, because the apparent is that he does not intend supererogatory while he has the obligation of Hajj of Islam.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage defines the third category of time-bound obligations (al-muwaqqat) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The time is problematic (mushkil) because it has aspects of both a measure (miyar) and a container (zarf). The example is Hajj: its time is the months of Shawwal, Dhul-Qi'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul-Hijjah, but only a few days are used for actual Hajj, so the remainder can host another Hajj in a future year. However, one's lifespan is uncertain, so it is ambiguous whether the time is strictly a measure (only one chance) or a container (multiple chances). The ruling: Imam Muhammad holds that delay (tarakhi) is permissible as long as Hajj is performed during one's lifetime. Imam Abu Yusuf, out of precaution (ihtiyat), holds that performance is immediately due in the first year to avoid missing it. The disagreement's practical effect (thamar) is limited to sin: according to Abu Yusuf, delaying beyond the first year incurs sin; according to Muhammad, sin only occurs if one dies without performing. It does not affect the validity of supererogatory (nafl) acts. If someone intends nafl Hajj while having an outstanding fard Hajj, the nafl is valid because the time (one's life) has capacity for both, and the slave's intention determines the act. The fard is not fulfilled by a nafl intention.

Key Terms
موقت (muwaqqat): Time-bound obligation; an act required to be performed within a specific time frame.
مشکل (mushkil): Problematic or ambiguous; here it refers to a time that is uncertain whether it is a measure (miyar) or a container (zarf) for the action.
تعیین (ta'yin): Determination or specification; here, the performer's intention determines whether the act is fard or nafl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, is it permissible to delay performing Hajj beyond the first year after it becomes obligatory?
A) Yes, without any conditions.
B) Yes, but only if he performs it before death.
C) No, it must be performed in the first year.
D) Yes, but only if he performs nafl first.

Key Takeaway
The third type of muwaqqat is defined by an ambiguous time; Hajj exemplifies this, leading to an internal Hanafi dispute on whether performance is immediate or can be delayed, with the difference solely affecting sin.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
12 min
The Dispute on the Cause of Qada: Same as Ada or New Text?
Analyzes the ikhtilaf regarding the cause of qada vs. ada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions on the cause of qada in Hanafi usul, explain the Hanafi argument for a single cause, and evaluate the opposing view's proof.

Core Idea
The Hanafis hold that qada is obligated by the same command as ada; the opposing view requires a new text for each make-up.

This lesson examines a foundational usul dispute: does the obligation to make up a missed worship (qada) arise from the same cause as the timely performance (ada), or does it require a fresh textual command? The Hanafi school, represented by the majority of its usul scholars, argues for a single cause based on rational extension (ma'qul) and qiyas, while many Shafi'is and Mu'tazila insist on separate texts. Understanding this ikhtilaf is crucial for correctly deriving rulings on missed vows and other non-textually specified acts.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the Hanafi position (same cause) and the opposing position (new text) as presented in the text. Note which scholars support each side.
The Hanafi position is attributed to 'most verifying Hanafi usul scholars' and the author; the opposing view to 'some Iraqi Hanafis, majority Shafi'is, and majority Mu'tazila'.
2
Examine the Hanafi proof (dalil)
The Hanafi proof is rational: the original obligation remains despite missing the time because the servant can perform a similar act. The virtue of time is lost without compensation, but the essence of the act remains. This reasoning (ma'qul) is found in the textually specified cases (prayer and fasting) and extends by qiyas.
The key texts are 'Establish prayer' (2:43) and 'Fasting is prescribed for you' (2:183).
3
Examine the opposing proof
The opposing school cites explicit texts for qada: for prayer, the hadith 'pray when you remember'; for fasting, the verse 'a number of other days' (2:184). Where no text exists, qada is caused by tafwit (missing the time).
They argue that each act of worship has its own separate cause for qada.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that those texts are not new causes; they merely remind that the previous obligation remains. Qiyas is only a manifestation (mazhar) of the ruling, not a new cause.
The passage clarifies that the dispute is only for acts that have a rational counterpart (ma'qul). For acts without such counterpart, consensus requires a new cause.
5
Apply to a specific case: vowed i'tikaf
The text gives the example of a vowed i'tikaf in Ramadan missed due to excuse. According to the adopted Hanafi view, qada is performed outside Ramadan with supererogatory fasts (sawm maqsud), not in the next Ramadan. This thamarah al-khilaf shows the practical difference.
Imam Zufar allowed qada in the next Ramadan; Imam Abu Yusuf waived qada entirely. The adopted view avoids both extremes.

الفيضُ الحجازي
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
معروف یعنی وقت مراد نہیں ہے، کیونکہ امر ہی وجوب ادا کا سبب ہوتا ہے ، اور وقت وہ نفس وجوب کا سبب ہے، عام محققین اصولیین احناف میں سے بعض اصحاب شافعی ، قاضی امام ابوزید شمس الائمہ اور خود مصنف ، ان سب کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ جس سبب سے ادا واجب ہوتی ہے اسی سے قضا بھی واجب ہوتی ہے، اور احناف میں سے بعض مشائخ عراق ، عام شوافع اور عام معتزلہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ قضا نص جدید سے واجب ہوتی ہے، وہ کہتے ہیں کہ نماز کی ادا کا سبب اقيموا الصلوۃ ہے اور قضا کا سبب وہ حدیث ہے من نام عن صلاة اونسيها فليصلها اذ اذكرها، یہ قضا کا سبب ہے، اور ادائے صوم کا سبب کتب علیکم الصیام ہے، اور قضا كا سبب فمن كان منكم مريضاً او على سفر فعدة من ايام اخر ہے، اور جہاں قضا کے لئے نص وارد نہیں ہوئی ہے، وہاں قضا کا سبب تفویت یا فوات ہے۔
فریق اول کہتا ہے کہ قضا کا وہی سبب ہے جو ادا کا سبب ہے، لہذا اقیمو الصلوۃ ادا اور قضا دونوں کا سبب ہے اور کتب علیکم الصیام ادا اور قضا روزہ دونوں کا سبب ہے، اور اذ انسی احدکم حدیث اور فعدة من ايام اخر یہ قضا کا سبب نہیں بلکہ یہ تو صرف یہ بتلانے کے لئے وارد ہوا ہے کہ سابق واجب تمہارے اوپر باقی ہے ختم نہیں ہوا، یہ بات ذہن میں رہے کہ مذکورہ اختلاف قضا بمثل معقول کے بارے میں ہے ورنہ اگر قضا بمثل غیر معقول ہے تو بالا تفاق قضا کے لئے سبب جدید کا ہونا ضروری ہے۔ لان بقاء اصل الواجب : - فریق اول دلیل یہ ہے کہ نماز اور روزہ جب قضا ہو گیا تو بندے پر اصل واجب باقی ہے کیونکہ بندہ اپنے پاس سے مثل دیگر اصل واجب کو ادا کر سکتا ہے رہ گئی وقت کی فضیلت تو چونکہ بندہ اس پر قادر نہیں کیونکہ وقت کی فضیلت جو نکل گئی اس کا کوئی مثل نہیں نہ اس کا کوئی ضمان ہے، لہذا اصل واجب اس کے مثل کے ذریعہ قدرت کی وجہ سے بندہ پر باقی رہے گا اور وقت کی فضیلت بغیر مثل وضمان کے ساقط ہو جائے گی چونکہ بندہ اس سے عاجز ہے، اور فضیلت وقت سے عاجز ہونے سے اصل واجب ساقط نہ ہوگا بلکہ اصل واجب اس پر باقی رہے گا، اور یہ دونوں باتیں یعنی مثل پر قدرت کی وجہ سے اصل واجب کا باقی رہنا اور فضیلت وقت کو حاصل کرنے سے عاجز ہونے کی وجہ سے فضیلت وقت کا بغیر مثل وضمان کے ساقط ہو جانا۔ منصوص علیہ میں امر معقول ہیں اور منصوص علیہ نماز اور روزے کی قضا ہے جس کے بارے میں نص وارد ہوئی ہے من نسى عن صلوة اور فعدة من ايام اخر اور جب منصوص علیہ میں یہ دونوں باتیں معقول ہیں تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ سابق واجب جو تھا وہی برقرار ہے وقت نکل جانے کی وجہ سے واجب ساقط نہیں ہوا، لہذا قضا کے لئے نص جدید کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ، پھر یہ جو نص ہے نماز روزہ میں اذ انسی احدکم اور فعدة من ايام اخر یہ سابق واجب کی یاد دہانی کے لئے ہیں۔
-
بہر حال جب منصوص علیہ میں یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی کہ قضا اسی سبب سے ہے جس سبب سے ادا ہے اور یہ دونوں باتیں کہ مثل پر قادر ہونے کی وجہ سے اصل واجب کا باقی رہنا اور وقت کی فضیلت کا عاجز ہونے کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو جانا، منصوص علیہ یعنی نماز، روزہ میں امر معقول ہے تو یہ حکم ان چیزوں کی طرف بھی متعدی ہوگا جن میں نص وارد نہیں ہوئی ہے، جیسے نماز روزہ اور اعتکاف کی نذر معین کہ ان میں ادا و لیوفوا نذروھم سے واجب ہوتی ہے اور قضا کے لئے کوئی نص نہیں ہے، لہذا ان کو بھی منصوص علیہ پر قیاس کرینگے ، اور یہاں بھی وہی حکم متعدی ہوگا کہ جو وجوب ادا کا سبب ہے وہی قضا کا سبب ہے، چونکہ دونوں عبادتیں ہیں۔ سوال:- آپ نے نذر معین کے اعتکاف ، نذر کا روزہ اور نماز کو منصوص علیہ یعنی نماز روزہ پر قیاس کیا ، اور قیاس سے نذر معین کی قضا کو ثابت کیا تو قیاس تو خود ایک سبب ہے لہذا قضا کے لئے سبب جدید پایا گیا جواب: - قیاس مظہر حکم ہوتا ہے، مثبت حکم نہیں ہوتا ہے، لہذا نذر معین میں قضا کا سبب تو وہی نص ہے جو ادا کا سبب ہے، البتہ اس کا اظہار قیاس سے ہوا ہے۔
وَفِيْمَا إِذَا نَذَرَأَنْ يَعْتَكِفَ شَهْرَ رَمَضَانَ فَصَامَ وَلَمْ يَعْتَكِفْ إِنَّمَا وَجَبَ الْقَضَاءُ بِصَومٍ مَقْصُوْد لِأَنَّهُ لَمَّا انْفَصَلَ الْاَعْتَكَافُ عَنْ صَوْمِ الْوَقْتِ عَادَ شَرْطَهُ إِلَى الْكَمَالِ الْاَصْلِي لَا لِاَنَّ الْقَضَاءَ وَجَبَ بِسَبَبٍ أَخَرَ
ترجمہ: اور اس صورت میں کہ جب نذر مانی یہ کہ وہ اعتکاف کرے گا رمضان کے مہینہ میں ، پس اس نے روزے رکھے اور اعتکاف نہیں کیا ، تو قضا واجب ہوگی صوم مقصود سے، اس لئے کہ جب اعتکاف جدا ہو گیا وقت کے روزے سے تو اس کی شرط کمال اصلی کی طرف لوٹ آئی ، نہ اس وجہ سے کہ قضا واجب ہوئی دوسرے سبب سے۔ تشریح : - احناف پر ایک اعتراض ہو رہا ہے، کہ اگر کسی نے نذر مانی کہ رمضان میں اعتکاف کرونگا پھر ہوا یہ کہ اس نے روزے تو رکھ لئے مگر کسی عذر سے اعتکاف نہ کر سکا، تو اب یہ اس اعتکاف کی قضا آئندہ رمضان میں نہیں کر سکتا ہے، بلکہ غیر رمضان میں صوم مقصود یعنی نفلی روزے رکھ کر اعتکاف واجب ہوگا۔ تو اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ قضا کا سبب وہ نہیں ہے جو ادا کا سبب ہے کیونکہ اگر وہی سبب ہوتا تو دوسرے رمضان میں اعتکاف کی قضا درست ہوتی جیسے پہلے رمضان میں اعتکاف کی ادا درست ہے، یا پھر امام زفر کا قول اختیار کیجئے کہ رمضان ثانی میں ان کے نزدیک اعتکاف درست ہے، یا امام ابو یوسف کا قول اختیار کریں کہ ان کے نزدیک اعتکاف کی قضا ہی ساقط ہو جاتی ہے، اور آپ کے نزدیک یہ دونوں باتیں نہیں ہیں، بلکہ آپ غیر رمضان میں نفلی روزے سے اعتکاف واجب کرتے ہیں،اس سے تو
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi, commentary in Urdu on Al-Muntakhab al-Husami. 'Known' meaning time is not intended, because the command itself is the cause of the obligation of ada, and time is the cause of the essence of obligation. The madhhab of the majority of verifying Hanafi usul scholars, some Shafi'i companions, Qadi Imam Abu Zayd Shams al-A'immah, and the author himself is that qada is obligated by the same cause by which ada is obligated. And the madhhab of some Hanafi scholars of Iraq, the majority of Shafi'is, and the majority of Mu'tazila is that qada is obligated by a new text. They say: the cause of ada of prayer is 'Establish prayer' (2:43), and the cause of qada is the hadith: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it.' That is the cause of qada. And the cause of ada of fasting is 'Fasting is prescribed for you' (2:183), and the cause of qada is 'But if any of you is ill or on a journey, then a number of other days' (2:184). And where no text has come for qada, there the cause of qada is tafwit (missing the time) or fawat (loss). The first party says that qada has the same cause as ada; therefore 'Establish prayer' is the cause of both ada and qada, and 'Fasting is prescribed for you' is the cause of both ada and qada of fasting. And the hadith 'when one of you forgets' and 'a number of other days' are not the cause of qada; rather they came only to inform that the previous obligation remains upon you and is not removed. Keep in mind that the mentioned disagreement concerns qada of something that is analogous to the original ('aql ma'qul); otherwise, if the qada is of something not analogous to the original (ghayr ma'qul), then by consensus a new cause is necessary for qada. 'Because the original obligation remains': the first party argues that when prayer and fasting are made up (qada), the original obligation remains upon the servant because the servant can perform from his side like the original obligation. As for the virtue of time, since the servant is incapable of it because the virtue of time that has passed has no like and no compensation, therefore the original obligation remains upon the servant due to his ability to perform its like, and the virtue of time falls away without like or compensation because the servant is incapable of it. And the inability to achieve the virtue of time does not cause the original obligation to fall; rather the original obligation remains. And these two matters — the remaining of the original obligation due to ability to perform its like, and the falling away of the virtue of time without like or compensation due to inability to attain it — are rational matters (umur ma'qul) in the textually specified cases (mansus 'alayh). The textually specified cases are the qada of prayer and fasting for which a text has come: the hadith 'whoever forgets a prayer' and 'a number of other days'. When these two matters are rational in the textually specified cases, it means that the previous obligation remains intact, and it was not removed due to the passing of time; therefore a new text is not needed for qada. Then these texts in prayer and fasting — 'when one of you forgets' and 'a number of other days' — are for reminding of the previous obligation. Anyway, when it is established in the textually specified cases that qada is from the same cause as ada, and that these two matters (that the original obligation remains due to ability to perform its like, and that the virtue of time falls away due to inability) are rational in the textually specified cases (prayer and fasting), then this ruling extends to things for which no text has come, such as a specified vow (nadhr mu'ayyan) of prayer, fasting, and i'tikaf: their ada becomes obligatory from 'And fulfill their vows' (22:29), and there is no text for qada; therefore we make qiyas on the textually specified cases, and there too the same ruling extends: that the cause of the obligation of ada is the same cause of qada, because both are acts of worship. Question: You made qiyas of the specified vow of i'tikaf, the fast of vow, and prayer on the textually specified cases (prayer and fasting), and proved the qada of specified vow by qiyas; but qiyas itself is a cause, so a new cause for qada is found. Answer: Qiyas manifests the ruling (mazhar hukm), it does not prove the ruling (muthbit hukm). Therefore in specified vow, the cause of qada is the same text that is the cause of ada; however, its manifestation occurred through qiyas. 'And in the case where he vows to observe i'tikaf in the month of Ramadan, then he fasted but did not observe i'tikaf — qada becomes obligatory with a intended fast (sawm maqsud), because when i'tikaf separated from the fast of the time, its condition returned to the original perfection, not because qada became obligatory by another cause.' Translation: And in the case where he made a vow that he will observe i'tikaf in the month of Ramadan, then he kept the fasts but did not observe i'tikaf, then qada will be obligatory with an intended fast (sawm maqsud), because when i'tikaf separated from the fast of the time, its condition returned to the original perfection, not because qada became obligatory by another cause. Elucidation: An objection is being raised against the Hanafis: if someone vowed to observe i'tikaf in Ramadan, then it happened that he kept the fasts but could not observe i'tikaf due to some excuse, then he cannot make up this i'tikaf in the next Ramadan; rather, outside Ramadan, by keeping intended fasts (i.e., supererogatory fasts), i'tikaf becomes obligatory. From this it is understood that the cause of qada is not that of ada, because if it were the same cause, then making up i'tikaf in the second Ramadan would be valid just as performing i'tikaf in the first Ramadan is valid. Or adopt the saying of Imam Zufar: according to him, i'tikaf in the second Ramadan is valid. Or adopt the saying of Imam Abu Yusuf: according to him, the qada of i'tikaf becomes waived. But according to you, neither of these two positions holds; rather you make i'tikaf obligatory outside Ramadan with supererogatory fasts. From this [it appears that the cause of qada is different].
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of a foundational usul al-fiqh dispute: does the obligation to make up (qada) a missed act of worship arise from the same original cause (sabab) that obligated the performance on time (ada), or does it require a fresh textual command? The commentator explains two positions. The first, upheld by most Hanafi usul scholars (including the author of the matn, al-Husami, and early authorities like Abu Zayd al-Dabusi), states that qada is obligated by the very same cause as ada. For example, the Qur'anic command 'Establish prayer' obligates both timely performance and make-up if missed. The second position, held by some Hanafi Iraqi scholars, the majority of Shafi'is and Mu'tazila, insists that qada requires a separate textual proof: for prayer, the hadith 'whoever sleeps... pray when he remembers'; for fasting, the verse 'a number of other days'. The commentator clarifies that this dispute only applies when the qada is 'ma'qul' (i.e., the act being made up is of a kind that can be performed similarly later, like prayer and fasting). For acts without a rational counterpart (ghayr ma'qul), consensus requires a new cause. The Hanafi argument centers on the idea that the original obligation (asl al-wajib) remains intact despite missing the time; the virtue of time (fadilat al-waqt) is lost without compensation, but the essence of the act can be performed later by a similar act. Since this reasoning is 'ma'qul' (rational) in the textually specified cases (prayer and fasting), it extends by qiyas to other acts like specified vows (nadhr mu'ayyan) of i'tikaf, prayer, and fasting. The commentator then addresses an objection: if qiyas is used to prove qada, doesn't that make qiyas itself a new cause? The response is that qiyas is only a 'mazhar' (manifestation) of the ruling, not a 'muthbit' (establishing source); the actual cause remains the original text. Later, the passage discusses a specific case: a person vows to observe i'tikaf in Ramadan, keeps the fasts but misses i'tikaf. According to the Hanafi position (as understood by the commentator), qada of i'tikaf requires fasting with intention (sawm maqsud), i.e., supererogatory fasts outside Ramadan, not in the next Ramadan. This seems to contradict the claim that qada and ada share the same cause; the objection is that if they shared the cause, qada in the next Ramadan should be valid (as Imam Zufar held) or qada should fall away (as Abu Yusuf held). The Hanafi answer (implied) is that the obligation of i'tikaf in a vow is tied to the specific time only for ada, but qada can be performed in any month with intended fasts, because the condition of i'tikaf (fasting) is detached from the time-linked fast of Ramadan. This does not create a new cause; it merely shows the ruling's application.

Key Terms
قضا (qada): Making up a missed act of worship after its time has passed.
ادا (ada): Performing an act of worship within its designated time.
سبب (sabab): The cause that brings about the legal obligation (wujub).
نذر معين (nadhr mu'ayyan): A vow to perform a specific act of worship at a specific time (e.g., i'tikaf in Ramadan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first party (majority Hanafi usul scholars), what is the cause of qada for a missed prayer?
A) The hadith 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer, let him pray when he remembers.'
B) The Qur'anic verse 'Establish prayer' (2:43).
C) The fact that the time has passed (tafwit).
D) A combination of the original command and the hadith.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi usul establishes that qada is obligated by the same cause as ada, based on the rationality of the persistent obligation; opposing views require new textual causes for each make-up.
