Dispute on Making Up Eid Takbirs in Ruku: Abu Yusuf vs. the Author
Dispute on qada of Eid takbirs when joining in ruku

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on making up missed Eid takbirs when joining in ruku, and identify the usul principle of qada shabih bil-ada used to justify it.

Core Idea
A missed wajib can be made up in a resembling posture, balancing obligations through caution.

When a latecomer joins the Eid prayer in ruku, the Eid takbirs (which are wajib in the Hanafi school) may have been missed. A key dispute arises between Imam Abu Yusuf and later Hanafi scholars: should these takbirs be made up? This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind both positions and introduces the usul concept of 'qada shabih bil-ada' (makeup that resembles the original performance).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the missing element
The latecomer misses the additional Eid takbirs (wajib) that are recited in qiyam. Determine what exactly is missed and its legal status.
In Hanafi fiqh, the extra takbirs of Eid are wajib, not fard.
2
Note the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and the author
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that no qada is required because there is no equivalent for the takbirs in ruku. The author (later Hanafi) holds that qada is wajib in ruku without raising hands.
The author represents the relied-upon position in the madhhab.
3
Follow Abu Yusuf's reasoning (qiyas with qira'ah and qunut)
Abu Yusuf analogizes the takbirs to qira'ah and qunut: these are specific to qiyam and are not compensated when missed. Since the takbirs have no equivalent in ruku, they should also not be made up.
This is a qiyas of the missing element to other missing elements.
4
Understand the author's response (resemblance between ruku and qiyam)
The author argues that ruku resembles qiyam in two ways: the lower body remains upright, and catching the imam in ruku counts as catching the whole rakah (including qiyam and qira'ah). Thus the takbirs are not completely lost; their 'place' partially remains.
This resemblance is the illa (cause) for making up the takbirs.
5
Apply the principle of qada shabih bil-ada
Because the substitute place (ruku) shares a key attribute with the original (qiyam), the performance of the takbirs in ruku is considered a makeup that resembles the original performance. Hence the term 'qada shabih bil-ada'.
Caution (ihtiyat) dictates that both the fard of ruku and the wajib of takbirs be fulfilled, adjusting the sunnah of hand placement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قیمت کا صدقہ واجب کیا۔ ولهذا قال ابويوسف - اور اسی وجہ سے یعنی کوئی چیز فوت ہو جائے اور اس کا کوئی مثل معقول نہ ہو تو اس کی قضا واجب نہیں ہوتی ہے، اسی وجہ سے امام ابو یوسف اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ کسی نے امام کو عید کی نماز میں رکوع میں پایا، اور اس کی زائد تکبیریں جو عید میں واجب ہیں چھوٹ گئیں ، تو وہ امام کے ساتھ رکوع میں شریک ہو جائے اور تکبیرات عید کی قضا نہ کرے، کیونکہ تکبیر بحالت قیام تھیں ، جب چھوٹ گئیں تو اب بندہ اپنے پاس سے اس کا مثل ادا کرنے پر قادر نہیں ہے جیسے قرآت یا دعاء قنوت فوت ہو جائے تو رکوع میں قضا نہیں کی جاتی ہے۔ لیکن ہمارے نزدیک رکوع میں ہاتھ اٹھائے بغیر ان تکبیرات کی قضا کرنا واجب ہے، کیونکہ رکوع فرض ہے اور تکبیرات واجب ہیں، تو جہاں تک ممکن ہو دونوں کی رعایت کی جائے گی یعنی رکوع بھی کیا جائے گا اور تکبیرات بھی کہہ لی جائے گی ،مگر ہاتھ نہ اٹھائے کیونکہ ہاتھوں کا کانوں تک اٹھانا سنت ہے، اور رکوع میں گھٹنوں پر ہاتھ رکھنا بھی سنت ہے، لہذا ایک سنت کے لئے دوسری سنت کو چھوڑ جائے گا مصنف نے یہ قضا مشابہ بالا داء کی نظیر بیان کر رہے ہیں۔ لكنا نقول :- امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ رکوع قیام کے مشابہ ہے، ایک تو اس لئے کہ رکوع میں نصف اسفل قیام کی طرح برقرار رہتا ہے، اور دوسرے اس وجہ سے کہ جو امام کو رکوع میں پالے تو وہ پوری رکعت پالیتا ہے حکماً اس کو قرآت اور قیام بھی مل گیا، اس مشابہت کی وجہ سے تکبیرات کا من کل وجہ فوت ہونا متحقق نہیں ہوگا ، کیونکہ رکوع قیام کے مشابہ ہے تو گویا تکبیرات کا من وجہ محل باقی ہے لہذا احتیاطاً تکبیرات کو رکوع میں ادا کیا جائے گا، تو گو یا تکبیرات اپنے محل یعنی قیام سے ہٹ گئیں، رکوع میں ادا ہو رہی ہیں اس لئے قضا ہے ،لیکن چونکہ رکوع قیام کے مشابہ ہے تو تکبیرات کی ادائیگی مشابہ بالاداء ہے اس طرح یہ قضا مشابہ بالا داء کی نظیر ہوگی ۔
He made the sadaqah of value wajib. And because of this, Abu Yusuf said - and for this reason, that when something is missed and there is no rational equivalent for it, then its qada is not wajib. For this reason, Imam Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) says: Someone found the imam in ruku during Eid prayer, and he missed the additional takbirs that are wajib in Eid. So he should join the imam in ruku and not make up the Eid takbirs, because the takbirs were in the state of qiyam. When they were missed, the person is not able to perform their equivalent from himself, just as if qira'ah or qunut supplication is missed, it is not made up in ruku. But according to us, it is wajib to make up these takbirs in ruku without raising the hands, because ruku is fard and the takbirs are wajib. So as much as possible, both should be observed: ruku should be performed and the takbirs should be recited, but without raising the hands because raising hands to the ears is sunnah, and placing hands on the knees in ruku is also sunnah. So one sunnah is left for the other. The author is presenting this as an example of qada shabih bil-ada. But we say: The response to Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that ruku resembles qiyam, first because the lower half of the body remains upright like in qiyam, and second because one who catches the imam in ruku has caught the entire rakah; ruling-wise, he has obtained qira'ah and qiyam as well. Due to this resemblance, the takbirs are not completely lost in every respect, because ruku resembles qiyam, so it is as if the place of takbirs remains in one respect. Therefore, out of caution, the takbirs are performed in ruku. So although the takbirs have left their original place (qiyam) and are performed in ruku, it is qada. But since ruku resembles qiyam, the performance is like ada (shabih bil-ada). Thus this qada is an example of qada shabih bil-ada.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and the author (likely a later Hanafi scholar) regarding the ruling on making up missed Eid takbirs when one joins the imam in ruku. The passage type is a madhhab internal dispute within the Hanafi school. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that since the takbirs are specific to qiyam and there is no equivalent in ruku, they are not made up, similar to qira'ah and qunut. The author counters that ruku resembles qiyam in significant ways: the lower body remains upright, and catching the imam in ruku counts as catching the whole rakah. Therefore, the takbirs are not completely lost; their place (mahal) partially remains. Out of caution, they should be performed in ruku without raising the hands, balancing the fard of ruku and the wajib of takbirs. This ruling exemplifies the concept of 'qada shabih bil-ada' (reperformance resembling original performance), where the makeup action is performed in a substitute place that shares some characteristics with the original. The passage shows how Hanafi scholars weigh obligations and use the principle of resemblance (mushabahah) to derive rulings.

Key Terms
قضا مشابہ بالاداء (qada shabih bil-ada): A makeup (qada) that resembles the original performance (ada) because the substitute place shares some characteristics.
تکبیرات عید (takbirat al-'id): The additional takbirs in the first two rak'at of Eid prayer, which are wajib according to the Hanafi school.
مشابہت (mushabahah): Resemblance – the attribute that allows a substitute place to be considered similar to the original for legal purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's position in the dispute, why are the missed Eid takbirs made up in ruku despite the general principle that qada is not wajib without an equivalent?
A) Because the author rejects the general principle.
B) Because ruku resembles qiyam, providing a partial equivalent.
C) Because the takbirs are fard and must always be made up.
D) Because Abu Yusuf's analogy with qira'ah and qunut is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of qada shabih bil-ada allows a missed wajib to be made up in a resembling posture, balancing multiple obligations through caution.

Types of Qadā' in Rights of People and the Case of Unspecified Slave Mahr
Commentary on types of substitute and a derivative dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qadā' bi-mithl maʻqūl and qadā' bi-mithl ghayr maʻqūl, and explain the Hanafi position on the validity of an unspecified slave as mahr and the classification of its value payment as qadā' mushābah bi'l-adā'.

Core Idea
Substitute types depend on whether the original item has a measurable like; value payment can be a substitute resembling performance.

In this lesson, we examine two categories of substitute (qadā') in rights of people: measurable equivalent (qadā' bi-mithl maʻqūl) and non-measurable equivalent (qadā' bi-mithl ghayr maʻqūl). We then apply these concepts to a practical dispute: whether an unspecified slave can be fixed as dower. The Hanafi view, which holds it valid, introduces the interesting concept of substitute that resembles performance (qadā' mushābah bi'l-adā'). The discussion reveals how Hanafi usul tolerates ambiguity when it can be resolved by reference to value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of qadā'
Read the matn statement: 'ضمان الغصب قضاء بمثل معقول' and 'ضمان النفس والأطراف بالمال قضاء بمثل غير معقول'. Notice that usurpation guarantee is measurable substitute, while life/limb guarantee is non-measurable.
2
Understand the sub-types of measurable substitute
The commentary explains that when the item is mithli (like wheat), giving the exact same item is complete measurable substitute, while giving its value is deficient measurable substitute (conceptual similarity only).
This distinction is unique to Hanafi thought.
3
Grasp why life/limb compensation is non-measurable
There is no commensurability between a living being or limb and wealth. The substitute is forced to be monetary, but it is not a 'like' in any sense. Hence it is qadā' bi-mithl ghayr maʻqūl.
4
Apply the framework to the unspecified slave mahr dispute
The Hanafi position: an unspecified slave as mahr is valid, and the husband owes an average slave. If he gives its value, it is qadā' but resembles adā' because the value is the means to determine the average. The Shafi'i position: such a mahr is invalid due to uncertainty. Analyse the difference.
The key usul point is that uncertainty (jahāla) that can be removed by reference to value is tolerated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَضَمَانُ الْغَصَبِ قَضَاءً بِمِثْلِ مَعْقُولٍ وَضَمَانُ النَّفْسِ وَالْأَطْرَافِ بِالْمَالِ قَضَاءً بِمِثْلِ غَيْرِ مَعْقُول وَإِذَا تَزَوَّجَ عَلَى عَبْدٍ بِغَيْرِ عَيْنِهِ كَانَ تَسْلِيْمُهُ الْقِيْمَةَ قَضَاءَ هُوَ فِي حُكمُ الْأَدَاءِ حَتَّى تُجْبَرَ عَلَى الْقَبُوْلِ كَمَا لَوْاتَاهَا بِالْمُسَمًّى ترجمہ: اور غصب کا ضمان قضا بمثل معقول ہے اور نفس اور اعضاء کا ضمان مال سے قضا بمثل غیر معقول ہے، اور جب نکاح کیا غیر معین غلام پر تو اس کی قیمت کا سپرد کرنا قضا ہے جو ادا کے حکم میں ہے، یہاں تک کہ عورت کو مجبور کیا جائے گا قبول کرنے پر جیسا کہ شوہر عورت کے پاس مسٹمی لاتا۔ شریح : - اداء اور قضاء جیسے حقوق اللہ میں ہوتے ہیں ایسے ہی حقوق العباد میں بھی پائے جاتے ہیں ، اداء کا بیان پورا ہو گیا اب حقوق العباد میں قضا کی مثالیں پیش کر رہے ہیں۔ کسی نے کوئی چیز غصب کی پھر اس کو ہلاک کر دیا، تو وہ شئی مغصوب اگر ذوات الا مثال میں سے ہے جیسے گیہوں ، جو وغیرہ تو اس پر اس کا مثل واجب ہوگا، اور اگر ذوات القیم میں سے ہے جیسے جانور تو اس پر قیمت واجب ہوگی ، اب غاصب اگر شئی مغصوب کا ضمان مثل سے دے رہا ہے جیسے گیہوں کے بدلہ گیہوں تو یہ قضا بمثل معقول کی مثال ہے، کیونکہ دونوں میں مماثلت ظاہر ہے ،بصورۃ اور معنی اور اگر قیمت سے ضمان دے رہا ہے تو یہ بھی قضاء بمثل معقول کی مثال ہے، اول قضا بمثل معقول کامل ہے، اور ثانی قضا بمثل معقول قاصر ہے، کیونکہ شئی مغصوب اور قیمت میں صرف معنوی مماثلت ہے ،صورۃ مماثلت نہیں ہے، اس لئے قاصر ہے، کسی نے خطا کسی کو قتل کر دیا تو قاتل پر دیت واجب ہوگی، اور اعضاء انسانی میں سے کوئی عضو کاٹ دیا تو اس پر دیت سے کم یعنی آرش واجب ہوگا، اور ازش کہتے ہیں کسی عضو کے بدلہ اس کے برابر واجب ہونے والا مالی بدل، بہر حال نفس یا عضو تلف کرنے پر دیت یا ارش واجب ہونا یہ قضا بمثل غیر معقول ہے، کیونکہ نفس اور عضو، اور مال کے درمیان مماثلت نہیں ہے ،صورۃ تو ظاہر ہے اور معنی اس لئے نہیں کہ نفس مالک ہے اور مال مملوک ہے۔ کسی نے عورت سے نکاح کیا، اور مہر میں ایک غیر معین غلام طے کیا، تو امام شافعی اللہ کے نزدیک تو غیر معین غلام کو مہر طے کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے لیکن ہمارے نزدیک درست ہے اور شوہر پر اوسط درجہ کا غلام واجب ہوگا، پس شوہر اوسط درجہ کا غلام خرید کر دے رہا ہے تو یہ اداء ہے لیکن غلام کے بجائے شوہر اس کی قیمت دے رہا ہے تو یہ قضا ہے کیونکہ مثل واجب کو سپرد کر رہا ہے، لیکن یہ قضا ادا کے حکم میں ہے، یعنی قضا مشابہ بالاداء ہے، قضا تو اس لئے ہے کہ واجب تو غلام ہے اور یہ اس کی قیمت دے رہا ہے یعنی مثل دے رہا ہے، اور ادا کے مشابہ اس لئے ہے کہ غلام مجہول ہے، معلوم نہیں کہ اعلی درجہ کا یا اوسط یا ادنی درجہ کا غلام مراد ہے، ایسی صورت میں اوسط درجہ کا غلام واجب ہوتا ہے اور اس کا اوسط ہونا قیمت ہی سے معلوم ہوسکتا ہے تو اس لحاظ سے قیمت اصل ہوئی ، لہذا قیمت دینا ادا تو نہ ہو گا لیکن ادا کے مشابہ ضرور
And the guarantee of usurpation is substitute with a measurable equivalent, and the guarantee of life and limbs is with wealth, a substitute with a non-measurable equivalent. And when one marries on an unspecified slave, its delivery of the value is a substitute which is in the ruling of performance, so that she is compelled to accept, just as if he brought the specified (slave) to her. Translation: And the guarantee of usurpation is substitute with a measurable equivalent, and the guarantee of life and limbs is with wealth, a substitute with a non-measurable equivalent. And when one marries on an unspecified slave, then giving its price is a substitute which is in the ruling of performance, to the extent that the woman will be compelled to accept, as if the husband brought the specified (slave) to her. Commentary: Performance and substitute occur in rights of Allah as well as in rights of people. The explanation of performance is complete; now we present examples of substitute in rights of people. Someone usurped something and then destroyed it. If the usurped item is of the type that has a measurable equivalent (mithliyyāt), like wheat, barley, etc., then its like is obligatory. If it is of the type that has value (qimiyyāt), like animals, then its value is obligatory. Now, if the usurper gives the like of the usurped item, e.g., wheat for wheat, this is an example of substitute with a measurable equivalent (qadā' bi-mithl maʻqūl) because similarity is apparent in form and meaning. If he gives the value, this is also an example of substitute with a measurable equivalent. The first is complete substitute with measurable equivalent, the second is deficient, because between the usurped item and the value there is only conceptual similarity, not formal similarity. Someone accidentally killed someone, then blood-money (diya) is obligatory on the killer. If he cuts off a human limb, then less than diya, i.e., arsh, is obligatory. Arsh is said to be the financial compensation equal to the limb. In any case, diya or arsh being obligatory for destroying life or limb is substitute with a non-measurable equivalent, because there is no similarity between life/limb and wealth—formally it is clear, and conceptually because life is an owner and wealth is owned. Someone married a woman and fixed an unspecified slave as dower. According to Imam Shafi'i, fixing an unspecified slave as dower is not valid, but according to us (Hanafis) it is valid, and an average slave is obligatory on the husband. So if the husband buys an average slave and gives him, it is performance; but if he gives its value instead of the slave, it is substitute, because he is giving a like (value) of what was obligatory. However, this substitute is in the ruling of performance, i.e., substitute resembling performance. It is substitute because the obligatory was a slave and he gives its value, i.e., a like. And it resembles performance because the slave is unspecified; it is not known whether a high-grade, average, or low-grade slave is intended. In such a case, an average slave is obligatory, and its being average can only be known through value. So from this perspective, value is the original; thus, giving value is not performance but definitely resembles performance.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on types of qadā' (substitute) in rights of people. It begins with the matn stating that guarantee for usurpation is qadā' bi-mithl maʻqūl (substitute with a measurable equivalent), while guarantee for life and limbs is qadā' bi-mithl ghayr maʻqūl (with a non-measurable equivalent). The commentary explains that if the usurped item is of a type that has a standard measure (mithliyyāt), the substitute is its like; if it is a unique item (qimiyyāt), the substitute is its value. The former is called qadā' bi-mithl maʻqūl and can be complete (when delivering the exact same type) or deficient (when delivering value, which is conceptually similar but not formally). For life and limbs, the substitute is financial (diya or arsh), which is qadā' bi-mithl ghayr maʻqūl because there is no commensurability between a person/limb and money. The passage then addresses a specific case: marrying on an unspecified slave as dower. The Hanafi position is that this is valid, and the husband must give an average slave. If he gives the same average slave, it is adā'; if he gives its value, it is qadā' but in the ruling of adā' (qadā' mushābah bi'l-adā') because the value indicates what is average and thus is effectively the original obligation. A disagreement with Imam Shafi'i is noted: Shafi'i does not permit fixing an unspecified slave as dower because it lacks specification. The Hanafi view relies on the ability to determine by value.

Key Terms
قضاء بمثل معقول (qadā' bi-mithl maʻqūl): Substitute by delivering a measurable equivalent, where similarity is apparent in form and meaning (e.g., wheat for wheat).
قضاء بمثل غير معقول (qadā' bi-mithl ghayr maʻqūl): Substitute by delivering a non-measurable equivalent, such as diya for life or arsh for limbs, where no formal or conceptual similarity exists.
ارش (arsh): Financial compensation for injuries to limbs, less than full diya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when a husband gives the value (price) of an unspecified slave fixed as mahr, instead of the slave itself?
A) It is adā' (performance)
B) It is qadā' (substitute) in the ruling of adā'
C) It is invalid, and the marriage is void
D) It is qadā' but not in the ruling of adā'

Key Takeaway
The classification of substitute into measurable and non-measurable determines the legal nature of the payment, and in contracts with unspecified items, value can serve as a substitute that functions like performance.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Qada' in Huquq al-Ibad: Rational vs Non-Rational Equivalent and the Dower Example
Expansion of qada' in huquq al-ibad with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between qada' bi mithl ma'qul and ghayr ma'qul to new cases and explain why qada' can be like ada' when the obligation is unspecified.

Core Idea
Qada' in huquq al-ibad can be with a rational equivalent or non-rational; when the wajib is unspecified, qada' may be treated as ada'.

This passage expands the usul principle that qada' (adjudication) applies to both rights of Allah and rights of people. It provides concrete examples from usurpation, homicide, and marriage dower to illustrate when qada' is considered 'rational' (ma'qul) or 'non-rational' (ghayr ma'qul) and when qada' is treated like ada' (performance). The dower case includes an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, highlighting the practical consequences of the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of qada' in huquq al-ibad
From the passage, distinguish between qada' bi mithl ma'qul (with a rational equivalent: mithli items like wheat, or qimi via value) and ghayr ma'qul (with a non-rational equivalent: life/limb for diyah/arsh). Note the basis: formal vs conceptual similarity.
Ma'qul means there is a comparable substitute; ghayr ma'qul means the substitute is not comparable in nature.
2
Analyze the usurpation examples for rational equivalence
If the usurped item is mithli (e.g., wheat), the wajib is its exact equivalent (mithl). Paying wheat is qada' ma'qul kamil; paying value is qada' ma'qul qasir (deficient) because only conceptual similarity exists. For qimi items (e.g., animals), value is wajib and is also considered ma'qul.
The passage explicitly classifies giving value for mithli as ma'qul qasir.
3
Understand the homicide example as non-rational equivalence
Diyah (blood money) for life or arsh for limbs is wajib, but there is no similarity between the life/limb and wealth. Therefore, this is qada' ghayr ma'qul. The reason: the soul is owner (malik) and wealth is owned (mamluk), so they are incomparable.
Contrast with mithli items where the substance is comparable.
4
Examine the dower case: qada' like ada'
When a man marries with an unspecified slave as dower, the wajib is an average slave. If he gives the slave, it is ada'. If he gives its value, it is qada' (since the wajib is the slave), but this qada' is in the ruling of ada' because the value clarifies the unspecified obligation. Consequently, the wife is compelled to accept the value just as she would be compelled to accept the average slave.
The passage says 'قضاء هو في حكم الأداء' – qada' that is like ada' in its binding effect.
5
Note the ikhtilaf with Shafi'i and its thamarah
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that specifying an unspecified slave as dower is invalid due to gharar. The Hanafi response is that the uncertainty is resolved by requiring an average slave, and paying its value is permissible. The practical difference: in Hanafi, the wife is compelled to accept the value; in Shafi'i, the marriage itself would be invalid.
This illustrates how usul differences (here, regarding clarity of obligation) lead to different fiqh outcomes.

الفيضُ الحجازي ۱۱۷ شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي قَضَاءً بِمِثْلِ غَيْرِ مَعْقُول وَإِذَا تَزَوَّجَ عَلَى عَبْدٍ بِغَيْرِ عَيْنِهِ كَانَ تَسْلِيْمُهُ الْقِيْمَةَ قَضَاءَ هُوَ فِي حُكمُ الْأَدَاءِ حَتَّى تُجْبَرَ عَلَى الْقَبُوْلِ كَمَا لَوَاتَاهَا بِالْمُسَمًّى ترجمہ: اور غصب کا ضمان قضا بمثل معقول ہے اور نفس اور اعضاء کا ضمان مال سے قضا بمثل غیر معقول ہے، اور جب نکاح کیا غیر معین غلام پر تو اس کی قیمت کا سپرد کرنا قضا ہے جو ادا کے حکم میں ہے، یہاں تک کہ عورت کو مجبور کیا جائے گا قبول کرنے پر جیسا کہ شوہر عورت کے پاس مسٹمی لاتا۔ شریح : - اداء اور قضاء جیسے حقوق اللہ میں ہوتے ہیں ایسے ہی حقوق العباد میں بھی پائے جاتے ہیں ، اداء کا بیان پورا ہو گیا اب حقوق العباد میں قضا کی مثالیں پیش کر رہے ہیں۔ کسی نے کوئی چیز غصب کی پھر اس کو ہلاک کر دیا، تو وہ شئی مغصوب اگر ذوات الا مثال میں سے ہے جیسے گیہوں ، جو وغیرہ تو اس پر اس کا مثل واجب ہوگا، اور اگر ذوات القیم میں سے ہے جیسے جانور تو اس پر قیمت واجب ہوگی ، اب غاصب اگر شئی مغصوب کا ضمان مثل سے دے رہا ہے جیسے گیہوں کے بدلہ گیہوں تو یہ قضا بمثل معقول کی مثال ہے، کیونکہ دونوں میں مماثلت ظاہر ہے ،بصورۃ اور معنی اور اگر قیمت سے ضمان دے رہا ہے تو یہ بھی قضاء بمثل معقول کی مثال ہے، اول قضا بمثل معقول کامل ہے، اور ثانی قضا بمثل معقول قاصر ہے، کیونکہ شئی مغصوب اور قیمت میں صرف معنوی مماثلت ہے ،صورۃ مماثلت نہیں ہے، اس لئے قاصر ہے، کسی نے خطا کسی کو قتل کر دیا تو قاتل على دیت واجب ہوگی، اور اعضاء انسانی میں سے کوئی عضو کاٹ دیا تو اس پر دیت سے کم یعنی آرش واجب ہوگا، اور ازش کہتے ہیں کسی عضو کے بدلہ اس کے برابر واجب ہونے والا مالی بدل، بہر حال نفس یا عضو تلف کرنے پر دیت یا ارش واجب ہونا یہ قضا بمثل غیر معقول ہے، کیونکہ نفس اور عضو، اور مال کے درمیان مماثلت نہیں ہے ،صورۃ تو ظاہر ہے اور معنی اس لئے نہیں کہ نفس مالک ہے اور مال مملوک ہے۔ کسی نے عورت سے نکاح کیا، اور مہر میں ایک غیر معین غلام طے کیا، تو امام شافعی اللہ کے نزدیک تو غیر معین غلام کو مہر طے کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے لیکن ہمارے نزدیک درست ہے اور شوہر پر اوسط درجہ کا غلام واجب ہوگا، پس شوہر اوسط درجہ کا غلام خرید کر دے رہا ہے تو یہ اداء ہے لیکن غلام کے بجائے شوہر اس کی قیمت دے رہا ہے تو یہ قضا ہے کیونکہ مثل واجب کو سپرد کر رہا ہے، لیکن یہ قضا ادا کے حکم میں ہے، یعنی قضا مشابہ بالاداء ہے، قضا تو اس لئے ہے کہ واجب تو غلام ہے اور یہ اس کی قیمت دے رہا ہے یعنی مثل دے رہا ہے، اور ادا کے مشابہ اس لئے ہے کہ غلام مجہول ہے، معلوم نہیں کہ اعلی درجہ کا یا اوسط یا ادنی درجہ کا غلام مراد ہے، ایسی صورت میں اوسط درجہ کا غلام واجب ہوتا ہے اور اس کا اوسط ہونا قیمت ہی سے معلوم ہوسکتا ہے تو اس لحاظ سے قیمت اصل ہوئی ، لہذا قیمت دینا ادا تو نہ ہو گا لیکن ادا کے مشابہ ضرور ہوا ، اس لئے اس کو قضا مشابہ بالا داء کہا۔ حتى تجبر : - قیمت چونکہ اداء کے مشابہ ہے اس لئے اگر عورت قیمت قبول کرنے سے انکار کرے گی تو قاضی اس کو مجبور کرے گا ، جیسے شوہر عبد سمی یعنی اوسط درجہ کا غلام سپر د کرے تو عورت کو قبول کرنے پر مجبور کیا جاتا ہے کیونکہ اوسط غلام کا دینا ادا ہے، تو جو اداء کے مشابہ ہے یعنی قیمت اس کا بھی یہی حکم ہے۔ یہ مذکورہ تفصیل اس صورت میں ہے جب کہ عبد غیر معین پر نکاح ہوا ہو، اگر معین غلام پر نکاح کیا ہے، تو قیمت ادا کر نا قضاء محض ہوگا۔
Adjudication like an equivalent is rational, and when one marries with an unspecified slave, his handing over of the price is adjudication which is in the ruling of performance, so that she is compelled to accept, as if he brought to her the specified (dower). Explanation: The guarantee of usurpation is adjudication with a rational equivalent, and the guarantee of life and limbs from wealth is adjudication with a non-rational equivalent. When marriage is contracted with an unspecified slave, handing over its price is adjudication which is in the ruling of performance, so much so that the woman will be compelled to accept, just as the husband brings the specified (dower). Commentary: Performance and adjudication occur both in rights of Allah and rights of people. The discussion of performance is complete; now examples of adjudication in rights of people are presented. If someone usurps an item then destroys it, if it is of the category of things with equivalents (mithliyyat) like wheat, barley etc., then the equivalent is obligatory; if it is of the category of things with value (qimiyyat) like animals, then its value is obligatory. The usurper paying the equivalent is an example of adjudication with a rational equivalent, because similarity in form and meaning is apparent. Paying value is also adjudication with a rational equivalent, but the first is complete and the second is deficient, because there is only conceptual similarity, not formal similarity. If someone kills another by mistake, then diyah is obligatory; if a limb is cut, then arsh (lesser compensation) is obligatory. This compensation for life or limb is adjudication with a non-rational equivalent, because there is no similarity between life/limb and wealth; formally obvious, and conceptually because the soul is owner and wealth is owned. A man married a woman with an unspecified slave as dower. According to Imam Shafi'i, this is invalid, but for us it is valid, and an average slave is obligatory. If the husband buys and gives an average slave, that is performance; but if he gives its price, that is adjudication because he is handing over the equivalent. However, this adjudication is in the ruling of performance, because the slave is unspecified, so the value clarifies the average. Hence giving the price is similar to performance. Because the price is similar to performance, if the woman refuses to accept it, the judge compels her, just as if the husband brings the average slave she is compelled to accept. This detail is when marriage was with an unspecified slave; if it was with a specified slave, giving the price is pure adjudication.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a commentary illustrating the concept of qada' (adjudication) in rights of people (huquq al-ibad) with concrete examples. The author first distinguishes between two types of qada' with rational equivalents (damān bi-mithl ma'qūl) and non-rational equivalents (damān bi-ghayr ma'qūl). In the case of usurpation of mithli items (like wheat), the equivalent is exact; for qimi items (like animals), the value is given, but that is still considered a rational equivalent because of conceptual similarity. For homicide or amputation, the compensation (diyah or arsh) is a rational equivalent but non-congruent (ghayr ma'qūl) because life/limb and wealth are not comparable. Then the commentary discusses a marriage dower case: marrying with an unspecified slave as dower. The Hanafi position holds this valid, unlike Shafi'i. The husband must give an average slave. If he gives the slave itself, it is ada' (performance); if he gives its value, it is qada' (adjudication), but this qada' is like ada' because the value clarifies the unspecified obligation. Consequently, the woman can be compelled to accept the value, just as she would be compelled to accept the average slave. If the slave was specified, paying value would be pure qada', not like ada'.

Key Terms
قَضَاء (qāḍāʼ): Adjudication; performing an obligation in a substitute form when the original obligation cannot be met (e.g., paying value instead of the exact item).
أَدَاء (adāʼ): Performance; fulfilling an obligation with its exact prescribed object.
ضَمَان بِمِثْل (ḍamān bi-mithl): Guarantee with an equivalent; compensation by giving an identical item (for mithli items).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi fiqh, if a man marries with an unspecified slave as dower and then gives its value, what is the ruling on the wife's acceptance?
A) She may refuse, and the marriage is invalid.
B) She is compelled to accept, because the value is treated like ada'.
C) She may refuse, and the husband must give the slave.
D) She is compelled to accept only if the slave is specified beforehand.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qada' in huquq al-ibad can be with a rational or non-rational equivalent, and when the wajib is unspecified, qada' may be treated like ada', compelling the recipient to accept.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Condition of Qudra for Ada' vs Qada' and Obligation at End of Time
Explaining the usul rule that qudra mumkina is a condition for wujub al-ada' but not for wujub al-qada', with the example of the end-of-time case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that qudra mumkina suffices for wujub al-ada' but not for wujub al-qada', and evaluate the disagreement with Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Core Idea
Possible capacity (qudra mumkina) suffices for the initial obligation; actual capacity is not required for the obligation to arise.

In this lesson, we examine a fundamental usul principle: the condition of capacity (qudra) differs between the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada') and the obligation of adjudication (wujub al-qada'). The Hanafi school holds that for ada', possible capacity (qudra mumkina) suffices, while for qada', even that is not required. This leads to a key dispute regarding prayer at the very end of its time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the usul principle
Read the passage and extract the rule: qudra mumkina is a condition for wujub al-ada' but not for wujub al-qada'.
The reason given: capacity is a condition for obligation, and obligation is not repeated in one wajib.
2
Understand the rationale
Note that the condition is that capacity be conceivable (mutawahham al-wujud), not actual (muhaqqaq al-wujud).
Actual capacity would have to precede performance, which is not required.
3
Apply to the end-of-time case
Apply the rule to a child attaining puberty or an infidel accepting Islam at the very end of prayer time. The Hanafi ruling: prayer is obligatory (wajib) and transfers to qada'.
The possibility of time extension (as for Prophet Sulayman) makes capacity conceivable.
4
Analyze the dispute
Compare with Zufar and al-Shafi'i, who require actual capacity and thus say no prayer is obligatory.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the person must make up the prayer.

ثُمَّ الشَّرْعُ فَرَقَ بَيْنَ وُجُوبِ الْآدَاءِ وَوُجُوبِ الْقَضَاءِ فَجَعَلَ الْقُدْرَةَ الْمُمَكَّنَةَ شَرْطًا لِوُجُوبِ الْآدَاءِ دُوْنَ الْقَضَاءِ لِأَنَّ الْقُدْرَةَ شَرْطُ الْوُجُوبِ وَلَا يَتَكَرَّرُ الْوُجُوبُ فِي وَاجِبٍ وَاحِدٍ وَالشَّرْطُ كَوْنُهُ مُتَوَهَّمَ الْوُجُودِ لَا كَوْنُهُ مُتَحَقَّقَ الْوُجُودِ فَإِنَّ ذَلِكَ لَا يَسْبِقُ الْأَدَاءَ وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا إِذَا بَلَغَ الصَّبِيُّ أَوْ أَسْلَمَ الْكَافِرُ فِي آخِرِ الْوَقْتِ تَلْزَمُهُ الصَّلَاةُ خِلَافًا لِزُفَرَ وَالشَّافِعِيِّ لِجَوَازِ أَنْ يَظْهَرَ فِي الْوَقْتِ امْتِدَادٌ بِتَوَقُفِ الشَّمْسِ كَمَا كَانَ لِسُلَيْمَانَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فَصَارَ الْأَصْلُ مَشْرُوعًا وَوَجَبَ النَّقْلُ لِلْعَجْزِ فِيهِ ظَاهِرًا كَمَا فِي الْحَلْفِ عَلَى مَسِّ السَّمَاءِ وَهُوَ نَظِيرُ مَنْ هَجَمَ عَلَيْهِ وَقْتُ الصَّلَاةِ وَهُوَ فِي السَّفَرِ أَنَّ خِطَابَ الْأَصْلِ يَتَوَجَّهُ عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ يَتَحَوَّلُ إِلَى التُّرَابِ لِلْعَجْزِ الْحَالِيِّ. ترجمہ: پھر شریعت نے فرق کیا ہے وجوب ادا اور وجوب قضا کے درمیان، پس شریعت نے قدرت ممکنہ کو وجوب ادا کے لئے شرط قرار دیا ہے نہ کہ قضا کے لئے، اس لئے کہ قدرت وجوب کی شرط ہے اور وجوب مکرر نہیں ہوتا ایک واجب میں، اور شرط اس قدرت کا متوھم الوجود ہونا ہے، نہ کہ اس کا محقق الوجود ہونا، اس لئے کہ یہ (قدرت کا محقق الوجود ہونا) ادا سے مقدم نہ ہوگا، اور اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ جب بچہ بالغ ہو جائے یا کافر مسلمان ہو جائے وقت کے آخر میں تو اس پر نماز لازم ہوگی امام زفر اور امام شافعی کے خلاف، اس بات کے ممکن ہونے کی وجہ سے کہ وقت میں امتداد ظاہر ہو جائے سورج کے ٹھہرنے کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ حضرت سلیمان علیہ السلام کے لئے ہوا، تو اصل (وجوب ادا) مشروع ہوگی، اور بظاہر اصل (وجوب ادا) میں عجز کی وجہ سے نقل (ادا سے قضاء کی طرف) واجب ہوگی جیسا کہ آسمان کو چھونے کی قسم کھانے میں، اور یہ اس شخص کی نظیر ہے جس پر نماز کا وقت آ جائے اور وہ سفر میں ہو، تو اصل (وضو) کا خطاب اس کی طرف متوجہ ہوگا، پھر اصل خطاب عجز حالی کی وجہ سے مٹی کی طرف منتقل ہو گا۔
Then the Lawgiver distinguished between the obligation of performance and the obligation of adjudication, making possible capacity a condition for the obligation of performance but not for adjudication, because capacity is a condition for obligation, and obligation is not repeated in one obligatory act, and the condition is that it be conceivable of existence, not that it be actually existent, for that does not precede performance. For this reason we said: When a child attains puberty or an infidel embraces Islam at the end of the time, prayer becomes obligatory upon him, contrary to Zufar and al-Shafi'i, because it is possible that extension appears in the time by the stopping of the sun as happened for Sulayman (peace be upon him). So the original (obligation) becomes legally established, and transfer (to qada') becomes obligatory due to apparent inability, as in the oath to touch the sky. And this is analogous to one upon whom the time of prayer arrives while he is in travel: the address of the original (ablution) is directed to him, then it shifts to earth (tayammum) due to current inability.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage presents a key usul principle: capacity (qudra) is a condition for the obligation of performance (ada') but not for the obligation of adjudication (qada'). The reason is that capacity is a condition for the initial obligation, and since obligation is not repeated, the condition needed is that capacity be conceivable (mutawahham al-wujud), not actual. For ada', if capacity is not actual at the time of performance, the obligation may transfer to qada'. This is supported by the case of a child who reaches puberty or a disbeliever who accepts Islam at the very end of the prayer time. According to the Hanafi school, the prayer is obligatory upon them even if there is no time left to perform it, because it is possible that the sun could stop and extend the time, as happened for Prophet Sulayman. Thus the original obligation of ada' is addressed to them, but due to apparent inability (time running out), the obligation becomes qada' (making up the prayer later). This contrasts with the positions of Zufar and al-Shafi'i, who say no prayer is obligatory because capacity is absent. The analogy is drawn with the case of swearing to touch the sky (impossible) where the oath is still valid but impossible to fulfill so kaffarah may be needed. Also, the traveler who encounters prayer time: the obligation of wudu is addressed, but due to inability (no water), he shifts to tayammum.

Key Terms
الْقُدْرَةُ الْمُمَكَّنَةُ (al-qudratu al-mumakkana): Possible capacity; the condition that the obligated person is theoretically capable of performing the act, even if actual circumstances prevent it.
وُجُوبُ الْأَدَاءِ (wujūb al-adāʼ): Obligation of performance; the initial demand to perform an act within its prescribed time with actual capacity.
وُجُوبُ الْقَضَاءِ (wujūb al-qadāʼ): Obligation of adjudication; the obligation to perform the act later as a substitute when the original performance was not possible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a disbeliever embraces Islam at the very last moment of Asr time (before sunset), what is the ruling?
A) Asr prayer is not obligatory because there is no time left.
B) Asr prayer is obligatory and must be performed immediately even after sunset.
C) Asr prayer is obligatory in principle, but due to lack of time, it becomes qada' (make-up).
D) The person must pray only Maghrib since Asr time has passed.

Key Takeaway
Possible capacity (qudra mumkina) is sufficient for the initial obligation; actual capacity is not required for wujub al-ada' to arise.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Distinction Between Obligation of Ada and Qada
Usul rule with proof and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between wujub al-ada and wujub al-qada by identifying the role of possible capability (qudra mumakkana) as a condition for ada but not qada, and apply this distinction to cases of late capability.

Core Idea
Ada requires merely possible capability; qada does not require capability at all, because obligation is not repeated for a single duty.

In this passage, the author explains a key usul principle: the Law distinguishes between the obligation to perform (ada) and the obligation to make up (qada). The condition for ada is possible capability (qudra mumakkana), not actual capability. This is proven by the case of a child reaching puberty at the end of prayer time: the prayer becomes obligatory due to the possibility of time extension, even if the person cannot actually perform it immediately. This leads to a transfer (qada). The Hanafi position is contrasted with Zufar and al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its components
Locate the statement that the Law distinguishes between wujub al-ada and wujub al-qada, and note the condition mentioned: possible capability is a condition for ada but not for qada.
The condition is 'qudra mumakkana' (possible capability).
2
Analyze the condition of possible capability
Understand that the condition for ada is not actual capability but the mere possibility of having capability. The passage states that the condition is 'imagined to exist' (mutawahham al-wujud), not 'actually existing'.
3
Examine the proof for the rule
The proof uses the possibility of time extension: the sun could stop as it did for Prophet Solomon (peace be upon him), making it possible that a person could perform the act. Also, an analogy is made to the traveler whose obligation of wudu shifts to tayammum due to incapacity.
The proof is based on possibility, not actual occurrence.
4
Understand the ikhtilaf
Zufar and al-Shafi'i disagree because they consider the miracle too improbable to base a ruling. The Hanafi response is that obligation is based on possibility, not probability.
The practical difference: Hanafi obligates qada; Shafi'i does not.
5
Apply the rule
Given a scenario where a person becomes capable at the end of a prayer time, use the rule to determine that the prayer is wajib (ada) and then qada is required due to actual incapacity.
This illustrates the distinction between the two obligations.

تو اصل (وضو) کا خطاب اس کی طرف متوجہ ہوگا، پھر اصل خطاب عجز حالی کی وجہ سے مٹی کی طرف منتقل ہو گا۔
(The commentary): 'Until she is compelled' - because the price resembles ada, so if the woman refuses to accept the price, the judge will compel her, just as if the husband delivers an average slave, the woman is compelled to accept because giving an average slave is ada. So what resembles ada (i.e., price) has the same ruling. This detail applies when the marriage is on an unspecified slave; if on a specified slave, paying price is pure qada. Then the Law differentiated between obligation of ada and obligation of qada: it made possible capability a condition for obligation of ada but not for qada, because capability is a condition for obligation, and obligation is not repeated for a single wajib, and the condition is that it is imagined to exist, not that it actually exists, because that does not precede ada. Hence we say: if a child reaches puberty or a disbeliever accepts Islam at the end of the time, prayer is obligatory for him, contrary to Zufar and al-Shafi'i, due to the possibility that the time may extend by the stopping of the sun as happened for Solomon (peace be upon him). So the original (obligation) is established, and the transfer becomes obligatory due to apparent incapacity, as in the case of swearing to touch the sky. And this is analogous to one upon whom the time of prayer arrives while he is traveling: the original address (of wudu) is directed to him, then it shifts to earth due to present incapacity. (Translation of the Arabic and Urdu commentary).
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and proof concerning the distinction between the obligation of performance (wujub al-ada) and the obligation of make-up (wujub al-qada). The author explains that possible capability (qudra mumakkana) is a condition for ada but not for qada, because capability is a condition for obligation and cannot be repeated for a single duty. The condition is the mere possibility of capability, not its actual existence beforehand. The proof is the case of a child reaching puberty or a disbeliever converting at the end of a prayer time: the prayer becomes obligatory due to the possibility of time extension (like the sun stopping for Solomon). This shows that ada is obligated despite apparent incapacity, leading to qada. The Hanafi position is contrary to Zufar and al-Shafi'i. The commentary in Urdu expands on the example of the slave and the judge's compulsion.

Key Terms
وجوب الأداء (wujub al-ada'): The obligation to perform an act within its time frame with actual capability.
وجوب القضاء (wujub al-qada'): The obligation to make up an act after its time due to incapacity.
قدرت ممكنہ (qudra mumakkana): Possible capability: the minimal power that allows the act, considered as a condition for obligation of ada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Prayer is not obligatory because the time has ended
B) Prayer is obligatory and must be performed immediately
C) Prayer is obligatory and then make-up is required if not performed
D) Prayer is not obligatory because the child had no prior ability

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes the obligation of ada from qada by making possible capability a condition for ada only, based on the possibility of time extension as shown by the miracle of Prophet Solomon.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Classification of Prohibitions: Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Nahy
Dispute on whether prohibition on physical vs. religious acts implies inherent or acquired evil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qabih li-'aynihi and qabih li-ghayrihi in Hanafi usul, and explain the Hanafi default for prohibitions on physical versus religious acts, including the Shafi'i objection and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Prohibitions differ: inherent evil vs. evil due to an inseparable attribute — the default hinges on whether the act is physical or religious.

The Shariah prohibits numerous acts, but not all prohibitions carry the same weight. A key debate in usul al-fiqh is whether the prohibition inherently makes the act evil (qabih li-'aynihi) or whether the evil is caused by an external attribute that cannot be separated (qabih li-ghayrihi). The Hanafi school makes a distinction based on whether the act is a physical act (hissi) or a religious act (shar'i), while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that all prohibitions default to qabih li-'aynihi. This passage dissects the two categories and presents the proof for each position.

Guided Path
1
Define the two categories of prohibition
Understand qabih li-'aynihi (inherently evil) and qabih li-ghayrihi (evil due to an inseparable external attribute). Note the examples given: physical act of zina (default inherently evil) vs. invalid sale (evil due to missing condition).
The key is that in qabih li-ghayrihi, the external factor is inseparable from the act.
2
Distinguish physical acts (af'al hissiyya) from religious acts (af'al shar'iyya)
Physical acts retain their original meanings after revelation (e.g., murder, zina). Religious acts have their meanings changed by the Shariah (e.g., salat, sawm, bay'). The default ruling of prohibition differs for each category.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the Hanafi default rule
For physical acts, nahy defaults to qabih li-'aynihi (makruh) unless a qarina indicates qabih li-ghayrihi (e.g., intercourse during menstruation due to 'adha). For religious acts, nahy defaults to qabih li-ghayrihi (fasid) unless a qarina indicates qabih li-'aynihi (e.g., sale of non-existent item).
The ruling outcome: first type → makruh; second type → fasid.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues by qiyas (analogy) that just as absolute amr demands the best good, absolute nahy demands the worst evil, so both categories default to qabih li-'aynihi. The Hanafi response rests on the nature of the acts and that the analogy does not hold because of the difference in the acts' relationship to Shariah.
The passage cites the example of zihar to refute the Shafi'i analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ اگر حالت حیض میں زوج ثانی نے وطی کی تو بیوی زوج اول کے لئے حلال ہو جائے گی ، یہ حلالہ کی صورت ہے ، اسی طرح حالت حیض میں وہلی سے واطی کا محصن ہونا ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ لہذا بعد میں اگر اس سے زنا کا صدور ہوگا تو رحم کیا جائے گا ، معلوم ہوا کہ حالت حیض کی ولی شرعا صحیح اور معتبر ہے۔ دوسری قسم قبیح لغیرہ وصفا ، یعنی جس غیر کی وجہ سے منہی عنہ میں قباحت آئی ہے وہ غیر منہی عنہ کا وصف لا زم ہو، اس کبھی جدا نہ ہو سکے، جیسے بیع فاسد، اور یوم النحر کا روزہ ۔ بیع فاسد جیسے غلام کو شراب کے بدلہ بیچا، تو یہ بیع فی نفسہ فتیح نہیں ہے کیونکہ ایجاب وقبول موجود ہے، بائع اور مشتری بیع کے اہل ہیں ، اور مبیع ( غلام ) مال متقوم ہے، مگر اس میں قباحت آئی خمر کو شمن بنانے سے، اور خمر مسلمان کے لئے حرام ہے، تو شمن کے سبب قباحت آئی اور شمن ایسا امر ہے جو بیچ کے لئے وصف لازم ہے، بیع سے ثمن کبھی جدا نہیں ہوتا ، پس بیع فاسد ہوگی ۔ اور یوم النحر کا روزہ فی نفسہ فتح نہیں ہے، اس میں قباحت اللہ کی ضیافت سے اعراض کی وجہ سے آئی کیونکہ عید کا دن اللہ کی طرف سے مہمانی کا دن ہے، تو اعراض ضیافت ایسا امر ہے جو یوم النحر کے روزہ کے لئے وصف لازم ہے۔ منہی عنہ فتیح لغیرہ وصفاً کا حکم یہ ہے کہ قباحت کے اتصال کی وجہ سے منہی عنہ فاسد ہوگا، جب کہ قسم اول میں مکروہ تھا، کیونکہ یہاں وہ غیر جس کی وجہ سے فتح آیا ہے وہ منہی عنہ کا وصف لازم ہے، اس سے کبھی جدا نہیں ہوتا، برخلاف پہلی قسم کہ اس میں وہ وصف جس کی وجہ سے قباحت آئی ہے، کبھی منہی عنہ سے جدا بھی ہو جاتا ہے ،غرض دونوں قسموں میں فرق ہے، اس لئے دونوں کے حکم میں بھی فرق ہے کہ اول میں منہی عنہ مکروہ اور ثانی میں فاسد ہے۔ وَالنَّهَى عَنِ الْأَفْعَالِ الْحِشِيَةِ يَقَعُ عَلَى الْقِسْمِ الْأَوَّلِ وَالنَّهَى عَنِ الْأَفْعَالِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ يَقَعُ عَلَى الْقِسْمِ الْآخِيْرِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ فِي الْبَابَيْنِ إِنَّهُ يَنْصَرِفْ إِلَى الْقِسْمِ الْاَوَّلِ إِلَّا بِدَلِيْلِ لِاَنَّ النَّهْيَ فِي اقْتِضَاءِ الْقُبْحِ حَقِيْقَةٌ كَالْأَمْرِ فِي اقْتِضَاءِ الْحُسْنِ فَيَنْصَرِفُ مُطْلَقُهُ إِلَى الْكَامِلِ مِنْهُ كَالْأَمْرِ وَلَا يَلْزَمُ الظُّهَارَ لِاَنَّ كَلَامَنَافِی حُكْمٍ مَطْلُوبٍ تَعَلَّقَ بِسَبَبٍ مَشْرُوعٍ لَهُ أَيَبْقَى سَبَبًا وَالْحُكْمُ بِهِ مَشْرُوْعًا مَعَ وَقُوعِ النَّهْيِ عَلَيْهِ وَأَمَا مَا هُوَ جَزَاءٌ شُرِعَ زَاجِرًا فَيَعْتَمِدُ حُرْمَةَ سَبَبَهِ كَالْقِصَاصِ۔ ترجمہ : ۔ اور افعال حسیہ سے نہی پہلی قسم پر واقع ہوتی ہے، اور افعال شرعیہ سے نہی دوسری قسم پر واقع ہوتی ہے، اور امام شافعی اللہ نے دونوں بابوں ( قسموں) کے بارے میں فرمایا کہ نہی لوٹتی ہے قسم اول کی طرف مگر کسی دلیل کی وجہ سے، اس لئے کہ نبی فتح کا تقاضا کرنے میں حقیقت ہے مثل امر کے حسن کا تقاضا کرنے میں ، پس مطلق نہی لوٹے گی کامل فتح کی طرف جیسے امر، اور ظہار سے اعتراض لازم نہ آئے گا، اس لئے کہ ہمارا کلام ایسے حکم مطلوب میں ہے جو متعلق ہو ایسے سبب کے ساتھ جو سبب اس حکم کے لئے مشروع ہو کہ کیا وہ سب سبب باقی رہے گا؟ اور اس سبب کی وجہ سے حکم مشروع باقی رہے گا اس پر نہی واقع ہونے کے باوجود ، اور بہر حال وہ حکم جو جزاء ہے مشروع ہوا ہے زاجر بن کر تو وہ اپنے سبب کی حرمت کا تقاضا کرتا ہے جیسے قصاص ۔ تشریح:- کچھ باتیں بطور تمہید کے سمجھیں، افعال حسیہ سے مراد وہ افعال ہیں کہ شریعت سے پہلے ان کے جو معانی تھے وہی بدستور باقی ہوں، شریعت نے ان میں کوئی تغیر نہ کیا ہو جیسے قتل، زنا، شراب پینا، کہ ان کے معانی و ماہیت جو شریعت سے پہلے تھے نزول تحریم کے بعد برقرار ہیں۔ افعال شرعیہ سے مراد وہ افعال ہیں جن کے معافی ورود شریعت کے بعد متغیر ہو گئے ہوں ، جیسے روزہ، نماز، بیج، اجاره وغیرہ کہ درود شرع کے بعد ان کے معانی اصلیہ میں تغیر ہو گیا جیسے نماز دعا کے معنی میں تھا، ورود شرع کے بعد مخصوص ہیئت کے ساتھ عبادت کا نام ہو گیا۔۔ روزہ مطلق امساک کا نام تھا، شریعت نے اس میں اضافہ کر دیا، امساك عن الأكل والشرب والجماع من طلوع الفجر الى الغروب وقس على هذا مصنف اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ افعال حسیہ پر جب نہیں وارد ہوگی تو وہ فتیح لعینہ پر محمول ہوگی الا یہ کہ کوئی قرینہ اس کے خلاف کا قائم ہو، جیسے حالت حیض میں وطی کرنا ، وطی کے فعل حسی ہونے کے باوجود قبیح لغیرہ پر محمول ہے یعنی حرام لغیرہ ہے کیونکہ یہاں قرینہ موجود ہے، ارشاد باری تعالیٰ ”قل هُوَ اذی“ یہ قرینہ ہے کہ ممانعت اذی کی وجہ سے ہے، اور افعال شرعیہ پر نبی وارد ہوگی تو وہ قبیح لغیرہ پر محمول ہوگی الا یہ کہ کوئی قرینہ اس کے خلاف کا قائم ہو جیسے مضامین وملا فتیح کی بیچ ، اس کی تفصیل سابق میں گذری ، باوجود فعل شرعی ہونے کے نتیج لعینہ ہے، اور دلیل یہ ہے کہ مبیع معدوم ہے اور معدوم کی بیع شرعا باطل ہے۔ امام شافعی اے افعال حسیہ اور افعال شرعیہ دونوں پر نبی کو فتیح العینہ پر محمول کرتے ہیں، لہذا ان کے نزدیک زنا، شراب، یوم النحر کا روزہ سب کی حرمت برابر ہے، ہاں اگر کوئی دلیل اس کے خلاف کی قائم ہو جائے تو امام شافعی بھی فتیح لغیرہ پر نہی کو محمول کرتے ہیں ۔ مصنف ع الله امام شافعی اے کی دلیل بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ جس طرح مطلق امر کوحسن لعینہ پر محمول کیا جاتا ہے ایسے ہی مطلق نبی سے بھی اس کا فرد کامل مراد ہوگا یعنی قبیح لعینہ پر محمول کیا جائے گا، کیونکہ امر کی حقیقت لغو یہ جیسے حُسن
For this reason we said that if the second husband has intercourse during menstruation, the wife becomes permissible for the first husband — this is the case of tahlil. Similarly, during menstruation, the husband being muhsan is established. If later he commits zina, he will be stoned. It is known that intercourse during menstruation is legally valid and sound. The second type is qabih li-ghayrihi sifatan, meaning that the external factor due which the prohibited thing becomes evil is an inseparable attribute of the prohibited thing, never separating from it, like an invalid sale (bay' fasid) and fasting on the day of Nahr (Eid al-Adha). An invalid sale, such as selling a slave for wine: this sale is not evil in itself because offer and acceptance are present, the seller and buyer are competent, the sold item (slave) is valuable property, but evil enters due to making wine the price, and wine is forbidden for Muslims. So evil enters due to the price, and the price is an inseparable attribute of the sale; the price never separates from the sale, so the sale becomes invalid. And fasting on the day of Nahr is not inherently evil; evil enters it due to avoiding Allah's hospitality because the day of Eid is a day of hospitality from Allah. So avoiding hospitality is something that is an inseparable attribute of fasting on the day of Nahr. The ruling of a prohibited thing that is evil due to an inseparable external attribute (qabih li-ghayrihi sifatan) is that due to the connection of evil, the prohibited thing becomes corrupt (fasid), whereas in the first type it was disliked (makruh). Because here the external factor that makes it evil is an inseparable attribute of the prohibited thing, never separating from it, unlike the first type where the attribute that causes evil sometimes separates from the prohibited thing. In short, there is a difference between the two types, and therefore there is also a difference in their ruling: in the first type the prohibited thing is makruh, and in the second it is fasid. And the prohibition on physical acts falls on the first type, and the prohibition on religious acts falls on the second type. And al-Shafi'i said in both categories that it (the prohibition) reverts to the first type unless there is a dalil, because the prohibition in demanding evil is a reality, like the command in demanding good. So its absolute form reverts to the complete form like the command. And the objection of zihar does not apply because our speech is in a sought ruling that is connected to a cause that is legislated for it: does that cause remain? And the ruling is legislated despite the prohibition being upon it. As for what is a penalty legislated as a deterrent, it depends on the prohibition of its cause, like qisas. Translation: And the prohibition on physical acts falls on the first type, and the prohibition on religious acts falls on the second type. And Imam al-Shafi'i said about both categories that the prohibition reverts to the first type except due to a dalil, because the prohibition in its demand of evil is a reality like the command in its demand of good. So the absolute prohibition will revert to the complete evil like the command. And the objection of zihar will not necessarily arise because our speech is in a sought ruling that is connected to a cause legislated for it: does that cause remain? And the ruling is legislated despite the prohibition being upon it. As for what is a penalty legislated as a deterrent, it depends on the prohibition of its cause, like qisas. Explanation: Let us understand some things by way of preface. Physical acts (af'al hissiyya) refer to those acts whose meanings before the Shariah remained as they were; the Shariah did not change anything in them, such as murder, zina, drinking wine — their meanings and essence that existed before the Shariah remain after the revelation of prohibition. Religious acts (af'al shar'iyya) refer to those acts whose meanings changed after the advent of the Shariah, such as prayer, fasting, sale, lease, etc. After the advent of the Shariah, their original meanings changed: for example, prayer (salat) originally meant supplication; after the advent of the Shariah, it became the name of worship with a specific form. Fasting (sawm) originally meant absolute abstention; the Shariah added to it: abstention from eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse from dawn to sunset. And so on. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) states that when a prohibition applies to physical acts, it is understood to be inherently evil (qabih li-'aynihi) unless there is a qarina (indication) to the contrary, such as intercourse during menstruation — despite being a physical act, it is deemed evil due to an external factor, i.e., forbidden for another reason, because here a qarina exists: the divine statement "Say: It is harm" — this is a qarina that the prohibition is due to harm. And when a prohibition applies to religious acts, it is understood to be evil due to an external factor (qabih li-ghayrihi) unless there is a qarina to the contrary, like the sale of something non-existent (majhul) — its details have passed earlier — despite being a religious act, it is inherently evil, and the proof is that the sold item is non-existent and selling a non-existent thing is invalid in Shariah. Imam al-Shafi'i interprets the prohibition on both physical acts and religious acts as inherently evil, so in his view, zina, wine, fasting on the day of Nahr — all are equal in prohibition. But if a contrary dalil is established, then Imam al-Shafi'i also interprets the prohibition as evil due to an external factor. The author is presenting Imam al-Shafi'i's proof: just as an absolute command is understood to be inherently good, so also from an absolute prohibition, its complete individual is intended, i.e., it will be understood as inherently evil, because the reality of command is like ...
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the classification of prohibitions (nahy) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh and the point of disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i. The author first completes the explanation of the two types of prohibitions: type one is where the evil is due to an external factor that can be separated (leading to makruh), and type two is where the evil is due to an inseparable attribute (leading to fasid). He then states the rule: prohibition on physical acts (af'al hissiyya) falls on the first type (evil due to a separable external factor, thus makruh) by default, but if there is a qarina (contextual indication) to the contrary, it can be evil due to an inseparable attribute. The example is intercourse during menstruation: it is a physical act, but the Quranic 'adha (harm) indicates the prohibition is due to an inseparable cause (the harm), thus it becomes qabih li-ghayrihi. On the other hand, prohibition on religious acts (af'al shar'iyya) falls on the second type (evil due to an inseparable attribute, thus fasid) by default, unless a qarina indicates it is inherently evil. For example, selling a non-existent item is a religious act but it is inherently invalid because of missing conditions. The author then presents Imam al-Shafi'i's opposing view: he holds that all prohibitions, whether on physical or religious acts, indicate inherent evil (qabih li-'aynihi) by default, unless a specific dalil overrides this. His proof is that the prohibition (nahy) is a real demand for evil just as a command (amr) is a real demand for good; therefore, the absolute form of each indicates the most complete form: amr indicates the most complete good, and nahy indicates the most complete evil. Thus, absolute nahy implies the act is evil in itself. The author mentions that the Hanafi arguments (like the case of zihar) are not affected by this objection. The passage concludes with a clarification that the Hanafi position distinguishes between physical and religious acts due to their nature, and this leads to different rulings: makruh for the first type and fasid for the second.

Key Terms
قبیح لعینه (qabih li-'aynihi): Inherently evil; an act that is prohibited because of its own essence regardless of external factors. Example: zina (adultery) in Hanafi view for physical acts default.
قبیح لغیره (qabih li-ghayrihi): Evil due to an external inseparable attribute; an act that is prohibited because of an attached factor that cannot be separated. Example: fasting on Eid (prohibited because it is a day of hospitality from Allah).
افعال حسیہ (af'al hissiyya): Physical acts whose meanings remain unchanged by Shariah, e.g., murder, zina, drinking wine.
افعال شرعیہ (af'al shar'iyya): Religious acts whose meanings are transformed by Shariah, e.g., prayer, fasting, sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi scholars in the passage, what is the default effect of a prohibition (nahy) on a religious act (like fasting on Eid)?
A) The act becomes makruh (disliked).
B) The act becomes fasid (invalid).
C) The act is considered inherently evil (qabih li-'aynihi).
D) The act is considered evil due to an external factor (qabih li-ghayrihi).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between prohibitions on physical acts (default: qabih li-'aynihi, leading to makruh) and religious acts (default: qabih li-ghayrihi, leading to fasid), unlike the Shafi'i view that all prohibitions default to qabih li-'aynihi.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
8 min
Why Marriage Without Witnesses is Void: Negation vs Prohibition
Responding to an objection about prohibiting marriage without witnesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between nahi (prohibition) and nafy (negation) to determine when a hadith nullifies a contract entirely versus merely making it sinful.

Core Idea
A hadith that negates existence (nafy) makes an act void; a prohibition (nahi) only makes it sinful but valid in essence.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi response to an objection about marriage without witnesses. The objection claims that since the hadith 'La nikaha illa bi shuhud' is a prohibition, the marriage should be valid but sinful according to the principle that prohibitions on shar'i acts render them defective in attribute but valid in essence. The Hanafi author provides two critical answers: first, the hadith is actually a negation and abrogation, not a prohibition; second, the nature of marriage itself makes any prohibition on its essential condition void the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Understand the objector's argument: they rely on the principle that prohibitions on shar'i acts keep the act valid in essence, so marriage without witnesses should be valid but sinful.
The principle is: 'al-nahi 'ala fi'l shar'i yufidu al-fasad al-wasfi la al-asli'
2
Examine the first answer
The author says the hadith is not nahi but nafy (negation) and naskh (abrogation). Explain how this changes the ruling: negation nullifies existence, not merely prohibits an attribute.
Hadith: 'La nikaha illa bi shuhud' - the 'illa' construction indicates negation.
3
Examine the second answer
Even if it were a prohibition, the nature of marriage (milk al-mut'ah) is inseparable from permissibility. Prohibition would contradict its very purpose.
Marriage is legislated out of necessity for procreation; it cannot exist without permissibility.
4
Contrast with sale
In sale, permissibility is subsidiary; sale can be valid but prohibited in some cases (e.g., selling a Zoroastrian slave-girl). This shows why the objection fails for marriage.
The author uses this contrast to highlight the unique nature of marriage.
5
Conclude the Hanafi ruling
Marriage without witnesses is void (batil). The usul principle about prohibitions on shar'i acts does not apply because this is not a prohibition but a negation, and even if it were, marriage's essence prevents it.
Mufta bihi: Hanafi ruling that witnesses are a condition of validity, not just obligation.

وَلَا يَلْزَمُ النِّكَاحَ بِغَيْرِ شُهُودٍ لِأَنَّهُ مَنْفِيٌّ بِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ لَا نِكَاحَ إِلَّا بِشُهُودٍ فَكَانَ نَسْخَاوَلانَ النِّكَاحَ شُرعَ لِمِلْكِ ضَرُورِي لَا يَنْفَصِلُ عَنِ الْحِلِ وَالتَّحْرِيمُ يُضَادُّهُ بِخِلَافِ الْبَيْعِ لِأَنَّهُ شُرِعَ لِمِلْكِ الْعَيْنِ وَالْحِلُ فِيْهِ تَابِعَ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّهُ شُرِعَ فِي مَوْضِعِ الْحُرْمَةِ وَفِيْمَالَا يَحْتَمِلُ الْحِلَّ أَصْلاً كَالْاَمَةِ الْمَجُوسِيَةِ وَالْعَبِيدِ وَالْبَهَائِم - ترجمہ : اور بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح سے اعتراض لازم نہ آئے گا، اس لئے کہ نکاح کی نفی کی گئی ہے آپ مسی یا یہ ہم کے اس ارشاد سے کہ نکاح نہیں ہے بغیر گواہوں کے، تو یہ نسخ ہوگا، اور اس لئے کہ نکاح مشروع کیا گیا ہے ایسی ملکِ ضروری کے لئے جوحلت سے جدا نہیں ہوتی ہے، اور تحریم حلت کی ضد ہے، برخلاف بیع کے اس لئے کہ بیع مشروع کی گئی ہے ملک عین کے لئے اور حلت بیج میں تابع ہے، کیا تو نہیں دیکھتا ہے کہ بیع مشروع ہے حرمت کی جگہ میں اور اس جگہ میں جو حالت کا بالکل احتمال نہیں رکھتی ہے، جیسے مجوسی باندی ، غلام اور چوپائے۔ تشریح:- ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے، جس کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ آپ نے ضابطہ بتایا کہ افعال شرعیہ سے نہبی قبیح لغیرہ پر محمول ہوتی ہے لہذا منہی عنہ اپنی اصل کے اعتبار سے مشروع اور وصف کے اعتبار سے غیر مشروع ہوتا ہے، تو بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح کرنے پر نہی وارد ہوئی ہے، اور نکاح فعل شرعی ہے، لہذا بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح مشروع رہنا چاہیے ، حالانکہ آپ کہتے ہیں کہ بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح مشروع ہی نہیں ہے، تو آپ کے بیان کردہ ضابطہ کے خلاف ہوا ؟ مصنف اس کے دو جواب دے رہے ہیں، پہلا جواب یہ ہے کہ نکاح بغیر شہود کی جو حدیث ہے ”لا نکاح الا بشهور “ یہ نبی نہیں ہے بلکہ نفی اور نسخ ہے، یعنی آپ مالی اینم کا منشاء اس سے نہی وارد کرنا نہیں ہے بلکہ نکاح کے معدوم ہونے کی خبر دینا ہے کہ بغیر گواہوں کے نکاح وجود میں ہی نہیں آتا، لہذا یہ اعتراض نہیں ہوسکتا ہے کیونکہ ہمارا کلام نہی کے بارے میں ہے۔ ولان النکاح : - سے دوسرا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ اگر ہم "لا نکاح الا بشهود کو نبی مان لیں تو اس جگہ نہی کی حقیقت پر عمل کرنا ممکن نہیں ہے، کیونکہ نکاح ضرورة مشروع ہوا ہے کیونکہ نکاح سے ایک آزاد عورت پر غلبہ اور تسلط ہوتا ہے، جو اس کی حریت کے خلاف ہے لیکن چونکہ نسل انسانی کا بقاء نکاح پر موقوف ہے، اس ضرورت سے نکاح مشروع ہوا ہے، اور ضرورۃ جو چیز ثابت ہوتی ہے وہ ضرورت کے بقدر مشروع رہتی ہے، لہذا نکاح سے عورت کا صرف ملک متعہ حلال ہوگا ، ملک متعہ کے علاوہ اجزا اور منافع نکاح کے بعد بھی عورت ہی کی ملک ہوں گے، لہذا عورت کا اگر کسی نے ہاتھ تو ڑ دیا تو اس کا جو ضمان ہو گا وہ عورت کا ہو گا مرد کا نہ ہوگا وغیرہ۔ بہر حال نکاح ضرورۃ ایسی ملک متعہ کے لئے مشروع ہوا ہے جو ملک متعہ حلت سے جدا نہیں ہوتی ، یعنی جب بھی نکاح سے ملک متعہ حاصل ہوگا ، تو اس سے استمتاع بھی حلال ہوگا ، ایسا نہیں ہو سکتا کہ نکاح سے ملک متعہ حاصل ہو اور استمتاع حلال نہ ہو، تو ملک متعہ
And marriage without witnesses is not binding because it is negated by his saying, peace be upon him: 'No marriage except with witnesses.' So it is abrogation. And because marriage was legislated for a necessary ownership that is inseparable from permissibility, and prohibition is its opposite, unlike sale because sale was legislated for ownership of the commodity and permissibility in it is subsidiary. Do you not see that it is legislated in a place of prohibition and in something that does not admit permissibility at all, like a Zoroastrian slave-girl, slaves, and animals. Translation: And an objection will not be necessary regarding marriage without witnesses, because marriage has been negated by the command of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'There is no marriage except with witnesses,' so this is abrogation. And because marriage has been legislated for a necessary ownership that does not separate from permissibility, and prohibition is its opposite, unlike sale because sale has been legislated for ownership of the commodity and permissibility in it is subsidiary. Do you not see that sale is legislated in a place of prohibition and in something that does not admit permissibility at all, such as a Zoroastrian slave-girl, slaves, and cattle. Elaboration: This is an answer to an objection. The objection is that you (author) stated the principle that prohibitions (nawāhi) regarding shar'i acts are interpreted as 'ugly due to an extrinsic attribute' (qabih li-ghayrihi), so the prohibited act remains valid in its essence but invalid in that attribute. Now, marriage without witnesses has been prohibited, and marriage is a shar'i act, so it should remain valid in essence, but you say it is not valid at all. This contradicts your principle. The author gives two answers. First: the hadith 'La nikaha illa bi shuhud' is not a prohibition but a negation and abrogation; it informs that such marriage does not exist at all. So it does not fall under the discussion of prohibitions. Second: even if we consider it a prohibition, applying the reality of prohibition is impossible here because marriage is legislated by necessity (darura). Marriage involves dominance over a free woman, which contradicts her freedom, but human survival depends on it, so it is legislated only to the extent of necessity. Thus, only ownership of intimacy (milk al-mut'ah) is permitted; other rights remain with the woman. So marriage is for a necessary ownership that is inseparable from permissibility; prohibition would contradict its essence.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection to the principle that prohibitions on shar'i acts render them invalid only in the prohibited attribute but keep the essence valid. The objector asks: if marriage without witnesses is prohibited, it should be valid in essence but defective in the attribute, yet the Hanafi position says it is void altogether. The author provides two responses. First, the hadith 'La nikaha illa bi shuhud' is not a prohibition (nahi) but a negation (nafy) and abrogation (naskh); it declares that such a marriage does not exist legally, so it does not fall under the principle. Second, even if it were a prohibition, marriage's essential nature prevents applying a prohibition that would invalidate it entirely. Marriage is legislated out of necessity for human procreation, and it grants only ownership of intimacy (milk al-mut'ah), which is inseparable from permissibility. Prohibition (tahrim) directly contradicts this purpose, unlike sale (bay'), where permissibility is subsidiary and can coexist with prohibition in some cases (e.g., selling prohibited items). Therefore, any prohibition on marriage's essential elements would nullify the contract altogether, making it void.

Key Terms
نفی (nafy): Negation; the hadith negates the existence of the contract without witnesses, not merely prohibits it.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation; the hadith abrogates any validity of marriage without witnesses.
ملک متعہ (milk al-mut'ah): Ownership of intimacy; the only right a husband gains over his wife through marriage, inseparable from permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first reason that marriage without witnesses is void, not merely prohibited?
A) Because it is prohibited by the Quran.
B) Because the hadith is a negation and abrogation, declaring such marriage non-existent.
C) Because marriage is not a shar'i act.
D) Because witnesses are not a condition in any case.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling that marriage without witnesses is void rests on interpreting the hadith as negation/abrogation and recognizing the inseparable nature of permissibility in marriage's essence.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
6 min
Two Signs of Causality: Idafah and Luzum in Hanafi Usul
Explaining idafah and luzum as indicators of sabab, with the case of sadaqat al-fitr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two signs of causality (sabab) in Hanafi usul—idafah and luzum—and apply them to distinguish a cause from a condition using the example of Sadaqat al-Fitr.

Core Idea
A cause is known by real attribution or by inseparable repetition; a condition is only metaphorically attributed.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, identifying the cause of a ruling is fundamental to istinbat. This lesson from Sharh al-Husami explains two key signs: attribution (idafah) and inseparability (luzum). Using the example of Sadaqat al-Fitr, we see how the head (person) is the cause despite the ruling being attributed to the day, because attribution to a condition is only metaphorical.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two signs
The passage states that causality is known through idafah (attribution) and luzum (inseparability). First, a ruling attributed to something indicates that thing is the cause—e.g., 'Salat al-Zuhr' where 'al-Zuhr' is the cause. Second, if repetition of a thing causes repetition of the ruling, that thing is the cause—e.g., annual Zakat repeats with the year.
Luzum is used when attribution is not present or needs confirmation.
2
Distinguish cause from condition
In Sadaqat al-Fitr, the ruling is attributed to both the head (Sadaqat al-Ra's) and the day (Sadaqat al-Fitr). The author explains that the head is the cause because the attribute of maintenance (mūnah) resides in the head, while the day is a condition. The attribution to the condition is metaphorical, not real.
The key is that attribution does not always imply causality; it can be metaphorical for conditions.
3
Understand the role of the effective attribute (wasf)
The cause is not the locus itself (head, wealth, land) but the attribute that triggers the ruling. For Sadaqat al-Fitr, the attribute is maintenance; for Zakat, it is growth (namā). These attributes renew over time, causing the ruling to repeat even if the locus remains the same.
This is the illa that justifies repetition.
4
Apply the second sign: luzum
The passage notes that repetition of the ruling by repetition of the cause's attribute is akin to the ruling being attached to the cause. For 'Ushr and Kharaj, the land is the cause, but the obligation repeats because the attribute (productivity) renews annually.
Luzum shows that the cause is inseparable from the ruling's recurrence.
5
Evaluate the objections
The passage addresses two objections: (1) why attribution to a condition (Fitr) does not make it a cause, and (2) why the head is preferred over the day as the cause. The answer lies in distinguishing real attribution (to the true cause) from metaphorical attribution (to a condition).
This shows the importance of analyzing the underlying attribute, not just the linguistic form.
