ترجمہ : ۔ اور سبب پہنچانا جاتا ہے حکم کی اس کی طرف نسبت کرنے سے، اور حکم کے اس کے ساتھ متعلق ہونے سے ، اس لئے کہ ایک چیز کی دوسری چیز کی طرف اضافت کرنے میں اصل یہ ہے کہ وہ چیز (مضاف الیہ ) اس چیز ( مضاف ) کے لئے سبب ہو، اور شرط کی طرف اضافت کی جاتی ہے مجاز ا، اور اسی طرح جب حکم کسی چیز کے ساتھ لازم ہو کہ اس کی تکرار سے حکم مکرر ہو تو یہ دلیل ہے اس بات کی کہ حکم اس چیز کی طرف مضاف ہے، اور صدقۂ فطر میں ہم نے راس کو سبب بنایا ہے اور فطر کو شرط ، ان دونوں کی طرف اضافت کے پائے جانے کے باوجود، اس لئے کہ وصف مؤنت راس کو ترجیح دیتا ہے اس کے سبب ہونے میں ، اور وجوب کا تکرار فطر کے تکرار سے بمنزلہ زکوۃ کے وجوب کی تکرار کے ہے حول (سال) کی تکرار سے، اس لئے کہ وہ وصف جس کی وجہ سے راس سبب ہے۔۔ اور وہ مؤنت ہے وہ متجدد ہوتا ہے زمانے کے تجدد سے، جیسا کہ وہ نما جس کی وجہ سے مال (نصاب ) سبب ہے زکوۃ کے وجوب کے لئے وہ متجد دہوتا ہے سال کے تجدد سے، تو سبب وصف کے تجد ڈ سے بمنزلہ مُجد د بنفسہ کے ہو جائے گا، اسی اصل پر عشر اور خراج مکرر ہوں گے سبب کے متحد ہونے کے باوجود اور وہ سبب ارض نامی ہے، عشر میں حقیقی پیداوار کے ساتھ اور خراج میں حکما پیداوار کے ساتھ ( جو حاصل ہوتی ہے ) زراعت پر قدرت سے۔ تشریح :- ماقبل میں بتایا کہ احکام کے لئے اللہ تعالی نے اسباب مقرر فرمائے ہیں، یہاں ان اسباب کی علامات ذکر کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ سب کو پہنچاننے کی دو علامتیں ہیں۔ (1) پہلی علامت یہ ہے کہ حکم کسی شئی کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے اور حکم اس شئی سے متعلق ہو تو یہ علامت ہے کہ وہ شئی اس حکم کا سبب ہے جیسے صلوۃ الظہر ، صوم رمضان ، حج بیت اللہ کفارہ قتل، ان میں مضاف الیہ مضاف کا سبب ہے، کیونکہ ایک شی کی دوسری شی کی طرف اضافت میں اصل یہ ہے کہ مضاف الیہ مضاف کا سبب ہو، اس لئے کہ اضافت اختصاص کو بتلاتی ہے کہ مضاف مضاف الیہ کے ساتھ خاص ہے، اور اختصاص میں سبیت اعلی درجہ ہے اس لئے مضاف الیہ مضاف کا سبب ہوگا۔ وانما يضاف الى الشرط: - ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے جس کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ جب اضافت سبیت کی دلیل ہے تو کبھی حکم کی اضافت شرط کی طرف ہوتی ہے جیسے صدقۃ الفطر میں فطر (عید کا دن) شرط ہے تو اضافت کی وجہ سے فطر کو بھی سبب کہنا چاہیے۔ اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ چونکہ شرط کو سبب کے ساتھ مشابہت ہے، اس طریقہ پر کہ جیسے سبب کے پائے جانے پر حکم پایا جاتا ہے، ایسے ہی شرط کے پائے جانے پر بھی حکم پایا جاتا ہے، تو اس مشابہت کی وجہ سے کبھی حکم کی شرط کی طرف مجازاً اضافت کر دی جاتی ہے، اور یہاں اضافت کے سبیت کی علامت ہونے میں حقیقت کا اعتبار ہے، مجاز کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، لہذا شرط کو سبب نہ کہیں گے۔ وكذا اذا لازمه: - سببیت کی دوسری علامت بتلا رہے ہیں کہ جس طرح اضافت سبیت کی علامت ہے ایسے ہی ایک شی کا دوسری شی کے ساتھ ایسا لزوم ہو کہ اس کی تکرار سے اس شی میں بھی تکرار ہو یہ بھی دلیل و علامت ہے کہ یہ شی اس کی طرف مضاف و منسوب ہے، اور اضافت سبیت کی دلیل ہے، لہذا یہ لزوم بھی سبیت کی علامت ہے۔ وفى صدقة الفطر : - یہ عبارت بھی ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے، جس کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ صدقہ کی اضافت راس اور فطر دونوں کی طرف ہوتی ہے، صدقۃ الراس بھی کہا جاتا ہے، اور صدقۃ الفطر بھی، تو آپ نے راس کو سبب قرار دیا، اور فطر کو شرط قراردیا، ایسا کیوں؟ جب کہ اضافت دونوں کی سبیت کی مقتضی ہے۔ اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ آپ کی بات درست ہے، کہ اضافت کا تقاضا تو یہ ہے کہ راس اور فطر دونوں سبب ہوں، حالانکہ سبب تو ایک ہی ہو سکتا ہے تو ہم نے دونوں میں سے راس کو سبب بنانے میں ترجیح دیدی، وجہ ترجیح یہ ہے کہ صدقہ فطر کا وجوب جو ہوا ہے وہ وصف مؤنت کی وجہ سے ہوا ہے، یعنی آدمی جس کا نفقہ اور خرچہ برداشت کرتا ہے، تو حدیث میں کہا کہ اس کا صدقۂ فطر کا خرچہ بھی برداشت کرلو۔ تو صدقہ فطر کا وجوب وصف مؤنت کی وجہ سے ہوا اور مؤنت راس میں ہے نہ کہ فطر میں ، کیونکہ راس یعنی انسان کا نفقہ ہوتا ہے اس لئے راس کو ترجیح دی۔ وتكرر الوجوب بتكرر الفطر - یہ بھی ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے، جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ راس اور فطر میں فطر کو سبب بنانا انسب ہے کیونکہ فطر (عید کا دن) میں تکرار ہے، اور اس کی وجہ سے صدقہ میں بھی تکرار ہے، اور راس میں تکرار نہیں ہے، راس تو وہی ہے حالانکہ صدقہ مکرر ہوتا ہے تو فطر کو سبب بنانا چاہیے۔
And the day of breaking the fast (Fitr) is a condition, along with the presence of attribution to both (head and day), because the attribute of maintenance (mūnah) gives preference to the head in being a cause. And the repetition of obligation by repetition of Fitr is like the repetition of the obligation of Zakat by repetition of the year, because the attribute due to which the head was a cause—which is maintenance—renews with the renewal of time, just as the growth (namā) due to which wealth was a cause for the obligation of Zakat renews with the renewal of the year. Thus the cause, by the renewal of the attribute, becomes like something renewed by itself. On this basis, 'Ushr and Kharaj are repeated despite the unity of the cause, which is the productive land: in 'Ushr, it is actual production; in Kharaj, it is legally due to the ability to farm. Translation: And a cause is recognized by attributing the ruling to it and by the ruling being related to it, because in attributing one thing to another, the original principle is that the thing attributed to (mudaf ilayh) is the cause for the thing attributed (mudaf). And attribution to a condition is done metaphorically. Similarly, when a ruling is inseparable from a thing such that its repetition causes the ruling to repeat, this is evidence that the ruling is attributed to that thing. In Sadaqat al-Fitr, we made the head a cause and Fitr a condition, despite attribution to both, because the attribute of maintenance gives preference to the head in being a cause. And the repetition of obligation by repetition of Fitr is like the repetition of the obligation of Zakat by repetition of the year, because the attribute due to which the head is a cause—maintenance—renews with the renewal of time, just as the growth due to which wealth is a cause for Zakat renews with the renewal of the year. Thus the cause, by renewal of the attribute, becomes like something renewed by itself. On this basis, 'Ushr and Kharaj are repeated despite the unity of the cause, which is the productive land: in 'Ushr, actual production; in Kharaj, legal production by ability to farm. Explanation: Earlier it was explained that Allah has appointed causes for rulings. Here the signs of these causes are mentioned. He says there are two signs to recognize a cause. (1) The first sign: when a ruling is attributed to something and the ruling is related to it, this is a sign that that thing is the cause of that ruling, like Salat al-Zuhr, Sawm Ramadan, Hajj Bayt Allah, Kaffarat al-Qatl. In these, the mudaf ilayh is the cause of the mudaf, because in attributing one thing to another, the original principle is that the mudaf ilayh is the cause of the mudaf, since attribution indicates specification, and in specification, causality is the highest degree, so the mudaf ilayh will be the cause. 'And it is attributed to the condition': This is an answer to an objection, the gist of which is: When attribution is evidence of causality, sometimes the ruling is attributed to a condition, like in Sadaqat al-Fitr, Fitr (the day of 'Eid) is a condition, so due to attribution, Fitr should also be called a cause. He answers that because the condition resembles the cause in that just as when the cause exists, the ruling exists, so too when the condition exists, the ruling exists, so due to this resemblance, sometimes the ruling is attributed metaphorically to the condition. But here, when attribution is a sign of causality, the real attribution is considered, not the metaphorical, so the condition will not be called a cause. 'And similarly when it is inseparable': He is stating the second sign of causality: just as attribution is a sign of causality, similarly, if one thing is inseparable from another such that its repetition causes repetition in that thing, this is also evidence and a sign that this thing is attributed and related to it, and attribution is evidence of causality, so this inseparability is also a sign of causality. 'And in Sadaqat al-Fitr': This phrase is also an answer to an objection, the gist of which is: The attribution of the charity is to both the head and Fitr; it is called both 'Sadaqat al-Ra's' and 'Sadaqat al-Fitr'. So you made the head a cause and Fitr a condition, why? When attribution requires causality of both. He answers: Your statement is correct; the requirement of attribution is that both head and Fitr should be causes, but a cause can only be one, so we gave preference to the head in being a cause. The reason for preference is that the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr came because of the attribute of maintenance, i.e., a person bears the expenses and costs of another. The hadith says: 'Pay Sadaqat al-Fitr for him too.' So the obligation of Sadaqat al-Fitr came due to the attribute of maintenance, and maintenance is in the head, not in Fitr, because the head (the person) is the one whose expenses are borne, so preference was given to the head. 'And the repetition of obligation by repetition of Fitr': This is also an answer to an objection, the gist of which is: Between the head and Fitr, making Fitr the cause is more appropriate because Fitr (the day of 'Eid) has repetition, and due to that, the charity also repeats, while the head has no repetition; the head remains the same, yet the charity is repeated, so Fitr should be made the cause.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Husami discusses the two signs of causality (sababiyyah) in usul al-fiqh. The author first explains that a ruling's cause is identified by proper attribution (idafah haqiqiyyah) and by inseparable concomitance (luzum). In the example of Sadaqat al-Fitr, the head (the person) is the cause because the attribute of maintenance (mūnah) resides in the head, not in the day. Although the ruling is attributed to both, the attribution to the condition (Fitr) is metaphorical due to resemblance. The repetition of obligation by repetition of the day is compared to Zakat, where the cause (wealth) renews through growth over time. Similarly, 'Ushr and Kharaj repeat despite the same land, because the attribute of productivity renews. The commentary then addresses objections: why attribution to a condition does not make it a cause (it is metaphorical), and why the head is preferred over the day (maintenance attribute). The second sign of causality is then stated: if a ruling is inseparable from a thing such that repetition of the thing causes repetition of the ruling, that indicates the thing is the cause. The passage concludes by refuting the objection that the day's repetition makes it more fitting as a cause; the Hanafi position maintains the head is the cause because the obligation arises from the attribute of maintenance, which is in the head, even though the obligation repeats with the day.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): The cause that necessitates a ruling; recognized by proper attribution or inseparable concomitance.
شرط (shart): A condition that resembles a cause in that the ruling exists upon its existence, but it is not the true cause; attribution to it is figurative.
اضافة (idafah): Linguistic attribution of a ruling to something; if real, it indicates causality; if metaphorical, it indicates conditionality.
لزوم (luzum): Inseparability: if a ruling repeats upon repetition of a thing, that thing is a cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary criterion for identifying a cause (sabab) in Hanafi usul, as opposed to a condition (shart)?
A) The ruling is attributed to it in a real sense
B) It is a time-based occurrence
C) It is mentioned in the same phrase as the ruling
D) It involves a monetary obligation

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a cause is identified by real attribution (idafah haqiqiyyah) or by inseparable concomitance (luzum) that shows the ruling repeats with the cause's renewal.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Definition and Ruling of Nafi (Supererogatory Acts) with Hanafi–Shafi'i Dispute on Qada
Defines nafi and presents the Hanafi–Shafi'i dispute on qada after breaking.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of nafi, distinguish its initial and subsequent rulings, and explain why the Hanafi school requires qada for a broken nafi act using qiyas on nazr.

Core Idea
Nafi is voluntary to start but binding to complete; breaking it obligates qada to protect the portion already offered to Allah.

This passage introduces the concept of nafi (supererogatory worship) and its twofold nature: initially optional, but once started, completion becomes necessary. The Hanafi school argues this based on the analogy to a vow (nazr). You will learn the definition, the default ruling, and the critical dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding the obligation to make up a broken nafi act.

Guided Path
1
Define nafi and its default ruling
Identify the meaning of nafi as 'increase' and note that it is supererogatory: reward for doing, no punishment for leaving.
2
Identify the Hanafi ruling on breaking nafi
The Hanafi school holds that if one starts a nafi act and breaks it, qada is wajib. Understand the rationale: the performed portion is entrusted to Allah.
This is the disagreement point.
3
Analyze the qiyas on nazr
The Hanafi proof analogizes starting nafi to making a vow (nazr). Just as a vow becomes binding upon utterance, starting nafi makes completion binding.
The qiyas is jaliy (clear analogy).
4
Contrast the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that since the beginning was optional, continuation remains optional; therefore no qada.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is considered stronger because the act is a trust once started; protection requires completion.
This is the mufta bihi view.

Source Text

الفیضُ الحجازی ۱۵۹ شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامی یا لا بأس به ، اور کسی جگہ کہا گیا ہے ویعِیدُ پس یہ وجوب کا حکم ہے۔ اور نفل نام ہے زیادتی کا پس عبادات کے نوافل ایسے زوائد ہیں جو مشروع ہیں ہمارے فائدہ کے لئے ، نہ کہ ہمارے ذمہ میں ہیں، اور نفل کا حکم یہ ہے کہ آدمی کو اس کے کرنے پر ثواب دیا جائے گا، اور اس کے چھوڑنے پر سزا نہیں دی جائے گی، اور اس کو شروع کر کے چھوڑ دینے سے ضامن ہوگا ہمارے نزدیک ، اس لئے کہ جو حصہ ادا کر دیا گیا وہ اللہ کے لئے ہو گیا درانحالیکہ وہ اللہ کی طرف سپر د کیا جا چکا ہے، اور یہ ( نفل کو شروع کر دینا ) نذر کی طرح ہے جو اللہ کے لئے ہو جاتی ہے نام لینے کے اعتبار سے، نہ کہ فعل کے اعتبار سے، پھر واجب ہوگئی نذر کی حفاظت کے لئے فعل کی ابتدا تو البتہ یہ کہ واجب ہو جائے ابتداء فعل کی حفاظت کے لئے اس کا بقاء یہ بدرجہ اولی ہوگا۔ والنفل اسم للزيادة : - چوتھی قسم نفل ہے نفل کے معنی زیادتی کے ہیں تو نفل عبادتیں ہمارے اوپر زائد ہیں ، جو ہمارے فائدے کے لئے شریعت نے مشروع کی ہیں، وہ ہمارے اوپر لازم نہیں ہیں۔ نفل کا حکم یہ ہے کہ بندہ کو اس کے کرنے پر ثواب ملے گا نہ کرنے پر عقاب نہ ہوگا۔ ويضمن بتركه بالشروع - مصنف سے ایک اختلافی مسئلہ چھیڑ رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے نفل شروع کر کے اس کو توڑ دیا تو اس پر قضاء ہے یا نہیں؟ امام شافعی سے فرماتے ہیں کہ قضا نہیں ہے، کیونکہ ابتداءالفل بندہ پر نہیں تو بقاء بھی لازم نہیں ہے، یعنی ابتداء جیسے بندہ کو اختیار ہے کہ کرے یا نہ کرے تو اسی طرح کرنے کے بعد بقاء میں بھی اختیار ہے چاہے تو باقی رکھے یا توڑے، لہذا توڑ سکتا ہے۔ اور احناف کے نزدیک نفل کو شروع کر کے توڑ دینے سے قضالازم آئے گی، کیونکہ بندہ نے نفل شروع کر کے جو حصہ ادا کر دیا، وہ اللہ کے سپر د ہوگیا، اور جو حصہ اللہ کے سپر د ہوا اس کی حفاظت ضروری ہے، اور اس کی حفاظت کی شکل یہی ہے کہ باقی حصہ بھی پورا کر لے، تا کہ تام ہو جائے ، اگر تام نہ کیا تو اس کی حفاظت نہ ہوئی ، لہذا مؤڈی کو باطل ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے اس کو پورا کرنا لازم ہے، اگر پورا نہ کیا اور توڑ دیا تو قضا سے اس کو تام کرے۔ وهو كالنذر : - مصنف نے کہتے ہیں نفل کو شروع کرنا ایسا ہے جیسے نذر مانا، کسی نے نذرمانی کہ میں اللہ کے لئے دو رکعت نماز پڑھونگا، تو بندے کے کہنے سے یہ نذراللہ کے لئے ہو گئی ، یہ نذر اللہ کے لئے صرف ذکر ا اور تسمیہ ہوئی نہ کہ فعلا ، کیونکہ فعل تو بندے نے ابھی نہیں کیا ہے، صرف نام لیا ہے، زبان سے تذکرہ کیا ہے تو یہ نذر صرف تذکرہ اور نام لینے کے اعتبار سے اللہ کے لئے ہو گئی۔ پھر اس زبانی ذکر اور قولی ذکر کی حفاظت ضروری ہے، اس کی حفاظت کے لئے فعل کی ابتدا ضروری ہے، کہ بندہ دورکعت فعلاً شروع کر دے تا کہ ذکر اور قولاً جو اس نے نذر مانی تھی اس کی حفاظت ہو جائے تو جب نذر ماننے والے کے قولی ذکر کی حفاظت کے لئے فعل کی ابتداء واجب ہے تو ابتداء فعل کی حفاظت کے لئے اس کی بقاء بدرجہ اولی واجب ہوگی، اور نفل شروع کرنے والا ابتداء فعل کر چکا ہے تو اس پر اس کی بقاء بدرجہ اولی واجب ہوگی، لہذا شروع فی النفل نذر کی طرح ہو گیا، بلکہ نذر سے ایک درجہ اوپر ہے۔
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi: 159: Urdu commentary on Al-Muntakhab al-Husami: 'La ba'sa bihi', and in some places it is said 'yu'eed', so this indicates obligation. And nafi is a name for increase; so supererogatory acts of worship are such increases that are legislated for our benefit, not that they are a duty upon us. The ruling of nafi is that a person will be rewarded for performing it, and not punished for leaving it. And if one starts it and then abandons it, he becomes liable (damin) according to us, because that portion which he performed has become for Allah, while it has been entrusted to Allah. And this (starting a nafi) is like a vow (nazr) which becomes for Allah in terms of naming, not in terms of action. Then it becomes obligatory to protect the vow to begin the action, but that the beginning of action becomes obligatory to protect its continuation, this is even more primary. And nafi is a name for increase: - The fourth category is nafi; nafi means increase. So supererogatory acts are additional upon us, which Shari'ah has prescribed for our benefit; they are not obligatory upon us. The ruling of nafi is that the servant will get reward for performing it, and no punishment for not performing it. 'And he becomes liable by breaking it after starting' - The author raises a disputed issue: If someone starts a nafi and then breaks it, is qada (making up) required? He reports that Imam Shafi'i says no qada is required, because the beginning is not obligatory, so continuation is also not necessary; meaning just as the servant has choice in beginning, similarly after starting he has choice in continuation - he may continue or break. Therefore he can break. And according to Hanafis, breaking a nafi after starting will necessitate qada, because the servant started the nafi and performed a portion; that portion has been entrusted to Allah, and it is necessary to protect what has been entrusted to Allah. The way to protect it is to complete the remaining portion so that it becomes complete. If he does not complete it, then protection is not achieved. Therefore, to protect the performed portion from being invalidated, completing it is necessary. If he does not complete and breaks it, then he must complete it through qada. And it is like a vow: - The author says starting a nafi is like making a vow. Someone vows: 'I will pray two rak'ahs for Allah.' By his saying, this vow becomes for Allah - this vow is for Allah only in terms of mention and naming, not in terms of action, because the action has not yet been done; only the name is taken, the tongue has mentioned it. So this vow is for Allah only in terms of mention and naming. Then the protection of this verbal mention is necessary. For its protection, beginning the action is necessary: the servant should actually start two rak'ahs so that the verbal vow he made is protected. Now, when for the protection of the verbal mention of the one who vows, the beginning of action is wajib, then for the protection of the beginning of the action, its continuation is even more primarily wajib. And the one who starts a nafi has already performed the beginning of the action, so for him its continuation is even more primarily wajib. Therefore, starting a nafi is like a vow, rather it is one degree above a vow.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi commentary defining nafi (supererogatory act) and its ruling, with a dispute regarding the obligation to complete it if broken after starting. The author begins by linking the discussion to previous terms: 'la ba'sa' (no harm) indicates permission, while 'yu'eed' indicates obligation. Nafi is defined as an increase—acts legislated for our benefit without being obligatory. The default ruling: reward for doing, no punishment for leaving. However, a Hanafi position is introduced: if one starts a nafi act and then breaks it, he becomes liable (damin), meaning he must make it up (qada). The reasoning: the portion performed has become entrusted to Allah; to protect it, the act must be completed. This is compared to a vow (nazr): when one verbally vows an act, the vow itself is binding, and the act must be initiated to fulfill the vow; by analogy, once a nafi is started, its continuation becomes necessary to protect what has been offered. The author then presents the Shafi'i view: since the act was not obligatory initially, continuation remains optional, so breaking does not require qada. Hanafis refute this by stressing the sanctity of the already performed portion. The commentary ends by strengthening the analogy: starting a nafi is like making a vow, but even stronger because the action itself has begun.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): A supererogatory act of worship legislated by Shari'ah, additional to the obligatory acts, reward for doing, no punishment for leaving, but completion becomes obligatory after starting
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed or broken obligatory act; in this context, required for a broken nafi act according to Hanafis
نذر (nazr): A vow where a person binds himself to perform an act for Allah; it becomes binding upon utterance

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He is excused; no further action needed
B) He must make up (qada) the prayer
C) He must give charity as expiation
D) His original prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated from scratch

Key Takeaway
Starting a nafi act creates a binding obligation to complete it; breaking it necessitates qada.

The Second Type of Rukhsah: Definition and Ruling on Preference
Defines second type of rukhsah with example and Hanafi view on preference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the second type of rukhsah, give its example, and apply the Hanafi rule that azimah is preferable unless harm is certain.

Core Idea
In the second type of rukhsah, azimah is superior because Allah's right outweighs the servant's right.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, rukhsah (concession) is divided into two types. The first type has both the prohibited cause and its prohibition present. The second type, which we study here, has the cause present but the prohibition postponed due to an excuse. The example of the sick and traveler in Ramadan illustrates this. The Hanafi school holds a unique position: it is superior to perform the original obligation (azimah) rather than take the concession, unless there is a risk of harm. This lesson unpacks the definition, the example, the Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute, and the rational proofs.

Guided Path
1
Define the second type of rukhsah
What is the second type of rukhsah and how does it differ from the first? Identify that in this type, the prohibited cause (sabab) exists but its ruling (hukm) is postponed.
The first type has both muharram and hurmah present; the second only has muharram.
2
Identify the example and its implications
How does the example of the traveler and sick person in Ramadan illustrate the postponement of prohibition? Note that if they die before making up the fasts, no fidya is required.
The obligation is postponed to 'other days'.
3
State the Hanafi position on preference
According to the Hanafi school, which action is superior: taking the rukhsah or performing the azimah? State the ruling clearly.
Performing azimah (fasting) is superior.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that rukhsah is superior based on hadiths. How does the Hanafi school rebut this? Understand the restriction to jihad context and the rational proofs.
The hadiths are specific to jihad, not general travel.
5
Determine the exception to the rule
When does taking the concession become obligatory? Identify the condition of risk of death or harm.
If fasting endangers life, rukhsah becomes necessary.

حقیقت رخصت کی اس دوسری قسم کا حکم یہ ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک عزیمت پر عمل کرنا اولی ہے، الہذا مریض و مسافر کے لئے باوجو د رخصت کے روزہ رکھنا اولی ہے، امام شافعی کے نزدیک رخصت اولی ہے، امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور سنی یا تم نے رمضان میں روزہ رکھنے والوں کے بارے میں فرمایا اولئک العصاة اولئک العصاة اور ایک حدیث میں فرمایا لیس من البر الصيام في السفر ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ دونوں حدیثیں جہاد پر محمول ہیں، جہاد میں افطار روزہ سے اولی ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ عزیمت اولی ہے، پہلی بات تو یہ ہے کہ کامل سبب یعنی شہود شہر موجود ہے، اگر چہ شریعت نے حکم کو مؤخر کیا ہے مگر یہ جلدی ادائیگی سے مانع نہیں ہے، جیسے ایک مہینہ کے ادھار پر کوئی چیز خریدی، تو اگر چہ مشن ایک مہینہ کے بعد لازم ہوگا لیکن اگر کوئی جلدی دینا چاہے تو دے سکتا ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رخصت میں تردد ہے، اس لیے کہ رخصت ہوتی ہے آسانی کے لئے اور یہاں افطار میں آسانی متعین نہیں ہے، کیونکہ جیسے روزہ نہ رکھ کر آسانی ہو سکتی ہے، ایسے ہی روزہ رکھنے میں بھی آسانی ہے، اس لیے کہ ابھی تمام مسلمانوں کے ساتھ روزہ رکھنا آسان ہے، بعد میں اکیلے کو روزہ رکھنا بھاری معلوم ہوگا ، غرض عزیمت میں بھی رخصت والے معنی یعنی میسر وسہولت ہو سکتی ہے، لہذا جب یسر رخصت میں بھی ہے اور عزیمت میں بھی تو عزیمت پر عمل اولی ہے، چونکہ اس سے حق اللہ کی ادائیگی ہوگی اور رخصت میں بندہ کا اپنا حق ہے اور بندہ کے اپنے حق کے مقابلہ میں حق اللہ کی ادائیگی اولی ہے ، جب کہ اس میں رخصت کے معنی بھی پائے جاتے ہیں، مگر ہاں اتنا تکلف نہ کرے کہ جان کا خطرہ ہو جائے ، اگر جان تلف ہونے کا خطرہ ہو تو بندہ کے لئے رخصت پر عمل ضروری ہے، کیونکہ وجوب تو بندہ سے بہر حال ساقط ہے، لہذا روزہ نہ رکھے، اگر روزہ سے جان چلی گئی تو گنہ گار ہوگا، برخلاف پہلی قسم کے کہ اس میں وجوب ساقط نہیں تھا، رخصت کے باوجود حرمت تھی ، لہذا اس میں اگر بندہ نے عزیمت پر عمل کیا اور مر گیا تو شہید کا درجہ حاصل کرے گا۔
As for the second type: The true concession is that which is declared permissible despite the persistence of the cause, and its ruling (of prohibition) is postponed. That is, the cause of prohibition exists but due to the excuse its ruling is postponed, and for now the act is declared permissible for the servant. This is the second type of concession. In the first type, both the prohibited thing and its prohibition exist; in the second type, the prohibited thing exists but its prohibition is postponed. Therefore, this second type is lesser than the first in being a true concession. Its example is the concession for the sick and traveler to break the fast in Ramadan, while the prohibited time (the month of Ramadan) exists, but its ruling (prohibition) is postponed to other days. Thus, if they fast, it is valid. If they die before making up the missed days, no bequest of fidya is necessary because the obligation was postponed. Its ruling according to us is that performing the azimah (fasting) is superior. Imam Shafi'i holds that taking the concession is superior. His proof: the Prophet said about those who fast in Ramadan while traveling: 'Those are the disobedient, those are the disobedient' and in another hadith: 'It is not righteousness to fast while traveling.' Our response: Both hadiths refer to jihad; in jihad, breaking the fast is superior. Our proof: Firstly, the complete cause (seeing the month) exists; postponement does not prevent immediate performance, like a one-month credit purchase where one can pay early. Secondly, concession involves hesitation; ease is not certain in breaking the fast because fasting also has ease (doing it with others is easier). When ease exists in both, performing azimah is superior because it fulfills Allah's right, while concession serves the servant's own right, and Allah's right takes precedence. However, if there is a risk of death, taking the concession is necessary; otherwise, one would be sinful if he dies from fasting. Unlike the first type, where the obligation was not removed, and if one performs azimah and dies, he attains martyrdom.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is a teacher's explanation of the second type of rukhsah (concession) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author first defines it: it is an act declared permissible despite the persistence of the shar'i cause (sabab) of prohibition, but the actual ruling (hukm) of prohibition is postponed due to an excuse. This contrasts with the first type, where both the prohibited thing (muharram) and its prohibition (hurmah) exist simultaneously. In the second type, only the prohibited thing exists; the prohibition is deferred. The example given is the concession for the sick or traveler to break the fast in Ramadan: the prohibition of fasting is postponed until after Ramadan. The author then derives a ruling: if they die before making up the fasts, no bequest for fidya is necessary because the obligation was not yet due. Then the author states the Hanafi position: it is superior (al-awla) to choose the azimah (full observance) over the rukhsah. He then engages in a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that taking the rukhsah is superior. Shafi'i's proof comes from hadiths that seem to criticize fasting while traveling. The Hanafi response restricts those hadiths to the context of jihad, where breaking the fast is indeed better. The Hanafi give two rational proofs: (1) The cause for obligation is present, so immediate performance is allowed, analogous to paying a debt early. (2) Rukhsah is meant for ease, but here the ostensible ease (not fasting) is not the only ease; fasting in a group is also easy, and later making up the fast alone might be harder. Since both paths contain ease, choosing the azimah is superior because it fulfills Allah's right, whereas rukhsah fulfills the servant's right. The concluding condition: if fasting poses a risk to life, then taking the concession becomes obligatory (wajib). This is the Hanafi doctrine: for the second type of rukhsah, azimah is generally superior unless harm is certain.

Key Terms
رخصة (rukhsah): A legal concession that permits an act despite the presence of a prohibiting cause, due to an excuse, making the act permissible even though the original ruling was prohibition.
عزيمة (azimah): The original, stronger ruling that is generally applicable without concession; in this context, observing the original obligation (fasting) despite the availability of a concession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of rukhsah has both the prohibited thing (muharram) and its prohibition (hurmah) present simultaneously?
A) The first type
B) The second type
C) The fourth type
D) All types

Key Takeaway
In the second type of rukhsah, the Hanafi school prefers the azimah (full observance) over the rukhsah, citing the presence of the cause, the postponement of prohibition, and the precedence of Allah's right.

Metaphorical Concession (Rukhsah Majaziyyah): Definition and Examples
Explains fourth type of rukhsah with examples and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define rukhsah majaziyyah, distinguish it from rukhsah haqiqiyyah, and apply the definition to examples from bay' salam, carrion, and khuff.

Core Idea
A concession is metaphorical when the original ruling (azimah) is absent for the specific case but remains for others.

In this passage, the commentator on Al-Husami explains the fourth type of concession (rukhsah majaziyyah) and provides three key examples from fiqh. Understanding this classification is essential for Hanafi usul, as it clarifies when a concession completely replaces the original ruling for a particular individual while the original rule remains in place for everyone else. The examples also highlight a significant disagreement within the Hanafi school and with Imam Shafi'i regarding the nature of the concession for the forced consumption of carrion.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of rukhsah majaziyyah
Identify that a rukhsah is metaphorical (majazi) when the azimah (original ruling) is completely absent for the specific subject but exists for others. This makes the concession 'incomplete' (naqis) in its metaphorical nature.
The opposite is rukhsah haqiqiyyah, where the azimah remains for the subject but is suspended.
2
Analyze the first example: bay' salam
In forward sale (salam), the condition of specifying the sold item (ta'yin al-mabi') is dropped. This is a rukhsah because the azimah (requirement of specification) exists for other sales. Since the azimah is absent only for salam, the concession is metaphorical.
The passage notes this type is less metaphorical (anqas) because azimah still exists for other sales.
3
Analyze the second example: carrion and wine under duress
For a forced or desperate person, the prohibition of carrion and wine is completely lifted according to the Hanafi school. The concession is metaphorical because the prohibition (azimah) remains for all others. Contrast this with the view of Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i who hold the prohibition remains but accountability is forgiven.
The Hanafi response explains that forgiveness in the Quranic verse refers to excess beyond necessity, not the lifting of prohibition.
4
Analyze the third example: wiping over khuffs
Washing the feet is azimah for everyone, but for one wearing khuffs, the obligation is replaced by wiping. Since washing the feet is completely absent for the khuff-wearer but remains for others, the concession is metaphorical.
Like the other examples, this is incomplete (naqis) metaphorically because azimah persists for others.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah) of the dispute
In the case of an oath not to eat haram, the Hanafi school says no oath-breaking occurs if the person eats carrion under duress, because the prohibition is lifted. Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i hold the oath is broken because the prohibition remains.
This shows how the classification of rukhsah directly affects fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مشروعیت ہے ہی نہیں ، جب مشروعیت یعنی عزیمت نہیں ہے تو بیع سلم میں اس شرط کے ساقط ہونے کو مجاز ارخصت کہا گیا ، اور چونکہ مسلم کے علاوہ بیچ کی باقی قسموں میں تعیین مبیع کی مشروعیت ہے تو عزیمت بالکلیہ مفقود نہ ہوئی ، لہذا یہ قسم مجاز ہونے میں انقص ہوگی۔
وكذلك الخمر والمتية : - نوع رابع کی دوسری مثال جیسے شراب اور مردار تمام لوگوں پر حرام ہیں، مگر مگرہ اور مضطر کے حق میں ان دونوں کی حرمت ساقط ہوگئی، کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے استثناء کیا ہے، "الاما اضطر رتم " تو مکرہ اور مضطر کے حق میں حرمت ساقط ہوگئی ، اور یہ چیزیں حلال ہوگئیں، یہ رخصت ہے، لہذا مکرہ اور مضطر کو ان دونوں چیزوں سے صبر کرنا جائز نہیں ، اگر نہ کھایا پیا اور مر گئے تو گنہگار ہوں گے، تو مکرہ ومضطر کے حق میں یہ دونوں چیزیں حلال ہوگئیں، ان کی حرمت بالکل باقی نہ رہی اس لئے اس پر رخصت کا اطلاق مجاز ا ہوگا، کیوں کہ مکرہ اور مضطر کے حق میں عزیمت ہے ہی نہیں یعنی حرمت ہے ہی نہیں لیکن چونکہ مکرہ اور مضطر کے علاوہ کے حق میں شراب و مردار کی حرمت باقی ہے یعنی بعض مادوں میں عزیمت موجود ہے، اس لئے یہ قسم مجاز ہونے میں انقص ہوگی ، امام ابو یوسف اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ مکرہ اور مضطر کے حق میں شراب اور مردار کی حرمت ساقط نہیں ہوتی بلکہ مجبوری کی وجہ سے اس پر مؤاخذہ نہ ہو گا۔۔ جیسے اکراہ کی صورت میں کلمہ کفر کہنے کی حرمت ساقط نہیں ہوتی لیکن کہہ لیا تو رخصت ہے، مؤاخذہ نہ ہوگا ، اس لحاظ سے ان دونوں بزرگوں کے نزدیک یہ مثال رخصت مجازیہ کی قسم اول کے قبیل سے ہوگی۔ ان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ارشاد فرمایا فمن اضطر غير باغ ولاعاد فلا اثم عليه، ان الله غفور رحیم، یہاں مغفرت کا لفظ بتا رہا ہے کہ حرمت ساقط نہیں ہوئی، حرمت تو باقی ہے لیکن مجبوری ہے تو اللہ معاف کر دے گا۔۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ مکرہ و مضطر کو بقدر ضرورت کھانے کی اجازت ہے، لیکن عام طور پر ضرورت سے زیادہ ہی آدمی کھا لیتا ہے، تو اس زائد مقدار سے مغفرت کا تعلق ہے کہ مقدار ضرورت سے جو زائد ہوگا اللہ اس کو معاف کر دے گا۔ اس اختلاف کا ثمرہ وہاں ظاہر ہوگا، جب کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ میں حرام نہیں کھاؤنگا، پھر اضطرار واکراہ کی حالت میں مردار کھا لیا، تو امام شافعی اور ابو یوسف کے نزدیک حانث ہو جائے گا، کیونکہ حرام کھا لیا، ان کے نزدیک حرمت ساقط نہیں ہوتی۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک حانث نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اضطر ا روا کراہ کی حالت میں ہمارے نزدیک حرمت ساقط ہو جاتی ہے، تو اس نے حرام چیز نہیں کھائی ہے۔
وكذلك الرجل: - نوع رابع کی تیسری مثال جیسے وضو میں پاؤں کا دھونا فرض ہے سب کے لئے ، البتہ موزے پہنے ہوں تو مدت مسح میں غسل رجلین ساقط ہو جاتا ہے، کیونکہ موزے کے سبب پیروں میں حدث سرایت نہیں کرتا ، تو غسل رجلین عزیمت ہے، اور موزوں پر مسح رخصت ہے، مگر موزے پہنے کی حالت میں عزیمت یعنی فسل رجلین بالکل ساقط ہے ، اس لئے مسح علی الخفین کو رخصت کہنا مجازی ہوگا، اس کے مقابل میں عزیمت نہیں ہے، مگر موزے والے کے علاوہ باقی تمام کے لئے عزیمت یعنی غسل رجلین موجود ہے، تو عزیمت بالکلیہ مفقود نہ ہوئی لہذا یہ صورت بھی مجاز ہونے میں تام نہ ہوگی بلکہ ناقص ہوگی۔
There is no legitimacy at all. When there is no legitimacy i.e. azimah, then the dropping of this condition in bay' salam was called rukhsah metaphorically. And since in other types of sale besides salam, the specification of the sold item has legitimacy, so the azimah was not completely absent; therefore this type will be less in being metaphorical. Similarly, wine and carrion: - the second example of the fourth type, like wine and carrion are forbidden for all people, but for the forced and the desperate their prohibition is dropped, because Allah Most High made an exception, 'except when you are forced'. So for the forced and desperate the prohibition is dropped, and these things become lawful; this is rukhsah. Therefore it is not permissible for the forced and desperate to abstain from these two things; if they do not eat and drink and die, they will be sinful. So for the forced and desperate, these two things become lawful; their prohibition is completely gone; therefore calling it rukhsah will be metaphorical, because for the forced and desperate there is no azimah at all, i.e., no prohibition. But since for others besides the forced and desperate, the prohibition of wine and carrion remains, i.e., in some individuals the azimah exists, this type will be less in being metaphorical. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i say that for the forced and desperate, the prohibition of wine and carrion is not dropped, rather due to coercion they will not be held accountable. Like in the case of coercion, the prohibition of uttering words of disbelief is not dropped, but if uttered it is a rukhsah; no accountability. Accordingly, according to these two great scholars, this example will fall under the first category of metaphorical rukhsah. Their proof is that Allah Most High said: 'But whoever is forced, neither desiring nor transgressing, no sin is upon him. Indeed, Allah is Forgiving and Merciful.' Here the word forgiveness indicates that the prohibition is not dropped; the prohibition remains but there is coercion, so Allah will forgive. Our response is that the forced and desperate are permitted to eat to the extent of necessity, but generally a person eats more than necessity; so forgiveness relates to that extra amount – what exceeds the necessary amount, Allah will forgive. The fruit of this disagreement will appear when someone swears an oath that he will not eat anything forbidden, then in a state of desperation or coercion he eats carrion: according to Imam Shafi'i and Abu Yusuf he will be an oath-breaker because he ate something forbidden; according to them the prohibition is not dropped. According to us he will not be an oath-breaker because in a state of desperation or coercion, according to us the prohibition is dropped, so he has not eaten a forbidden thing. Similarly, the foot: - the third example of the fourth type, like washing the feet in wudu is obligatory for everyone, but if one wears khuffs, during the period of wiping, washing the feet is dropped, because due to the khuff, the state of ritual impurity does not reach the feet. So washing the feet is azimah, and wiping over khuffs is rukhsah. But in the state of wearing khuffs, the azimah i.e. washing the feet is completely dropped; therefore calling wiping over khuffs a rukhsah is metaphorical; there is no azimah in its comparison. But for all others besides the one wearing khuffs, the azimah i.e. washing the feet exists; so the azimah is not completely absent; therefore this case too will not be complete in being metaphorical but will be incomplete.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the fourth type of rukhsah (metaphorical concession) in the commentary of Al-Husami. It provides three examples: (1) the condition in bay' salam (advance sale), (2) wine and carrion for one forced or desperate, and (3) wiping over khuffs. The author classifies these as metaphorical concessions (rukhsah majaziyyah) because the azimah (original ruling) is completely absent for the specific subject but exists for others, making the concession incomplete (naqis). In the carrion example, the Hanafi position holds that the prohibition is truly lifted for the forced and desperate, so they must eat if needed. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Shafi'i disagree, arguing the prohibition remains but accountability is forgiven, based on the Quranic verse where forgiveness indicates remaining prohibition. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the amount of necessity and excess. The practical effect appears in oaths: if a person swears not to eat haram and then eats carrion under duress, Hanafis say no oath-breaking occurs, while Abu Yusuf and Shafi'i say he breaks his oath. The khuff example follows the same logic: washing feet is azimah for all, but for one wearing khuffs it is completely replaced by wiping, yet azimah remains for others, so the concession is metaphorical and incomplete.

Key Terms
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession that makes permissible what is otherwise prohibited, due to necessity or difficulty.
عزیمت (azimah): The original, primary ruling that applies generally without exception.
رخصة مجازية (rukhsah majaziyyah): A metaphorical concession where the original ruling (azimah) is completely absent for the specific case but exists for others.
ثمرة الخلاف (thamarah al-khilaf): The practical consequence of a scholarly disagreement, especially in fiqh rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the disagreement regarding carrion under duress?
A) The forced person may eat carrion only if he will die otherwise.
B) If a person swears not to eat haram and then eats carrion under duress, he breaks his oath.
C) If a person swears not to eat haram and then eats carrion under duress, he does not break his oath according to the Hanafis.
D) The forced person must not eat carrion even if it means death.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a rukhsah majaziyyah is a concession that occurs when the original ruling (azimah) is completely absent for a specific individual but remains in effect for all others, making the concession inherently incomplete (naqis) in its metaphorical nature.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Rukhsat Isqat vs Tarkhis: The Nature of Qasr in Hanafi Usul
Explaining and proving the Hanafi view that qasr is a concession of dropping the original obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi concept of rukhsat isqat and the Shafi'i concept of rukhsat tarkhis, and apply the hadith of Umar to justify the Hanafi position.

Core Idea
Qasr is a complete dropping of the obligation, not a choice; the traveler must shorten.

In this lesson, we explore a key usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the nature of the concession (rukhsah) for shortening prayer during travel. The Hanafi school holds that this concession is a rukhsat isqat — it entirely removes the original obligation (azimah) for the traveler. The Shafi'i school, by contrast, considers it a rukhsat tarkhis — a facilitation that permits a lighter option while the original remains valid. Understanding this distinction has practical implications for the traveler's prayer obligations.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on qasr
The Hanafi school holds that qasr is a rukhsat isqat: the traveler's obligation is two rak'ahs, not four. The full prayer is invalid and sinful if performed intentionally.
2
Identify the Shafi'i opposing view
The Shafi'i school treats qasr as a rukhsat tarkhis: the traveler may choose to pray two or four, and four is preferable (azimah).
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil from hadith
Examine the hadith of Umar where the Prophet called qasr a 'sadaqah' (charity). Explain how the Hanafis derive isqat from the term sadaqah, using the analogy of forgiving retaliation (al-afw 'an al-qisas).
The hadith is narrated in Sunan Abu Dawud and Muslim.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rational proof
Concessions are for ease (rifq), and ease is fully realized only in qasr; thus ikmal (completion) falls away entirely. Choice without ease is unbefitting of servitude.
5
Evaluate the Shafi'i proof and Hanafi response
Shafi'i cite Quran 4:101 (negation of sin) and analogy with fasting. Hanafi response: the verse removed a misconception; the condition of fear is incidental; fasting is different because the text gives choice, not sadaqah.

وَكَذَلِكَ قَصْرُ الصَّلٰوةِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُسَافِرِ رُخْصَةُ اِسْقَاطِ عِنْدَنَا وَلِهَذَا قُلْنَا إِنَّ ظُهْرَ الْمُسَافِر وَفَجْرَهُ سَوَاءٌ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ الزيَادَةَ عَلَيْهِ وَإِنَّمَا جَعَلْنَاهَا إِسْقَاطًا مَحْضًا اِسْتِدْلَالًا بِدَلِيْلِ الرُّخْصَةِ وَمَعْنَاهَا. أَمَّا الدَّلِيلُ فَمَا رُوِيَ عَنْ عُمَرَ أَنَّهُ قَالَ أَنَقْصُرُ الصَّلٰوةَ وَنَحْنُ آمِنُونَ فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ هَذِهِ صَدَقَةٌ تَصَدَّقَ اللهُ بِهَا عَلَيْكُمْ فَاقْبَلُوْا صَدَقَتَهُ سَمَّاهُ صَدَقَةً وَالتَّصَدُّقُ بِمَا لَا يَحْتَمِلُ التَّمْلِيْكَ اِسْقَاطٌ مَحُضْ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ الرَّدَّ كَالْعَفُو عَنِ الْقِصَاصِ وَأَمَّا الْمَعْنَى فَهُوَ أَنَّ الرُّخْصَةَ لِطَلَبِ الرِّفْقِ وَالرِّفْقُ مُتَعَيِّنٌ فِي الْقَصْرِ فَسَقَطَ الْإِكْمَالُ أَصْلًا وَلِأَنَّ الْإِخْتِيَارَ بَيْنَ الْقَصْرِ وَالْإِكْمَالِ مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَتَضَمَّنَ رِفْقًا لَا يَلِيقُ بِالْعُبُودِيَةِ بِخِلَافِ الصَّوْمِ لِأَنَّ النَّصَّ جَاءَ بِالتَّخْيِيرِ دُونَ الصَّدَقَةِ وَالْيُسْرُ فِيهِ مُتَعَارِضٌ فَصَارَ التَّخْيِيرُ فِيهِ لِطَلَبِ الرِّفْقِ. (شرح: ترجمہ: اور اسی طرح نماز کا قصر مسافر کے حق میں رخصت اسقاط ہے ہمارے نزدیک ، اور اسی وجہ سے ہم نے کہا کہ مسافر کی ظہر اور اس کی فجر برابر ہیں، اس پر زیادتی کا احتمال نہیں ہے، اور ہم نے اس رخصت کو صدقہ کے ساتھ ، اور میسر روزہ میں متعارض ہے تو روزہ میں اختیار دینا رفق کو طلب کرنے کے لئے ہوگا۔ تشریح: - نوع رابع کی چوتھی مثال جیسے مسافر کو شریعت نے نماز میں رخصت دی، تمام لوگوں کے لئے چار رکعت ہے اور مسافر کے لئے دورکعت ہے، ہمارے نزدیک یہ قصر رخصت اسقاط ہے یعنی عزیمت کو ساقط کرنے والی ہے، پس مسافر کے حق میں عزیمت ہے ہی نہیں تو قصر کو رخصت کہنا مجاز ہوا، کیونکہ اس کے مقابل میں عزیمت نہیں ہے، لہذا مسافر دوہی رکعت پڑھے گا، اس کی ظہر اور فجر برابر ہوگی، اگر چار پڑھے گا تو گنہگار ہوگا، اگر چار پڑھی اور دورکعت پر قعدہ کیا تو دوسری دو نفل ہو جائے گی لیکن نفل کو فرض کے ساتھ قصد املا نا جائز نہیں ہے، اور اگر قعدہ نہیں کیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی، مگر چونکہ مسافر کے علاوہ میں عزیمت موجود ہے تو قصر صلوۃ پر مجاز کا اطلاق تام نہ ہوگا، ناقص ہوگا، کیونکہ عزیمت بالکلیہ مفقود نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی رحمہ اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ رخصت ترفیہ ہے یعنی مسافر کو آسانی کے لئے دو رکعت کی رخصت دی گئی ہے، لیکن عزیمت یعنی چار رکعت اولی ہے، جیسے رمضان میں روزہ رکھنے کی مسافر کو رخصت دی ہے مگر عزیمت یعنی روزہ رکھنا اولی عمر رضی اللہ عنہ نے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم سے عرض کیا کہ ہم نماز میں قصر کریں جب کہ ہم امن کی حالت میں ہیں۔ حضرت عمر رضی اللہ عنہ نے ان خفتم کی قید سے شاید یہ سمجھا ہو کہ قصر خوف کے ساتھ مختص ہے۔ تو حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا یہ رخصت اللہ کا بندوں پر صدقہ ہے، اسے قبول کرو، تو حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے قصر صلوۃ کو صدقہ قرار دیا، اور ایسی چیز کا صدقہ کرنا جو تملیک کا احتمال نہ رکھے اسقاط محض ہے۔)
And similarly, shortening of prayer for the traveler is a concession of dropping according to us, so we said: the traveler's Zuhr and Fajr are equal, it does not admit increase. And we made it a pure dropping, seeking evidence from the evidence of concession and its meaning. As for the evidence: what is narrated from Umar that he said: 'Should we shorten prayer while we are secure?' The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'This is a charity which Allah has given as charity to you, so accept His charity.' He called it a charity, and charity of something that does not admit ownership is a pure dropping that does not admit return, like forgiveness of retaliation. As for the meaning: concession is for seeking ease, and ease is specifically found in shortening, so completion falls away entirely. And because choice between shortening and completion without containing ease is unbefitting of servitude, unlike fasting because the text came with choice without charity, and ease in it is conflicting, so the choice in it is for seeking ease.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage discusses the usul classification of the concession (rukhsah) for shortening prayer during travel. According to the Hanafi school, this concession is a rukhsat isqat, meaning it entirely drops the original obligation (azimah) for the traveler. For a traveler, the full four-rak'ah prayer is no longer required; the two-rak'ah prayer is the only lawful obligation. If a traveler prays four rak'ahs, he incurs sin. This contrasts with the Shafi'i view, which holds that the concession is a tarkhis (facilitation), where the azimah remains valid and preferable. The Hanafis provide two proofs: First, the hadith where the Prophet (SAW) called it a 'sadaqah', indicating it is a pure dropping of what was due, not a choice. Second, rational proof: concessions are for ease, and ease is fully realized only in shortening, so the complete prayer is entirely dropped. The debate about the Quranic verse (al-Nisa: 101) is also addressed: the negation of sin (junah) in the verse is interpreted by Hanafis as removing doubt, not indicating permissibility alone. The passage also explains that even though the azimah is dropped for the traveler, it remains for others, so applying the term 'rukhsah' to qasr is a valid but incomplete metaphor (majaz naqis).

Key Terms
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession that relaxes an original ruling due to a valid excuse, such as travel.
عزیمت (azimah): The primary, inflexible ruling that applies to all under normal conditions, e.g., four rak'ahs for Zuhr.
اسقاط (isqat): The complete dropping of an obligation, leaving no option for the original.
ترفیہ (tarkhis): A facilitation that allows a lighter option while the original remains valid and preferable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if a traveler prays the full four rak'ahs of Zuhr intentionally?
A) The prayer is valid and he is rewarded for performing the azimah.
B) The prayer is valid but he is sinful for leaving the rukhsah.
C) The prayer is invalid and he is sinful.
D) The prayer is valid as nafil but not as fard.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi classification of qasr as rukhsat isqat means the traveler must shorten; full prayer is no longer an option.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
12 min
Refutation of Qiyas between Qasr and Sawm
Refutes Shafi'i qiyas of qasr salat to sawm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the validity of a qiyas by distinguishing between types of rukhsah (sadaqah vs. postponement) in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
A rukhsah that removes azimah differs fundamentally from one that postpones it; qiyas between them fails.

This passage presents a Hanafi critique of Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy between the traveler's shortening of prayer (qasr) and his concession for fasting. The key lies in understanding the nature of each concession: while fasting merely postpones the obligation, qasr completely removes the original ruling. Through this analysis, you will see how usul al-fiqh distinguishes between concessions and why analogies must respect these distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i argument
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes qasr salah to the traveler's fasting concession, arguing that since both are rukhsah for travel, they should share the same ruling: the traveler has a choice.
The opposing school typically holds that both concessions give the traveler an option.
2
Locate the textual basis for sawm
The Hanafi response cites Quran 2:184—'a number of other days'—which indicates postponement (ta'khir) of the obligation, not its removal.
The dalil is the Quranic phrase itself; its dalalah (indication) is zanni according to Hanafi usul.
3
Distinguish the two rukhsah types
Qasr is termed a sadaqah (charity) that completely removes the azimah, whereas sawm only postpones the azimah, leaving it intact. This fundamental difference invalidates the qiyas.
In Hanafi thought, a rukhsah can be either a full replacement (sadaqah) or a mere postponement.
4
Analyze the Hanafi reasoning on ease (yusr)
In fasting, ease exists on both sides (concession and strict ruling due to community conformity), so choice is appropriate. In qasr, ease is only in the concession, so shortening is determined.
This additional argument reinforces the textual distinction.
5
Conclude the validity of the qiyas
Since the illa (effective cause) for each rukhsah differs, the qiyas is invalid. The Hanafi position that qasr is wajib (no choice) is upheld.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi traveler must shorten; Shafi'i traveler may choose.

معنی رخصت سے دوسرا طریق استدلال یہ ہے کہ اگر بندہ کو قصر اور اکمال میں اختیار دیا جائے جب کہ عزیمت میں کسی طرح سے یسر نہیں ہے، تو یہ شان عبدیت کے خلاف ہے، کیونکہ بندہ کا کوئی فعل غرض اور نفع سے خالی نہیں ہوتا، یہ تو صرف اللہ کی شان ہے کہ اس کے کسی کام میں غرض ونفع وابستہ نہیں ہوتا، لہذا اختیار نہ ہوگا، قصر متعین ہوگا ، اور پوری نماز پڑھنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ بخلاف الصوم : - امام شافعی نے قصر صلوۃ کو مسافر کے روزے پر قیاس کیا تھا، مصنف اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ مسافر کے روزے میں رخصت کی جو نص وارد ہوئی ہے وہ روزے کی ادائیگی کے مؤخر ہونے کو بتلا رہی ہے، یعنی مسافر بھی روزہ نہ رکھے بعد میں قضا کر لے، کیونکہ فَعِدَّةٌ مِنْ أَيَّامٍ أُخَرَ کہا گیا، روزہ کو صدقہ نہیں کہا گیا، لہذا روزے میں عزیمت ساقط نہ ہوگی، بلکہ عزیمت بھی باقی رہے گی، کیونکہ روزے کو مؤخر کیا گیا ہے، اور مؤخر کو معجل کیا جاسکتا ہے، جیسے دین مؤجل مدت سے پہلے دیا جا سکتا ہے، اور زکوۃ حولان حول سے پہلے ادا ہو سکتی ہے، برخلاف قصرِ صلوۃ کے کہ اس کو تو صدقہ قرار دیا گیا جس سے عزیمت بالکل ساقط ہو جاتی ہے، لہذا یہ قیاس درست نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ دونوں میں فرق ہے، مسافر کے روزے میں یسر متعارض ہے، یسر کا تعارض ہے یعنی ئیسر دونوں طرف ہے، رخصت میں بھی ہے اور موافقت مسلمین کی وجہ سے عزیمت میں بھی یسر ہے، لہذا یسر اور رفق کی طلب کے لئے مسافر کو اختیار دیا جائے گا، اور قصر صلوۃ میں یسر دونوں طرف نہیں ہے، صرف قصر میں یسر ہے لہذا یہاں قصر متعین ہوگا۔
The second method of inference from the meaning of concession is that if a servant is given choice between shortening and completion while there is no ease in the strict ruling, then this is against the status of servitude, because the servant's actions are never free from purpose and benefit; that is only the attribute of Allah that His actions have no purpose or benefit attached. Therefore, there will be no choice; shortening is determined, and praying the full prayer is not valid. Contrary to fasting: Imam Shafi'i had analogized the shortening of prayer to the traveler's fasting. The author is responding that the text that came regarding concession in the traveler's fasting indicates the postponement of the fasting's performance, i.e., the traveler should not fast and later make it up, because it is said 'a number of other days'; fasting has not been termed charity. Hence, in fasting, the strict ruling is not removed entirely; rather, the strict ruling remains, because the fast is postponed, and what is postponed can be expedited, like a deferred debt can be paid before its term, and zakat can be paid before the year elapses. In contrast to the shortening of prayer, which has been declared charity, by which the strict ruling is completely removed. Therefore, this analogy is not valid. Because there is a difference: in the traveler's fasting, ease is conflicting; there is conflict of ease, meaning ease is on both sides; it is in the concession and also in the strict ruling due to conformity with Muslims. So for seeking ease and comfort, the traveler will be given choice. But in the shortening of prayer, ease is not on both sides; there is ease only in shortening, so here shortening is determined.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage contains a Hanafi refutation of Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy (qiyas) that the concession of shortening prayer (qasr) for a traveler is analogous to the concession of not fasting for a traveler. The Hanafi argument distinguishes the two: in fasting, the Quranic text (2:184) merely postpones the obligation to other days, so the strict ruling (azimah) remains in effect; the traveler may choose to fast or postpone. In contrast, shortening prayer is termed a 'sadaqah' (charity) from Allah, which entirely removes the strict ruling of full prayer. Thus the traveler must shorten; he has no choice. The passage also argues that in fasting, ease (yusr) exists on both sides (concession and strict ruling because of community conformity), whereas in prayer, ease is only in the concession. Therefore, the analogy fails due to a clear difference.

Key Terms
عزیمت (azimah): The strict, original ruling of an obligation without concession.
رخصت (rukhsah): A concession from the original ruling due to necessity or hardship.
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'ah prayer to two rak'ahs for a traveler.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why does the traveler have no choice between qasr and full prayer?
A) Because there is no ease in full prayer.
B) Because qasr is a sadaqah that removes the azimah entirely.
C) Because the traveler is too weak.
D) Because the Quran commands shortening.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the nature of a rukhsah—whether it removes or postpones the azimah—determines the ruling; analogies between concessions must respect this distinction.

The Hanafi Principle of Ease and Choice: Mughayarah
Answers objection about slave's choice between Jumu'ah and Zuhr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when two acts differ in kind (mughayarah), ease (rufk) is not automatically determined in the lesser one, and derive the ruling for a slave permitted for Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
When acts differ in kind, ease is not simply a matter of fewer rak'ahs; both may have their own ease.

This passage resolves a classic objection to the Hanafi position on a slave's choice between Jumu'ah and Zuhr. It clarifies that the principle of selecting the easier act only applies when acts are of the same type. When they are different (mughayarah), ease may exist in both, so choice is given. Understanding this nuance is key to applying Hanafi usul correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Someone argues that the Hanafi principle that the easier act is determined when only one has ease is contradicted here: Jumu'ah is easier (2 rak'ahs) than Zuhr (4), yet Hanafis give choice.
The objector sees only the count-based ease.
2
State the Hanafi principle
The principle: if ease is only in one act, that act is determined; if ease is in both, choice is allowed.
3
Distinguish between act types
Key distinction: Jumu'ah and Zuhr are different acts (mughayarah). When acts differ, ease is not determined solely by the lesser number because the greater may have its own ease from other aspects (e.g., Zuhr has no sermon or travel).
Mughayarah is about the legal kind, not just numerical difference.
4
Apply to the slave case
Since both acts have ease (Jumu'ah in fewer rak'ahs, Zuhr in absence of burdens), the slave is given choice.
5
Contrast with traveler's qasr
The traveler's 2 and 4 rak'ah Zuhr are the same act; only the count differs, so ease is determined in the lesser (2 rak'ahs), and no choice is given.
This shows the rule's consistent application.

وَلَا يَلْزَمُ الْعَبْدَ الْمَأْذُونَ فِي الْجُمْعَةِ لِأَنَّ الْجُمْعَةَ غَيْرُ الظُّهْرِ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَجُوْزُ بِنَاءُ أَحَدِهِمَا عَلَى الْآخَرِ وَعِنْدَ الْمُغَايَرَةِ لَا يَتَعَيَّنُ الرِّفْقُ فِي الْأَقَلِ عَدَدًا وَأَمَّا ظُهْرُ الْمُسَافِرِ وَالْمُقِيمِ وَاحِدٌ فَبِالتَّخْيِيرِ بَيْنَ الْقَلِيلِ وَالْكَثِيرِ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ شَيْءٌ مِنْ مَعْنَى الرِّفْقِ۔ ترجمہ: اور اعتراض لازم نہیں آئے گا اس غلام کا جس کو جمعہ کی اجازت دی گئی، اس لئے کہ جمعہ ظہر کے علاوہ ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے جائز نہیں ہے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کی بنا دوسرے پر اور مغایرت کے وقت رفق متعین نہیں ہوتا ہے کم عدد والے میں، اور بہر حال مسافر اور مقیم کی ظہر ایک ہے تو قلیل اور کثیر کے درمیان اختیار دینے سے رفق کا کچھ بھی معنی متحقق نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح: ایک اعتراض کا جواب دے رہے ہیں جس کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ آپ (احناف) نے کہا کہ رخصت اور عزیمت دونوں میں یسر ہو تو اختیار دیا جائے گا، اور اگر ایک میں یسر ہو تو اختیار نہیں دیا جائے گا، بلکہ یسر والی چیز پر عمل کرنا متعین ہو جائے گا، حالانکہ اس مسئلہ میں آپ اصول توڑ رہے ہیں، کہ جب غلام کو آقا نے جمعہ پڑھنے کی اجازت دی، تو آپ کہتے ہیں کہ غلام کو جمعہ اور ظہر پڑھنے میں اختیار ہو گا، چاہے جمعہ پڑھے، چاہے ظہر پڑھے، حالانکہ یہاں جمعہ میں رفق ویسر متعین ہے، ظہر میں یسر نہیں ہے، کیونکہ یہ چار رکعت ہے اور جمعہ دو رکعت ہے، تو جمعہ متعین ہونا چاہیئے کیونکہ جمعہ میں ہی رفق ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حضرت والا! جمعہ اور ظہر دو الگ الگ چیزیں ہیں، اسی لئے جمعہ ظہر کی نیت سے ادا نہیں ہوتا ہے، اور نہ ظہر جمعہ کی نیت سے، اسی طرح جمعہ پڑھنے والا ظہر پڑھنے والے کی اقتدا نہیں کر سکتا ہے، اور نہ اس کا برعکس، پس جب دونوں میں مغایرت ہے تو رفق قلیل میں متعین نہیں ہوسکتا، ہو سکتا ہے کثیر میں بھی رفق ہو، ہاں جب دونوں ایک ہی جنس ہوں تو تقلیل میں کثیر کے مقابلہ میں رفق ہو سکتا ہے، جیسے مسافر کی چار رکعت، اور دو رکعت، لیکن جب دونوں چیزیں الگ الگ ہوں تو قلیل میں رفق کا تعین نہیں ہو سکتا، کثیر میں بھی ہو سکتا ہے جیسے یہاں جمعہ میں رفق قلیل ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے کہ یہ دو ہی رکعت ہے، اور ظہر میں جو کثیر ہے اس میں بھی رفق ہے، اس طرح کہ ظہر میں خطبہ نہیں ہے، سعی الی الجمعہ نہیں ہے، لہذا جب رفق دونوں میں ہے، تو غلام کو جمعہ اور ظہر کا اختیار دیا جائے گا۔ اور ہمارا زیر بحث مسئلہ یعنی مسافر کی ظہر قصر اور مقیم کی چار رکعت یہ دونوں ایک ہی ہیں، اسی لئے مقیم و مسافر دونوں ایک دوسرے کی اقتدا کر سکتے ہیں، جب دونوں ایک ہی ہیں تو قلیل میں یعنی دو رکعت میں رفق متعین ہوگا، چار رکعت میں کوئی رفق نہیں ہے، تو مسافر کو دو رکعت پڑھنا متعین ہو جائے گا، قصر اور اکمال میں اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ یہ ساری تقریر تو اس صورت میں ہے جب عبد مأذون فی الجمعہ کو جمعہ اور ظہر میں اختیار حاصل ہو۔ لیکن صاحب نامی شارح حسامی نے غایۃ التحقیق کے حوالہ سے لکھا ہے کہ عبد مأذون فی الجمعہ پر جمعہ لازم ہے، اس کو اختیار نہیں ہے، اگر ایسی صورت ہے تو پھر کوئی اعتراض ہی نہیں ہے۔
And it does not necessarily follow concerning the slave who is permitted for Friday [prayer], because Friday prayer is other than Zuhr, and for this reason it is not permissible to base one of them on the other, and in the case of difference, comfort is not determined in the lesser in number. As for the Zuhr of the traveler and the resident, it is the same; so by giving choice between the few and the many, nothing of the meaning of comfort is realized. Translation: The objection will not apply to the slave who is given permission for Friday, because Friday is other than Zuhr, and for this reason it is not permissible to base one of them on the other, and in the case of difference, comfort is not determined in the lesser number. And in any case, the Zuhr of the traveler and resident is the same, so giving choice between the few and the many does not realize any meaning of comfort. Commentary: He is answering an objection whose formulation is that you (Hanafis) said that if there is ease in both the concession and the strict ruling, then choice will be given; and if there is ease in only one, then no choice is given, rather acting upon the one with ease is determined. Yet in this issue you are breaking the principle: when the master permits the slave to pray Friday, you say the slave has choice between Friday and Zuhr, whether he prays Friday or Zuhr, while here Friday has determined ease and comfort, Zuhr has no ease because it is four rak'ahs and Friday is two, so Friday should be determined because ease is only in Friday. The answer is that Friday and Zuhr are two separate things; therefore Friday is not valid with the intention of Zuhr, nor Zuhr with the intention of Friday; similarly, one who prays Friday cannot follow one who prays Zuhr, nor vice versa. So when there is difference, comfort is not determined in the lesser; it is possible that comfort is in the greater as well. Yes, when both are of the same kind, then in the lesser there is comfort compared to the greater, like the traveler's four rak'ahs and two rak'ahs. But when the two are separate, comfort cannot be determined in the lesser; it may also be in the greater, as here Friday has comfort due to it being two rak'ahs, but Zuhr, though greater in number, also has comfort because it has no sermon and no going out for Friday. So when comfort is in both, the slave is given choice between Friday and Zuhr. And our topic under discussion, i.e., the traveler's shortened Zuhr and the resident's four rak'ahs, are the same; therefore, resident and traveler can follow one another in prayer. When both are the same, the comfort is determined in the lesser, i.e., two rak'ahs; there is no comfort in four rak'ahs. So the traveler is determined to pray two rak'ahs; there is no choice between shortening and completion. All this discussion is when the slave permitted for Friday has choice between Friday and Zuhr. But the commentator Sahib Nami has written quoting Ghayat al-Tahqiq that Friday is obligatory upon the slave permitted for Friday; he has no choice. If that is the case, then there is no objection at all.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection to the Hanafi principle regarding ease and choice. The objection claims inconsistency: Hanafis say that if ease is only on one side, that side becomes determined; yet in the case of a slave permitted to attend Jumu'ah, they allow choice between Jumu'ah and Zuhr, even though Jumu'ah (2 rak'ahs) is easier than Zuhr (4 rak'ahs). The response distinguishes between acts that are of the same kind (e.g., qasr and full prayer, both being Zuhr) and acts that are different (Jumu'ah vs. Zuhr). When acts are different, ease is not necessarily determined in the lesser number because the greater may also have ease from other aspects (e.g., Zuhr has no sermon). Thus the slave is given choice. In the traveler's case, qasr and full prayer are the same act (Zuhr), so the lesser is determined. The passage also notes a different opinion where Jumu'ah is obligatory on the permitted slave, making the objection moot.

Key Terms
مغایرت (mughayarah): Difference in kind between two acts, such that they are not interchangeable.
رفق (rufk): Comfort, ease, or facility that makes an act lighter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school give the slave choice between Jumu'ah and Zuhr, despite Jumu'ah having fewer rak'ahs?
A) Because the slave is not required to pray at all.
B) Because Jumu'ah and Zuhr are different acts, and Zuhr may also have ease (no sermon, no journey).
C) Because the slave is more virtuous.
D) Because the master's permission is invalid.

Key Takeaway
When two acts differ in kind, ease is not automatically determined in the lesser; both may have their own ease, allowing choice.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Mursal of Later Generations: Dispute and Exception
Dispute on later generation mursal with Hanafi internal divergence and Shafi'i exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi internal dispute on accepting mursal of later generations and evaluate the Shafi'i position with its exception.

Core Idea
Mursal of later generations is accepted among Hanafis when transmitted by trustworthy narrators, but Shafi'i restricts it to Companions except for Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab.

This lesson explores the acceptance of mursal hadith from narrators who belong to generations after the three best generations (Companions, Tabi‘in, Taba‘ Tabi‘in). The Hanafi school itself is divided, with some scholars like al-Karkhi accepting such mursal based on the narrator's reliability, while others like 'Isa ibn Aban reject it due to the corruption of later times. The author presents a resolution: when trustworthy narrators (thiqāt) transmit these mursal reports, they become acceptable by consensus, as they are effectively like musnad. Meanwhile, Imam al-Shafi‘i takes a stricter stance, accepting only mursal of Companions, with a single exception for the Tabi‘i Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab. By the end of this lesson, you will be able to navigate these positions and understand the practical implications for hadith acceptance.

Guided Path
1
State the core issue
Identify the question: should mursal hadith from narrators after the three best generations (beyond the Taba‘ Tabi‘in) be accepted as evidence?
The disagreement applies to narrators who are not from the qurūn thalātha.
2
Map the Hanafi internal dispute
Identify the two opposing views within the Hanafi school: al-Karkhi accepts based on common 'illa (reliability), while 'Isa ibn Aban rejects because the hadith 'The best of generations...' limits testimony to the three generations.
The author adds a middle ground: acceptance when thiqāt narrate the mursal.
3
Understand the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i accepts only mursal of Companions; for others, he requires external support (definitive proof or sound qiyas). He makes an exception for Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab due to his unique reliability.
This exception is significant because Sa'id is a Tabi'i, not a Companion.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis may use later mursal in legal rulings (when thiqāt narrate), whereas Shafi'is restrict to Companions or conditional acceptance. This affects the strength of legal arguments in different schools.
The author implies that the Hanafi view (via al-Karkhi or the thiqāt condition) is more flexible.
5
Evaluate the author's proposed resolution
The author suggests that disagreement disappears when thiqāt narrate the mursal – it becomes like musnad. This harmonizes the internal Hanafi dispute and narrows the gap with Shafi'i when narrators are reliable.
Note the correction: Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani is from the third generation, not later.

واما مراسيل من دون هؤلاء - صحابہ، تابعین اور تبع تابعین کے بعد کے لوگوں کی مرسل روایتوں کے قبول ورد میں خود علمائے احناف میں اختلاف ہے، بعض علمائے احناف جیسے امام کرخی عالی وغیرہ کہتے ہیں کہ ان مراسیل کو قبول کیا جائے گا کیونکہ قرون ثلثہ کے مراسیل کو قبول کرنے کی جو علت سے یعنی ان کا عادل ہونا وغیرہ وہ بعد کے لوگوں میں بھی ہے، اور بعض مشائخ احناف جیسے عیسی بن ابان وغیرہ کہتے ہیں کہ ان کی مراسیل قبول نہیں کی جائے گی، کیونکہ قرون ثلثہ کے بعد کا زمانہ فسق و فجور کا زمانہ ہے، کیونکہ حضور صلی اا اینم نے ان کی عدالت کی شہادت نہیں ہے، صرف تین زمانوں کی شہادت دی ہے خیر القرون قرنی ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم الاان يروى الثقات : - مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ قرونِ ثلثہ کے بعد کے لوگوں کی مراسیل میں اسی وقت اختلاف ہے جب کہ ثقہ لوگ ان کے مراسیل کو روایت نہ کرتے ہوں، ورنہ اگر ثقہ لوگ ان کی مراسیل کو اسی طرح روایت کرتے ہوں جس طرح ان کی مسانید کو روایت کرتے ہیں، تو ان کے مراسیل کو قرون ثلثہ کے مراسیل کی طرح بالا تفاق قبول کر لیا جائے گا جیسے امام محمد ہے اور ان جیسوں کے مراسیل مقبول ہیں۔ اس جگہ امام محمد النے کو مثال میں پیش کرنا درست نہیں کیونکہ امام محمد قرون ثلثہ میں ہیں، تبع تابعین میں ہیں، قرون ثلثہ کے بعد کے لوگوں میں نہیں ہیں۔ رحمة وقال الشافعى الله لا اقبل : - امام شافعی سے فرماتے ہیں کہ میں صرف صحابہ کے مراسیل قبول کرتا ہوں، ان کے بعد والوں کے نہیں، البتہ اگر حجت قطعیہ یا قیاس صحیح وغیرہ سے ان مراسیل کی تائید ہو جائے تو وہ مقبول ہیں، امام شافعی اللہ نے اپنے قول لا اقبل سے سعید بن المسیب ( جو کہ تابعی ہیں ) کے مراسیل کا استثناء کیا اور فرمایا کہ صحابہ کے بعد کے لوگوں میں صرف سعید بن المسیب کے مراسیل قبول کرتا ہوں، وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ جب میں
And as for the mursal of those besides these – after the Companions, Tabi‘in, and Taba‘ Tabi‘in – there is disagreement among the Hanafi scholars themselves regarding acceptance and rejection. Some Hanafi scholars, like Imam al-Karkhi and others, say that these mursal reports will be accepted because the cause (‘illa) for accepting the mursal of the three generations, i.e., their being ‘adl etc., also exists in later people. Other Hanafi mashāyikh, like ‘Isa ibn Aban and others, say that their mursal will not be accepted because the period after the three generations is an era of sin and corruption, and because the Prophet, peace be upon him, did not testify to their justice; he only testified to three generations: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them.' Unless thiqāt (reliable narrators) narrate them: The author says that the disagreement regarding the mursal of those after the three generations exists only when thiqāt do not narrate their mursal. Otherwise, if thiqāt narrate their mursal just as they narrate their musnad, then their mursal will be accepted by agreement, like Imam Muhammad [al-Shaybani] – but mentioning Imām Muhammad as an example here is not correct because Imam Muhammad belongs to the three generations, he is among the Taba‘ Tabi‘in, not after the three generations. Rahima [Allah]. And al-Shafi‘i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'I do not accept except mursal of the Companions. As for those after them, no, unless a definitive proof or sound analogy supports them, then they are accepted.' Imam al-Shafi‘i, may Allah have mercy on him, made an exception from his statement 'I do not accept' for the mursal of Sa‘id ibn al-Musayyab (who is a Tabi‘i) and said: 'Among those after the Companions, I only accept the mursal of Sa‘id ibn al-Musayyab.' Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage deals with mursal hadith from narrators after the best three generations (the Companions, Tabi‘in, and Taba‘ Tabi‘in). Among Hanafis there is an internal dispute: Imam al-Karkhi argues that the same reason for accepting mursal of the early generations – namely, the narrators' reliability – applies to later generations, so their mursal should be accepted. Others like ‘Isa ibn Aban reject later mursal because the later period is characterized by sin and corruption, and the Prophet's testimony of goodness only covers three generations (hadith: 'The best of generations is my generation...'). The author then presents a resolution: if reliable narrators (thiqāt) transmit the mursal of these later figures, then it becomes acceptable by agreement, as they would report it like musnad. The author criticizes an example given (Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) as being from the third generation, not later. The passage then shifts to Imam al-Shafi‘i's position: he accepts only mursal from Companions, and conditionally from others, but he makes an exception for Sa‘id ibn al-Musayyab (a famous Tabi‘i) due to his unique reliability. The text ends mid-sentence, possibly continuing on a missing page.

Key Terms
قرون ثلثہ (qurūn thalātha): The three best generations: Companions, Tabi‘in, and Taba‘ Tabi‘in as per the hadith of the Prophet.
امام کرخی (al-Karkhi): A Hanafi usuli scholar who accepted mursal of later generations based on 'illa of reliability.
عیسی بن ابان (‘Isa ibn Aban): A Hanafi scholar who rejected mursal of later generations due to corruption and lack of prophetic testimony.
سعید بن المسیب (Sa‘id ibn al-Musayyab): A prominent Tabi‘i; Shafi‘i made an exception for his mursal due to his high reliability.

Checkpoint
According to the author, when is the mursal of later generations accepted by agreement among Hanafis?
A) Always, because all mursal is accepted
B) When thiqāt (reliable narrators) narrate their mursal
C) Only if supported by a definitive proof
D) Never, because they are from a corrupt era

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of mursal from later narrators hinges on the reliability of transmitters, with Hanafis adopting a more flexible approach through the thiqāt condition, while Shafi‘is maintain stricter requirements with a notable exception for Sa‘id ibn al-Musayyab.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Acceptance of Mursal Hadith: Hanafi and Shafi'i Perspectives
Discusses validity of mursal reports and differences among scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which Hanafis accept mursal hadith from later generations and explain the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
Mursal from later narrators is accepted if trustworthy narrators transmit it.

This lesson examines the Hanafi view on mursal hadith, especially from narrators after the first three generations. We will explore an intra-Hanafi dispute, the Shafi'i stricter position, and the resolution that trustworthiness is key. Understanding this helps you navigate differences in hadith acceptance across schools.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection about mursal and abrogation
The passage begins by addressing an objection: if mursal is superior to musnad, it should have the power to abrogate the Quran. The response clarifies that mursal's superiority is based on ijtihad, not explicit text, so it cannot abrogate.
This distinction between textual and ijtihadi strength is crucial in Hanafi usul.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement on mursal after the three generations
Some Hanafis (e.g., al-Karkhi) accept mursal from later generations because the 'illa of justice is continuous. Others (e.g., Isa ibn Aban) reject it, citing the hadith praising only the first three generations.
The debate hinges on whether the hadith 'Khayr al-qurun' is exclusive or simply declarative of virtue.
3
Analyze the author's resolution
The author states that the disagreement only arises when trustworthy narrators (thiqat) do not transmit the mursal. If they do, the mursal is accepted by consensus.
Trustworthiness overcomes generational concern.
4
Examine the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i only accepts mursal from the Sahaba, with the sole exception of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, whose mursal reports were found to have supporting chains (musnad).
This exception shows that the Shafi'i rule is not absolute; corroboration can change the ruling.
5
Recognize the fourth kind of mursal
A hadith that is mursal from one chain and musnad from another is accepted by giving precedence to the musnad aspect. Example: 'La nikaha illa bi wali' narrated by Isra'il as musnad and Shu'bah as mursal.
This type is not in the original matn but is added as a benefit in the commentary.
