الفيضُ الحجازي
۱۷۸
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
کر حدیث روایت کرتا ہے، برخلاف مسند کے کہ اس میں راوی کو کامل وثوق نہیں ہوتا اسی لئے وہ اس کو اپنے سر لینا
نہیں چاہتا بلکہ وہ اپنے استاذ کا نام لیکر اور استاذ کی طرف حدیث کو منسوب کر کے اپنے ذمہ کو فارغ کر دیتا ہے۔ ولكن هذا ضرب مزية :- ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے جس کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ جب مرسل مسند سے بڑھ کر ہے اور مسند کی تین قسمیں ہیں، متواتر ، مشہور، آحاد، اور مسند سے مرسل کا درجہ بڑھا ہوا ہے تو اعلی نہ سہی کم از کم متوسط یعنی مشہور کے درجہ میں ہوگی اور خبر مشہور سے کتاب اللہ کا سخ جائز ہے تو مرسل سے بھی جائز ہونا چاہیے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مرسل کی فوقیت وفضیلت مسند پر چونکہ اجتہاد اور رائے سے ثابت ہوتی ہے، اس لئے نسخ جائز نہیں تاکہ رائے اور قیاس سے کتاب اللہ کا نسخ لازم نہ آئے ، برخلاف مسند مشہور کے کہ اس کی فضیلت وقوت رائے
اور اجتہاد سے نہیں بلکہ نص سے ثابت ہوتی ہے اس لئے مشہور سے کتاب اللہ پر نسخ و زیادتی جائز ہے۔ واما مراسيل من دون هؤلاء - صحابہ، تابعین اور تبع تابعین کے بعد کے لوگوں کی مرسل روایتوں کے قبول ورد میں خود علمائے احناف میں اختلاف ہے، بعض علمائے احناف جیسے امام کرخی عالی وغیرہ کہتے ہیں کہ ان مراسیل کو قبول کیا جائے گا کیونکہ قرون ثلثہ کے مراسیل کو قبول کرنے کی جو علت سے یعنی ان کا عادل ہونا وغیرہ وہ بعد کے لوگوں میں بھی ہے، اور بعض مشائخ احناف جیسے عیسی بن ابان وغیرہ کہتے ہیں کہ ان کی مراسیل قبول نہیں کی جائے گی، کیونکہ قرون ثلثہ کے بعد کا زمانہ فسق و فجور کا زمانہ ہے، کیونکہ حضور صلی اا اینم نے ان کی عدالت کی شہادت نہیں ہے، صرف تین زمانوں کی شہادت دی ہے خير القرون قرني ثم الذين يلونهم ثم الذين يلونهم الاان يروى الثقات : - مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ قرونِ ثلثہ کے بعد کے لوگوں کی مراسیل میں اسی وقت اختلاف ہے جب کہ ثقہ لوگ ان کے مراسیل کو روایت نہ کرتے ہوں، ورنہ اگر ثقہ لوگ ان کی مراسیل کو اسی طرح روایت کرتے ہوں جس طرح ان کی مسانید کو روایت کرتے ہیں، تو ان کے مراسیل کو قرون ثلثہ کے مراسیل کی طرح بالا تفاق قبول کر لیا جائے گا جیسے امام محمد ہے اور ان جیسوں کے مراسیل مقبول ہیں۔ اس جگہ امام محمد النے کو مثال میں پیش کرنا درست نہیں کیونکہ امام محمد قرون ثلثہ میں ہیں، تبع تابعین میں ہیں، قرون ثلثہ کے بعد کے لوگوں میں نہیں ہیں۔
رحمة
وقال الشافعى الله لا اقبل : - امام شافعی سے فرماتے ہیں کہ میں صرف صحابہ کے مراسیل قبول کرتا ہوں، ان کے بعد والوں کے نہیں، البتہ اگر حجت قطعیہ یا قیاس صحیح وغیرہ سے ان مراسیل کی تائید ہو جائے تو وہ مقبول ہیں، امام شافعی اللہ نے اپنے قول لا اقبل سے سعید بن المسیب ( جو کہ تابعی ہیں ) کے مراسیل کا استثناء کیا اور فرمایا کہ صحابہ کے بعد کے لوگوں میں صرف سعید بن المسیب کے مراسیل قبول کرتا ہوں، وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ جب میں
نے ان کے مراسیل کی تحقیق کی تو سب مراسیل کو مسانید پایا، اور مسند کو قبول کرنے میں تامل نہ ہونا چاہیے، تو گو یا سعید بن مسیب کے مراسیل من وجہ مرسل اور من وجہ مسند ہوئے، پس جہت اسناد کو ترجیح دیکر قبول کر لیا گیا۔ فائدہ: - مرسل کی چوتھی قسم من وجہ مرسل من وجہ مسند، عام علماء کے نزدیک مقبول ہے، کیونکہ مرسل راوی کے حال سے ساکت ہے اور مسند راوی کے حال کو بتاتی ہے، تو ان دونوں میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہے، لہذا اسناد کو ارسال پر غلبہ دیکر قبول کر لیں گے جیسے " لا نکاح الا بولی " اس کو اسرائیل ابن یونس نے مسند ا روایت کیا ہے اور شعبہ نے مرسلاً بیان کیا ہے، یہ چوتھی قسم ہے جس کو مصنف نے متن میں ذکر نہیں کیا ہے۔
He narrates hadith, unlike musnad where the narrator does not have complete confidence; therefore he does not take it upon himself but rather mentions his teacher's name and attributes the hadith to his teacher, freeing himself from responsibility. But this is a kind of excellence: it is an answer to an objection which is that since mursal is superior to musnad, and musnad has three types—mutawatir, mashhur, ahad—and mursal is higher than musnad, then at least it would be of the medium level, i.e., mashhur, and abrogation of the Book of Allah by mashhur is permissible, so it should be permissible by mursal. The answer is that the superiority of mursal over musnad is established by ijtihad and opinion, so abrogation is not permissible, lest abrogation of the Book of Allah by opinion and qiyas become necessary, unlike mashhur musnad whose superiority is established by text, not by opinion and ijtihad, so abrogation and addition to the Book of Allah by mashhur is permissible. As for the mursal of those after these (Sahaba, Tabi'un, and Tabi' al-Tabi'in), there is disagreement among Hanafi scholars themselves regarding acceptance. Some Hanafi scholars like Imam al-Karkhi say they will be accepted because the reason for accepting the mursal of the first three generations, i.e., their being just, also exists in later people. Some Hanafi mashayikh like Isa ibn Aban say they will not be accepted because the time after the first three generations is a time of sin and immorality, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not testify to their justice; he only testified for three generations: 'The best of generations is my generation, then those who follow them, then those who follow them.' Unless the trustworthy narrate: The author says that the disagreement about the mursal of those after the first three generations is only when trustworthy people do not narrate their mursal; if trustworthy people narrate their mursal as they narrate their musnad, then their mursal will be accepted by consensus like Imam Muhammad and those like him. But mentioning Imam Muhammad as an example here is incorrect because Imam Muhammad is among the first three generations, among the Tabi' al-Tabi'in, not among those after them. And al-Shafi'i said: I do not accept mursal: Imam Shafi'i says that I only accept the mursal of the Sahaba, not of those after them, unless it is supported by a definitive proof or sound analogy. Imam Shafi'i excluded Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab (a Tabi'i) from his statement 'I do not accept' and said that among those after the Sahaba, I only accept the mursal of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab because when I investigated his mursal, I found all of them to be musnad, and there should be no hesitation in accepting musnad. So his mursal is mursal from one perspective and musnad from another, so the aspect of isnad was given preference and accepted. Benefit: The fourth type of mursal, which is mursal from one perspective and musnad from another, is accepted by general scholars because the mursal is silent about the narrator's state while the musnad informs about it, so there is no contradiction; therefore we give the isnad precedence over the irsal and accept it, such as 'No marriage without a guardian' narrated by Isra'il ibn Yunus as musnad and by Shu'bah as mursal. This is the fourth type that the author did not mention in the text.
Source pages p. 179

Commentary
This passage addresses the status of mursal hadith and its acceptability. The author first responds to an objection that if mursal is superior to musnad, it should be equivalent to mashhur and thus capable of abrogating the Quran. The response clarifies that mursal's superiority comes from ijtihad, not from explicit text, so it cannot abrogate. The discussion then focuses on the acceptance of mursal from narrators after the first three generations (Sahaba, Tabi'un, Tabi' al-Tabi'in). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam al-Karkhi accepts them based on the same 'illa (reason) of justice, while Isa ibn Aban rejects them because the Prophet only praised the first three generations. The author (the matn writer) resolves that if trustworthy narrators report their mursal, it is accepted. Imam Shafi'i's stricter position is presented: he only accepts mursal from Sahaba, except for Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab because his reports are found to have chains. Finally, a fourth type of mursal is introduced—one that is also musnad from another angle—which is accepted due to the stronger aspect of isnad. The passage is a typical Hanafi usul al-hadith discussion showing how different usul principles affect the acceptance of reports.

Key Terms
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where the narrator omits the Companion and directly attributes to the Prophet
مسند (musnad): A hadith with a complete chain reaching the Prophet
قرون ثلثہ (qurūn thalātha): The first three generations: Sahaba, Tabi'un, and Tabi' al-Tabi'in

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position presented, under what condition is the mursal of a narrator after the first three generations accepted?
A) It is always accepted because the 'illa of justice continues.
B) It is accepted only if the narrator is from the first three generations.
C) It is accepted if trustworthy narrators transmit it in the same way as musnad.
D) It is accepted only if it is supported by a definitive proof from the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis accept mursal from later generations if trustworthy narrators transmit it; otherwise, there is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Mastur al-Hal's Report: Two Hanafi Narrations
Internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on mastur al-hal's report

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on mastur al-hal's report about water impurity and identify the mufta bihi view with its thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Mastur al-hal's report on water impurity: one narration says like adil, another like fasiq; the correct view is like fasiq.

In Hanafi usul, not all narrations from the founding imams carry equal weight. This passage presents a classic internal ikhtilaf: how to treat the report of a person whose justice is unknown (mastur al-hal) when he declares water impure. Two transmitted views are weighed, and the author rules in favor of one, teaching us the method of tarjih within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two narrations
Note the two reports: (1) Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa: mastur is like adil. (2) Imam Muhammad in Kitab al-Istihsan: mastur is like fasiq.
Both are from authoritative sources within the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Work out the practical consequence: if mastur is like adil, his report is accepted → must do tayammum. If like fasiq, report is rejected → wudu is allowed.
This difference affects daily worship.
3
Analyze the tarjih mechanism
The author explicitly declares the second view (mastur like fasiq) as sahih (correct). This is an internal tarjih; no external madhhab objection.
Tarjih here relies on the statement of Imam Muhammad and the principle of caution in accepting reports without clear justice.
4
Apply the mufta bihi view
Conclude that until a mastur al-hal's justice is apparent, his report on water impurity is not credible, so one may perform wudu with that water.
This is the operative position for fatwa.

وَرَوَى الْحَسَنُ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ أَنَّهُ مِثْلُ الْعَدْلِ فِيْمَا يُخْبِرُ عَنْ نَجَاسَةِ الْمَاءِ وَذَكَرَ فِي كِتَابِ الْإِسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّهُ مِثْلُ الْفَاسِقُ فِيْهِ وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ
ترجمہ : ۔ اور حسن بن زیاد نے امام ابوحنیفہ عالیہ سے روایت کی ہے کہ مستور عادل کے مانند ہے اس خبر میں جو حمة يه وہ نجاست ماء کے بارے میں دیتا ہے، اور امام محمد نے مبسوط کے کتاب الاستحسان میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ مستور اس بارے میں فاسق کے مانند ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے۔
تشریح:- مصنف عالی ایک فقہی مسئلہ بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ نماز کا وقت آگیا اور ایک برتن میں پانی ہے، اس کے علاوہ پانی نہیں ہے ، اب کسی عادل نے خبر دی کہ ناپاک ہے تو اس کی خبر معتبر ہوگی ، لہذا اس پانی سے وضو نہیں کیا جائے گا، بلکہ تیم کر کے نماز ادا کرے اور اگر فاسق نے خبر دی کہ ناپاک ہے تو اس کی خبر غیر معتبر ہے، لہذا اس سے وضو کرنا جائز ہے لیکن اگر خبر دینے والا مستور الحال ہے، اس کا عادل و فاسق ہونا معلوم نہیں ہے تو حسن بن زیاد نے امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت کرتے ہوئے مستور کو عادل کے مثل قرار دیا ہے، لہذا عادل کی طرح مستور کی خبر معتبر ہوگی تو اس پانی سے وضونہ ہوگا بلکہ تیم کیا جائے گا، اور امام محمد عالیہ نے مبسوط کے کتاب الاستحسان میں مستور کو فاسق کے ساتھ لاحق کیا ہے، لہذا فاسق کی طرح مستور کی خبر غیر معتبر ہوگی تو اس پانی سے وضو کرنا جائز ہوگا ، مصنف یہ کہتے ہیں یہی صحیح ہے کہ مستور فاسق کے ساتھ لاحق ہو، لہذا جب تک اس کی عدالت ظاہر نہ ہو جائے اس کی خبر پر اعتماد نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he (mastur) is like the just (adil) regarding what he reports about the impurity of water. And he (Imam Muhammad) mentioned in Kitab al-Istihsan that he (mastur) is like the sinner (fasiq) in that, and this is correct. Translation: And Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa (may he be exalted) that mastur is like the just in the report he gives about the impurity of water. And Imam Muhammad mentioned in al-Mabsut, Kitab al-Istihsan, that mastur in this regard is like the fasiq, and this is correct. Commentary: The author (may he be exalted) is presenting a fiqhi issue: the time for prayer has come, and there is water in a vessel, no other water. If a just person reports that it is impure, his report is credible, so wudu will not be performed with that water, rather tayammum and then prayer. If a fasiq reports that it is impure, his report is not credible, so it is permissible to do wudu with it. But if the informant is mastur al-hal, whose being adil or fasiq is unknown, then according to what Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa, mastur is considered like the just, so his report is credible like that of a just person, and wudu will not be done with that water, rather tayammum will be performed. And according to Imam Muhammad (may he be exalted) in al-Mabsut, Kitab al-Istihsan, mastur is attached to the fasiq, so his report is not credible like that of a fasiq, and it is permissible to do wudu with that water. The author says that this (the view that mastur is like fasiq) is correct, so as long as his justice is not apparent, his report will not be relied upon.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage discusses an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the status of a mastur al-hal (person whose justice is unknown) when he reports the impurity of water. Two narrations are presented: (1) from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa, stating that such a person is treated like an adil (just person), so his report is accepted and one must perform tayammum, not wudu. (2) from Imam Muhammad in Kitab al-Istihsan, stating that he is treated like a fasiq (sinner), so his report is not accepted and one may perform wudu. The author (the commentator) declares the second view as correct (sahih), meaning the relied-upon position is that mastur al-hal is like a fasiq until his justice becomes apparent. This is a classic example of how Hanafi fiqh handles conflicting transmissions within the madhhab, preferring the view that aligns with usul principles of caution in accepting reports.

Key Terms
مستور الحال (mastur al-hal): A person whose justice or sinfulness is unknown.
نجاسة الماء (najasat al-ma'): Impurity of water, a specific fiqhi issue.
كتاب الاستحسان (Kitab al-Istihsan): A book by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, part of al-Mabsut, dealing with rulings based on istihsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Like a just person's report; wudu is not allowed
B) Like a sinner's report; wudu is allowed
C) It is ignored completely
D) One must always perform tayammum

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that a mastur al-hal's report about water impurity is not credible; the water remains pure and wudu is valid.

The Role of Taharri and Zann Ghalib in Acting on Reports (Tayammum Case)
Ruling with proof about tayammum based on taharri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish which reporters' information may be acted upon after taharri and explain the basis of the ruling according to Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Tayammum after a report of water impurity is based on the individual's strong presumption (zann ghalib), not on the reporter's moral or legal standing.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: a person needs to perform ablution but receives a report that the water is impure. The Hanafi school allows tayammum under certain conditions, but the legal basis is nuanced. The key is understanding when personal investigation (taharri) is required and whose report can trigger it. We will see that the ruling hinges on the individual's own conviction, not the reporter's reliability, and that different reporters—fasiq, child, or disbeliever—are treated differently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act is performing tayammum when water is believed to be impure. The condition is a report from someone about the impurity.
2
Locate the basis (illa)
The passage states that the permissibility of tayammum is due to the individual's strong presumption (zann ghalib) after taharri, not due to the fasiq's report itself.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position: the legal cause is the personal conviction, not the incoming report.
3
Contrast the treatment of reporters
For a fasiq, taharri is wajib. For a child, disbeliever, or insane person, taharri is not legally binding; their report cannot form the basis for conviction in matters of worship.
This shows a hierarchy of reliability: the school considers such reporters' testimony as non-binding in worship contexts.
4
Analyze the exception
If the person discards the water after receiving the non-binding report, tayammum becomes permissible because he is now factually without water.
The ruling reverts to the principle that lacking water permits tayammum, regardless of how that state came about.
5
Extract the usul rule
The general rule: in matters of worship, actions are based on the individual's dominant conviction (zann ghalib) formed through legitimate means, not on reports from those lacking legal reliability.
This rule is applied to the case of tayammum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آدمی جس کو وضو کر کے نماز پڑھنی ہے وہ اپنی رائے کو فیصل بنائے تحری کرے تحری کے بعد اس کے دل میں یہ بات آئی کہ یہ خبر دینے والا سچا ہے، واقعی پانی ناپاک ہے، تو اس کو تیم کرنا جائز ہے، اور پانی کو گرانے کی بھی ضرورت نہیں ہے، اور پانی کے ہوتے ہوئے بھی یہ شخص پانی نہ پانے والا سمجھا جائے گا، اور اگر وہ پانی کو گرا دے اور تمیم کرے تو اور زیادہ احتیاط کی بات ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں یہ شخص حقیقتہ پانی کو نہ پانے والا شمار ہوگا ،مگر یہ بات یادرکھیں کہ تحری کے بعد تیم کا وجوب ، اور اس پانی سے وضو کرنا جائز نہ ہونا، فاسق کی خبر کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے بلکہ تحری کرنے والے کے ظن غالب کی وجہ سے ہے، اس کے دل کے فیصلہ کی وجہ سے ہے، اگر فاسق کی خبر پر ہوتا تو تحری واجب ہی نہ ہوتی۔ اور اگر نجاست ماء کی خبر کافر، یا بچہ یا معتوو [؟] دے رہا ہے، اور تحری کے بعد اس کے دل میں یہ بات آئی کہ یہ تینوں سچی خبر دے رہے ہیں، تو بھی یہ پانی ناپاک نہ سمجھا جائے گا ، اس سے وضو کرے گا، تیم کی اجازت نہ ہوگی، کیونکہ ان تینیوں کی خبر شرعاً معتبر نہیں ہے لیکن اگر اس نے پانی بہاد یا [؟]، پھر تم کیا تو یہ افضل ہے، کیوں کہ ان کی خبر اگر چہ معتبر نہیں ہے، مگر یہ احتمال ضرور ہے کہ وہ اپنی خبر میں بچے ہوں، اور پانی واقعی ناپاک ہو، مگر جب پانی بہادیا تو اب یہ شخص حقیقتا پانی نہ پانے والا ہو گیا، لہذا بلاتر در تیم جائز ہوگا۔
A person who needs to perform ablution and then pray should make his opinion decisive and perform taharri. After taharri, if it occurs in his heart that this informant is truthful and the water is actually impure, then tayammum is permissible for him, and there is no need to discard the water. Even with water present, he will be considered as one not having water. And if he discards the water and performs tayammum, that is more precautionary, because in that case he will be counted as truly not having water. But remember: the obligation of tayammum after taharri and the impermissibility of using that water for ablution are not due to the report of the fasiq, but due to the strong presumption (zann ghalib) of the one performing taharri, due to the decision of his heart. If it were based on the fasiq's report, taharri would not be obligatory. And if the report of impurity of water is given by a disbeliever, a child, or an insane person [?], and after taharri it occurs in his heart that these three are giving a true report, then still the water will not be considered impure; he will perform ablution with it, and tayammum will not be permitted, because the report of these three is not legally reliable. But if he discards the water and then performs tayammum, that is better, because even though their report is not reliable, there is a possibility that they are truthful in their report and the water is actually impure. When he discards the water, then he has truly become without water, so without delay tayammum is permissible.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of a report about the impurity of water for the purpose of tayammum. The key principle is that tayammum is based on the personal conviction (zann ghalib) of the individual, not on the inherent reliability of the reporter. If a fasiq (sinner) reports impurity, the individual must perform taharri (investigation) to form a conviction; the taharri itself is wajib. If a child, disbeliever, or insane person reports, their report is not legally considered in matters of worship, so even if the individual becomes convinced, he cannot act on it regarding taharri or tayammum. However, if he discards the water, he becomes factually without water, and tayammum becomes permissible. This shows the distinction between the legal reliability of the reporter and the factual state of the individual.

Key Terms
تحری (taharri): Investigation to determine the truthfulness of a report or the actual state of affairs.
ظن غالب (zann ghalib): Predominant belief or strong presumption that shapes legal action.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking 'adalah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal basis for permissibility of tayammum after a fasiq's report?
A) The fasiq's report itself is considered reliable
B) The person's strong presumption (zann ghalib) formed after taharri
C) The lack of available water due to discarding
D) The general principle of necessity

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, acting on a report about impurity hinges on the individual's legally formed presumption (zann ghalib), which is only validly formed through taharri when the reporter is a fasiq, but not when the reporter is a child, disbeliever, or insane person.

Acceptance of Narration from Ahl al-Hawa (People of Desires)
Stating the relied-upon madhhab on rejecting narrations from propagators of heresy and classifying types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on accepting narrations from ahl al-hawa, distinguish between propagators and non-propagators, and apply the categorization to determine the acceptance or rejection of their riwayah and shahadah.

Core Idea
The narration of a propagator of heresy is rejected because his zeal leads to fabrication.

In Hanafi usul, the reliability of a narrator is paramount. This passage addresses a specific category: people of desires (ahl al-hawa) who deviate from orthodox beliefs and actively propagate their views. The relied-upon position rejects their narrations due to the inherent risk of fabrication to support their sect. However, not all such individuals are treated equally; the text explains nuanced distinctions between those whose beliefs constitute kufr and those who remain within the fold of Islam, and between riwayah (narration) and shahadah (testimony). Let us unpack this important rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
Read the first sentence: the relied-upon madhhab is that the narration of one who adopts desire as religion and calls people to it is not accepted.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Recognize the rational proof (dalil aqli)
The text provides the cause: arguing and calling to desire lead to fabrication. Thus, such a person cannot be trusted with the hadith of the Prophet.
This is a rational evidence, not a textual one.
3
Distinguish the two categories of ahl al-hawa
The fa'idah (benefit) divides ahl al-hawa into: (1) those whose beliefs reach kufr (e.g., extremist rawafid, Qadianis), and (2) those who remain within the fold of Islam (beliefs not reaching kufr).
The ruling differs for each category.
4
Examine the ikhtilaf for non-kufr ahl al-hawa
For the second type, there is disagreement: some reject both riwayah and shahadah; the jumhur accept shahadah but differ on riwayah; Sahib al-Husami conditions rejection on open propagation and bias.
This demonstrates the nuanced Hanafi approach.
5
Apply the categorization
Using the distinctions, determine for a given scenario: does the person propagate? Have their beliefs reached kufr? What type of report (riwayah or shahadah) is being considered?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا صَاحِبَ الْهَوَى فَالْمَذْهَبْ الْمُخْتَارْ أنه لا تُقْبَلْ رِوَايَةُ مَنْ إِنْتَحَلَ الْهَوى وَدَعَا النَّاسَ إِلَيْهِ لانَ الْمَحَاجَةَ وَالدَّعْوَةَ إِلَى الْهَوَى سَبَبْ دَاعِ إِلَى التَقَولِ فَلَا يُؤْتَمَنْ عَلَى حَدِيثِ رَسُولِ الله صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ-. ترجمہ : ۔ اور بہر حال نفسانی خواہش والا تو مذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ اس شخص کی روایت قبول نہیں کی جائے گی جس نے خواہشات نفسانی کو دین بنالیا ہو، اور لوگوں کو اس کی جانب دعوت دیتا ہو، اس لئے کہ اس کا حجت پکڑنا اور خواہشات کی طرف دعوت دینا ایسا سبب ہے جو داعی ہے بات کو گھڑنے کی طرف تو اس پر اعتماد نہیں کیا جائے گا رسول اللہ صلی ال اسلام کی حدیث کے بارے میں ۔ تشریح : جو شخص خواہش نفس کا پجاری ہو، اور اہل حق کے عقائد سے ہٹ کر خواہشات نفسانی کو اپنا دین و مذہب بنالیا ہو، اور لوگوں کو اپنے مذہب کی دعوت و ترغیب بھی دیتا ہو اور اپنے دین و مذہب کی حقانیت پر حجت بازی کرتا ہو، ایسا آدمی اگر حدیث روایت کرے تو مذہب مختار یہ ہے کہ اس کی روایت قبول نہیں کیجائے گی جیسے غالی روافض ، قادیانی وغیرہ کیونکہ ان کا اپنے دین کو حق سمجھنا اور اہل حق کے ساتھ بحث و مباحثہ کرنا ، یہ ان کو حدیثیں گھڑنے تک پہنچائے گا، تو ایسے لوگوں پر حدیث رسول کے بارے میں کیسے اعتماد کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ فائدہ : - اہل ہوی دو طرح کے ہیں ، بعض وہ ہیں جن کے عقائد کفر تک پہنچ چکے ہیں، جیسے خالی روافض ، فرقۂ مجسمہ، قادیانی، ان کے بارے میں بعض اہل اصول کہتے ہیں کہ ان کی روایت و شہادت سب مقبول ہیں کیونکہ یہ اہل قبلہ ہیں اور اپنے آپ کو مسلمان سمجھتے ہیں، لیکن محققین علماء اس پر متفق ہیں کہ یہ کافر ہیں، ان کی روایت و شہادت سب نا قابل قبول ہیں۔ دوسرے وہ جن کے عقائد کفر تک نہ پہنچے ہوں ، تو ان کے بارے میں علماء کی ایک جماعت کہتی ہے کہ ان کی روایت و شہادت سب مردود ہیں، کیونکہ یہ فاسق ہیں جن کو جھوٹ اور گناہوں کی پروا نہیں ہے ، مگر جمہور کا مسلک یہ ہے کہ شہادت تو قبول ہوگی مگر روایت میں بعض کے نزدیک مطلقا قبول ہے، اور بعض علماء جن میں صاحب حسامی بھی ہے کہ اگر وہ متعصب ہے اور اس نے اپنی خواہشات کو دین و مذہب بنالیا ہے اور لوگوں کو کھلے عام اس کی دعوت بھی دے رہا ہے تو اس کی خبر معتبر نہ ہوگی۔
And as for the person of desire (sahib al-hawa), the relied-upon madhhab is that the narration of one who adopts desire as his religion and calls people to it is not accepted, because arguing and calling to desire is a cause that leads to fabrication; so he cannot be trusted with the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. Translation: And in any case, regarding the person of vain desire, the chosen madhhab is that the narration of a person who has made vain desires his religion and calls people to it will not be accepted, because his holding an argument and calling to desires is a cause that leads to fabrication; so he will not be trusted concerning the hadith of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. Elaboration: A person who worships his vain desire, who deviates from the beliefs of the people of truth and makes his vain desires his religion and faith, and also invites and encourages people to his religion and argues for the truthfulness of his religion—if such a person narrates a hadith, the chosen madhhab is that his narration will not be accepted, like the extremist rawafid, qadianis, etc., because their considering their religion as true and debating with the people of truth will lead them to fabricate hadiths. So how can trust be placed in such people regarding the hadith of the Messenger? Benefit: Ahl al-hawa are of two types: Some are those whose beliefs have reached kufr, like the ghali rawafid, the Mujassima sect, Qadianis. Regarding them, some usul scholars say their narration and testimony are all acceptable because they are ahl al-qibla and consider themselves Muslims. But the verifying scholars agree that they are disbelievers; their narration and testimony are all unacceptable. The second type are those whose beliefs have not reached kufr. Regarding them, a group of scholars says that both their narration and testimony are rejected because they are fasiqs who do not care about lying and sins. But the majority view is that their testimony will be accepted, but regarding narration, some hold it absolutely accepted, and some scholars, including Sahib al-Husami, hold that if the person is biased and has made his desires his religion and openly calls people to it, then his report is not credible.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage states the Hanafi rule on accepting narrations from ahl al-hawa (people of heretical desires). The relied-upon (mukhtar) position is that the narration of those who adopt desire as a religion and propagate it is rejected because their zeal leads to fabricating hadith to support their views. The commentator expands by giving examples like extremist rawafid and Qadianis (whose beliefs amount to disbelief), thus their narration and testimony are both rejected. A benefit (fa'idah) further categorizes ahl al-hawa into two: those whose beliefs reach kufr (majority of verifying scholars consider them kafir, rejecting all their reports), and those whose beliefs do not reach kufr. For the latter, there is ikhtilaf: some reject both narration and testimony because they are fasiq; the jumhur (majority) accept their testimony but differ on narration. Sahib al-Husami's position is that if the person is biased and openly propagates his desires, his report is not credible. This shows the nuanced Hanafi approach: not all ahl al-hawa are treated the same; the degree of deviation and propagation matters.

Key Terms
صاحب الهوى (ṣāḥib al-hawā): A person who adopts his vain desires as religion and calls others to it, potentially leading to fabrication.
رواية (riwāyah): Narration or transmission of hadith; distinct from testimony (shahadah) in legal contexts.
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony in court; in this context, the jumhur accept it from non-kafir ahl al-hawa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon madhhab, when is the narration of a person of desire (sahib al-hawa) rejected?
A) Always rejected regardless of propagation
B) Rejected if he adopts desire as religion and calls people to it
C) Accepted if he does not propagate
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul rejects the narration of a propagator of heresy due to the rational risk of fabrication, but allows acceptance of testimony and narration from non-propagators, with nuanced scholarly differences.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Tartib al-Hujaj and Taqrir al-Asl
Explains the order of proofs and the principle of taqrir al-asl in case of insoluble conflict

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the order of proofs (tartib al-hujaj) when conflicts arise and identify when taqrir al-asl becomes obligatory, using the case of su'r al-himar as a model.

Core Idea
When all proofs conflict at every level, we return to the original ruling before the proofs — taqrir al-asl.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, conflicts between proofs are resolved by turning to a higher or different type of proof in a fixed order. But what happens when every level of proof is itself conflicted? The classical scholars teach us that in such a case, we do not pick arbitrarily; we revert to the original legal state before any proof arrived. This lesson unpacks that principle and its application to a classic problematic case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflict and its level
Determine which two proofs are in conflict (e.g., two verses, two hadiths, etc.) and note they are of equal strength.
The conflict (ta'arud) must be genuine – both proofs are equally strong.
2
Apply tartib al-hujaj to find a non-conflicting proof
Use the hierarchical order: when two verses conflict, turn to Sunnah; two Sunnahs conflict, turn to qawl sahabi then qiyas (or qiyas then qawl sahabi per some). Select a proof of a different type that is not itself in conflict.
The dominant Hanafi order places qawl sahabi before qiyas.
3
Check for multiple-level conflict
If the next type of proof also has conflict (e.g., qawl sahabi are also conflicting), continue to the next type. If all types are conflicted, recourse to any later proof becomes impossible.
This is the condition for taqrir al-asl: ta'azzur (impossibility of recourse).
4
Apply taqrir al-asl
When recourse is impossible, set aside all conflicting proofs and return to the original ruling that existed before any of these proofs came. This is the established principle (asl).
The original ruling is certain; doubt from conflicting proofs does not overturn certainty.
5
Work through the example of su'r al-himar
See how conflicts exist at every level: hadith, qawl sahabi, and qiyas. Since no recourse is possible, taqrir al-asl says water remains pure. However, due to the doubt, it does not remove hadath, requiring tayammum as well.
This illustrates both the application and a nuance: the pure-yet-doubtful status.

مشکوک کہا جاتا ہے۔
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi 205. Urdu commentary of Al-Muntakhab al-Husami. They (in these cases) analogy will be given precedence. The author says: 'On the order of proofs' meaning that the order which exists among proofs will be considered; that is, when two verses conflict, one turns to the Sunnah, and when two Sunnahs conflict, one turns to the sayings of the Companions, then to analogy, and according to some, among whom is the author of al-Husami, to analogy then to the sayings of the Companions. An example of conflict between two Sunnahs is the hadith of Abu Dawood from Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As that the Messenger of Allah (saw) prayed the eclipse prayer and in each rak'ah he made one bow and two prostrations. Opposing this is another hadith narrated from Aisha (ra) that the Prophet (saw) prayed four rak'ahs with four bows and four prostrations, i.e., in each rak'ah two bows and two prostrations. So there was conflict between the two hadiths. Therefore, to resolve the conflict we turned to analogy, and by analogy to other prayers, we said that in the eclipse prayer also there will be one bow and two prostrations in each rak'ah. The author says that recourse to later proofs is only when possible; if not possible, then recourse is not valid, rather taqrir al-usul (establishing the principle) becomes obligatory. He is explaining this further. 'Because conflict cancels (the proofs)': he is explaining the evidence of conflict: when two proofs conflict, both proofs fall because they repel each other due to conflict. Then recourse is made to later proofs that are not of the same type as these two conflicting proofs, like when two verses conflict, recourse is made to Sunnah, and Sunnah is not of the type of verses. Similarly for other proofs. 'And when recourse is impossible': if when two verses conflict it is difficult to turn to a third proof, such that there is also conflict between two Sunnahs, between the sayings of the Companions, and between two analogies, then taqrir al-usul becomes obligatory, i.e., everything is left in its original state, i.e., the ruling that was before the conflict is maintained. For example, in the matter of donkey's (su'r) water, there are conflicting proofs. There is the hadith of Jabir (ra) that the Messenger of Allah (saw) was asked about the leftover water of donkeys, whether one can perform wudu with it, and he said yes. From this hadith it is known that the leftover is pure. And there is another hadith from Anas (ra) that the Messenger of Allah (saw) forbade the meat of domestic donkeys and said it is impure. From this hadith it is known that the leftover is impure because whatever meat is impure, its leftover is also impure. In the matter of donkey, the sayings of the Companions are also conflicting: Ibn Umar (ra) says that donkey's leftover is impure, and Ibn Abbas (ra) says that a donkey that eats fodder and straw, its leftover is pure. And in the matter of donkey, analogies are also conflicting: if we analogize to sweat, the leftover should be pure because donkey's sweat is pure; if we analogize to donkey's milk, the leftover will be impure. Also, we cannot say it is impure by analogizing donkey's leftover to dog's leftover because the need for donkeys is greater and for dogs there is no need. And we cannot say it is pure by analogizing to cat's leftover because the need for cats is greater than for donkeys. Now if we analogize donkey to a (domestic?) animal and say pure, or analogize to dog and say impure, this would be establishing an analogy without a common cause, and this is invalid because analogy without a cause has no capacity to initially prove a ruling. In any case, when proofs are conflicting in the matter of donkey, taqrir al-usul becomes obligatory, i.e., the state before the proofs is considered. And the leftover of donkey was originally pure before the proofs, because water is pure by its nature. Therefore, due to conflict, it will not become impure, because the contamination of donkey's saliva creates doubt about impurity, and based on the original state, the purity of water is certain, and certainty is not removed by doubt. So if there is no other water, using it for wudu is necessary. However, this water will not remove the state of ritual impurity (hadath) of a person, because a person's hadath is certain, and the purity of the water is doubtful, and doubt does not remove certainty. Therefore, it will not remove hadath. To remove hadath, along with wudu from this water, tayammum is also necessary. The leftover of donkey is called mashkuk (doubtful) because of the conflicting proofs and the ambiguity of the ruling.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is an elaboration of the principles of conflict and preference (ta'arud and tarjih) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. It first establishes the order of proofs (tartib al-hujaj) when conflict arises: when two Quranic verses conflict, recourse is to the Sunnah; when two Sunnah texts conflict, recourse is to the sayings of the Companions (aqwal al-sahaba), then to analogy (qiyas). However, the author notes a difference of opinion: some, including the author of al-Husami, place qiyas before the sayings of the Companions. This is an internal Hanafi dispute regarding the hierarchy, though the dominant Hanafi view places qawl sahabi before qiyas. The example of the eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) illustrates conflict between two hadiths: one from Abdullah ibn Amr indicating one bow per rak'ah, another from Aisha indicating two bows per rak'ah. Since both are of the same type (Sunnah), one cannot use another Sunnah to resolve; so one turns to qiyas, analogizing the eclipse prayer to regular prayers, concluding one bow per rak'ah. The passage then clarifies a crucial condition: recourse to a later proof (like qiyas) is only valid when possible. If later proofs are also in conflict (i.e., if there is multiple-level conflict at the level of Sunnah, qawl sahabi, and qiyas), then one cannot simply pick one; instead, taqrir al-asl (returning to the original ruling) becomes obligatory. This means the ruling is left as it was before the conflicting proofs arrived. To illustrate, it presents the famous case of su'r al-himar (donkey's leftover water). Here, conflicts occur at every level: hadith (one indicating purity, another indicating impurity via prohibition of meat), sayings of the Companions (Ibn Umar says impure, Ibn Abbas says pure under certain conditions), and qiyas (analogizing to sweat gives purity, analogizing to milk gives impurity; analogies to dog or cat are rejected due to lack of common cause or difference in need). Since no level of proof can resolve the conflict, the principle of taqrir al-asl applies: water is originally pure, so it remains pure. However, the passage adds a practical nuance: while the water is considered pure enough for wudu when no other water is available, it does not remove hadath (ritual impurity) because hadath is certain and the water's purity is only presumed due to conflict. So one must perform both wudu and tayammum. This ruling is based on the principle that certainty cannot be removed by doubt (al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk). The passage concludes by terming this case 'mashkuk' (doubtful).

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict between two proofs such that each demands an opposite ruling for the same case at the same time, and they are equal in strength.
ترتیب الحجج (tartib al-hujaj): The hierarchical order in which proofs are consulted when conflict arises: Quran, then Sunnah, then qawl sahabi, then qiyas (with dispute on the last two).
تقریر الاصول (taqrir al-usul): The principle of returning to the original ruling (asl) when all proofs conflict and no recourse is possible; the original state before revelation is considered.
سور حمار (su'r al-himar): The leftover water (or liquid) from a donkey after it has drunk; in this context, it is considered mashkuk (doubtful) due to conflicting proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of su'r al-himar (donkey's leftover water), after conflicting hadiths, conflicting qawl sahabi, and conflicting qiyas, what is the final ruling according to the principle explained?
A) It is impure because one of the hadiths indicates impurity.
B) It is pure and can be used for wudu only, but tayammum is also required because it is doubtful.
C) It is pure and can fully remove hadath because water is originally pure.
D) It is impure because of qiyas with dog's leftover.

Key Takeaway
When all proofs at every level conflict and recourse is impossible, the ruling returns to the original state (taqrir al-asl), as illustrated by su'r al-himar.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate

Rukn and Shart of Ta'arud (Conflict of Proofs)
Explaining the conditions for true ta'arud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rukn (equality in strength) and shart (unity of time and subject) of ta'arud and apply them to determine whether a true conflict exists between two proof texts.

Core Idea
True conflict in usul requires equality in strength and unity of time and subject.

In this opening section, the commentator clarifies that for two proofs to be in actual conflict (ta'arud), they must be equal in strength (the rukn) and must address opposite rulings on the same subject at the same time (the shart). Without these conditions, there is no conflict—only a need for tarjih (preference) or a recognition that the proofs govern different contexts.

Guided Path
1
Define rukn and shart in usul
Distinguish the intrinsic element (rukn) of ta'arud from its conditions (shurut). The rukn is equality in strength; the shart includes unity of time and subject.
The rukn is what makes the concept what it is; the shart is necessary for its realization.
2
Identify the rukn of ta'arud
State that both proofs must be equal in qawwa (strength). If one is stronger (e.g., mutawatir vs. ahad), there is no conflict, only tarjih.
Examples: mutawatir vs. mashhur, mashhur vs. khabar wahid, 'amm vs. khass—inequality prevents true ta'arud.
3
Identify the shart of ta'arud
State that the two proofs must establish opposite rulings on the same subject at the same time. If time or subject differ, there is no conflict.
Time difference: wine was halal initially then haram later—no conflict. Subject difference: marriage to mahram vs. non-mahram—different subjects, no conflict.
4
Apply to given examples
Use the wine and marriage examples from the text to confirm that the conditions are not met, so no ta'arud exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
میں سور حمار میں تعارض کے وقت تو آپ نے استصحاب حال پر عمل کیا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وہ ضرورۃ کیا گیا ہے۔ ثم التعارض انما يتحقق مصنف معارضہ کا حکم بیان کرنے کے بعد رکن اور شرط کو ایک ساتھ بیان کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ تعارض متحقق ہونے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ دو حجتیں قوت میں برابر ہوں، کوئی ایک حجت ذات وصفت میں دوسری حجت سے بڑھ کر نہ ہو، ورنہ تعارض نہیں کہا جائے گا، بلکہ قوی حجت کو ضعیف پر ترجیح ہوگی، لہذا خبر متواتر اور مشہور مشہور اور خبر واحد ، عام مخصوص منہ البعض اور خاص ، ان میں مساوات نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک دوسری پر ذات کے اعتبار سے بڑھی ہوئی ہے ، لہذا تعارض ثابت نہ ہوگا تو گویا دو مجنتوں میں تساوی فی القوة رکن معارضہ ہے۔ معارضہ کی شرط یہ ہے کہ دو حجتوں میں سے ایک حجت ایک حکم کو ثابت کرتی ہو اور دوسری اس کی ضد کو ثابت کرتی ہو، اور دونوں کا وقت بھی ایک ہو محل بھی ایک ہو، ورنہ تعارض ثابت نہ ہوگا، جیسے شراب ابتدائے اسلام میں حلال تھی ،ایک حجت سے، پھر حرام ہو گئی دوسری حجت سے ، تو حلت و حرمت دونوں ثابت ہیں، مگر ایک ہی وقت میں نہیں بلکہ الگ الگ وقت ہے تو اتحاد وقت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تعارض متحقق نہ ہوگا، اسی طرح غیر محرمات سے نکاح کی حلت یک دلیل و حجت سے ثابت ہے اور محرمات سے نکاح کی حرمت دوسری دلیل سے ثابت ہے، تو حلت وحرمت دونوں کا محل الگ الگ ہے، حلت کا مل غیر محرمات ہیں، اور حرمت کا عمل محرمات ہیں تو اتحاد مل نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے معارضہ ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ وَاخْتَلَفَ مَشَائِخْنَا فِي أَنَّ خَبَرَ النَّفْيِ هَلْ يُعَارِضُ خَبَرَ الْإِثْبَاتِ أَمْ لَا وَاخْتَلَفَ عَمَلُ أَصْحَابِنَا الْمُتَقَدِ مِينَ فِي ذَلِكَ فَقَدْ رُوِيَ أَنَّ بَرِيْرَةَ أَعْتِقَتْ وَزَوْجُهَا عَبْدٌ وَرُوِيَ أَنَّهَا أُعْتِقَتْ وَزَوْجُهَا حُرِّمَعَ اِتِّفَاقِهِمْ عَلَى إِنَّهُ كَانَ عَبْدًا فَأَصْحَابُنَا اَخَذَوْا بِالْمُثْبِت وَرُوِيَ أَنَّ رَسُوْلَ الله صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ تَزَوَجَ مَيْمُوْنَةَ وَهُوَ حَلَالٌ وَرُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ تَزَوَجَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمْ وَاتَّفَقَتِ الرِّوَايَاتُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي الْحِلِ الْاَصْلِي فَجَعَلَ أَصْحَابُنَا الْعَمَلَ بِالنَّافِي أَوْلَى وَقَالُو فِي الْجَرْح وَالتَّعْدِيْلِ اَنَّ الْجَرحَ أَوْلى وَهُوَ المُثبت. ترجمہ : ۔ اور ہمارے مشائخ نے اختلاف کیا ہے اس بارے میں کہ کیا نفی کی خبر اثبات کی خبر سے معارض ہوتی ہے یا نہیں؟ اور اس بارے میں ہمارے اصحاب متقدمین کا عمل مختلف ہے، پس روایت کی گئی کہ بریرہ آزاد کی گئی اس حال میں کہ ان کے شوہر غلام تھے ، اور روایت کی گئی کہ بریرہ آزاد کی گئی اور ان کے شوہر آزاد تھے ، رواۃ کے متفق ہونے کے باوجود اس بات پر کہ ان کے شوہر غلام تھے ، تو ہمارے اصحاب نے مثبت کو اختیار کیا، اور روایت کی گئی کہ رسول اللہ صلی نیلم نے حضرت میمونہ سے نکاح کیا اس حال میں کہ آپ حلال تھے ، اور روایت کی گئی کہ آپ سائنسی اپی تم نے ان سے نکاح کیا اس حال میں کہ آپ محرم تھے ، اور روایات متفق ہیں اس پر کہ آپ سی ایم حل اصلی میں نہیں تھے، تو ہمارے اصحاب نے نافی پر عمل کو اولی قرار دیا ہے، اور مشائخ نے کہا ہے جرح و تعدیل میں کہ جرح اولی ہے اور وہ مثبت ہے۔ تشریح:- مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ ہمارے مشائخ کا اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ کیا خبر نفی اور خبر اثبات میں تعارض ہوتا ہے یا نہیں؟ شیخ ابوالحسن کرخی اور اصحاب شافعی کہتے ہیں کہ ان میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہوتا بلکہ جب نفی اور اثبات میں صورۃ تعارض ہوگا تو اثبات نفی پر مقدم ہوگا، تو حقیقہ تعارض نہیں ہوتا ہے،صورۃ ہوسکتا ہے، اور عیسی بن ابان وغیرہ کہتے ہیں کہ اثبات و نفی میں حقیقہ تعارض ہوتا ہے، خبر اثبات (مثبت) سے مراد وہ خبر ہے جو کوئی زائد چیز کو ثابت کرے جو پہلے نہیں تھی ، اور مبر نفی (نافی) سے مراد وہ خبر ہے جو اس زائد چیز کی نفی کرے اور حکم کو اپنی اصل پر باقی رکھے۔ مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ ہمارے علماء متقدمین (امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین) کا عمل اس سلسلہ میں مختلف ہے، بعض جگہ انہوں نے مثبت پر عمل کیا ہے اور بعض جگہ نافی پر، جیسے خیار عتق کے مسئلہ میں ہمارے علماء نے مثبت پر عمل کیا ہے، اور نکاح محرم کے مسئلہ میں نافی پر عمل کیا ہے۔ خیار عتق کا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ منکوحہ باندی اگر آزاد ہوئی اور اس کا شوہر آزاد ہے تو اس کو خیار عتق ملے گا یعنی چاہے تو نکاح فسخ کرے یا باقی رکھے، جیسے شوہر کے غلام ہونے کی صورت میں خیار ملتا ہے، یہ احناف کا مسلک ہے، لیکن امام شافعی کے نزدیک باندی کو خیار عتق صرف اسی صورت میں ملتا ہے جب کہ اس کا شوہر غلام ہو۔ اس سلسلہ میں دوروایتیں ہیں، پہلی روایت عروہ بن زبیر عن عائشہ ہے کہ جب بریرہ کو آزاد کیا گیا تو ان کا شوہر غلام تھا، اور حضور صلی اما پیام نے خیار عتق دیا۔ یہ حدیث نافی ہے، اس میں حریت زوج کی نفی کی گئی ہے، اور دوسری روایت اسود عن عائشہ ہے کہ بریرہ جس وقت آزاد ہوئی، ان کا شوہر اس وقت آزاد تھا۔۔ یہ حدیث مثبت ہے، اس میں حریت زوج کو ثابت کیا گیا ہے۔ اس پر تو تمام رواۃ متفق ہیں کہ بریرہ کے شوہر مغیث حقیقہ غلام تھے بعد میں آزاد ہوئے ، البتہ اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ بریرہ کے آزاد ہونے کے وقت وہ غلام تھے یا آزاد؟ احناف نے مثبت پر عمل کیا اور کہا کہ بریرہ کو خیار عتق جب ملا، اس وقت ان کے شوہر آزاد تھے، لہذا منکوحہ باندی کو شوہر کے آزاد
In the case of conflict in the case of the donkey, you acted upon istishab al-hal, and the answer is that it was done out of necessity. Then the author, after stating the ruling of mu’arada, mentions the rukn and shart together: He says that for ta’arud to be realized, it is necessary that two proofs be equal in strength, no proof superior to another in essence and attribute; otherwise it will not be called ta’arud, rather the stronger proof will be given preference over the weak. Therefore, mutawatir and mashhur, mashhur and khabar wahid, ‘amm and khass mukhassas min al-ba’d, and khass—among these there is no equality; rather one is superior to the other in essence, so ta’arud is not established. So equality in strength (tasawi fi al-quwwa) is the rukn of mu’arada. The shart of mu’arada is that one of the two proofs establishes a ruling and the other establishes its opposite, and both must be in the same time and the same subject (mahall); otherwise ta’arud will not be established. For example, wine was halal in early Islam by one proof, then became haram by another proof; so both permissibility and prohibition are established, but not at the same time, they are at separate times, so due to lack of unity of time, ta’arud is not realized. Similarly, permissibility of marriage to non-mahram women is established by one evidence, and prohibition of marriage to mahram women by another evidence; the subject of permissibility is non-mahram women, and the subject of prohibition is mahram women, so due to lack of unity of subject, mu’arada is not established. And our mashayikh differed as to whether a report of negation (khabar al-nafi) conflicts with a report of affirmation (khabar al-ithbat) or not? And the practice of our early companions (mutaqaddimin) differed in that regard. It is narrated that Barira was set free while her husband was a slave, and it is narrated that she was set free while her husband was free, despite their agreement that he was a slave. So our companions took the affirming report (muthbit). And it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) married Maymunah while he was halal (non-muhrim), and it is narrated that he married her while he was muhrim. All narrations agree that he was not in the original state of halal. So our companions considered acting upon the negating report (nafi) as more appropriate. And they said in jarh and ta’dil that jarh is more appropriate and it is the affirming report (muthbit). Translation: Our mashayikh differed on whether a negating report conflicts with an affirming report or not? And our early companions’ practice in this regard varied. So it is narrated that Barira was freed while her husband was a slave, and it is narrated that Barira was freed while her husband was free, despite the narrators’ agreement that her husband was a slave. So our companions adopted the affirming report. And it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) married Maymunah while he was halal, and it is narrated that he married her while he was muhrim. The narrations agree that he was not in the original state of halal. So our companions considered acting upon the negating report as preferable. And the mashayikh said that in jarh and ta’dil, jarh is preferable and it is the affirming report. Commentary: The author says that our mashayikh differed on whether a negating report and an affirming report conflict or not? Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and the Shafi’i scholars say there is no real conflict between them; rather when in form there is conflict, the affirming is given precedence over the negating, so there is no actual conflict; it only appears. Isa ibn Aban and others say that there is actual conflict between affirmation and negation. By khabar ithbat (muthbit) is meant a report that establishes an additional thing that was not previously there, and by khabar nafi (nafi) is meant a report that negates that additional thing and keeps the ruling on its original basis. The author says that our early scholars (Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) differed in practice: in some places they acted upon the muthbit and in others upon the nafi. For example, in the issue of khiyar al-‘itq (option of emancipation), our scholars acted upon the muthbit, and in the issue of the marriage of a muhrim, they acted upon the nafi. The issue of khiyar al-‘itq: If a married slave-woman is freed and her husband is free, she gets khiyar al-‘itq, i.e., she may either annul the marriage or keep it, just as she gets the option if the husband is a slave. This is the Hanafi position, but according to Imam al-Shafi’i, a slave-woman gets khiyar al-‘itq only when her husband is a slave. On this matter, there are two narrations: first, ‘Urwa ibn al-Zubayr from ‘A’isha that when Barira was freed, her husband was a slave, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) granted her the option. This hadith is nafi, negating the husband’s freedom. Second, al-Aswad from ‘A’isha that when Barira was freed, her husband was free. This hadith is muthbit, affirming the husband’s freedom. All narrators agree that Barira’s husband Mughith was originally a slave and later freed; the dispute is whether at the time of Barira’s emancipation he was still a slave or free. The Hanafis acted upon the muthbit, saying that when Barira got the option, her husband was free, so a married slave-woman gets the option upon her husband’s freedom.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Al-Husami, explaining the conditions for ta'arud (conflict) between two proofs. The author first clarifies the rukn (pillar) and shart (condition) of mu'arada. The rukn is equality in strength: both proofs must be of equal force; if one is stronger (e.g., mutawatir vs. ahad), there is no true conflict, only preference. The shart is that both proofs must address the same ruling and its opposite, at the same time, and regarding the same subject. Examples are given: wine's permissibility and prohibition are at different times, so no conflict; marriage to mahram and non-mahram involve different subjects, so no conflict. The passage then moves to a specific ikhtilaf: whether a hadith that negates (nafi) something can conflict with a hadith that affirms (muthbit) the same thing. The Hanafi mashayikh disagreed: Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and the Shafi'is held that there is no real conflict—affirmation always takes precedence. Isa ibn Aban and others held that true conflict occurs. The Hanafi early scholars' practice varied: in the case of Barirah's khiyar al-'itq, they preferred the affirming hadith that her husband was free at the time of her emancipation, thus granting her the option. In the case of the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah while in ihram, they preferred the negating hadith that he was halal (not in ihram), thus upholding the prohibition of muhrim marriage. This shows that the Hanafi school does not have a single rule; rather, preference is determined by contextual factors. The passage also notes that in jarh wa ta'dil, jarh (criticism) is preferred and it is considered muthbit (affirming a defect).

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'arud): Apparent conflict between two proofs that are equal in strength, addressing opposite rulings on the same subject at the same time.
ركن (rukn): The essential element of ta'arud: equality in strength between two proofs.
شرط (shart): Condition for valid ta'arud: both proofs must be opposite in ruling, same time, same subject.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the rukn of ta'arud?
A) Unity of time
B) Unity of subject
C) Equality in strength
D) Both proofs being from the Qur'an

Key Takeaway
Ta'arud requires equality, same time, same subject; otherwise there is preference, not conflict.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
advanced
12 min
The Nafi vs. Muthbit Dispute in Hanafi Usul
Dispute on conflict between nafi and muthbit reports

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi disagreement on whether a negating report (nafi) conflicts with an affirming report (muthbit), and state the thamarah al-khilaf in the case of khiyar al-'itq.

Core Idea
Early Hanafis sometimes preferred the affirming report and sometimes the negating report—context determines preference.

This passage introduces a specific ikhtilaf among Hanafi usul scholars: does a report that negates an attribute (nafi) truly conflict with a report that affirms it (muthbit)? While some, like Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, argued that affirmation always prevails (so no real conflict), Isa ibn Aban held that true conflict occurs. Importantly, the early Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) did not follow a single rule; in the case of Barirah they preferred the muthbit, and in the case of the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah they preferred the nafi. This contextual approach is a hallmark of Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
State the ikhtilaf
Recognize that the Hanafi mashayikh disagreed whether a negating report (nafi) can truly conflict with an affirming report (muthbit).
Nafi negates an additional ruling/attribute; muthbit affirms it.
2
Present the view of Karkhi and Shafi'is
They hold that there is no real conflict; affirmation always takes precedence because it adds new information. The apparent conflict is resolved by preferring the muthbit.
They consider the nafi as merely retaining the original state, so it is weaker.
3
Present the view of Isa ibn Aban
He holds that true conflict can occur between nafi and muthbit, and neither automatically prevails.
This position allows for case-by-case analysis.
4
Examine the early Hanafi practice
Analyze the two examples: Barirah's case (muthbit preferred) and the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah (nafi preferred). Show that the early imams chose based on contextual evidence, not a rigid rule.
In Barirah, despite consensus that her husband was originally a slave, the affirming hadith that he was free at emancipation was acted upon. In Maymunah's case, despite agreement that the Prophet was not in the original state of halal, the negating hadith that he was halal was preferred.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Explain the practical difference: In khiyar al-'itq, Hanafis grant a freed slave-woman the option to annul her marriage even if her husband is free (following the muthbit). Shafi'is restrict the option to cases where the husband is a slave (following the nafi).
This shows how the preference for nafi or muthbit directly affects fiqh rulings.

میں سور حمار میں تعارض کے وقت تو آپ نے استصحاب حال پر عمل کیا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ وہ ضرورۃ کیا گیا ہے۔ ثم التعارض انما يتحقق مصنف معارضہ کا حکم بیان کرنے کے بعد رکن اور شرط کو ایک ساتھ بیان کر رہے ہیں، فرماتے ہیں کہ تعارض متحقق ہونے کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ دو حجتیں قوت میں برابر ہوں، کوئی ایک حجت ذات وصفت میں دوسری حجت سے بڑھ کر نہ ہو، ورنہ تعارض نہیں کہا جائے گا، بلکہ قوی حجت کو ضعیف پر ترجیح ہوگی، لہذا خبر متواتر اور مشہور مشہور اور خبر واحد ، عام مخصوص منہ البعض اور خاص ، ان میں مساوات نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک دوسری پر ذات کے اعتبار سے بڑھی ہوئی ہے ، لہذا تعارض ثابت نہ ہوگا تو گویا دو مجنتوں میں تساوی فی القوة رکن معارضہ ہے۔ معارضہ کی شرط یہ ہے کہ دو حجتوں میں سے ایک حجت ایک حکم کو ثابت کرتی ہو اور دوسری اس کی ضد کو ثابت کرتی ہو، اور دونوں کا وقت بھی ایک ہو محل بھی ایک ہو، ورنہ تعارض ثابت نہ ہوگا، جیسے شراب ابتدائے اسلام میں حلال تھی ،ایک حجت سے، پھر حرام ہو گئی دوسری حجت سے ، تو حلت و حرمت دونوں ثابت ہیں، مگر ایک ہی وقت میں نہیں بلکہ الگ الگ وقت ہے تو اتحاد وقت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے تعارض متحقق نہ ہوگا، اسی طرح غیر محرمات سے نکاح کی حلت یک دلیل و حجت سے ثابت ہے اور محرمات سے نکاح کی حرمت دوسری دلیل سے ثابت ہے، تو حلت وحرمت دونوں کا محل الگ الگ ہے، حلت کا مل غیر محرمات ہیں، اور حرمت کا عمل محرمات ہیں تو اتحاد مل نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے معارضہ ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ وَاخْتَلَفَ مَشَائِخْنَا فِي أَنَّ خَبَرَ النَّفْيِ هَلْ يُعَارِضُ خَبَرَ الْإِثْبَاتِ أَمْ لَا وَاخْتَلَفَ عَمَلُ أَصْحَابِنَا الْمُتَقَدِ مِينَ فِي ذَلِكَ فَقَدْ رُوِيَ أَنَّ بَرِيْرَةَ أَعْتِقَتْ وَزَوْجُهَا عَبْدٌ وَرُوِيَ أَنَّهَا أُعْتِقَتْ وَزَوْجُهَا حُرِّمَعَ اِتِّفَاقِهِمْ عَلَى إِنَّهُ كَانَ عَبْدًا فَأَصْحَابُنَا اَخَذَوْا بِالْمُثْبِت وَرُوِيَ أَنَّ رَسُوْلَ الله صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ تَزَوَجَ مَيْمُوْنَةَ وَهُوَ حَلَالٌ وَرُوِيَ أَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ تَزَوَجَهَا وَهُوَ مُحْرِمْ وَاتَّفَقَتِ الرِّوَايَاتُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ فِي الْحِلِ الْاَصْلِي فَجَعَلَ أَصْحَابُنَا الْعَمَلَ بِالنَّافِي أَوْلَى وَقَالُو فِي الْجَرْح وَالتَّعْدِيْلِ اَنَّ الْجَرحَ أَوْلى وَهُوَ المُثبت. ترجمہ : ۔ اور ہمارے مشائخ نے اختلاف کیا ہے اس بارے میں کہ کیا نفی کی خبر اثبات کی خبر سے معارض ہوتی ہے یا نہیں؟ اور اس بارے میں ہمارے اصحاب متقدمین کا عمل مختلف ہے، پس روایت کی گئی کہ بریرہ آزاد کی گئی اس حال میں کہ ان کے شوہر غلام تھے ، اور روایت کی گئی کہ بریرہ آزاد کی گئی اور ان کے شوہر آزاد تھے ، رواۃ کے متفق ہونے کے باوجود اس بات پر کہ ان کے شوہر غلام تھے ، تو ہمارے اصحاب نے مثبت کو اختیار کیا، اور روایت کی گئی کہ رسول اللہ صلی نیلم نے حضرت میمونہ سے نکاح کیا اس حال میں کہ آپ حلال تھے ، اور روایت کی گئی کہ آپ سائنسی اپی تم نے ان سے نکاح کیا اس حال میں کہ آپ محرم تھے ، اور روایات متفق ہیں اس پر کہ آپ سی ایم حل اصلی میں نہیں تھے، تو ہمارے اصحاب نے نافی پر عمل کو اولی قرار دیا ہے، اور مشائخ نے کہا ہے جرح و تعدیل میں کہ جرح اولی ہے اور وہ مثبت ہے۔ تشریح:- مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ ہمارے مشائخ کا اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ کیا خبر نفی اور خبر اثبات میں تعارض ہوتا ہے یا نہیں؟ شیخ ابوالحسن کرخی اور اصحاب شافعی کہتے ہیں کہ ان میں کوئی تعارض نہیں ہوتا بلکہ جب نفی اور اثبات میں صورۃ تعارض ہوگا تو اثبات نفی پر مقدم ہوگا، تو حقیقہ تعارض نہیں ہوتا ہے،صورۃ ہوسکتا ہے، اور عیسی بن ابان وغیرہ کہتے ہیں کہ اثبات و نفی میں حقیقہ تعارض ہوتا ہے، خبر اثبات (مثبت) سے مراد وہ خبر ہے جو کوئی زائد چیز کو ثابت کرے جو پہلے نہیں تھی ، اور مبر نفی (نافی) سے مراد وہ خبر ہے جو اس زائد چیز کی نفی کرے اور حکم کو اپنی اصل پر باقی رکھے۔ مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ ہمارے علماء متقدمین (امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین) کا عمل اس سلسلہ میں مختلف ہے، بعض جگہ انہوں نے مثبت پر عمل کیا ہے اور بعض جگہ نافی پر، جیسے خیار عتق کے مسئلہ میں ہمارے علماء نے مثبت پر عمل کیا ہے، اور نکاح محرم کے مسئلہ میں نافی پر عمل کیا ہے۔ خیار عتق کا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ منکوحہ باندی اگر آزاد ہوئی اور اس کا شوہر آزاد ہے تو اس کو خیار عتق ملے گا یعنی چاہے تو نکاح فسخ کرے یا باقی رکھے، جیسے شوہر کے غلام ہونے کی صورت میں خیار ملتا ہے، یہ احناف کا مسلک ہے، لیکن امام شافعی کے نزدیک باندی کو خیار عتق صرف اسی صورت میں ملتا ہے جب کہ اس کا شوہر غلام ہو۔ اس سلسلہ میں دوروایتیں ہیں، پہلی روایت عروہ بن زبیر عن عائشہ ہے کہ جب بریرہ کو آزاد کیا گیا تو ان کا شوہر غلام تھا، اور حضور صلی اما پیام نے خیار عتق دیا۔ یہ حدیث نافی ہے، اس میں حریت زوج کی نفی کی گئی ہے، اور دوسری روایت اسود عن عائشہ ہے کہ بریرہ جس وقت آزاد ہوئی، ان کا شوہر اس وقت آزاد تھا۔۔ یہ حدیث مثبت ہے، اس میں حریت زوج کو ثابت کیا گیا ہے۔ اس پر تو تمام رواۃ متفق ہیں کہ بریرہ کے شوہر مغیث حقیقہ غلام تھے بعد میں آزاد ہوئے ، البتہ اس میں اختلاف ہے کہ بریرہ کے آزاد ہونے کے وقت وہ غلام تھے یا آزاد؟ احناف نے مثبت پر عمل کیا اور کہا کہ بریرہ کو خیار عتق جب ملا، اس وقت ان کے شوہر آزاد تھے، لہذا منکوحہ باندی کو شوہر کے آزاد
In the case of conflict in the case of the donkey, you acted upon istishab al-hal, and the answer is that it was done out of necessity. Then the author, after stating the ruling of mu’arada, mentions the rukn and shart together: He says that for ta’arud to be realized, it is necessary that two proofs be equal in strength, no proof superior to another in essence and attribute; otherwise it will not be called ta’arud, rather the stronger proof will be given preference over the weak. Therefore, mutawatir and mashhur, mashhur and khabar wahid, ‘amm and khass mukhassas min al-ba’d, and khass—among these there is no equality; rather one is superior to the other in essence, so ta’arud is not established. So equality in strength (tasawi fi al-quwwa) is the rukn of mu’arada. The shart of mu’arada is that one of the two proofs establishes a ruling and the other establishes its opposite, and both must be in the same time and the same subject (mahall); otherwise ta’arud will not be established. For example, wine was halal in early Islam by one proof, then became haram by another proof; so both permissibility and prohibition are established, but not at the same time, they are at separate times, so due to lack of unity of time, ta’arud is not realized. Similarly, permissibility of marriage to non-mahram women is established by one evidence, and prohibition of marriage to mahram women by another evidence; the subject of permissibility is non-mahram women, and the subject of prohibition is mahram women, so due to lack of unity of subject, mu’arada is not established. And our mashayikh differed as to whether a report of negation (khabar al-nafi) conflicts with a report of affirmation (khabar al-ithbat) or not? And the practice of our early companions (mutaqaddimin) differed in that regard. It is narrated that Barira was set free while her husband was a slave, and it is narrated that she was set free while her husband was free, despite their agreement that he was a slave. So our companions took the affirming report (muthbit). And it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) married Maymunah while he was halal (non-muhrim), and it is narrated that he married her while he was muhrim. All narrations agree that he was not in the original state of halal. So our companions considered acting upon the negating report (nafi) as more appropriate. And they said in jarh and ta’dil that jarh is more appropriate and it is the affirming report (muthbit). Translation: Our mashayikh differed on whether a negating report conflicts with an affirming report or not? And our early companions’ practice in this regard varied. So it is narrated that Barira was freed while her husband was a slave, and it is narrated that Barira was freed while her husband was free, despite the narrators’ agreement that her husband was a slave. So our companions adopted the affirming report. And it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) married Maymunah while he was halal, and it is narrated that he married her while he was muhrim. The narrations agree that he was not in the original state of halal. So our companions considered acting upon the negating report as preferable. And the mashayikh said that in jarh and ta’dil, jarh is preferable and it is the affirming report. Commentary: The author says that our mashayikh differed on whether a negating report and an affirming report conflict or not? Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and the Shafi’i scholars say there is no real conflict between them; rather when in form there is conflict, the affirming is given precedence over the negating, so there is no actual conflict; it only appears. Isa ibn Aban and others say that there is actual conflict between affirmation and negation. By khabar ithbat (muthbit) is meant a report that establishes an additional thing that was not previously there, and by khabar nafi (nafi) is meant a report that negates that additional thing and keeps the ruling on its original basis. The author says that our early scholars (Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) differed in practice: in some places they acted upon the muthbit and in others upon the nafi. For example, in the issue of khiyar al-‘itq (option of emancipation), our scholars acted upon the muthbit, and in the issue of the marriage of a muhrim, they acted upon the nafi. The issue of khiyar al-‘itq: If a married slave-woman is freed and her husband is free, she gets khiyar al-‘itq, i.e., she may either annul the marriage or keep it, just as she gets the option if the husband is a slave. This is the Hanafi position, but according to Imam al-Shafi’i, a slave-woman gets khiyar al-‘itq only when her husband is a slave. On this matter, there are two narrations: first, ‘Urwa ibn al-Zubayr from ‘A’isha that when Barira was freed, her husband was a slave, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) granted her the option. This hadith is nafi, negating the husband’s freedom. Second, al-Aswad from ‘A’isha that when Barira was freed, her husband was free. This hadith is muthbit, affirming the husband’s freedom. All narrators agree that Barira’s husband Mughith was originally a slave and later freed; the dispute is whether at the time of Barira’s emancipation he was still a slave or free. The Hanafis acted upon the muthbit, saying that when Barira got the option, her husband was free, so a married slave-woman gets the option upon her husband’s freedom.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on Al-Husami, explaining the conditions for ta'arud (conflict) between two proofs. The author first clarifies the rukn (pillar) and shart (condition) of mu'arada. The rukn is equality in strength: both proofs must be of equal force; if one is stronger (e.g., mutawatir vs. ahad), there is no true conflict, only preference. The shart is that both proofs must address the same ruling and its opposite, at the same time, and regarding the same subject. Examples are given: wine's permissibility and prohibition are at different times, so no conflict; marriage to mahram and non-mahram involve different subjects, so no conflict. The passage then moves to a specific ikhtilaf: whether a hadith that negates (nafi) something can conflict with a hadith that affirms (muthbit) the same thing. The Hanafi mashayikh disagreed: Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi and the Shafi'is held that there is no real conflict—affirmation always takes precedence. Isa ibn Aban and others held that true conflict occurs. The Hanafi early scholars' practice varied: in the case of Barirah's khiyar al-'itq, they preferred the affirming hadith that her husband was free at the time of her emancipation, thus granting her the option. In the case of the Prophet's marriage to Maymunah while in ihram, they preferred the negating hadith that he was halal (not in ihram), thus upholding the prohibition of muhrim marriage. This shows that the Hanafi school does not have a single rule; rather, preference is determined by contextual factors. The passage also notes that in jarh wa ta'dil, jarh (criticism) is preferred and it is considered muthbit (affirming a defect).

Key Terms
نفي (nafi): A report that negates an additional ruling or attribute, keeping the ruling on its original basis.
اثبات (ithbat): A report that affirms an additional ruling or attribute that was not previously established.
تعارض (ta'arud): Apparent conflict between two proofs that are equal in strength, addressing opposite rulings on the same subject at the same time.
خیار عتق (khiyar al-'itq): The option of a freed slave-woman to annul her marriage upon emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of Barirah, which report did the early Hanafis prefer and what was the practical result?
A) They preferred the negating report, so she did not get the option to annul.
B) They preferred the affirming report, so she got the option to annul even if her husband was free.
C) They rejected both reports and used qiyas.
D) They followed the Shafi'i view.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi usul does not have a blanket rule for nafi vs. muthbit; practice varied based on contextual evidence.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
10 min
Strength of Negative Reports vs Positive Reports
Explaining three scenarios of negative reports and their strength against positive reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three scenarios for negative reports in Hanafi usul and apply the rule to determine when a negative report conflicts with a positive report.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, a negative report based on istishab does not conflict with a positive report based on proof.

This passage lays out a fundamental Hanafi usul principle: the strength of a negative report (nafi) depends on its basis. If it rests on a proof, it is strong; if on istishab, it is weak. When the basis is unclear, we investigate. This rule resolves conflicts between contradictory reports.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of report
First, determine whether each conflicting report is affirmative (ithbat) or negative (nafi). Affirmation is always considered based on some proof. Negation may have different bases.
Ithbat is always dalil-based; nafi is the variable.
2
Classify the basis of the negative report
Determine if the negative report is based on a clear proof (dalil), on istishab (presumption of continuity), or if its basis is unknown. This classification determines its evidentiary strength.
The three scenarios correspond to these three possibilities.
3
Apply the rule for conflict
If the negative report is based on a proof, it is strong and will conflict with the positive report. If based on istishab, it is weak and does not conflict; the positive report prevails. If the basis is unknown, investigate: if it turns out to be istishab, it is weak; if based on proof, it is strong and conflicts.
No conflict means no need for tarjih; the positive is automatically taken.
4
Resolve the conflict if present
When both reports are strong, a reason for preference (tarjih) must be found. Istishab can serve as a tarjih factor even though it is not a proof. Other factors include the reliability of narrators.
In the Maimunah example, Ibn Abbas was preferred due to his accuracy.
5
Map to real examples
Connect the rule to the hadith examples: Barirah (negation based on istishab, no conflict) and Maimunah (both based on proof, conflict resolved by preferring Ibn Abbas's narration). Also apply to the water/food purity example.
These examples cement the practical application of the rule.
