اور اگر نفی کی بنیاد کسی دلیل پر نہیں ہے بلکہ استصحاب پر ہے یعنی تیسری صورت تو اس وقت نفی اور اثبات میں ایک درجہ کی قوت نہ ہوگی ، بلکہ اثبات قومی ہوگا کیونکہ دلیل پر مبنی ہے اور نفی ضعیف ہوگی کیونکہ نفلی دلیل پر مبنی نہیں ہے، لہذا تعارض نہ ہوگا بلکہ اثبات نفی پر مقدم ہوگا۔
اور اگر نفی کا حال مشتبہ ہو یعنی معلوم نہ ہو کہ اس کی بنیاد دلیل پر ہے یا استصحاب پر تو اس وقت خبر دینے والے کی حالت میں غور کریں گے، اگر یہ بات ثابت ہو جائے کہ اس نے استصحاب کو دلیل بنایا ہے تو اس کی خبر معتبر نہ ہوگی اور اگر اس کی خبر دلیل معرفت پر مبنی ہے یعنی اس نے ایسی دلیل پر اعتماد کیا ہے جو معرفت نفی کا سبب ہے تو نفی دلیل پر مبنی ہونے کی وجہ سے اثبات کی طرح قوی ہو جائے گی ، لہذا تعارض ہوگا، اور اس کے دفع کے لئے وجہ ترجیح کی ضرورت پڑے گی۔
اس قاعدہ کلیہ کے بعد مصنف" کہتے ہیں کہ خیار عشق کے مسئلہ میں حدیث بریرہ میں جو نفی ہے کہ حضور سما ہنی پریتم نے حضرت بریرہ کو خیار عشق دیا، اس حال میں کہ ان کے شوہر غلام تھے اس میں حریت کی نفی کسی دلیل پر مبنی نہیں ہے بلکہ استصحاب پر مبنی ہے یعنی وہ اصل میں غلام تھے تو اب بھی غلام ہوں گے، اور استصحاب ہمارے نزدیک حجت نہیں ہے، لہذا یہ حدیث اس دوسری حدیث کے معارض نہ ہوگی جو مثبت ہے کہ بریرہ کے شوہر آزاد تھے کیونکہ اثبات دلیل پر ہی مبنی ہوتا ہے، اور نافی بغیر دلیل کے استصحاب پر مبنی ہے، تو مثبت کو لینگے اور نافی کو چھوڑ دینگے، لہذا منکوحہ باندی کو ہر حال میں خیار عتق ملے گا، یہاں نفی کی مذکورہ تین صورتوں میں تیسری صورت ہے۔
اور حدیث میمونہ میں بھی دو روایتیں ہیں ایک نافی اور ایک مثبت ، جو نافی روایت ہے کہ رسول اللہ نے حضرت میمونہ سے نکاح کیا، اس وقت آپ محرم تھے یہ دلیل پر مبنی ہے، وہ دلیل آپ سانی یا پیہم کی جیت ہے کہ آپ کی حالت محرم جیسی تھی ، آپ سلے ہوئے کپڑوں میں نہ تھے ، حلق و قصر نہ ہوا تھا، یہ سب دلیل ہے کہ آپ محرم تھے، لہذا یہ اس دوسری روایت کے معارض ہوگی جو مثبت ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی یا پیام اس وقت حلال تھے یہ اثبات بھی دلیل پر مبنی ہے کیونکہ اثبات کسی نہ کسی دلیل سے ہوتا ہے، لہذافی اور اثبات دونوں جب دلیل پر مبنی ہیں تو تعارض ہوگا، اور اس کو دور کرنے کے لئے وجہ ترجیح کی ضرورت ہوگی، لہذا احناف نے ابن عباس کی روایت کو جو نافی ہے ترجیح دی یزید بن اصم کی روایت پر جو نافی ہے، کیونکہ ضبط واتقان میں ابن عباس کو ترجیح حاصل ہے، یہ فی کی مذکورہ تین صورتوں میں پہلی صورت ہے۔
جب نفی مشتبہ الحال ہو یعنی نفی کی دوسری صورت ، اس کی مثال طہارت ماء اور طعام وشراب کی حلت ہے تفصیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ ایک برتن میں پانی ہے، یا کھانا ہے، ایک آدمی خبر دیتا ہے کہ یہ پانی ناپاک ہے یا یہ کھانا حرام ہے، اور دوسرا آدمی خبر دیتا ہے پاک ہے، تو پہلے آدمی کی خبر مثبت ہے جس سے نجاست اور حرمت ثابت ہو رہی ہے اور خبر دلیل پر معنی ہے، کیونکہ اس نے نجاست و حرمت کا کوئی سبب دیکھا ہوگا جس کی بنیاد پر خبر دے رہا ہے، اور دوسرے آدمی کی خبر نافی ہے جس سے نجاست و حرمت کی نفی ہورہی ہے، خبر نافی کا حال مشتبہ ہے،معلوم نہیں کہ استصحاب حال کی بنا پر پاک اور حلال ہونے کی خبر دے رہا ہے، کیونکہ کھانے، پینے کی چیزوں میں اصل یہ ہے کہ وہ حلال و پاک ہوں، تو وہ اصل کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے پاک و حلال کہہ رہا ہے یا اس کی خبر دلیل پر مبنی ہے، جب اس کی خبر مشتبہ ہے، تو ہم نے تحقیق کی ، پتہ چلا کہ اصل کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے وہ پاک اور حلال کہہ رہا ہے یعنی استصحاب حال سے کہہ رہا ہے تو اس کی خبر معتبر نہ ہوگی ، رہا کیونکہ یہ نافی بغیر دلیل کے ہے، لہذا خبر نفی اور خبر اثبات میں تعارض نہ ہوگا ، بلکہ خبر اثبات پر عمل کرتے ہوئے پانی اور کھانے کو نا پاک و حرام کہا جائے گا، اور اگر تحقیق کرنے پر معلوم ہوا کہ اس کی خبر دلیل پر مبنی ہے، استصحاب سے نہیں کہہ رہا ہے ، جیسے ایک آدمی نے نہر سے پانی لیا اور اس سے بالکل جدا نہیں ہوا کہ اس میں نجاست کے گرنے کا وہم ہو پھر خبر دے رہا ہے، تو اس کی یہ خبر جس سے نجاست و حرمت کی نفی ہورہی ہے دلیل پر مبنی ہونے کی وجہ سے قوی ہوگئی ، اور اثبات کی خبر بھی جس سے نجاست و حرمت ثابت ہو رہی ہے قوی ہے، جب دونوں خبریں قوت میں ایک درجہ کی ہیں تو تعارض ہوگا، لہذا اس وقت اصل کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے پانی کو پاک اور کھانے کو حلال کہا جائے گا، اور اصل یعنی استصحاب حال کو ہی ہم وجہ ترجیح بنائیں گے، اگر چہ استصحاب حال دلیل نہیں بن سکتا لیکن مُرَج بن سکتا ہے، لہذا خبر اثبات پر ترجیح دیں گے استصحاب حال کی وجہ سے۔
And if the basis of negation is not on any proof but on istishab, i.e., the third scenario, then negation and affirmation will not be of equal strength; rather, affirmation will be strong because it is based on proof, and negation will be weak because it is not based on proof, so there will be no conflict, and affirmation will take precedence over negation. And if the state of negation is ambiguous, i.e., it is unknown whether it is based on proof or istishab, then we will consider the state of the informant: if it becomes established that he used istishab as evidence, his report will not be reliable; and if his report is based on a proof of knowledge, i.e., he relied on a proof that is the cause of knowledge of negation, then negation, being based on proof, will become as strong as affirmation, so there will be conflict, and a reason for preference will be needed to resolve it. After this general rule, the author says that in the issue of khiyar al-'itq (option of emancipation) in the hadith of Barirah, the negation that the Prophet gave Barirah the choice despite her husband being a slave - this negation of freedom is not based on any proof but on istishab: that he was originally a slave, so he would still be a slave. And istishab is not a proof according to us, so this hadith will not conflict with the other hadith which affirms that Barirah's husband was free, because affirmation is based on proof, and the negator relies on istishab without proof; so we will take the affirmative and leave the negative. Thus, the enslaved wife will get the option of emancipation in all cases. This is the third scenario of the three mentioned. And in the hadith of Maimunah, there are also two narrations: one negative and one affirmative. The negative narration that the Prophet married Maimunah while he was in ihram is based on proof: the proof is his state being similar to ihram – he was not in sewn clothes, he had not performed halq and qasr – all this is evidence that he was in ihram. So this will conflict with the other narration that says he was halal at that time, because this affirmation is also based on proof, as affirmation is always based on some proof. Thus, when both negation and affirmation are based on proof, there will be conflict, and a reason for preference is needed. Therefore, the Hanafis gave preference to the narration of Ibn Abbas (the negator) over the narration of Yazid ibn Asamm (the affirmant) because Ibn Abbas has superiority in accuracy and trustworthiness. This is the first scenario of the three. When the state of negation is ambiguous (the second scenario), its example is the purity of water and the permissibility of food and drink. The details are: there is a vessel of water or food; one person reports that this water is impure or this food is forbidden, and another person reports it is pure. The first person's report is affirmative, establishing impurity and prohibition, and it is based on proof because he must have seen some cause of impurity/prohibition. The second person's report is negative, negating impurity/prohibition. The state of this negative report is ambiguous: it is unknown whether he is reporting purity/halal based on istishab of the original state (since the original state of food is that it is halal and pure) or whether his report is based on proof. When his report is ambiguous, we investigate: if it is found that he is relying on the original state, i.e., istishab, then his report is not reliable because this negation is without proof, so there will be no conflict, and we act on the affirmative report, declaring the water impure and the food forbidden. And if upon investigation it is found that his report is based on proof, not on istishab – for example, a person took water from a river and did not become separate from it such that there would be any suspicion of impurity falling in, and he then reports its purity – then this report negating impurity and prohibition becomes strong because it is based on proof, and the affirmative report is also strong. When both reports have equal strength, there will be conflict. In that case, we will consider the original state and declare the water pure and the food halal, and we will make the original state (i.e., istishab) a reason for preference. Although istishab cannot be a proof, it can serve as a factor for preference; thus, we give preference to the affirmative report due to istishab of the original state.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi usul rule about conflicting reports (nafi vs ithbat). It explains three scenarios regarding the strength of a negative report when it encounters a positive report. The ruling: (1) If the negator has a proof, the negative report is strong and conflicts with the positive, requiring tarjih. (2) If the negator has no proof but relies on istishab (presumption of continuity), his report is weak and does not conflict; the positive report takes precedence. (3) If the basis of the negative is unknown, we investigate: if it turns out to be istishab, it is weak; if based on proof, it becomes strong and conflicts. The author then applies these scenarios to historical hadith examples: the case of Barirah (where the negative of freedom was based on istishab, so no conflict) and the case of Maimunah (where both reports had proof, causing conflict resolved by preferring Ibn Abbas). Finally, a practical example of water and food purity illustrates the second scenario. The key principle: Hanafis do not consider istishab as a proof (hujjah) for establishing a ruling, but it can be used as a factor for preference (tarjih) when two equally strong reports conflict.

Key Terms
نفی (nafi): A report that negates a legal status (e.g., purity, permissibility).
اثبات (ithbat): A report that affirms a legal status.
استصحاب (istishab): Presumption of continuity of a prior state (e.g., assuming a person is still a slave because he was originally a slave).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the basis of a negative report is istishab, which of the following is true?
A) It is strong and conflicts with the positive report.
B) It is weak and does not conflict with the positive report.
C) It is weak but still conflicts with the positive report.
D) It is considered a proof (hujjah) and thus is strong.

Key Takeaway
The strength of a negative report hinges on its basis: proof-based negatives are strong and conflict, while istishab-based ones are weak and yield to positives.

Tarjih by Number of Narrators: A Rejected Method
Critique of tarjih by number and physical qualities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tarjih by number of narrators and explain why it is rejected by ijma of the Salaf.

Core Idea
Tarjih by mere number of narrators is invalid — the Salaf abandoned it.

In this passage, the author presents an alternative view that some scholars gave preference to reports with more narrators, masculinity, and freedom. However, he immediately rejects this view by citing the consensus of the early generations (Salaf) that abandoned such a method. Let's analyze this dispute and understand the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opposing claim
Some scholars argued that in tarjih between conflicting reports, preference should be given to the one with a greater number of narrators. They also considered masculinity and freedom when numbers are equal.
This is a method that relies on quantity rather than quality of narrators.
2
Analyze their evidence
They claim the heart is more inclined to many narrators and that proof is complete only with numbers. They cited examples from issues of water (presumably hadiths about water purity).
These issues are not specified in the text, but they are considered weak by the author.
3
Identify the Hanafi response
The Hanafi position declares this method 'abandoned by the consensus of the Salaf' (مَثْرُوكَ بِاجْمَاعِ السَّلَفِ). This means it is not a valid basis for tarjih.
Ijma is a strong proof; the Salaf collectively agreed to abandon this method.
4
Evaluate the strength of the response
Ijma of the Salaf is considered a decisive (qat'i) proof. Therefore, the opposing view is not merely weak but invalid altogether.
The Hanafi school relies on more substantive criteria such as the reliability of narrators (like Ibn Abbas vs. Yazid ibn Asamm).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَنْ رَخَجَ بِفَضْلِ عَدَدِ الرُّوَاتِ لِاَنَّ الْقَلْبَ  ِإلَيْهِ أَمْيَلُ وَبالذُكُورَةِ وَالْحُرِيَّةِ فِي الْعَدَدِ دُونَ الْإِفْرَادِ لِاَنَ بِهِ تَتِمُّ الْحُجَّةُ فِي الْعَدَدِ وَاسْتَدَلَّ بِمَسَائِلِ الْمَاءِ الَا اَنَ هَذَا مَثْرُوكَ بِاجْمَاعِ السَّلَفِ. ترجمہ : ۔ اور لوگوں میں سے بعض وہ ہیں جنہوں نے ترجیح دی ہے رواۃ کے عدد کی زیادتی کے ساتھ ، اس لئے کہ دل اس کی طرف زیادہ مائل ہوتا ہے، اور ترجیح دی ہے عدد میں ذکورۃ اور حریت کے ساتھ نہ کہ افراد میں، اس لئے کہ اس کی وجہ سے حجت تام ہوتی ہے عدد میں اور استدلال کیا ہے پانی کے مسائل سے مگر یہ متروک ہے سلف کے اجماع تشریح :۔ مصنف "فرماتے ہیں کہ دو متعارض خبروں میں ترجیح دینے کے لئے بعض حضرات رواۃ کی کثرت کا
And among the people are those who have given preference by the abundance of the number of narrators, because the heart is more inclined towards it; and by masculinity and freedom in the number, not in individuals, because through it the proof is complete in numbers. And they argued with the issues of water, but this is abandoned by the consensus of the predecessors. Translation: And among people are those who have given preference by the excess of the number of narrators, because the heart is more inclined towards it, and they have given preference in number by masculinity and freedom, not in individuals, because by it the proof is complete in number, and they argued with the issues of water, but this is abandoned by the consensus of the Salaf. Explanation: The author says that for giving preference between two conflicting reports, some people consider the abundance of narrators.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents an alternative view on tarjih (preference) between conflicting reports. Some scholars preferred a report based on a greater number of narrators, arguing that the heart is more inclined to accept many narrators. They also considered masculinity and freedom (i.e., narrators who are male and free) as factors when the numbers are equal, but not when comparing individuals singly. They supported their view with examples from issues of water (likely referring to hadiths about water purity). However, the author states that this position is rejected (مَثْرُوكَ) by the consensus (ijma) of the Salaf (the early generations of Muslims). The commentary begins: 'The author says that for giving preference between two conflicting reports, some people consider the abundance of narrators...' (cut off). The Hanafi position is that such tarjih by mere number is not valid; instead, preference is based on other criteria such as the reliability of narrators (like Ibn Abbas vs. Yazid ibn Asamm as earlier mentioned).

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjih): Giving preference to one conflicting report over another.
عدد الرواة (adad al-ruwat): The number of narrators in a chain.
ذکورۃ (dhukura): Masculinity (as a quality of narrators).
حریت (hurriyyah): Freedom (not being a slave, as a quality of narrators).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of giving preference by the number of narrators?
A) It is a valid method of tarjih.
B) It is abandoned by the consensus of the Salaf.
C) It is recommended by the Salaf.
D) It is only valid when considering individual narrators.

Key Takeaway
Tarjih by number of narrators, masculinity, or freedom is invalid because the Salaf abandoned it by consensus; the Hanafi school relies on other criteria.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Invalid Bases for Tarjih: Number, Gender, and Status
Explains invalid tarjih factors and refutes them with ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the invalid bases for tarjih (number, masculinity, freedom) and apply the Hanafi rule that only narrator reliability (dhabt, itqan, 'adalah) determines preference, citing the ijma of the Salaf.

Core Idea
Tarjih relies on narrator reliability, not quantity or social status; the Salaf’s ijma rejects counting, gender, and freedom.

This lesson examines an important usul al-fiqh principle: when two reports conflict, what factors are legitimate for preferring one over the other? The text first illustrates how istishab (presumption of continuity) can serve as a murajjih (preponderator) when reports are equal in strength, but istishab itself is not a proof. Then it addresses a key disagreement: some scholars argue for tarjih based on the number of narrators, masculinity, and freedom. The Hanafi position, supported by the consensus of the Salaf, rejects these extrinsic factors. Only the intrinsic qualities of the narrators – precision (dhabt), mastery (itqan), and justice/reliability ('adalah, thiqah) – are valid bases.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the role of istishab as a murajjih
Read the opening scenario: two reports about water/food, one affirmative, one negative. The text shows that if the negative report is based on istishab (default assumption of purity), it has no evidentiary weight, and the affirmative report prevails. However, if the negative report is also based on evidence, then both are equal, and istishab becomes a preponderator to favor purity. Note: istishab does not constitute a proof (dalil) but can tip the scale when reports are equally strong.
This sets the stage for the main dispute: what other factors might be used for tarjih?
2
Identify the proposed invalid tarjih factors
The Arabic matn mentions that some scholars (e.g., Abdullah al-Jurjani, Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, some Shafi'is) give preference to a report with more narrators, or with male or free narrators (when in number, not individually). They argue that the heart inclines to more narrators, and that in number, masculinity and freedom complete the proof.
These are external social/demographic factors, not related to narrator reliability.
3
Understand the Hanafi refutation via ijma
The author declares that this view is 'abandoned by consensus of the Salaf'. The early scholars (Salaf) only considered dhabt (precision), itqan (mastery), 'adalah (justice), and thiqah (reliability) as legitimate grounds for tarjih. They did not count the number of narrators, gender, or freedom status. The opposing analogy from water/food cases is rejected because those cases are specific and not generalizable.
Ijma here serves as the decisive proof (dalil) that these factors are invalid.
4
Apply the rule to a hadith conflict example
Consider two conflicting hadiths: one narrated by 100 weak narrators (e.g., all known for poor memory), another by 2 highly reliable, precise scholars. According to the Hanafi rule, the latter is preferred, despite being fewer in number, because reliability outweighs quantity. The Salaf's practice confirms this.
This practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) shows the importance of the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس کی یہ ہے کہ ایک برتن میں پانی ہے، یا کھانا ہے، ایک آدمی خبر دیتا ہے کہ یہ پانی ناپاک ہے یا یہ کھانا حرام ہے، اور دوسرا آدمی خبر دیتا ہے پاک ہے، تو پہلے آدمی کی خبر مثبت ہے جس سے نجاست اور حرمت ثابت ہو رہی ہے اور خبر دلیل پر معنی ہے، کیونکہ اس نے نجاست و حرمت کا کوئی سبب دیکھا ہوگا جس کی بنیاد پر خبر دے رہا ہے، اور دوسرے آدمی کی خبر نافی ہے جس سے نجاست و حرمت کی نفی ہورہی ہے، خبر نافی کا حال مشتبہ ہے،معلوم نہیں کہ استصحاب حال کی بنا پر پاک اور حلال ہونے کی خبر دے رہا ہے، کیونکہ کھانے، پینے کی چیزوں میں اصل یہ ہے کہ وہ حلال و پاک ہوں، تو وہ اصل کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے پاک و حلال کہہ رہا ہے یا اس کی خبر دلیل پر مبنی ہے، جب اس کی خبر مشتبہ ہے، تو ہم نے تحقیق کی ، پتہ چلا کہ اصل کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے وہ پاک اور حلال کہہ رہا ہے یعنی استصحاب حال سے کہہ رہا ہے تو اس کی خبر معتبر نہ ہوگی ، رہا کیونکہ یہ نافی بغیر دلیل کے ہے، لہذا خبر نفی اور خبر اثبات میں تعارض نہ ہوگا ، بلکہ خبر اثبات پر عمل کرتے ہوئے پانی اور کھانے کو نا پاک و حرام کہا جائے گا، اور اگر تحقیق کرنے پر معلوم ہوا کہ اس کی خبر دلیل پر مبنی ہے، استصحاب سے نہیں کہہ رہا ہے ، جیسے ایک آدمی نے نہر سے پانی لیا اور اس سے بالکل جدا نہیں ہوا کہ اس میں نجاست کے گرنے کا وہم ہو پھر خبر دے رہا ہے، تو اس کی یہ خبر جس سے نجاست و حرمت کی نفی ہورہی ہے دلیل پر مبنی ہونے کی وجہ سے قوی ہوگئی ، اور اثبات کی خبر بھی جس سے نجاست و حرمت ثابت ہو رہی ہے قوی ہے، جب دونوں خبریں قوت میں ایک درجہ کی ہیں تو تعارض ہوگا، لہذا اس وقت اصل کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے پانی کو پاک اور کھانے کو حلال کہا جائے گا، اور اصل یعنی استصحاب حال کو ہی ہم وجہ ترجیح بنائیں گے، اگر چہ استصحاب حال دلیل نہیں بن سکتا لیکن مُرَج بن سکتا ہے، لہذا خبر اثبات پر ترجیح دیں گے استصحاب حال کی وجہ سے۔ وَمِنَ النَّاسِ مَنْ رَخَجَ بِفَضْلِ عَدَدِ الرُّوَاتِ لِاَنَّ الْقَلْبَ  ِإلَيْهِ أَمْيَلُ وَبالذُكُورَةِ وَالْحُرِيَّةِ فِي الْعَدَدِ دُونَ الْإِفْرَادِ لِاَنَ بِهِ تَتِمُّ الْحُجَّةُ فِي الْعَدَدِ وَاسْتَدَلَّ بِمَسَائِلِ الْمَاءِ الَا اَنَ هَذَا مَثْرُوكَ بِاجْمَاعِ السَّلَفِ. ترجمہ : ۔ اور لوگوں میں سے بعض وہ ہیں جنہوں نے ترجیح دی ہے رواۃ کے عدد کی زیادتی کے ساتھ ، اس لئے کہ دل اس کی طرف زیادہ مائل ہوتا ہے، اور ترجیح دی ہے عدد میں ذکورۃ اور حریت کے ساتھ نہ کہ افراد میں، اس لئے کہ اس کی وجہ سے حجت تام ہوتی ہے عدد میں اور استدلال کیا ہے پانی کے مسائل سے مگر یہ متروک ہے سلف کے اجماع تشریح :۔ مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ دو متعارض خبروں میں ترجیح دینے کے لئے بعض حضرات رواۃ کی کثرت کا اعتبار کرتے ہیں، یعنی جس خبر کے راوی زیادہ ہوں وہ رائج ہوگی اور جس خبر کے راوی کم ہوں وہ مرجوح ہوگی، کیونکہ جس خبر کے راوی زیادہ ہیں وہ خبر قوی ہو گی، اور آدمی کا دل بھی اس کی طرف مائل ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح ذکورت ( مرد ہونا ) اور حریت (آزاد ہونا ) کو بھی وجہ ترجیح بناتے ہیں، جب کہ یہ عدد میں ہو نہ کہ افراد میں، لہذا اگر دو متعارض خبروں میں ایک خبر کے راوی دو مرد ہوں، اور ایک کے راوی دو عورتیں ہوں تو پہلی خبر کو ترجیح ہوگی ، ایسے ہی ایک خبر کے راوی دو آزاد ہوں اور ایک کے راوی دو غلام ہوں تو اول کو ترجیح ہوگی لیکن ایک مرد کی خبر ایک عورت کی خبر پر راج نہ ہوگی ، اسی طرح ایک آزاد کی خبر ایک غلام کی خبر پر راج نہ ہوگی کیونکہ یہاں عدد نہیں ہے بلکہ فرد ہے، اور ذکورت وحریت سے عدد میں تو حجت تام ہوتی ہے، افراد میں حجت تام نہیں ہوتی ہے، کیونکہ ایک نصاب خبر نہیں، خبر کا نصاب کم از کم دو ہے۔ بعض حضرات سے مراد عبد الله جرجانی ، شیخ ابوالحسن کرخی اور بعض اصحاب شافعی ہیں ، مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ یہ حضرات جو کثرت رواۃ اور ذکورت و حریت کو وجہ ترجیح بناتے ہیں، ان کا استدلال پانی کے مسائل سے ہے، امام محمد نے مبسوط کے کتاب الاستحسان میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے پانی کی طہارت اور کھانے کی حلت کی خبر دی اور دو آدمیوں نے پانی کی ناپاکی اور کھانے کی حرمت کی خبر دی تو دو آدمیوں کی خبر کو ترجیح ہوگی۔اسی طرح دو آزاد مردوں نے طہارت وحلت کی گواہی دی اور دو غلاموں نے نجاست و حرمت کی گواہی دی تو حرین کی خبر کو عبدین کی خبر پر ترجیح ہوگی۔اسی طرح اگر دو مردوں نے طہارت وحلت کی خبر دی اور دو عورتوں نے نجاست و حرمت کی خبر دی تو مردوں کی خبر کو ترجیح ہوگی۔ تو جب پانی اور کھانے کے مسائل میں کثرت رواۃ اور ذکورت وحریت سے ترجیح ہوتی ہے تو اخبار و احادیث میں بھی اس چیزوں کا اعتبار ہوگا، مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ مذکورہ چیزوں کو ترجیح کی بنیاد بنانا سلف کے اجماع سے متروک ہے، اس لئے کہ سلف نے ضبط واتقان ، اور عدالت وثقہ ہونے کی زیادتی وغیرہ کو تو وجہ ترجیح بنایا ہے، کثرت رواۃ اور ذکورت وحریت وغیرہ کو وجہ ترجیح نہیں بنایا ہے۔
This is that: There is a vessel with water or food. One person reports that this water is impure or this food is forbidden, and another person reports it is pure. The first person's report is affirmative establishing impurity and prohibition, and it is based on evidence, because he must have seen some cause for impurity/prohibition. The second person's report is negative, negating impurity/prohibition. The state of the negative report is ambiguous: it is unknown whether he is reporting purity/halal based on istishab (presumption of continuity) because the original principle in food/drink is that they are halal and pure, so he might be considering that principle, or his report is based on evidence. When his report is ambiguous, we investigate: it turns out that considering the principle he says pure and halal, i.e., based on istishab, so his report is not reliable because it is a negation without evidence. Therefore, there is no conflict between the negative and affirmative reports; rather, acting on the affirmative report, the water and food are deemed impure and forbidden. But if upon investigation it becomes known that his report is based on evidence, not istishab, e.g., a person took water from a canal and never separated from it such that there is doubt about impurity falling into it, then his report negating impurity/prohibition becomes strong because based on evidence, and the affirmative report is also strong. When both reports are equal in strength, conflict arises. Then, considering the original principle, the water is deemed pure and the food halal, and we take the original principle (istishab) as the basis for preference, even though istishab cannot be a proof (dalil) but can be a preponderator (murajjih). So we prefer the affirmative report due to istishab. And among people are some who give preference by excess in number of narrators, because the heart inclines more to it, and by masculinity and freedom in number, not individually, because through it the proof is complete in number. And they deduced from issues of water, but this is abandoned by consensus of the Salaf. Translation: And among people are some who gave preference by increase in number of narrators, because the heart inclines more to it, and gave preference in number by masculinity and freedom, not individually, because through it the proof is complete in number, and they deduced from issues of water, but this is abandoned by consensus of the Salaf. Explanation: The author says that for giving preference between two conflicting reports, some people consider the multitude of narrators, i.e., the report with more narrators will be preferred and the one with fewer will be outweighed, because the report with more narrators is stronger and the heart inclines to it. Similarly, they make masculinity (being male) and freedom (being free) a basis for preference when it is in number, not individually. So if between two conflicting reports, one has two male narrators and the other has two female narrators, the first report is preferred. Similarly, if one has two free narrators and the other has two slave narrators, the first is preferred. But one man's report is not preferable over one woman's report, similarly one free person's report over one slave's report, because here it is individual, not number. And by masculinity and freedom in number the proof is complete, but in individuals the proof is not complete, because one is not the minimum for a report; the minimum for a report is at least two. By 'some people' are meant Abdullah al-Jurjani, Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, and some Shafi'is. The author says that these people who make multitude of narrators and masculinity and freedom a basis for preference deduce from issues of water. Imam Muhammad mentioned in al-Mabsut, in Kitab al-Istihsan, that if one person reports the purity of water and halal of food, and two persons report the impurity of water and prohibition of food, the report of the two persons is preferred. Similarly, if two free men testify to purity and halal, and two slaves testify to impurity and prohibition, the report of the free men is preferred over the slaves. Similarly, if two men report purity and halal, and two women report impurity and prohibition, the men's report is preferred. So when in issues of water and food preference occurs by multitude of narrators and masculinity/freedom, then in reports and hadiths these things will also be considered. The author says that making the mentioned things a basis for preference is abandoned by consensus of the Salaf, because the Salaf considered increase in precision (dhabt), mastery (itqan), and justness/reliability ('adalah, thiqah) as basis for preference, not multitude of narrators and masculinity/freedom etc.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of tarjih (preference) between conflicting reports. The author first presents a scenario: one person says water/food is impure/forbidden (positive report), another says it is pure/halal (negative report). The key issue is whether the negative report is based on evidence or on the default principle (istishab). If based on istishab, it has no evidentiary weight, so no conflict arises; the positive report prevails. If the negative report is based on evidence (e.g., the person saw the water was never contaminated), then both reports are strong and conflict. In that case, the default principle (istishab) is used as a preponderator (murajjih) to decide in favor of purity and halal, even though istishab itself is not a valid dalil. The text then quotes the Arabic matn, which states that some scholars (Abdullah al-Jurjani, Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, and some Shafi'is) prefer reports based on greater number of narrators, masculinity, and freedom when in number (not individually), using examples from water/food rulings. The author refutes this view by stating it is abandoned by consensus of the Salaf. The Salaf only gave preference based on the qualities of dhabt (precision), itqan (mastery), and 'adalah/thiqah (justice/reliability). Thus, the Hanafi position is that these external factors (quantity, gender, status) are not valid bases for tarjih; only the intrinsic reliability of narrators matters. The passage is a typical usul al-fiqh discussion on tarjih methodology.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): Preference given to one evidence over another when they conflict.
استصحاب حال (istiṣḥāb al-ḥāl): Presumption of the continuation of a state (e.g., purity or permissibility) until a contrary evidence arises.
اجماع (ijmāʿ): Consensus of the scholars (Salaf) indicating the rejection of a certain tarjih factor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the view that gives preference based on number of narrators, masculinity, and freedom considered invalid?
A) Because such factors are not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because the Salaf unanimously rejected them and only considered narrator reliability.
C) Because the opposing scholars are not reliable.
D) Because the water/food examples are weak hadiths.

Key Takeaway
The Salaf's ijma establishes that tarjih between conflicting reports must be based on narrator reliability (dhabt, itqan, 'adalah, thiqah), not on the number, gender, or freedom status of the narrators.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
6 min
Criteria for Tarjih: Number, Gender, and Freedom
Dispute on tarjih criteria: number, gender, freedom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position on using narrator quantity, gender, and freedom as criteria for tarjih, and apply the consensus of the Salaf to reject qiyas arguments.

Core Idea
The Salaf's consensus on tarjih nullifies qiyas based on narrator number, gender, or freedom.

In usul al-fiqh, when two narrations conflict, we need criteria to prefer one. Some scholars proposed that a report with more narrators, or narrators who are male and free, should be preferred. This lesson examines their argument and the Hanafi response, which relies on the practice of the Salaf. By understanding this dispute, you will learn how the Hanafi school defends its method of tarjih based on precision and reliability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed criteria
The passage mentions three criteria: kathrat al-ruwāt (greater number of narrators), dhukūrat (masculinity), and ḥurriyyat (freedom). Note that these apply only when there is plurality (two vs. two, etc.), not at the individual level.
The opposing scholars restrict these criteria to cases where both sides have at least two narrators.
2
State the opposing view and its proof
Abdullah al-Jurjani, Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, and some Shafi'is argue using qiyas from water and food cases reported by Imam Muhammad. In those cases, reports with more narrators, male narrators, or free narrators were preferred. They extend this to all reports and hadiths.
The qiyas is based on the presumption that what holds for daily life matters should hold for transmitted reports.
3
Apply the Hanafi response
The author refutes by invoking the consensus (ijma') of the Salaf. The Salaf never used these criteria; they preferred based on dhabt (precision), itqan (mastery), 'adala (uprightness), and thiqat (reliability). This consensus makes the opposing qiyas invalid.
The Hanafi position treats the Salaf's practice as the authoritative source, overriding analogical reasoning.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if two men and two women narrate conflicting reports, the Hanafi does not automatically prefer the men; both are evaluated on reliability. The opposing school would prefer the men's report.
This illustrates how the difference affects actual juridical practice.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The author clearly adopts the Hanafi view, declaring the opposing view matruk (abandoned). For fatwa, one must follow the Salaf's method.
The strength of the dalil (ijma' qat'i) ensures this position is relied upon.

Source Text

اعتبار کرتے ہیں، یعنی جس خبر کے راوی زیادہ ہوں وہ رائج ہوگی اور جس خبر کے راوی کم ہوں وہ مرجوح ہوگی، کیونکہ جس خبر کے راوی زیادہ ہیں وہ خبر قوی ہو گی، اور آدمی کا دل بھی اس کی طرف مائل ہوتا ہے۔
اسی طرح ذکورت ( مرد ہونا ) اور حریت (آزاد ہونا ) کو بھی وجہ ترجیح بناتے ہیں، جب کہ یہ عدد میں ہو نہ کہ افراد میں، لہذا اگر دو متعارض خبروں میں ایک خبر کے راوی دو مرد ہوں، اور ایک کے راوی دو عورتیں ہوں تو پہلی خبر کو ترجیح ہوگی ، ایسے ہی ایک خبر کے راوی دو آزاد ہوں اور ایک کے راوی دو غلام ہوں تو اول کو ترجیح ہوگی لیکن ایک مرد کی خبر ایک عورت کی خبر پر راج نہ ہوگی ، اسی طرح ایک آزاد کی خبر ایک غلام کی خبر پر راج نہ ہوگی کیونکہ یہاں عدد نہیں ہے بلکہ فرد ہے، اور ذکورت وحریت سے عدد میں تو حجت تام ہوتی ہے، افراد میں حجت تام نہیں ہوتی ہے، کیونکہ ایک نصاب خبر نہیں، خبر کا نصاب کم از کم دو ہے۔
بعض حضرات سے مراد عبد الله جرجانی ، شیخ ابوالحسن کرخی اور بعض اصحاب شافعی ہیں ، مصنف کہتے ہیں کہ یہ حضرات جو کثرت رواۃ اور ذکورت و حریت کو وجہ ترجیح بناتے ہیں، ان کا استدلال پانی کے مسائل سے ہے، امام محمد نے مبسوط کے کتاب الاستحسان میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ ایک آدمی نے پانی کی طہارت اور کھانے کی حلت کی خبر دی اور دو آدمیوں نے پانی کی ناپاکی اور کھانے کی حرمت کی خبر دی تو دو آدمیوں کی خبر کو ترجیح ہوگی۔اسی طرح دو آزاد مردوں نے طہارت وحلت کی گواہی دی اور دو غلاموں نے نجاست و حرمت کی گواہی دی تو حرین کی خبر کو عبدین کی خبر پر ترجیح ہوگی۔اسی طرح اگر دو مردوں نے طہارت وحلت کی خبر دی اور دو عورتوں نے نجاست و حرمت کی خبر دی تو مردوں کی خبر کو ترجیح ہوگی۔ تو جب پانی اور کھانے کے مسائل میں کثرت رواۃ اور ذکورت وحریت سے ترجیح ہوتی ہے تو اخبار و احادیث میں بھی اس چیزوں کا اعتبار ہوگا، مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ مذکورہ چیزوں کو ترجیح کی بنیاد بنانا سلف کے اجماع سے متروک ہے، اس لئے کہ سلف نے ضبط واتقان ، اور عدالت وثقہ ہونے کی زیادتی وغیرہ کو تو وجہ ترجیح بنایا ہے، کثرت رواۃ اور ذکورت وحریت وغیرہ کو وجہ ترجیح نہیں بنایا ہے۔
They consider [the number of narrators], meaning: the report whose narrators are more will be prevalent, and the report whose narrators are fewer will be outweighed, because the report with more narrators is a strong report, and a person's heart also inclines towards it. Similarly, they make masculinity (being male) and freedom (being free) a cause for preference, provided this is in number, not in individuals. Thus, if between two conflicting reports, one has two male narrators and the other two female narrators, the former report will be given preference. Similarly, if one report has two free narrators and the other two slaves, the former will be given preference. But one male's report will not outweigh one female's report, nor will one free person's report outweigh one slave's report, because here there is number, not individual, and in number masculinity and freedom constitute a complete proof, but in individuals they do not constitute a complete proof, because one does not constitute a proof; the minimum for a proof is two. By 'some personages' are meant Abdullah al-Jurjani, Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, and some Shafi'i followers. The author says: these personages who make multiplicity of narrators, masculinity, and freedom a basis for preference, their argument is from issues of water. Imam Muhammad mentioned in al-Mabsut in Kitab al-Istihsan that a man gave news of water purity and food lawfulness, and two men gave news of water impurity and food prohibition; then the report of the two men will be given preference. Similarly, if two free men testified to purity and lawfulness, and two slaves testified to impurity and prohibition, then the report of the free men will be given preference over that of the slaves. Similarly, if two men reported purity and lawfulness, and two women reported impurity and prohibition, then the report of the men will be given preference. So, when in matters of water and food preference is given based on multiplicity of narrators, masculinity, and freedom, then in reports and hadiths these matters will also be considered. The author says: making the aforementioned things a basis for preference is abandoned by the consensus of the Salaf, because the Salaf made precision and mastery, and increase in trustworthiness and reliability, etc., a basis for preference, and did not make multiplicity of narrators, masculinity, and freedom a basis for preference.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a dispute in usul al-fiqh about the criteria for preferring one narration over another when they conflict (ta'arud). The author first presents the view of some scholars (Abdullah al-Jurjani, Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, and some Shafi'is) who consider three factors as grounds for tarjih: greater number of narrators (kathrat al-ruwat), the narrators being male (dhukurat), and their being free (hurriyat). They argue that these factors strengthen the report as a proof (hujja). However, they restrict this to when there is plurality (two narrators vs. two, etc.) and not at the individual level (one male vs. one female). Their evidence is based on qiyas to cases concerning water and food, as narrated by Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut: if one person reports tahara and halal, while two report najasa and haram, the report of the two is preferred; similarly, two free men are preferred over two slaves, and two men over two women. They argue that since these factors affect tarjih in daily life matters (water/food), they should also apply to reports and hadiths. The author (the commentator) then refutes this by stating that such criteria are abandoned (matruk) by the ijma' of the Salaf. The Salaf based preference on dhabt (precision), itqan (mastery), 'adala (uprightness), and thiqat (reliability) — not on mere quantity, gender, or freedom status. This is a classic usul dispute where the Hanafi position (as represented by the author) follows the Salaf's practice and rejects the qiyas of these scholars. Note: The author emphasizes that the method of the Salaf is authoritative; their consensus abrogates any analogical reasoning to the contrary.

Key Terms
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): Preferring one evidence over another when they conflict.
کثرت رواۃ (kathrat al-ruwāh): Greater number of narrators of a report.
ذکورت (dhukūrat): Masculinity of narrators.
حریت (ḥurriyyat): Freeness of narrators (as opposed to slavery).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what was the basis for the Salaf's preference of narrations?
A) Greater number of narrators
B) Narrators being male and free
C) Precision, mastery, uprightness, and reliability
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects using narrator number, gender, or freedom for tarjih, relying instead on the Salaf's consensus emphasizing precision and reliability.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
The Nature of Istithna: Hanafi vs Shafi'i Dispute
Explains the Hanafi and Shafi'i disagreement on the linguistic operation of exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the linguistic operation of istithna and identify the practical difference when the excepted item is of a different genus.

Core Idea
Istithna prevents speech about the excepted item (Hanafi) or contradiction forces exclusion (Shafi'i).

This lesson examines a core usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: what exactly happens linguistically when a speaker makes an exception? While both schools often reach the same result in standard cases, their differing conceptual frameworks lead to divergent rulings when the excepted item is of a different genus. Understanding this dispute deepens your grasp of the linguistic foundations of legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on istithna
State that according to the Hanafis, when a speaker says 'X except Y,' the speech is considered to encompass only the remainder (X minus Y). The excepted item (Y) was never spoken about, so it carries no ruling.
Hanafis emphasize that the speaker's intention is the remainder, not a contradiction.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position on istithna
State that according to Imam al-Shafi'i, the speaker utters both the base (X) and the excepted item (Y). However, the two parts contradict each other, and the contradiction forces the exclusion of Y from the ruling of X.
Shafi'is see istithna as an exception that overrides the general ruling through opposition.
3
Compare using the Quranic and ring examples
Apply both positions to the verse about Prophet Nuh (a thousand years minus fifty) and the ring analogy. Note that both schools reach the same outcome in these examples, but the conceptual path differs.
The Hanafi view holds that the number 'thousand' remains a thousand; the exception subtracts from the number, not from the general term.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical fruit)
Examine the case where the excepted item is of a different genus (e.g., 'a thousand dirhams except a garment'). Here the schools differ: Hanafis invalidate the exception, Shafi'is validate it and deduct the value.
This is the key practical difference: Hanafis require homogeneity (jins) for a valid exception.
5
Recognize the parallel with ta'liq bil-shart
Note that the author draws an analogy between istithna and the earlier discussed ta'liq bil-shart (suspension by condition). The same conceptual divide applies: Hanafis say the condition prevents the cause, Shafi'is say it prevents the ruling.
This reinforces the systematic nature of the Hanafi approach to linguistic operations.

تَعَالَى فَلَبِثَ فِيهِمْ اَلْفَ سَنَةٍ إِلَّا خَمْسِيْنَ عَامًا فَالْخَمْسِينَ تَعَرَّضَ لِلْعَدَدِ الْمُثْبَتِ  ِبالْاَلْفِ لَا لِحُكْمِ مَعَ بَقَاءِ الْعَدَدِ لِاَنَّ الْأَلْفَ مَتى بَقِيَتْ أَلْفًا لَمْ تَصْلَحْ اِسْمًا لِمَادُوْنَهَا بِخِلَافِ الْعَامِ كَاسْمِ الْمُشْرِكِيْنَ إِذَاخْضَ مِنْهُ نَوْعٌ كَانَ الْاِسْمُ وَاقِعًا عَلَى الْبَاقِي بَلَاخَلَلٍ ثُمَّ الْإِسْتِثْنَاء نَوْعَان مُتَّصِل وَهُوَ الْأَصْلُ وَتَفْسِيْرُهُ مَا ذَكَرْنَا وَمُنْفَصِلٌ وَهُوَ مَالَا يَصْلَحُ اسْتِخْرَاجَهُ مِنَ الْأَوَّلِ لِاَنَّ الصَّدْرَ لَمْ يَتَنَاوَلُهُ فَجُعِلَ مُبْتَدَاءً مَجَازًا قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى فَإِنَّهُمْ عَدُوّلَى الْارَبَّ الْعَلَمِيْنَ اى لكِنَّ رَبَّ الْعَلَمِيْنَ ترجمہ: اور اسی اصل پر امام شافعی نے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے قول لا تبيعوا الطعام بالطعام الاسواء بسواء“ میں صدر کلام کو عام قرار دیا ہے، مگر یہ کہ استثناء صدر کلام کے معارض ہو گیا خاص طور پر مکسیلی چیزوں میں، تو باقی رہا صدر کلام عام اس کے علاوہ میں، اور ہم نے کہا کہ یہ حالت کا استثناء ہے، لہذا صدر کلام احوال میں عام ہوگا
Commentary: Just as there is disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding specification (takhsis) of the general ('amm), similarly there is disagreement regarding the operation of exception (istithna). According to us, istithna prevents speech about the excepted item along with its ruling—that is, after excluding the excepted item from the exception base, the remaining part is as if only that was spoken; the speaker did not speak about the excepted item at all. When the excepted item is not spoken, its ruling is also nonexistent. Imam al-Shafi'i says that istithna does not prevent speech about the excepted item—rather, the speaker spoke about both the excepted item and the exception base. Then, due to contradiction, the excepted item is excluded from the exception base. For example, 'So-and-so owes me one thousand dirhams except one hundred.' According to us, after removing the excepted item (one hundred) from the exception base (one thousand), what remains is nine hundred—the speaker spoke only about that. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, speech occurred about both the exception base and the excepted item, but there was contradiction. 'So-and-so owes me one thousand' requires that one thousand be obligatory, and 'except one hundred' requires that one hundred be removed from the thousand, i.e., nine hundred becomes obligatory. Thus, due to contradiction, the one hundred is excluded from the thousand. The same disagreement exists for specification of the general. For example, someone said, 'This ring is for Khalid, and its gemstone is for Hamid.' The ring is like a general term encompassing both the band and the gemstone. Then he specified the gemstone. So for both us and Imam al-Shafi'i, the ring is for Khalid and the gemstone is for Hamid. However, the nature of specification differs: according to us, the specified item (the gemstone) was never included in the general (the ring); after specification, what remains of the general (the ring's band) is what the speaker spoke about. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the specified item was included in the general, then due to specification there was contradiction, so the specified item left the ruling of the general. (Whichever way you take it, the result is the same.) The author says: The disagreement over istithna is like the previously mentioned disagreement over ta'liq bil-shart (suspension by condition). According to us, ta'liq prevents the cause (sabab) from arising; according to Imam al-Shafi'i, it prevents the ruling (hukm) from occurring. That is, according to us, before the condition occurs, the suspended statement does not even become a cause. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, it becomes a cause but the ruling does not occur. For example, in 'You are divorced if you enter the house,' according to us, 'You are divorced' does not become a cause; when entry into the house occurs, then 'You are divorced' becomes a cause. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, 'You are divorced' became a cause now, but due to the condition, the ruling (occurrence of divorce) does not occur yet. In any case, according to us, istithna is the speech about the remainder after excluding the amount of the excepted item. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, speech occurred about both, but due to contradiction the excepted item is excluded from the exception base. Hence, the statement 'So-and-so owes me one thousand dirhams except one hundred' would be: 'So-and-so owes me nine hundred.' According to Imam al-Shafi'i, he confessed to one thousand, then says 'except one hundred, so it is not upon him.' Thus due to contradiction, one hundred is excluded from the thousand, leaving nine hundred obligatory. The result is the same for both. A student's question arises: Then what is the practical fruit of this disagreement? The answer is that this disagreement also yields fruit in certain issues, when the excepted item is of a different genus than the exception base. For example, someone said: 'So-and-so owes me one thousand dirhams except a garment.' According to us, this exception is invalid because exception of a non-homogeneous item is not permissible. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, it is valid, so the value of the garment is deducted from the thousand. Because, according to him, istithna is like an opposing proof, and opposition occurs as possible, and deducting the value of a garment from a thousand is possible. (Lesson of Husami) And upon this basis, Imam al-Shafi'i considered the beginning of the statement in the Prophet's (peace be upon him) saying, 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal,' as general in small and large quantities, except that the exception opposed it specifically in measured items, so it remained general in other than that. We said this is an exception of condition, so the beginning of the statement is general in conditions, and that is only valid regarding quantity. Our companions (may Allah be pleased with them) argued with His statement, 'So he stayed among them a thousand years less fifty years.' The fifty (years) relate to the number established by the thousand, not to the ruling, with the number remaining. Because when the thousand remains a thousand, it is not a name for what is less than it, unlike the general term like the name 'polytheists'—when a type is excluded from it, the name applies to the remaining without defect. Then istithna is of two types: muttasil (connected), which is the original, and its explanation is what we mentioned; and munfasil (disconnected), which is that which cannot be extracted from the first statement because the beginning does not include it, so it is metaphorically made a new beginning. Allah said, 'Indeed they are enemies except the Lord of the worlds'—meaning 'but the Lord of the worlds.' Translation: Upon this same principle, Imam al-Shafi'i considered the beginning of the statement in the Prophet's (peace be upon him) saying, 'Do not sell food for food except equal for equal,' as general, but the exception opposed it specifically in measured items, so the beginning remained general in other than that. We said this is an exception of condition, so the beginning is general in conditions, and that is only valid regarding quantity.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage from Al-Faiz al-Hijazi (an Urdu commentary on Al-Husami) presents the Hanafi position on the nature of istithna (exception) and contrasts it with the Shafi'i position. The author first explains that the disagreement parallels the earlier disagreement on takhsis (specification of a general term). For Hanafis, when a speaker makes an exception (e.g., 'I owe you a thousand dirhams except one hundred'), the speech act effectively ignores the excepted item: the speaker is considered to have spoken only about the remainder (nine hundred). The excepted item was never part of the speech, so no ruling attaches to it. For Shafi'is, the speaker uttered both the general and the exception, but they contradict each other, so the exception overrides the general. The practical outcome in standard cases is the same (nine hundred owed), but the conceptual basis differs. The author then draws an analogy to ta'liq bil-shart (suspension by condition): Hanafis say the condition prevents the cause from existing, Shafi'is say the condition prevents the ruling from taking effect. The passage then addresses the student question: if the result is the same, what is the practical benefit? The answer is that when the excepted item is of a different genus (e.g., 'a thousand dirhams except a garment'), Hanafis declare the exception invalid because valid exception requires homogeneity. Shafi'is accept it, deducting the value of the garment. This shows a real difference. The passage then discusses a hadith on selling food and the Quranic verse about Prophet Nuh (peace be upon him) staying a thousand years less fifty, arguing that the exception affects the number, not the general term. Finally, it defines two types of istithna: muttasil (connected, where the excepted item can be extracted from the general) and munfasil (disconnected, where it cannot, and is treated as a new statement).

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): Exception: a linguistic construction that excludes something from the scope of a previous statement. The text discusses its operation.
مستثنى (mustathna): The excepted item (e.g., 'one hundred' in 'a thousand except one hundred').
مستثنى منه (mustathna minhu): The exception base (e.g., 'a thousand') from which the excepted item is removed.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general term by removing some of its individuals.
تعليق بالشرط (ta'liq bil-shart): Suspension of a ruling on a condition (e.g., 'You are divorced if you enter the house').
عام ('amm): A general term that encompasses all individuals/instances it refers to.
متصل (muttasil): Connected exception: the excepted item can be extracted from the general statement (e.g., 'a thousand except fifty').
منفصل (munfasil): Disconnected exception: the excepted item cannot be extracted from the first statement (e.g., 'they are enemies except the Lord of the worlds').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example 'Zaid owes me a thousand dirhams except a garment,' what is the Hanafi ruling according to this passage?
A) The exception is valid and the value of the garment is deducted from the thousand.
B) The exception is invalid because the excepted item is not of the same genus, so the full thousand is owed.
C) The exception is valid and the full thousand is owed, but the garment is given separately.
D) The exception is invalid only if the garment is worth more than a thousand.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on istithna hinges on whether the exception prevents speech about the excepted item or forces exclusion by contradiction, with the practical difference appearing when the excepted item is of a different genus.

Hanafi vs Shafi'i on the Nature of Istithna
Dispute on whether istithna removes mustathna from speech or merely prevents ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafis define istithna as removal from speech and evaluate the Shafi'i objection using the Quranic verse as proof.

Core Idea
For Hanafis, istithna removes the excepted item from speech itself; for Shafi'is, it only suspends the ruling.

This passage presents a core usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the nature of istithna (exception). The Hanafis argue that istithna functions to remove the mustathna entirely from the speech act, citing the Quranic verse about Prophet Noah (1000 years minus 50). The Shafi'is counter by drawing an analogy with takhsis of a general term. Understanding this dispute is key to grasping how each school interprets exceptional statements in the Quran and in legal language.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on istithna
The Hanafis hold that istithna removes the mustathna from the mutakallam (speech) itself. After istithna, the speaker is only talking about the remainder.
This is not merely a semantic point; it affects how legal statements are understood.
2
Examine the Hanafi Quranic proof
Analyze Quran 29:14 (falbitha fihim alfa sanatin illa khamsoona 'aman). How does this verse support the Hanafi view?
The word 'alf' is not spoken for less than 1000, so the exception effectively cancels the word.
3
Understand the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'is argue that istithna only prevents the hukm (ruling), not the speech. They draw an analogy with 'amm makhsus: after takhsis, the general term still applies to the remainder.
They claim that just as 'mushrikun' remains applicable after excluding some polytheists, 'alf' remains applicable after excluding 50.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The author refutes the analogy, showing that in takhsis, applying the general term to the remainder causes no linguistic corruption, but in istithna, applying the mustathna minhu to the remainder would corrupt language by using a term for less than its true meaning.
The distinction hinges on whether the term's meaning inherently excludes or includes the excepted item.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: If someone says 'I owe you 1000 dirhams except 10,' Hanafis say he owes 990 (the 1000 is not spoken), while Shafi'is say he owes 1000 with a suspended ruling (the word remains).
This affects how contracts, oaths, and Quranic exceptions are interpreted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج اصحابنا : - احناف کے نزدیک استثناء مستثنی کی مقدار کو خارج کرنے کے بعد باقی کے تکلم کا نام ہے، اور مستدل آیت باری تعالی ہے فلبث فيهم الف سنة الاخمسين عامل اس میں مستثنی یعنی خمسین کو الف سے نکالنے کے بعد باقی کا تکلم ہے، تو اللہ تعالی حضرت نوح کے اپنی قوم میں ساڑھے نوسوسال قیام کی خبر دے رہے ہیں، گو یا الف کا تکلم ہوا ہی نہیں ہے، احناف کے نقطہ نظر سے آیت میں کوئی اشکال نہیں ہے، اگر امام شافعی کے نقطہ نظر سے یہاں استثنا کو صرف مانع حکم قرار دیا جائے ، اور مانع تکلم نہ قرار دیا جائے تو آیت میں اشکال و خرابی لازم آئے گی، کیونکہ آیت کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ الف کا عدد تو باقی ہے مگر اس کا حکم باقی نہیں ہے یعنی الف سے ہزار مراد نہیں بلکہ الامین کے معارض ہونے کی وجہ سے ساڑھے نو سو مراد ہے، تو الف کا اطلاق مادون الالف پر ہورہا ہے اور یہ غلط ہے، کیونکہ الف الف رہتے ہوئے الف سے کم پر نہیں بولا جاتا ہے۔ بخلاف العام : - شوافع کے جواب کی تردید ہے، وہ کہتے ہیں کہ الف کا اطلاق مادون الالف پر ہوسکتا ہے، الف بولکر ساڑھے نو سو مراد لے سکتے ہیں، جیسے عام مخصوص منہ البعض میں، باوجود یکہ مخصوص عام کے حکم سے خارج ہے، پھر بھی عام بولا جاتا ہے جیسے مشرکین کا لفظ ہند، سندھ ، روم سب جگہ کے مشرکین کو شامل ہے، اگر مشرکین ہند کو بذریعہ تخصیص خارج کر دیا جائے تو بھی باقی مشرکین پر یہ لفظ بولا جاتا ہے، ایسے ہی استثنا میں مستثنی کو خارج کرنے کے بعد بقیہ پر مستثنی منہ کو بولا جاسکتا ہے۔ مصنف اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ استثنا کو عام پر قیاس کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے، کیونکہ عام میں تخصیص کے بعد مابقیہ پر عام کا اطلاق کرنے میں کوئی خرابی وخلل لازم نہیں آتا، اور استثنا میں مستثنی کو خارج کر کے بقیہ پر مستثنی منہ کے اطلاق سے خرابی لازم آتی ہے جیسے او پر تفصیل سے گذرا۔
And our companions argued: According to the Hanafis, istithna is the name of speech about the remainder after removing the quantity of the mustathna. The proof is the verse of Allah: 'So he stayed among them a thousand years minus fifty.' Here, the mustathna, i.e., fifty, is taken out from a thousand, and then speech is about the remainder. So Allah informs about Noah's stay among his people of nine hundred and fifty years; it is as if a thousand were never spoken. From the Hanafi perspective, there is no problem in the verse. If, from Imam Shafi'i's perspective, istithna here is considered only a preventer of the ruling and not a preventer of speech, then a problem and corruption would necessarily arise in the verse. Because the meaning of the verse would be: the number 'thousand' remains, but its ruling does not remain, i.e., a thousand does not mean a thousand, but due to the opposition of 'fifty', nine hundred and fifty is meant. Then the word 'thousand' would be applied to less than a thousand, and this is wrong because 'thousand' while remaining thousand is not spoken for less than a thousand. Contrary to al-amm: This is a refutation of the Shafi'i response. They say that the word 'thousand' can be applied to less than a thousand; they can say 'thousand' and mean nine hundred and fifty, just as in a general (amm) that is specified (makhsus) from some of its parts; even though the specified part is excluded from the ruling of the general, still the general term is uttered, e.g., the word 'mushrikun' includes the polytheists of Hind, Sindh, and Rome. If the polytheists of Hind are excluded by takhsis, still the word is uttered for the remaining polytheists. Similarly, in istithna, after excluding the mustathna, the mustathna minhu can be uttered for the remainder. The author responds that analogy between istithna and amm is not correct, because in amm, after takhsis, applying the general term to what remains does not entail any corruption or disorder, while in istithna, after excluding the mustathna, applying the mustathna minhu to the remainder necessarily entails corruption, as detailed above.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage presents a core usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the nature of istithna (exception). The Hanafis argue that istithna functions to remove the mustathna (the excepted item) entirely from the speech act (takallum). They cite the Quranic verse about Prophet Noah (1000 years minus 50) to show that after the exception, the word 'thousand' is effectively not used at all; only the remainder (950) is spoken. If, as the Shafi'is claim, istithna only prevents the ruling (hukm) but does not remove the mustathna from speech, then the verse would imply that 'thousand' remains spoken but means less than a thousand, which is linguistically impossible. The Shafi'is respond by drawing an analogy with 'amm (general) and takhsis (specification): just as a general term remains applicable to its remaining individuals after specification, so too the mustathna minhu can be applied to the remainder after exception. The author rebuts this by noting a crucial difference: in takhsis, applying the general term to what remains does not cause any linguistic corruption, while in istithna, applying the mustathna minhu to the remainder would indeed lead to corruption because the mustathna minhu includes the mustathna by definition. This is a classic Hanafi position emphasizing the literal and operative difference between takhsis and istithna.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithna'): Removing the mustathna from the mutakallam and then speaking about the remainder.
المستثنى (al-mustathna): The item excepted, which is taken out from the mustathna minhu.
المستثنى منه (al-mustathna minhu): The general expression from which exception is made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, when someone says 'I owe you 1000 dirhams except 10,' what is the status of the word '1000'?
A) The word '1000' is spoken but only 990 is meant.
B) The word '1000' is not spoken at all; only 990 is the intended speech.
C) The word '1000' remains spoken with its full meaning but the ruling is only for 990.
D) The word '1000' is figurative and means 990.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between istithna and takhsis is crucial: istithna removes the excepted item from speech, preserving linguistic precision.

Taqlid of the Companions: Conditions and Scholarly Disagreement
Three opinions on taqlid of Sahaba with conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi conditions for taqlid of a Companion and evaluate the three scholarly opinions on the issue.

Core Idea
Taqlid of a Companion is obligatory only in matters beyond analogy and when no disagreement or silent consensus exists.

In this passage, we examine a foundational usul dispute: is a later mujtahid bound by the opinion of a Companion? The Hanafi school, through al-Karkhi, distinguishes between rulings derived by analogy (qiyas) and those that are not, and sets two conditions. Understanding this distinction clarifies when taqlid is valid and when ijtihad remains open.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three opinions
The text implies three positions: (1) absolute obligation (unstated but implied), (2) al-Karkhi's conditional obligation, (3) al-Shafi'i's absolute prohibition. Note the proponent of each.
The first opinion is not explicitly quoted but serves as foil.
2
Analyze al-Karkhi's distinction
Al-Karkhi separates rulings into mudrak bil-qiyas (perceptible by analogy) and ghair mudrak (not perceptible). In the latter, the Companion's statement is presumed from the Prophet because he cannot have derived it by analogy, and Companions do not lie. Therefore, taqlid is wajib.
Rulings like ritual purity limits often fall under ghair mudrak.
3
Understand the two conditions
Condition 1: No other Companion dissents. Condition 2: The statement did not reach other Companions and receive their silent approval. If silent consent occurs, it becomes ijma' sukuti, making taqlid wajib by agreement.
The conditions restrict taqlid to reliable, uncontested statements.
4
Consider the second issue
When Companions differ, truth is confined to their opinions. A later mujtahid cannot introduce a third opinion; he must choose one of theirs using evidence.
This contrasts with Shafi'i view that later mujtahid may override.
5
Compare with al-Shafi'i's view
Al-Shafi'i and most Mu'tazila/Ash'ara reject taqlid of any Companion entirely. The practical difference: Hanafis may follow a Companion's statement in non-qiyasi matters; Shafi'is do not consider it binding.
The dispute hinges on whether Companions' statements are proof (hujja).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تقلید صحابہ کے بارے میں دوسرا قول امام ابوالحسن کرخی کا ہے، وہ کہتے ہیں کہ صحابہ کی تقلید صرف ان مسائل میں واجب ہیں جن کا قیاس سے ادراک نہیں ہو سکتا ہے، کیونکہ اس میں یہ بات طے ہوگی کہ صحابی کا قول حضور سے سماع پر محمول ہے، وہ اپنی رائے اور قیاس سے نہیں کہہ رہا ہے، اس لئے کہ حکم غیر مدرک بالقیاس ہے، اور صحابہ سے کذب کا بھی تصور نہیں ہے، لہذا یہ متعین ہو جائے گا کہ صحابی حضور سے سنکر ہی بیان کر رہا ہے، اور اگر مسائل مدرک بالقیاس ہیں تو ان میں صحابی کے قول کی تقلید نہیں کی جائے گی ، اس میں یہ احتمال ہے کہ صحابی نے رائے اور قیاس سے یہ حکم بیان کیا ہو، اور رائے میں خطا کا امکان ہے اس لیے کہ صحابہ غیر معصوم ہیں ۔ وقال الشافعی : - تیسرا قول امام شافعی صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ہے، کہ کسی صحابی کی تقلید نہیں کیجائے گی چاہے حکم مدرک بالقیاس ہو یا غیر مدرک بالقیاس ہو، اکثر معتزلہ اور اشاعرہ کا بھی یہی مذہب ہے۔ وهذا الخلاف فى كل ما ثبت تقلید صحابی میں یہ مذکورہ اختلاف اس وقت ہے جب یہ دو شرطیں پائی و جائیں۔ (۱) کسی صحابی نے کوئی بات کہی اور دوسرے صحابی سے اس میں کوئی اختلاف ثابت نہ ہو، کیونکہ اگر دوسرے صحابی کی طرف سے اختلاف ثابت ہو گیا تو پھر بالاتفاق تقلید واجب نہ ہوگی بلکہ مجتہد کوحق ہوگا کہ ان دونوں میں سے جس پر چاہے عمل کرے۔ (۲) دوسری شرط یہ ہے کہ یہ بات بھی ثابت نہ ہو سکی ہو کہ یہ قول صحابی دوسرے صحابہ تک پہنچا اور اس پر ان سب حضرات نے سکوت کیا، کیونکہ اگر ایسی صورت ہوئی کہ وہ قول صحابہ کے پاس پہنچا اور انہوں نے سکوت اختیار کیا تو بالا تفاق تقلید واجب ہوگی کیونکہ یہ اجماع سکوتی کہلائے گا۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہاں یہ سمجھیں کہ اگر کسی مسئلہ میں صحابہ نے اختلاف کیا ہو اور چند اقوال ہو گئے ہوں، تو حق ان اقوال سے متجاوز نہ ہوگا، بلکہ حق انہی اقوال میں منحصر ہوگا، لہذا بعد کے مجتہد کے لئے جائز نہ ہوگا کہ ان اقوال کے علاوہ اور کوئی قول اختیار کرے بلکہ اس کے لئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ انہی اقوال میں سے کسی قول کو دلائل کی روشنی میں ترجیح
Regarding taqlid of the Companions: The second opinion is of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi. He says that taqlid of a Companion is obligatory only in matters that cannot be perceived by analogy (qiyas). Because in that it is determined that the Companion's statement is attributed to hearing from the Prophet, and he is not speaking from his own opinion and analogy, since the ruling is not perceived by analogy, and there is no concept of lying from the Companions. Therefore it will be determined that the Companion is relating what he heard from the Prophet. And if the matters are perceivable by analogy, then taqlid of the Companion's statement will not be done, because there is a possibility that the Companion expressed this ruling by his own opinion and analogy, and there is possibility of error in opinion, since the Companions are not infallible. And al-Shafi'i said: The third opinion is of Imam al-Shafi'i (peace be upon him): that no Companion is to be followed, whether the ruling is perceivable by analogy or not. Most Mu'tazila and Ash'ara hold this view. And this disagreement, regarding every established taqlid of a Companion, is when these two conditions are present: (1) A Companion said something and no disagreement from another Companion is established. Because if disagreement from another Companion is established, then by consensus taqlid is not obligatory; rather the mujtahid has the right to act on whichever he wishes. (2) The second condition is that it is not established that this statement of the Companion reached other Companions and they all remained silent. Because if the statement reached the Companions and they remained silent, then by agreement taqlid is obligatory, as this is called silent consensus (ijma' sukuti). The second issue to understand here: If the Companions differed in a matter and several opinions existed, then the truth does not go beyond these opinions, rather the truth is confined to these opinions. Therefore it is not permissible for a later mujtahid to adopt an opinion other than these; rather he must prefer one of these opinions in the light of evidence.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute in usul regarding taqlid of the Companions (qawl al-sahabi). The author, explaining the matn, gives three opinions: first (not quoted but implied) is likely absolute obligation; second is al-Karkhi's view limiting taqlid to matters not subject to qiyas; third is al-Shafi'i's absolute prohibition. The Hanafi position, derived from al-Karkhi and the conditions, is that taqlid of a Companion is permissible and even obligatory when there is no known opposition and no silent consensus. The two conditions ensure that the Companion's statement is not contradicted or tacitly approved by others (which would constitute ijma'). The second issue clarifies that when Companions differ, their opinions are not void; rather the truth is among them, and a later mujtahid must choose one using evidence, similar to conflicting analogies.

Key Terms
تقلید (taqlīd): Following the opinion of another scholar without knowing the evidence.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning to derive a ruling from an original case.
اجماع سکوتی (ijmā‘ sukūtī): Consensus inferred from the silence of scholars when a ruling is presented.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Karkhi, when is taqlid of a Companion obligatory?
A) In all matters, whether perceptible by analogy or not
B) Only in matters that are not perceptible by analogy (ghair mudrak bil-qiyas)
C) Only in matters that are perceptible by analogy (mudrak bil-qiyas)
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Taqlid of a Companion is not universally binding; it is obligatory only when the ruling is beyond analogy and when no dissent or silent consensus exists.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

Handling Conflicting Opinions of the Companions: Not Dropped, But Preferred
Refutes the claim that conflicting opinions of Sahaba should be entirely dismissed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why conflicting opinions of the Companions (when no hadith is cited) are not automatically discarded and apply the principle of tarjih to resolve them.

Core Idea
Conflicting Sahaba opinions (without hadith) are like conflicting qiyas — they survive and require tarjih.

A common doubt is raised: if the Companions disagree on a ruling, why not simply dismiss all their opinions? The author of al-Husami addresses this directly. He argues that since no Companion cited a hadith, these are ijtihad-based opinions that stand in the position of qiyas. Just as conflicting analogies do not invalidate each other but are weighed, so too must the mujtahid evaluate and prefer among the Companions' views.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Recognize the doubt: 'When the statements of the Companions conflict, all statements should be dropped.' This is the view the author refutes.
2
Note the Absence of Hadith
The author points out that no Companion cited a hadith. This absence indicates the matter is based on ra'y (opinion), not transmitted text.
If a hadith existed, it would have been cited.
3
Understand the Qiyas Analogy
These opinions are like qiyas (analogical reasoning). In Hanafi usul, conflicting qiyas do not become invalid (batil); rather, one is given preference (tarjih).
Recall the earlier lesson on conflicting qiyas.
4
Apply Tarjih to Sahaba Opinions
Therefore, the mujtahid must not drop all opinions but must weigh them using preference criteria (e.g., strength of reasoning, number of supporters, alignment with Quran and Sunnah).
The result is a preferred opinion, not a nullification.
5
Conclude the Refutation
The objection is refuted: conflicting opinions of the Companions (without hadith) are not canceled but are subject to ijtihad and tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يسقط البعض بالبعض :- مصنف االلہ ایک شبہ کا جواب دے رہے ہیں، شبہ یہ ہے کہ جب صحابہ کے اقوال میں تعارض ہے تو تمام اقوال کو ساقط کر دینا چاہیے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ باہم اختلاف کے باوجود کسی صحابی نے حدیث پیش نہیں کی تو یہ دلیل ہے کہ اس سلسلہ میں کوئی حدیث نہیں ہے، ورنہ وہ حدیث پیش کرتے ، لہذا یہ سب اقوال صحابہ کی رائے سے ہوئے ، اور ہر صحابی کا قول قیاس کے قائم مقام ہوگا ، اور پہلے آپ پڑھ چکے ہیں کہ جب دو قیاسوں میں تعارض ہوتا ہے، تو قیاس باطل نہیں ہوتا ہے، بلکہ کسی ایک قیاس کو ترجیح دی جاتی ہے، اسی طرح اقوال صحابہ جب بمنزلہ قیاس ہیں، تو یہ اقوال ساقط نہ ہوں گے بلکہ مجتہد کسی ایک قول کو دلائل سے ترجیح دے گا ، اور عمل کرے گا۔
And not cancelling some by others: The author is answering a doubt. The doubt is: When the statements of the Companions conflict, all statements should be dropped. The answer is: Despite the mutual disagreement, no Companion presented a hadith, which is evidence that there is no hadith in this matter, otherwise they would have presented it. Therefore all these statements are from the Companions' opinions, and each Companion's statement will be in the position of analogy (qiyas). And you have previously learned that when two analogies conflict, the analogy does not become invalid; rather one analogy is given preference. Similarly, when the statements of the Companions are in the position of analogy, these statements will not be dropped; rather the mujtahid will prefer one statement with evidence and act upon it.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential objection to the previous ruling that truth is confined to the Companions' differing opinions. The objection claims that when opinions conflict, they should all be rejected. The author refutes this by noting that since no Companion cited a hadith, these are opinions based on ijtihad, akin to analogical reasoning (qiyas). Conflicting analogies do not invalidate each other; one is chosen based on preponderance (tarjih). Similarly, conflicting opinions of Companions are not nullified but must be weighed, and the mujtahid selects the strongest.

Key Terms
تعارض (ta‘āruḍ): Conflict or contradiction between two evidences or rulings.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical deduction; here used as a parallel to show how conflicting qiyas are handled.
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): Preference given to one evidence or ruling over another based on strength.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why do conflicting opinions of Companions not get dropped?
A) Because each Companion's opinion is based on a hadith
B) Because they are considered like conflicting analogies, which are not invalidated but one is preferred
C) Because the Companions are infallible
D) Because the later mujtahid must accept all of them

Key Takeaway
Conflicting opinions of the Companions, when no hadith is cited, are not nullified but treated as qiyas, requiring tarjih to determine the strongest view.
