Taqlid of the Tabi'un: An Internal Hanafi Dispute
Discusses the permissibility of taqlid of Tabi'un with two opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding taqlid of a Tabi'i and explain the reasoning and thamarah al-khilaf of each.

Core Idea
Taqlid of a Tabi'i is a matter of ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school — two contradictory narrations from Abu Hanifa survive.

This passage presents an internal Hanafi dispute about whether it is permissible to follow the fatwa of a Tabi'i (a Follower of the Companions). The text records two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa, one prohibiting and one allowing, along with their justifications. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the Hanafi hierarchy of authority and the role of Tabi'un in istinbat al-ahkam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the specific scenario under discussion? The fatwa of a Tabi'i that was prevalent in the era of the Companions and conflicts with a Companion's fatwa.
2
State the two positions among Hanafi mashayikh
Some Hanafi mashayikh permitted taqlid of a Tabi'i, while others did not. The example of 'Ali and Qadi Shurayh is given to illustrate a real conflict.
3
Extract the two narrations from Abu Hanifa
First narration: Abu Hanifa said 'I will not do taqlid of a Tabi'i because they are men like us.' Second narration: 'I will do taqlid of them because the Companions used to refer to their statements.'
4
Analyse the evidence for each
Prohibition: Tabi'un are fallible human beings (rijāl) like later scholars, so no special authority. Permission: The Companions themselves respected and referenced the opinions of Tabi'un, indicating their opinions carry weight.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
A Hanafi mufti may or may not adopt the fatwa of a Tabi'i depending on which narration he relies upon. This affects whether the opposing Companion's view is followed or the Tabi'i's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واما التابعی - اگر کسی تابعی کا فتوی دور صحابہ میں مروج ہو اور وہ صحابی کے فتوی سے مزاحم ہو جائے تو اس تابعی کی تقلید کے بارے میں دو قول ہیں، ہمارے بعض مشائخ کے نزدیک تابعی کی تقلید جائز ہے اور بعض کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے، جیسے حضرت علی کے نزدیک بیٹے کی شہادت باپ کے حق میں جائز تھی اور قاضی شریح جو تابعی ہیں ان کا فتوی عدم جواز کا تھا۔ امام ابوحنیفہ سے بھی اس میں دو روایتیں ہیں ، پہلی روایت ہے کہ امام صاحب نے کہا کہ میں تابعی کی تقلید نہیں کرونگا، اس لئے کہ وہ بھی ہماری طرح رجال ہیں، اور دوسری روایت یہ ہے کہ میں ان کی تقلید کرونگا، کیونکہ صحابہ ان کے اقوال کی طرف رجوع کرتے تھے۔
And as for the Tabi'i: If the fatwa of a Tabi'i was prevalent in the era of the Companions and it conflicts with a Companion's fatwa, then there are two opinions regarding taqlid of that Tabi'i. According to some of our mashayikh, taqlid of a Tabi'i is permissible, and according to some it is not permissible. For example, according to 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), the testimony of a son in favor of his father was permissible, while Qadi Shurayh, who is a Tabi'i, gave a fatwa of impermissibility. There are also two narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa regarding this: The first narration is that Imam said, 'I will not do taqlid of a Tabi'i, because they are men like us.' The second narration is that ['I will do taqlid of them] because the Companions used to refer to their statements.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage briefly covers the issue of taqlid of the Tabi'un (the generation after the Companions). The author mentions that there is disagreement among Hanafi scholars. Some of the early mashayikh allowed it, while others did not. An example is given: 'Ali (RA) allowed a son's testimony for his father, but Qadi Shurayh (a Tabi'i) ruled otherwise. Imam Abu Hanifa himself has two reports: one refusing taqlid of Tabi'un because they are fallible like later scholars, and one accepting it because the Companions themselves sought their opinions. This reflects an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on the authority of Tabi'i opinions.

Key Terms
تابعی (tābi‘ī): A Muslim who saw or accompanied a Companion but not the Prophet (SAW).
تقلید (taqlīd): Following the opinion of a scholar without knowing the evidence.
رجال (rijāl): Men; referring to the fact that Tabi'un are ordinary humans subject to error.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what reason did Imam Abu Hanifa give in one narration for not doing taqlid of a Tabi'i?
A) Because the Tabi'i's fatwa conflicts with the Qur'an
B) Because the Tabi'i is a man like us (fallible)
C) Because the Tabi'i never met the Companions
D) Because the Tabi'i's opinion is not recorded

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school records two conflicting narrations from Abu Hanifa on taqlid of Tabi'un, reflecting a legitimate internal ikhtilaf on the authority of the second generation.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement

The Hanafi Response to Takhsis al-Illa
Explaining the Hanafi view that the forgetful person's fast remains valid because the cause is absent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects takhsis al-illa for derived causes and distinguish this from textually specified causes.

Core Idea
In derived causes, a missing cause is not a prevented cause — the fast remains valid because the act is legally absent.

This lesson unpacks a critical usul dispute between the Hanafis and their opponents regarding the concept of specification of a cause (takhsis al-illa). The concrete case of a forgetful person eating during a Ramadan fast serves as the battleground. By understanding the Hanafi reinterpretation of the Prophet's hadith, you will grasp the foundational principle that governs many subsidiary rulings in this chapter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
What is the specific case? A forgetful person eats while fasting. Does the fast break? What is the cause (illa) that would invalidate it?
The cause is the loss of abstention (fawat al-imasak).
2
State the opponent's argument
The opponent claims the cause is present but a preventer (the hadith) blocks the ruling of invalidity. This is takhsis al-illa.
Opponents likely include the Shafi'i school who accept takhsis.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis say the cause itself is absent because the act is attributed to Allah. How does this shift the argument?
The hadith is taken as evidence for absence of cause, not a preventer.
4
Distinguish derived vs. textually specified causes
The tanbih clarifies that this response applies only to derived causes. Why does the Hanafi school accept takhsis for textually specified causes?
Textually specified causes like adultery for hadd can be blocked by doubt.
5
Apply the principle
See how this foundation resolves other cases in this chapter: any act by a person without intention (forgetful, sleepwalker) does not break the fast because the cause is absent.
This is the basis for many furu' issues in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی نے کھا پی لیا تو اس کا روزہ نہیں ٹوتا ہے، حالانکہ علت پائی گئی روزہ کا رکن یعنی امساک فوت ہو گیا تو روزہ ٹوٹنا چاہیے۔ تو فریق اول جو خصیص علت کا قائل ہے وہ تو کہتا ہے کہ یہاں علت تو پائی گئی ( یعنی فوات امساک ) مگر حکم ( فسادِصوم ) ایک مانع کی وجہ سے نہیں پایا گیا ، مانع وہ حدیث ہے جس میں فرمایا انما اطعمه الله وسقاه ، اس کو اللہ نے کھلایا پلایا ہے، ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ ناسی کے روزہ کا عدم فساد عدم علت کی وجہ سے ہے، ہمارے نزدیک علت یعنی فوات امساک ہوا ہی نہیں، کیونکہ ناسی کا فعل اللہ کی طرف منسوب ہے یعنی اللہ نے اس کو کھلایا پلایا تو گو یا اس نے کھایا پیا ہی نہیں، لہذا اس سے جنایت کے معنی ساقط ہو جا ئیں گے اور اس سے جو کھانے پینے کا فعل ہوا ہے وہ معاف ہو جائے گا، تو روزہ کا رکن باقی ہے، اس لئے روزہ باقی ہے، ایسا نہیں ہے کہ روزہ کا رکن تو فوت ہو گیا مگر مانع کی وجہ سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹا۔ الغرض فریق اول نے جس چیز کو ( حدیث رسول انما اطعمه الله وسقاه ) تخصیص علت کی دلیل قراردیا، اسی چیز کو ہم نے عدم علت کی دلیل قرار دیا جس کی وضاحت تشریح میں ہو گئی۔ مصنف یہ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ یعنی تخصیص علت کی دلیل کو عدم علت کی دلیل قرار دینا، اس فصل کی بنیاد ہے، اس کو یاد کرلو،مضبوط کرلو، اس میں بہت سافقہ ہے اس باب کے بہت سارے مسائل اس اصل پر متفرع ہیں اور اس میں بہت سارے اعتراضات سے چھٹکارا ہے۔
الله
تنبيه :- مصنف عالیہ نے کتاب میں ملک کا بیان کیا ہے اس سے مراد علمک مستنبطہ ہیں، عللِ منصوصہ مراد نہیں ہیں، یعنی وہ علتیں مراد ہیں جو ادلہ اربعہ سے مستنبط ہیں، وہ نہیں جن پر نص وارد ہوتی ہیں، کیونکہ اکثر فقہاء علک منصوصہ میں تخصیص کے قائل ہیں، جیسے زنا حد کی علت منصوصہ ہے، سرقہ قطع ید کی علت منصوصہ ہے، علل منصوصہ میں بعض صورتوں میں علت کے باوجود کسی مانع کی وجہ سے کم نہیں پایا جاتا جیسے زنا یا سرقہ پایا گیا کسی شبہ کی وجہ سے ثبوت نہ ہو سکا تو با وجود علت کے حکم محقق نہ ہوگا ، غرض علل منصوصہ میں کسی مانع کے سبب حکم کا علت سے مختلف جائز ہے۔
If someone ate and drank, his fast does not break, although the cause (i.e., the loss of the essential element of fasting, which is abstention) is found, so the fast should break. So the first party, who believes in specification of the cause, says that the cause is present (i.e., loss of abstention) but the ruling (invalidity of the fast) is not present due to a preventer; the preventer is the hadith in which it was said: 'Indeed, Allah fed him and gave him drink.' Our response is that the non-invalidity of the forgetful person's fast is due to the absence of the cause. According to us, the cause (i.e., loss of abstention) did not occur at all, because the act of the forgetful person is attributed to Allah, meaning Allah fed him and gave him drink, so as if he did not eat or drink at all. Hence the meaning of transgression falls away from him, and the act of eating and drinking that occurred is forgiven. Thus the essential element of fasting remains, therefore the fast remains. It is not that the essential element of fasting is lost but the fast does not break due to a preventer. In short, what the first party took as evidence for specification of the cause (the hadith 'Indeed, Allah fed him and gave him drink'), we have taken as evidence for the absence of the cause, as explained in the commentary. The author says: This—making the evidence for specification of the cause into evidence for absence of the cause—is the foundation of this chapter. Remember it, strengthen it; there is great [؟] in it. Many issues of this chapter are derived from this principle, and it provides relief from many objections. 
Allah
Note: The author mentioned 'mulk' in his book; by it he means derived causes, not textually specified causes. That is, those causes that are derived from the four sources of evidence, not those for which a text exists. Because most jurists believe in specification of textually specified causes, like adultery is the textually specified cause for the hadd punishment, theft is the textually specified cause for amputation of the hand. In textually specified causes, in some cases, despite the cause, due to some preventer the ruling is not realized, like if adultery or theft occurred but due to some doubt it could not be proven, then despite the cause the ruling will not be effectuated. In short, in textually specified causes, it is permissible for the ruling to differ from the cause due to a preventer.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a dispute in usul al-fiqh between Hanafis and opponents on the concept of takhsis al-illa (specification of the cause). The opponent argues that in the case of a forgetful person eating during Ramadan, the cause (loss of abstention) is present but the ruling (invalidity of fast) is prevented by the hadith 'Indeed, Allah fed him and gave him drink.' The Hanafi response, following the author's reasoning, is that the cause itself is absent because the forgetful person's act is attributed to Allah, so legally it is as if he did not eat. Thus the ruling does not apply due to absence of cause, not due to a preventer. The author emphasizes that this reinterpretation is the foundation for many subsidiary issues in this chapter. The note (tanbih) clarifies that the discussion is about derived causes (illah mustanbatah), not textually specified causes (illah mansusah), because in the latter, specification is generally accepted by jurists (e.g., adultery triggers hadd, but doubt prevents it). This distinction is crucial: in derived causes, Hanafis reject specification; in textually specified causes, they accept it. All examples and arguments are strictly within the Hanafi usul framework.

Key Terms
تخصیص العلۃ (takhsis al-illa): The view that a cause can be present but the ruling is not applied due to a preventer (man').
علت مستنبطہ (illa mustanbatah): A cause derived from the four sources of evidence through ijtihad.
علت منصوصہ (illa mansusah): A cause explicitly mentioned in the text (Quran or hadith) for a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented, why does the fast of a forgetful person not break?
A) Because a preventer (man') blocks the ruling despite the cause being present.
B) Because the cause (loss of abstention) is absent due to attribution of the act to Allah.
C) Because the hadith specifies that the act is excused only for the forgetful.
D) Because the ruling of breaking only applies if the person remembers.

Key Takeaway
In derived causes, the Hanafi school rejects takhsis al-illa; the non-invalidity of the forgetful person's fast is due to absence of cause, not a preventer.

The Fourth Type of Refuting Transitive Causes: Contradiction (Munāqaḍa)
Explaining contradiction as a method to refute transitive causes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define munāqaḍa, distinguish it from naqḍ, and apply the method to refute a transitive cause in Hanafi uṣūl debate.

Core Idea
Contradiction (munāqaḍa) exposes a fatal inconsistency: the claimed cause is present but the ruling is absent without a preventer.

This passage introduces the fourth and final method of repelling a transitive cause in Hanafi usul: contradiction (munāqaḍa). After comparing it to the more severe corruption of position (fasād al-waḍ‘), the author defines munāqaḍa and distinguishes it from invalidating (naqḍ). The extended example from the debate on intention in wudū' illustrates how the Hanafis use munāqaḍa to break the Shāfi‘ī analogy and ultimately force the acceptance of effective causes.

Guided Path
1
Define Munāqaḍa
Read the definition: contradiction occurs when the positor's claimed cause is present in some instances but the ruling is absent, without a preventer. Distinguish from naqḍ (invalidating) where a preventer causes the absence.
The presence or absence of a preventer (māni‘) is the key distinction.
2
Contrast with Fasād al-Waḍ‘
Note the comparison: fasād al-waḍ‘ is a fatal objection that leaves no room for reply, while munāqaḍa allows the opponent to attempt a defense by distinguishing the cases.
3
Analyze the Shāfi‘ī Argument
The Shāfi‘ī claims intention is obligatory in wudū' because it shares the genus of purification with tayammum, where intention is obligatory. Identify this as a transitive cause (qiyas).
The cause is 'being purification'.
4
Apply the Hanafi Counterexample
The Hanafi points out that washing the body (ghusl) and washing a garment are also purification but do not require intention. This is the contradiction: the cause (purification) exists but the ruling (intention) is absent.
This exposes the flaw in the Shāfi‘ī's cause.
5
Evaluate the Shāfi‘ī Response and Hanafi Rebuttal
The Shāfi‘ī tries to distinguish between real and legal purification, claiming legal purification (wudū') is devotional. The Hanafi rebuts by showing that wudū' is actually rational (removing impurity by water) and thus does not require intention, unlike tayammum which is irrational.
The final Hanafi position is that intention is not required in wudū'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

کہیں گے کہ غسل ثوب اور غسل بدن سے آپ کا یہ دعوی ٹوٹ جاتا ہے، کیونکہ غسل بدن اور غسل ثوب بھی طہارت ہے، مگر اس میں نیت فرض نہیں ہے ،۔۔اس مناقضہ سے بچنے کے لئے وہ مجبور ہوں گے کہ وضو اور غسل ثوب میں فرق کرنا امر تعبدی و غیر معقول ہے ،اس لئے اس میں نیت فرض ہے ،لہذا وضو میں بھی نیت فرض ہوگی ، کیونکہ امور تعبدیہ میں نیست فرض ہے جیسے نماز روزہ وغیرہ، گویا انہوں نے یہ ثابت کرنے کی کوشش کی کہ حکم کا علت سے متخلف نہیں ہوا ، کیونکہ نیت حکم ہے اور طہارت حکمیہ علت ہے، نہ کہ مطلق طہارت، لہذا غسل ثوب و بدن سے دعوی نہ ٹوٹے گا۔شوافع نے جو تو جیہ اور وجہ فرق بیان کیا ، ہم اس کو اس طرح توڑیں گے کہ نجاست نکلنے سے طہارت کا زائل ہونا اور بدن کا ناپاک ہونا امر معقول ہے، کہ جس طرح منی نکلنے سے پورا بدن ناپاک ہو جاتا ہے، اسی طرح پیشاب وغیرہ کے نکلنے سے بھی پورا بدن ناپاک ہو جاتا ہے تو قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ پیشاب وغیرہ نکلنے سے بھی پورے بدن کا غسل واجب ہوتا جیسے منی نکلنے کی صورت میں۔۔ مگر چونکہ خروج منی کا تحقق کم ہوتا ہے تو پورے بدن کے غسل سے حرج و تنگی نہ ہوگی، اور پیشاب وغیرہ کا خروج کثرت سے ہوتا ہے تو ہر دفعہ پورے بدن کا غسل واجب ہوتا تو حرج دونگی پیدا ہو جاتی ، پس پیشاب وغیرہ نکلنے کی صورت میں شریعت نے پورے بدن کا غسل واجب نہیں کیا، بلکہ خلاف قیاس اعضاء اربعہ کے دھونے پر اکتفار کرنے کا حکم دیا۔ تو اگر چہ پورے بدن کو پاک کرنے کے لئے اعضاء اربعہ پر اکتفار کرنا خلاف عقل و قیاس ہے لیکن خروج نجاست سے پورے بدن کا ناپاک ہونا اور پانی کے ذریعہ بصورت وضو نجاست کا زائل ہونا عقل کے عین مطابق ہے، اور امر معقول ہے، اور امر معقول میں نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، لہذا وضو میں نیت کی ضرورت نہیں برخلاف مٹی سے تیم کرنا کیونکہ مٹی سے طہارت حاصل ہونا یہ امر غیر معقول ہے، لہذا اس میں نیت کی ضرورت ہے، غرض انہوں نے توجیہ کر کے وضو اور تیم کو ایک کر دیا تھا اور ہم نے دونوں میں فرق ظاہر کر دیا۔ مصنف اللہ کہتے ہیں کہ عللِ طردیہ کو دفع کرنے کی یہ چار قسمیں جو ماقبل میں تفصیل سے بیان ہوئیں وہ اصحاب طرد ( شوافع ) کو تاثیر کے قائل ہونے پر مجبور کرتی ہیں، لامحالہ ان کو علت موثرہ کو ماننا پڑے گا بغیر اس کے چھٹکارہ نہیں ہے۔
The objection of corruption of position (fasād al-waḍ‘) is the heaviest against the one who posits the cause, because after this objection, there remains no room for the positor to reply, unlike contradiction (munāqaḍa) etc., where the positor can find a way of escape through various interpretations. An example of corruption of position: like in testimony, a witness says something contrary to the claim, ruining the case; after that, there is no question of investigating whether the witness is upright or righteous, rather the claim itself falls. As for contradiction (al-munāqaḍa): The fourth type of repelling a transitive cause is contradiction. Contradiction is when the attribute that the positor has made the cause is found in some instances but the ruling is absent from the cause, i.e., the cause exists but the ruling is not found—this absence may be due to a preventer or without a preventer. Those who allow specification of the cause say: if the absence is without a preventer, it is contradiction; but if due to a preventer, it is not called contradiction but rather in the art of debate it is called invalidating (naqḍ). An example of contradiction: Imam al-Shāfi‘ī says: just as intention is obligatory in tayammum, so too is it obligatory in wudū’, because both share in the genus of purification. But we say: washing a garment and washing the body break your claim, because washing the body and washing a garment are also purification, yet intention is not obligatory in them. To avoid this contradiction, he is compelled to distinguish between wudū’ and washing a garment. He distinguishes by saying: in washing a garment, purification is achieved by removing real impurity—this is consistent with reason, so intention is not required. In wudū’, however, purification is legal (ḥukmī) because there is no impurity on the limbs of wudū’; thus legal purification is a devotional and irrational matter, and in devotional and irrational matters, intention is required, like tayammum, because achieving purification with earth is devotional and irrational, so intention is obligatory. Therefore, intention will be obligatory in wudū’ as well, because in devotional matters intention is obligatory, like prayer and fasting. Thus, he attempts to prove that the ruling is not absent from the cause, because intention is the ruling and legal purification is the cause, not absolute purification; so the claim is not broken by washing a garment or body. The Shāfi‘īs have given this justification and distinction. We break it as follows: The removal of purity by the exit of impurity and the body becoming impure is a rational matter—just as the entire body becomes impure by the exit of semen, similarly by the exit of urine etc., the entire body becomes impure. Analogy requires that the entire body be washed in case of urine etc., as in the case of semen. But because the occurrence of semen emission is rare, washing the whole body causes no hardship, whereas urine etc. are frequent; if washing the entire body were obligatory each time, hardship would arise. So the Law did not obligate washing the whole body for urine etc., but contrary to analogy, it ordered limiting to washing the four limbs. Although limiting to the four limbs to purify the whole body is contrary to reason and analogy, the fact that the body becomes impure by the exit of impurity and that impurity is removed by water through wudū’ is precisely rational and a rational matter, and intention is not needed in rational matters. Hence, intention is not needed in wudū’, unlike tayammum with earth because purification with earth is an irrational matter, so intention is needed. In short, they had equated wudū’ and tayammum through justification, and we have shown the difference between them. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, says: These four types of repelling transitive causes, detailed previously, force the proponents of transitive causes (the Shāfi‘īs) to accept the cause as effective; inevitably they must acknowledge the effective cause—there is no escape.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth method of repelling a transitive cause (ʿilla ṭardiyya) in debate: contradiction (munāqaḍa). The author first contrasts it with corruption of position (fasād al-waḍ‘), which is the heaviest objection because it leaves no room for response. Then he defines munāqaḍa: when the attribute claimed as a cause is present in some instances but the ruling is absent, either with or without a preventer. The difference between munāqaḍa (contradiction) and naqḍ (invalidating) is explained—the latter involves a preventer. The example given is from the debate between Hanafis and Shāfi‘īs on intention in wudū’. The Shāfi‘ī argues that since both wudū’ and tayammum are purification, intention should be obligatory in wudū’ as in tayammum. The Hanafi responds with a counterexample: washing a garment and washing the body are also purification without intention, breaking the analogy. The Shāfi‘ī then distinguishes between real and legal purification, asserting that legal purification is devotional and requires intention. The Hanafi refutes this by showing that wudū’ (legal purification) is actually rational because the removal of impurity by water is rational, so intention is not needed; only tayammum remains irrational. The passage concludes that these four repelling methods force the opposition to accept effective causes (ʿilla muʾaththira), moving the debate to a higher level. The author's summary reinforces the structure of argumentation in Hanafi uṣūl.

Key Terms
مناقضة (munāqaḍa): A type of refutation of a transitive cause where the claimed cause exists but the ruling is absent without a preventer.
فساد وضع (fasād al-waḍ‘): A fatal objection against the positor of a cause where his argument is inherently contradictory, leaving no room for response.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes munāqaḍa from naqḍ in Hanafi usul?
A) Munāqaḍa involves the absence of the ruling with the cause present due to a preventer, while naqḍ is without a preventer.
B) Munāqaḍa involves the absence of the ruling without a preventer, while naqḍ involves a preventer.
C) Both terms are synonymous.
D) Munāqaḍa is used only in kalam, while naqḍ is used in fiqh.

Key Takeaway
Munāqaḍa is a powerful tool in Hanafi usul to refute a transitive cause by showing that the claimed cause exists without the ruling, forcing the opponent to either refine their cause or abandon it.

Introduction to Mu'arada and Qalb
Defines mu'arada and qalb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mu'arada, distinguish its two types, and explain the first type of qalb as the inversion of cause and ruling.

Core Idea
Mu'arada containing contradiction is qalb: inversion of cause and ruling to expose inconsistency.

In juristic debates (munazarat), scholars often counter an opponent's reasoning by attacking the causal link (ta'lil). This passage introduces the concept of mu'arada (counter-argument) and its first category: mu'arada that involves contradiction (munafada), called qalb (inversion). Understanding qalb is essential for critically evaluating analogical arguments (qiyas) and engaging in advanced usul debates.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of mu'arada
The text defines mu'arada as a counter-argument presented to contest the opponent's ta'lil.
Mu'arada is a tool of naqd (objection) in usul.
2
Break down the two types of mu'arada
Mu'arada is of two types: one containing contradiction (munafada) and one pure (khalisah). The first type is called qalb.
The passage focuses on qalb.
3
Define qalb
Qalb is the inversion of the cause (illa) into a ruling (hukm) and the ruling into a cause. It is derived from the inversion of a vessel (qalb al-ina').
This is a specific form of mu'arada.
4
Understand the condition for qalb
Qalb is only valid when the opponent's ta'lil (causal reasoning) is based on the ruling itself, not on an independent cause.
Example: if the illa is derived from the ruling (hukm), inversion is possible.
5
Examine the incomplete example
The text begins an example from hadd for zina: the disbeliever's impurity is linked to flogging/stoning. Qalb would invert this relationship, but the text is cut off.
Despite being incomplete, the example illustrates the mechanics of qalb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اَمَّا الْمُعَارَضَةً فَهيَ نَوْعَانِ مُعَارَضَةٌ فِيهَا مَنَا قَضَةٌ وَمُعَارَضَةٌ خَالِصَةً أَمَا الْمُعَارَضَةُ الَّتِي فِيهَا مُنَاقَضَةً فَالْقَلْب وَهُوَ نَوْعَان اَحَدُهُمَا قَلب الْعِلَّةِ حُكْمًا وَالْحُكْمِ عِلَّةً وَهُوَ مَا خُوْذْ مِنْ قَلْبِ الْإِنَاءِ وَإِنَّمَا يَصِحُ هَذَا فِيْمَا يَكُونُ التَّعْلِيْلُ فِيه بِالْحُكْمِ مِثْلُ قَوْلِهِمْ الْكَفَّارُ جِئْسٌ يُجَلَّدُ بِكْرَهُمْ مِائَةً فَيُرْجَمْ ثَبِبُهُمْ كَا
As for mu'arada (counter-argument), it is of two types: mu'arada containing a contradiction and pure mu'arada. As for mu'arada containing a contradiction, it is qalb (inversion), and it is of two types: one is inverting the cause into a ruling and the ruling into a cause, and it is derived from the inversion of a vessel. This is valid only where the ta'lil (causal reasoning) is by the ruling, such as their saying: 'the disbeliever is impure; their unmarried one is flogged one hundred lashes, and their married one is stoned, like...'
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage introduces a new topic: mu'arada (counter-argument in juristic debate). It states that mu'arada is of two kinds: one that involves contradiction (munafada) and one that is pure. The first type is called qalb (inversion), which itself has two forms. The first form is inverting the cause into a ruling and the ruling into a cause. This is a technique used when the ta'lil (reasoning) is based on the ruling itself. An example is given from the law of hadd for zina: the disbeliever's status (kufr) is considered an illa for impurity, and then the ruling of flogging and stoning is related. The text is cut off, but this lays the foundation for understanding qalb as a method of challenging the opponent's argument by swapping the roles.

Key Terms
معارضة (mu'arada): A counter-argument presented to contest the opponent's ta'lil (causal reasoning).
قلب (qalb): Inversion of the cause and ruling in the opponent's argument to create a contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the first type of mu'arada?
A) Pure mu'arada.
B) Mu'arada containing contradiction, which is qalb.
C) Qalb of cause to ruling.
D) Qalb of ruling to cause.

Key Takeaway
Mu'arada with contradiction (qalb) inverts the cause and ruling to expose an inconsistency, and it is valid only when the ta'lil is based on the ruling itself.

Types of Mu'arada: Qalb (Inversion) in Hanafi Usul
Defines mu'arada and its types with qalb as a refutation tool.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mu'arada and its two types, distinguish it from munaqada, and apply qalb to refute an opponent's qiyas when ta'lil is based on the ruling.

Core Idea
Qalb inverts cause and ruling to expose a weakness in the opponent's analogy.

This passage from the commentary defines two key terms in Hanafi usul: Mu'arada (opposing argument) and Munaqada (contradictory argument). It then explains Qalb, a specific type of Mu'arada where the opponent's causal link is inverted, valid only when the causation (ta'lil) is by the ruling itself. Through the example of hadd punishments, we will see how Qalb refutes an analogy by showing its susceptibility to inversion.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish Mu'arada and Munaqada
Understand the key difference: in Mu'arada, the objector presents a counter-proof without attacking the original proof; in Munaqada, the objector directly invalidates the opponent's proof and turns it into his own.
Mu'arada does not attack the proof; it establishes the opposite claim with a separate proof.
2
Identify the two types of Mu'arada
Mu'arada is of two types: one containing Munaqada (called Qalb) and pure Mu'arada (without Munaqada). Recognize that Qalb combines both aspects: from one perspective it is Mu'arada (opposing the claim), from another it is Munaqada (the proof becomes invalid for the opponent).
The author emphasizes that Mu'arada is primary, Munaqada is incidental.
3
Define Qalb as inversion
Qalb literally means 'turning over' and is derived from upending a vessel. In usul, it means turning the cause (illa) into the ruling (hukm) and the ruling into the cause. This inversion is valid only when the causation (ta'lil) is based on the ruling itself.
Example: 'A causes B' becomes 'B causes A'.
4
Determine when Qalb is valid
Qalb is valid only where ta'lil is bi al-hukm (causation by the ruling). That is, when the ruling itself is used as the cause for another ruling, the inversion becomes possible.
If the cause is a non-ruling attribute (like genus or property), qalb may not be applicable.
5
Apply Qalb to the Shafi'i example
The Shafi'i argues that disbelievers are like Muslims in hadd punishments: the unmarried are flogged and the married are stoned based on common genus. The Hanafi inverts: Muslims are flogged because they are stoned (i.e., the ruling of stoning for the married is the cause for flogging the unmarried), breaking the analogy.
The inversion shows that the original causal link is not fixed, so the analogy fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفيضُ الحجازي
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
طہارت میں تجری لازم نہ آئے ، اور نہ بہنے کی صورت میں نجاست کی جگہ کو دھونا واجب نہیں ہے، تو پورے بدن یعنی اعضاء وضو کا دھونا بھی واجب نہیں ہوگا، کیونکہ وصف خروج جس معنی کی وجہ سے علت بنا تھا وہ معنی نہیں پایا گیا تو وصف خروج علت نہیں بنا لہذا حکم ( نقض وضو ) بھی نہیں پایا گیا، تو علت کے معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے حکم معدوم ہو گیا، یہ جو ہم نے شوافع کے نقض کو دفع کیا ، اس کا نام ہے دفع بالمعنی الثابت بالوصف۔ اس پر امام شافعی صلى الله عليه وسلم کی طرف سے دوسرا نقض و اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے، وہ یہ ہے کہ جس شخص کا زخم برابر بہتارہتا ہو تو اس کا وضو ٹوٹ جانا چاہیے کیونکہ وصف خروج نجاست بھی پایا گیا، اور وہ معنی جو وصف سے دلالۂ ثابت ہے یعنی موضع نجاست کا دھونا یہ بھی پایا گیا ، کیونکہ اس پر نجاست کی جگہ کا دھونا واجب ہے،لہذا وضوٹوٹ جانا چاہیے حالانکہ آپ کہتے ہیں کہ بقاء وقت تک اس کا وضو باقی رہتا ہے، تو یہ علت کا حکم سے مختلف ہے۔ مصنف یہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس نقض کو بھی ہم دو طرح سے دفع کریں گے ، (۱) ایک تو دفع بالحکم یعنی ہم حکم کو ثابت مانتے ہیں یعنی ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ علت (خروج) کی وجہ سے حکم (حدث ) ثابت ہے، ہم نہیں کہتے ہیں کہ اس کا وضو نہیں ٹوٹا ، لہذا علت کی وجہ سے حکم ثابت ہو گیا، علت کا حکم سے تخلف نہیں ہوا، لیکن جو حکم ہے یعنی وضو ٹو ٹنا یہ اس کے عذر کی وجہ سے مؤخر ہو گیا ، وقت کے بقاء تک اس کو لمبا کر دیا ، اسی لئے وقت کے ختم سے اس پر وضو لا زم ہوگا ، چاہے دوسرا کوئی حدث پیش نہ آیا ہوں۔ یہ جو ہم نے نقض کو دفع کیا اس کا نام ہے دفع بالحکم ۔ اس نقض کو دفع کرنے کا (۲) دوسرا طریقہ دفع بالغرض ہے، وہ یہ ہے کہ ہم نے مسلسل خون آنے کو مسلسل پیشاب پر قیاس کیا ہے، اب اگر کسی کو پیشاب کے قطرات مسلسل آ رہے ہوں ،سلس بول کا مریض ہو تو آپ کے نزدیک بھی اس کا وضو وقت کے ختم ہونے تک باقی رہتا ہے ،تو ہم نے زخم پر مسلسل خون آنے کو پیشاب پر قیاس کیا ، اور اصل ( پیشاب ) اور فرع ( زخم ) میں برابری ثابت کردی، تو علت کی غرض پائی گئی ، اور وہ غرض اصل اور فرع میں برابری ثابت کرنا ہے ، لہذا اگر خون بھی برابر جاری رہا تو وہ بھی وقت کے ختم ہونے تک معاف ہوگا، اصل (بول ) اور فرع ( خون ) دونوں برابر ہو جائیں گے، یہ جو نقض کو ہم نے دفع کیا اس کا نام ہے دفع بالغرض۔ أَمَّا الْمُعَارَضَةً فَهيَ نَوْعَانِ مُعَارَضَةٌ فِيهَا مَنَا قَضَةٌ وَمُعَارَضَةٌ خَالِصَةً أَمَا الْمُعَارَضَةُ الَّتِي فِيهَا مُنَاقَضَةً فَالْقَلْب وَهُوَ نَوْعَان اَحَدُهُمَا قَلب الْعِلَّةِ حُكْمًا وَالْحُكْمِ عِلَّةً وَهُوَ مَا خُوْذْ مِنْ قَلْبِ الْإِنَاءِ وَإِنَّمَا يَصِحُ هَذَا فِيْمَا يَكُونُ التَّعْلِيْلُ فِيه بِالْحُكْمِ مِثْلُ قَوْلِهِمْ الْكَفَّارُ جِئْسٌ يُجَلَّدُ بِكْرُهُمْ مِائَةً فَيُرْجَمْ ثَبِبُهُمْ كَالْمُسْلِمِيْنَ قُلْنَا الْمُسْلِمُونَ إِنَّمَا يُجَلدُ بِكْرُهُمْ مِائَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ يُرْجَمُ ثَيْبُهُمْ فَلَمَّا احْتَمَلَ الْإِنْقِلَابَ فَسَدَ الْأَصْلُ وَبَطَلَ الْقِيَاسُ ترجمہ: بہر حال معارضہ پس وہ دو قسم پر ہے، ایسا معارضہ جس میں مناقضہ ہو، اور خالص معارضہ، بہر حال وہ معارضہ جس میں مناقضہ ہو پس ، وہ قلب ہے ، اور قلب کی دو قسمیں ہیں ،ان میں سے ایک علت کوحکم سے اور حکم کو علت سے بدل دینا ہے، اور یہ قلب الاناء سے ماخوذ ہے، اور قلب کی یہ قسم صحیح ہوتی ہے اس صورت میں کہ تعلیل اس میں حکم کے ذریعہ ہو ، جیسے شوافع کا قول کہ کفار ایسی جنس ہے کہ ان کے بکر کو سو کوڑے مارے جاتے ہیں تو ان کے حبیب کو رجم کیا جائے گا مسلمانوں کی طرح، ہم کہیں گے کہ مسلمان ، ان کے پکر کو سو کوڑے مارے جائیں گے ، اس لئے کہ ان نیب کو رجم کیا جاتا ہے، پس جب تعلیل انقلاب کا احتمال رکھتی ہے تو اصل فاسد ہوگی اور قیاس باطل ہو گیا۔ تشریح :۔ مصنف عالی مناقضہ کے بیان سے فارغ ہو کر معارضہ کا بیان شروع کر رہے ہیں، معارضہ کہتے ہیں معلل نے اپنے دعوی پر جو دلیل قائم کی ہے معترض اس کے خلاف پر دلیل قائم کر دے اور معتل کی دلیل سے تعرض نہ کرے، اور مناقضہ یہ ہے کہ معترض معلل کی دلیل کو باطل کر دے، اور اسی کو اپنی دلیل بنا دے دونوں میں فرق یہ ہے کہ معارضہ میں معلل کی دلیل سے کوئی تعرض نہیں ہوتا بلکہ اپنی دلیل سے اس کے مدعی کی ضد کو ثابت کیا جاتا ہے، اور مناقضہ میں معلل کی دلیل سے تعرض کر کے باطل کیا جاتا ہے اور وہ معترض کی دلیل بن جاتی ہے، پھر معارضہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں ، معلل کی دلیل بعینہ معترض کی دلیل بن جائے تو یہ پہلی قسم ہے، اور اگر ایسا نہ ہو تو دوسری قسم ہے، (۱) پہلی قسم کا نام معارضہ فیھا مناقضہ ہے یعنی ایسا معارضہ جس میں مناقضہ ہو، اور (۲) دوسری قسم کا نام ہے معارضہ خالصہ، پہلی قسم کا دوسرا نام قلب بھی ہے، اس قسم اول کا نام معارضہ فیھا معارضہ اس لئے ہے کہ اس میں من وجہ معارضہ ہے من وجہ مناقضہ ہے، اس لحاظ سے کہ یہ معلل کے دعوی کے خلاف پر دلالت کرتا ہے معارضہ ہے، اور اس لحاظ سے کہ دلیل میں خلل ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ دلیل معلل کے حق میں دلیل بننے کے قابل نہ رہی، بلکہ معارض کی دلیل بن گئی ، مناقصہ ہے لیکن اس میں معارضہ ہی اصل ہے، مناقضہ تو ضمناً اور صورۃ ہے، اس لئے کہ پہلے بتایا کہ علت مؤثرہ میں نقض وارد نہیں ہو سکتا ہے، اس لئے مصنف نے نام بھی معارضہ فیھا مناقضہ رکھا،مناقضہ فیھا معارضہ نہیں رکھا۔ سوال: معارضہ فیھا مناقضہ میں تو اجتماع ضدین لازم آتا ہے، کیوں کہ معارضہ میں معلل کی دلیل سے تعرض کئے بغیر اس کے مدعی کی ضد کو ثابت کیا جاتا ہے، اس کا مطلب ہے کہ اس کی دلیل مسلم ہے، اور مناقضہ میں اس کی دلیل سے تعرض کر کے دلیل ہی کو باطل کر دیا جاتا ہے، تو معارضہ اور مناقضہ تو اجتماع ضدین ہوا۔
As for Mu'arada (opposition), it is of two types: Mu'arada containing Munaqada (contradiction) and pure Mu'arada. As for Mu'arada containing Munaqada, it is Qalb (inversion), and it is of two types: one is turning the cause (illa) into the ruling (hukm) and the ruling into the cause, and it is derived from upending a vessel. This is valid only where the causation (ta'lil) is by the ruling, like their saying: 'The disbelievers are a genus: their unmarried one is flogged a hundred, and their married one is stoned, like the Muslims.' We say: 'The Muslims, their unmarried one is flogged a hundred because their married one is stoned.' So when the causation becomes susceptible to inversion, the foundation (asl) becomes corrupt and the analogy (qiyas) becomes invalid. Explanation: The author, having finished the discussion of Munaqada, begins the discussion of Mu'arada. Mu'arada is when the objector (mu'tarid) establishes a proof against the opponent's claim without attacking the opponent's proof itself. Munaqada is when the objector invalidates the opponent's proof and makes it his own proof. The difference is that in Mu'arada, the opponent's proof is not attacked; rather, his own proof is used to establish the opposite of the opponent's claim. In Munaqada, the opponent's proof is attacked and invalidated, and it becomes the objector's proof. Then Mu'arada is of two types: if the opponent's proof becomes exactly the objector's proof, that is the first type; otherwise, it is the second type. The first type is called 'Mu'arada containing Munaqada' (i.e., an opposition that contains contradiction), and the second type is called 'Pure Mu'arada.' The first type is also called Qalb. It is called 'Mu'arada containing Munaqada' because in one respect it is Mu'arada and in another respect it is Munaqada: from the perspective that it indicates the opposite of the opponent's claim, it is Mu'arada; from the perspective that due to a defect in the proof, it is no longer valid as the opponent's proof but becomes the objector's proof, it is Munaqada. However, Mu'arada is primary, and Munaqada is incidental and formal, because it was previously established that an effective cause cannot be invalidated. Hence, the author named it 'Mu'arada containing Munaqada,' not 'Munaqada containing Mu'arada.' Question: In 'Mu'arada containing Munaqada,' there seems to be a combination of opposites (ijtima' diddayn), because in Mu'arada the opponent's proof is not attacked and the opposite of his claim is established, meaning his proof is accepted, while in Munaqada the opponent's proof is attacked and invalidated. So how can Mu'arada and Munaqada come together?
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage from the commentary defines two key terms in Hanafi usul: Mu'arada (opposing argument) and Munaqada (contradictory argument). The author first distinguishes them: in Mu'arada, the objector presents a counter-proof without attacking the original proof; in Munaqada, the objector directly invalidates the original proof and turns it into his own. Then Mu'arada is divided into two types: one that contains Munaqada (called Qalb or inversion) and a pure one. Qalb specifically occurs when the causation (ta'lil) is based on a ruling, allowing the objector to invert the causal relationship. The example given is the analogy between disbelievers and Muslims in hadd punishments: if the Shafi'i argues that the unmarried disbeliever is flogged like the Muslim unmarried because the married disbeliever is stoned like the Muslim married, the Hanafi can invert: the Muslim married is stoned because the Muslim unmarried is flogged, thus breaking the analogy. The commentary then explains that in Qalb, Mu'arada is the primary aspect, while Munaqada is incidental, because the effective cause is not directly attacked but the inversion shows a flaw in the opponent's reasoning. The question about combining opposites is resolved by noting that in Qalb, the opponent's proof is not directly invalidated; rather, it is reinterpreted, so there is no actual contradiction.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-mu'arada): Presenting a counter-proof against the opponent's claim without attacking the original proof itself.
المناقضة (al-munaqada): Invalidating the opponent's proof and turning it into one's own proof.
القلب (al-qalb): Inversion: switching the cause and the ruling in a causation argument, derived from upending a vessel.
التعليل (al-ta'lil): The act of assigning a cause (illa) to a ruling in analogical reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, when is Qalb (inversion) valid in Hanafi usul?
A) Always, in any type of analogical reasoning.
B) Only when the causation (ta'lil) is based on the ruling (ta'lil bi al-hukm).
C) Only when the opponent uses a pure analogical argument.
D) Only in cases of hadd punishments.

Key Takeaway
Mu'arada with munaqada (qalb) is a potent refutation tool in Hanafi usul when the causation is by the ruling itself.

Ikhtilaf — Scholarly Disagreement
intermediate
8 min
Qalb al-Illa: The Ramadan Fasting Example
Demonstrating qalb al-illa in the dispute over intention in Ramadan fast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of qalb al-illa to rebut a qiyas argument by augmenting the cause with a condition from the Lawgiver.

Core Idea
Qalb al-illa: inverting the opponent's cause by adding a condition that makes it support your own ruling.

This passage introduces the usul principle of qalb al-illa (inversion of the cause) as a rebuttal technique in qiyas. Through the concrete example of fasting intention, you will see how Hanafi usul transforms an opponent's illa into a proof for its own position. The Shafi'is argued that obligation requires specifying intention; the Hanafis responded by adding the condition that Allah has already specified Ramadan, making obligation a cause for non-specification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's qiyas
State the Shafi'i analogy: both Ramadan and make-up fasts are obligatory (common illa), so both require specifying intention (hukm).
The Shafi'is use obligation (fardiyyah) as the cause for ta'yin al-niyyah.
2
Locate the Hanafi counter-argument
The Hanafis accept the analogy but argue that the illa must be augmented: Ramadan's obligation comes with Allah's specification, so obligation now indicates non-specification.
This augmentation is an interpretation (tafsir) of the same attribute, not a change.
3
Analyse the augmentation
The added condition is that the Lawgiver has already determined the time of Ramadan. This makes human specification redundant.
The same illa now supports the opposite ruling due to the additional condition.
4
Evaluate the inversion
This is qalb al-illa: the illa is preserved in essence but its legal effect is inverted. Hanafi usul accepts this as a valid rebuttal (mu'aradah).
Mutakallimun reject qalb as sophistry; Hanafis see it as legitimate istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دعوی پر دلیل بنارہا ہے ، تو ایک وصف کا دو متنافی حکموں لئے دلیل بننا لازم آئے گا جو عقلا نا ممکن ہے ۔۔اس لئے مصنف اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مُنتدِل کے وصف میں کچھ زیادتی کر دی جائے مگر وصف پر جو زیادتی ہے وہ اسی وصف کی تفسیر ہو، اس وصف کو متغیر نہ کر دے کہ اس کا وصف آخر ہو نا لا زم آئے۔ جیسے شوافع کہتے ہیں کہ رمضان کا روزہ فرض ہے تو بغیر تعیین نیت کے ادانہ ہوگا، جیسے قضاء کا روزہ فرض ہے تو بغیر تعیین نیت کے ادا نہیں ہوتا۔ تو شوافع نے فرضیت کو تعیین نیت کی علت بنایا ، اور رمضان کے روزہ کو قضا روزہ پر قیاس کیا، ہم نے معارضہ بالقلب کے ذریعہ جواب دیا اور کہا کہ فرضیت تعیین نیت کی علت نہیں بلکہ عدم تعیین کی علت ہے ، وہ اس طرح کہ رمضان کا روزہ فرض ہے، لہذا خود سے تعین کی ضرورت نہیں ہے، کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے اس کو متعین کر دیا ہے، جیسے قضاء کا روزہ ایک مرتبہ متعین کرنے کے بعد دوبارہ اس میں تعیین کی ضرورت نہیں ،غرض رمضان کا روزہ اور قضاء روزہ دونوں میں علت فرضیت ہے، اور دونوں اس بات میں برابر ہیں کہ ایک بار تعیین کے بعد دوبارہ اس میں تعیین کی ضرورت نہیں لیکن چونکہ رمضان کے روزہ میں ایک مرتبہ تعین منجانب اللہ ہو چکی ہے، لہذا دوبارہ تعیین کی ضرورت نہیں ، اور قضاء روزہ نیت سے شروع کرنے سے متعین ہوتا ہے، لہذا ایک مرتبہ شروع کر کے جب متعین کر دیا تو دوبارہ اس میں بھی نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ کیوں کہ فرضیت جو مستدل کی دلیل تھی ، اس میں تھوڑی زیادتی کر دی جو زیادتی اسی وصف فرضیت کی تفسیر ہے وہ یہ کہ فرضیت رمضان میں تعیین اللہ کی طرف سے ہو چکی ہے، تو اب یہ دلیل مستدل کے دعوی کے خلاف یعنی عدم تعیین کی دلیل بن گئی ۔ غرض ہم نے فرضیت کو عدم تعیین کی علت قرار دیا ، یہ معارضہ بالقلب ہے۔
He is making the claim a proof, so it would require that one attribute be a proof for two contradictory rulings, which is rationally impossible. Therefore, the author states that a slight addition should be made in the attribute of the one who uses the proof, but that addition is an interpretation of that attribute, not changing it so that its attribute becomes something else. For example, the Shafi'is say: The fast of Ramadan is obligatory, so without specifying intention it is not performed, just as the make-up fast is obligatory and without specifying intention it is not performed. So the Shafi'is made obligation the cause for specifying intention, and analogized the fast of Ramadan to the make-up fast. We responded by way of inversion (qalb) and said: Obligation is not the cause for specifying intention, but rather the cause for not specifying intention. That is: The fast of Ramadan is obligatory, therefore it does not need specification by itself, because Allah has specified it. Just as after specifying a make-up fast once, it does not need specification again. In short, both the fast of Ramadan and the make-up fast share the cause of obligation, and both are equal in that after being specified once, they do not need specification again. But since the fast of Ramadan has been specified once by Allah, it does not need specification again, while the make-up fast becomes specified by starting with intention; so after starting and specifying it once, it too does not need intention again. Because the obligation that was the opponent's proof was slightly augmented, and that augmentation is an interpretation of that very attribute of obligation, namely that the specification of Ramadan is from Allah. Thus this proof became a proof against the opponent's claim, i.e., for non-specification. In short, we made obligation the cause for non-specification. This is the inversion (qalb).
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage demonstrates the usul principle of qalb al-illa (inversion of the cause) as a method of rebutting analogical reasoning (qiyas). The author explains that when an opponent uses an attribute as a cause for a ruling, the Hanafi can augment that attribute with a detail that changes its application without altering its essence. The example given is the Shafi'i claim that the obligation of Ramadan fast requires specifying intention, based on analogy with make-up fasts. The Shafi'is argue that obligation is the cause for specifying intention. The Hanafi response inverts this: obligation is actually the cause for not specifying intention, because Allah has already specified the time of Ramadan, making human specification unnecessary. This inversion (qalb) is a valid form of istihsan in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
قلب (qalb): Inversion of the cause (illah) by adding a condition that changes its legal effect while keeping the essence intact.
تعیین نیت (ta'yin al-niyyah): Specifying the intention for which act one is performing (e.g., specifying whether the fast is for Ramadan or make-up).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Ramadan fasting example, how did the Hanafis invert the Shafi'i 'illa to reject their qiyas?
A) They argued that obligation is not a valid cause at all.
B) They added that Allah has already specified Ramadan, so obligation becomes a cause for non-specification.
C) They denied the analogy between Ramadan and make-up fasts entirely.
D) They argued that intention is never required in any fast.

Key Takeaway
Qalb al-illa is a valid Hanafi method for rebutting qiyas by augmenting the opponent's cause with a condition from the Lawgiver.
